    钦定四库全书　　　　　子部十二
    　　北梦琐言　　　　　　　小説家一【杂事之属】提要
    　　【臣】等谨案北梦琐言二十卷宋孙光宪撰光宪字孟文自号葆光子十国春秋作贵平人而自题乃称富春考光宪自序言生自岷峨则当为蜀人其曰富春葢举郡望也仕唐为陵州判官旋依荆南高季兴为从事后劝高继冲以三州归宋太祖嘉之授黄州刺史以终五代史荆南世家载之甚明旧以为五代人者悮矣所着有荆台集橘斋集玩笔佣集巩湖编玩蚕书续通厯等书自宋代已散佚惟是书独传于后其曰北梦琐言者以左传称田于江南之梦而荆州在江北故以命名葢仕高氏时作也所载皆唐及五代士大夫逸事每条多载某人

    Explanation

    1

    The Complete Works of the Imperial Library　　　　　Category Twelve: Miscellaneous
    　　Trifles of the Northern Dream　　　　　　　Subcategory One: Miscellaneous Stories【Miscellaneous Affairs】Summary
    　　We officials respectfully submit that Trifles of the Northern Dream consists of twenty volumes and was written by Song Dynasty's Sun Guangxian. Sun Guangxian, courtesy name Mengwen, self-proclaimed Baoguangzi. The Ten Kingdoms Spring and Autumn records him as a native of Guiping, but his own inscription refers to him as Fuchun. Upon examining Sun Guangxian's preface, which states that he was born in the region around Mount Emei and Mount Min, it is evident that he should be considered a native of Shu. The reference to Fuchun is actually a reference to his clan name. He served as a judge in Lingzhou during the Tang Dynasty, then served under Gao Jixing in Jingnan as an official. Later, he advised Gao Jichong to surrender three states to the Song Dynasty, which Emperor Taizu praised. He was appointed as the governor of Huangzhou, and his career is clearly recorded in the "Jingnan Biographies" of the Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period. Previously, it was mistakenly believed that he lived during the Five Dynasties period. He wrote other works such as the "Jingtai Collection," "Juzhai Collection," "Wanbichen Collection," "Gonghu Compilation," "Wancan Book," and "Continued Tongli," but these have been lost since the Song Dynasty. Only this book has survived. The title "Trifles of the Northern Dream" is derived from a passage in the Zuo Zhuan, which mentions a dream about tilling land in the south of the river, while Jingzhou is located north of the Yangtze River, hence the name. It was written during his service to the Gao family. The content of the book includes anecdotes about officials from the Tang and Five Dynasties periods, and each entry often mentions a specific person.

    2

    所説以示有征葢用杜阳编之例其记载颇猥叙次亦颇冗防而遗文琐语往往可资考证故宋李昉等编太平广记多采其文晁公武读书志载光宪续通厯十卷辑唐及五代事以续马总之书叅以黄巢李茂贞刘守光按巴坚【案按巴坚原作阿保机今改正】吴唐闽广吴越两蜀事迹太祖以所纪多不实诏毁其书而此书未尝议及则语不甚诬可知矣世所行者凡二本一为明商维濬稗海所刻脱悮殆不可读近时扬州新刻乃元华亭孙道明所藏犹宋时陜西刋板差完整有绪故今以扬州本著录不用商氏本云乾隆四十三年三月恭校上

    Explanation

    2

    What is said to show evidence is based on the example of the Du Yang compilation. Its records are quite disordered, and its sequence is also quite redundant. However, the remnants and trivial words can often be used for verification. Therefore, during the Song Dynasty, Li Fang and others compiled Tai Ping Guang Ji and drew much from its text. Chao Gongwu's Reading Records mentions Guangxian's continuation of the Tong Li in ten volumes, which compiled events from the Tang and Five Dynasties to continue Ma Zong's book, and included references to Huang Chao, Li Maodun, Liu Shouguang, and An Baqin, as well as events from Wu, Tang, Min, Guang, Wu-Yue, and the two Shus. Emperor Taizu, because much of what it recorded was not accurate, ordered the book to be destroyed. But this book has never been criticized, so it is not very false, which can be known. There are two versions in circulation; one is the edition by Ming's Shang Weijun in Bai Hai, with many omissions and errors, making it nearly unreadable. Recently, a new edition from Yangzhou is a collection by Yuan's Hua Ting Sun Daoming, still somewhat complete and orderly as the Song Dynasty's Shaanxi edition. Therefore, the Yangzhou edition is recorded, and the Shang edition is not used. March of the 43rd year of Qianlong, respectfully submitted for proofreading.

    总纂官【臣】纪昀【臣】陆锡熊【臣】孙士毅
    　　总　校　官　【臣】　陆　费　墀

    　　北梦琐言序
    　　唐自广明乱离秘籍亡散武宗已后寂寞无闻朝野遗芳莫得传播仆生自岷峨官于荆郢咸京故事每愧面墙游处之间专于博访顷逢故凤翔杨玭少尹多话秦中平时旧说常记于心他日渚宫见元澄中允欵狎笑语多符其说元公谓旧族一二子弟曰诸贤生在长安闻事不迨富春此则存好问之所宏益也厥后每聆一事未敢孤信三复防校然始濡毫非但
    垂之空言亦欲因事劝戒三纪拾筐箧爰因公退咸取编连先以唐朝逹贤一言一行列于谈次其有事相近自唐至后唐梁蜀江南诸国所得闻知者皆附其末凡纂得事成二十卷禹贡云云土梦作又传有畋于江南之梦鄙从事于荆江之北题曰北梦琐言琐细形言大即可知也虽非经纬之作庶勉后进子孙俾希仰前事亦丝麻中菅蒯也通方者幸勿多诮焉

    Explanation

    3

    Chief Compiler [Minister] Ji Yun, [Minister] Lu Xixiong, [Minister] Sun Shiyi
    Chief Proofreader [Minister] Lu Feichi

    Preface to North Dream Trifles
    From the time of the chaos during the Guangming era, secret and rare books were lost and scattered. After the reign of Emperor Wuzong, there was a period of silence and obscurity, and the lingering fragrance of the court and countryside could not be spread. I was born in Min and E, and served in Jing and Ying, where I often felt ashamed of my ignorance. In my travels and stays, I dedicated myself to seeking out information. Recently, I met the former Deputy Prefect of Fengxiang, Yang Pin, who often spoke of the old customs and traditions of the Qin region, which I always kept in mind. Later, at the Palace by the Lake, I met Yuan Cheng, the Middle Scholar, and had friendly and intimate conversations with him. Many of his stories matched what I had heard before. Yuan Gong said to a few of his family members: "You all were born in Chang'an, but you did not hear as much as those in Fuchun. This is where the value of asking questions and thus expanding one's knowledge lies." Thereafter, whenever I heard something, I did not dare to trust it alone, but carefully verified and cross-checked it multiple times before writing it down. Not only did I aim to record these events, but also to use them to offer advice and encouragement. Over three decades, I gathered and compiled all the words and deeds of eminent Tang scholars, arranging them in order of their importance. Any events that were similar in nature, from the Tang dynasty to the Later Tang, Later Liang, Shu, and Southern dynasties, that I had heard or known, I added to the end. The total number of compiled events amounted to twenty volumes. The Yugong (The Tribute of Yu) describes the geography and administration of ancient China, and there is a dream of hunting in the south of the Yangtze River. I have been serving in the north of the Jing River, and titled this work North Dream Trifles. It is trivial and detailed, but the main points can be understood. Although it is not a work of great depth, it is hoped that it will encourage future generations and make them look up to past events. It is also like the coarse grass among silk and hemp. May those who understand not criticize too harshly.

    钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷一
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　宣宗称进士
    　　唐宣宗皇帝好儒雅每直殿学士从容未尝不论前代兴亡颇留心贡举尝于殿柱上自题曰乡贡进士李某或宰相出镇赋诗以赠之词皆清丽凡对宰臣言政事即终日忘倦洎僖宗皇帝好蹴毬鬭鸡为乐自以能于歩打谓俳优石野猪曰朕作歩打进士亦合得一状元野猪对曰或遇尧舜禹汤作礼部侍郎陛下不免且落第帝笑而已原其所好优劣即圣政可知也
    　　李太尉英俊
    　　太尉李徳幼神俊宪宗赏之坐于膝上父吉甫每以敏辩夸于同列武相元衡召之谓曰吾子在家所嗜何书意欲探其志也徳裕不应翌日元衡具告吉甫因戏曰公诚涉大痴耳吉甫归以责之徳曰武公身为帝弼不问理国调隂阳而问所嗜书者成均礼部之职也其言不当所以不应吉甫复告元衡大慙由是振名

    Explanation

    4

    The Complete Library in Four Branches of Literature
    　　Trifles of the Northern Dream, Volume One
    　　By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty
    　　Emperor Xuanzong's Appreciation for Jinshi
    　　Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty was fond of learning and culture. Whenever he conversed with the scholars in the palace, he would often discuss the rise and fall of past dynasties. He took a keen interest in the imperial examinations and once inscribed on the palace pillars, "Jinshi Li from the local examination." When a chancellor left office, he would compose poetry to send him off, the verses being both elegant and refined. Whenever he discussed state affairs with the chancellors, he would be engrossed for the entire day. By the time of Emperor Xizong, who enjoyed playing football and cockfighting for amusement, he boasted about his skill in "buddai jinshi" (a type of scholar) and said to the court jester Shi Yezhu, "Even if I were to become a jinshi, I should be eligible for the title of Zhuangyuan (top scholar)." Shi Yezhu replied, "If you were to meet the sage-kings Yao, Shun, Yu, and Tang as the head of the Ministry of Rites, Your Majesty would still be destined to fail." The emperor laughed and left it at that. From this, one can discern the difference in their preferences and understand the state of governance.

    　　The Bravery of Vice-Chancellor Li Deyu
    　　When Li Deyu, the Vice-Chancellor, was young, he was exceptionally intelligent and quick-witted. Emperor Xianzong was so impressed that he seated him on his knees. Li Jifu, Li Deyu's father, often boasted about his son's cleverness to his colleagues. Wu Yuanheng, the chancellor, summoned Li Deyu and asked him, "What books does your son enjoy at home? I wish to understand his aspirations." Li Deyu remained silent. The next day, Wu Yuanheng informed Li Jifu of the incident and joked, "You are indeed quite foolish!" Li Jifu returned home and scolded Li Deyu. Li Deyu replied, "Wu Gong, as the emperor's advisor, should not ask about the books my son enjoys but rather inquire about the state of governance and the balance of yin and yang. Asking about books is the responsibility of the Ministry of Rites, and his question was inappropriate. That is why I did not respond." Li Jifu then reported this to Wu Yuanheng, who was deeply embarrassed. From that day on, Wu Yuanheng's reputation grew.

    郑光免税
    　　宣宗舅郑光勅赐云阳鄠县两庄皆令免税宰臣奏恐非宜诏曰朕以光元舅欲优异之初不细思是免其赋尔等每于匡救必尽公忠亲戚之间人所难议茍非爱我岂尽嘉言事事能如斯天下何忧不治有始有卒当共守之寻罢葆光子同寮尝买一庄喜其无税乃谓曰天下庄产未有不征同寮以私券见拒尔后子孙为县宰定税求祈不暇国舅尚尔庶寮胡为
    　　再兴释教
    　　武宗嗣位宣宗居皇叔之行密游外方或止江南名山多识髙道僧人初听政谓宰相曰佛者虽异方之教深助理本所可存而勿论不欲过毁以伤令徳乃遣下诏防昌中灵山古迹招提弃废之地并令复之委长吏择僧之髙行者居之唯出家者不得妄度也懿宗即位唯以崇佛为事相国萧仿裴坦时为常侍谏议上疏极谏其畧云臣等闻元

    Explanation

    5

    Viceroy Zheng Guang's Tax Exemption
    　　During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong, his maternal uncle Zheng Guang was granted two estates in Yunyang and Hu counties, and was exempted from taxes. The chancellors submitted a petition stating that this was not appropriate. The emperor replied, "I wish to show special favor to Guang because he is my maternal uncle, but I did not think carefully at the beginning. This tax exemption is granted. You all must always offer advice with the utmost loyalty and integrity. It is difficult to discuss matters involving relatives. If they do not love me, how could they offer good advice? If everything can be handled like this, what worries would there be in governing the world? There must be a beginning and an end, and we must all adhere to it." Soon after, the chancellors were dismissed. Zheng Guang's son, who was a fellow official, once bought an estate and was pleased that it was tax-free. He then said, "There is no property in the world that is not taxed." His fellow official refused to sell to him with a private note. Later, Zheng Guang's descendants served as county magistrates and set the taxes, leaving no time to seek blessings. Even a maternal uncle like Zheng Guang is so, what about common officials?

    Reviving Buddhism Again
    　　After Emperor Wuzong succeeded to the throne, Emperor Xuanzong, who was his uncle, secretly traveled to foreign lands or stopped at famous mountains in southern Jiangnan, meeting many high-ranking Taoist and Buddhist monks. When he first heard of politics, he said to the chancellors, "Buddhism, though a foreign religion, deeply supports the fundamental principles of governance. It is possible to preserve without discussing. I do not want to excessively criticize and harm good virtue." He then issued an edict to restore ancient temples and abandoned sites, entrusting local officials to select high-ranking monks to reside there. Only those who have taken monastic vows are not to be ordained indiscriminately. After Emperor Yizong ascended the throne, he devoted himself solely to promoting Buddhism. Chancellor Xiao Fang and Pei Tan, who were serving as Attendants and Advisors at the time, submitted a memorial with strong advice, the main points being: "We hear that the original..."

    6

    祖之道用慈俭为先素王之风以仁义是首相沿百世作则千年至圣至明不可易也如佛者生于天竺去彼王宫割爱中之至难取灭后之殊胜名归象外理出尘中非为帝王所能慕也广引无益有损之义文多不録文理婉顺与韩愈元和中上请除佛骨表不异也懿皇虽听览称奬竟不能止末年迎佛骨才至京师俄而晏驾识者谓大丧之兆也
    　　郑氏女庐墓
    　　唐大中年兖州奏先差赴庆州行营押官郑神佐阵没其室女年二十四先亡父未行营已前许嫁右骁雄军健李元庆未受财礼阿郑知父神佐阵没遂与李元庆休亲截髪往庆州北懐安镇亡父遗骸到兖州瑕丘县进贤乡与亡母合讫便于茔内筑庐识者曰女子适邉取父遗骸合烈而且孝诚可嘉也庐墓习于近俗国不能禁非也广引礼经而证之

    Explanation

    6

    The Way of the Ancestor uses benevolence and frugality as its foremost principles, while the style of the Simple King is characterized by righteousness. Passed down through a hundred generations, it serves as a model for a thousand years, being the most sage and the most wise, and cannot be changed. As for the Buddha, born in Tianzhu (India), leaving the royal palace, he cut off the deepest attachments, achieving the extraordinary after attaining Nirvana, with fame returning beyond the realm and principles emerging from the mundane. This is not something that emperors can aspire to. Extensively citing the meanings of what is futile and harmful, much of which is not recorded, the style is gentle and smooth, similar to Han Yu's petition to remove the Buddha bones during the Yuanhe period. The wise emperor, though he listened and praised, could not stop it. In his later years, when the Buddha bones arrived in the capital, he soon passed away. Those who understand consider it a sign of great mourning.

    The daughter of the Zheng family built a thatched hut over her father's grave. In the Dazhong period of the Tang dynasty, the governor of Yan state reported that Zheng Shen Zuo, who was sent to guard the camp in Qingzhou, died in battle. His daughter, aged twenty-four, had already been betrothed to Li Yuanqing, a soldier in the Right Xiangxiong unit, but had not yet received the betrothal gifts. After learning that her father Zheng Shen Zuo had died in battle, she divorced Li Yuanqing, shaved her head, went to Huai'an in the north of Qingzhou to retrieve her father's remains, and buried them together with her mother in the Jinxiang area of Xuxiu County, Yan state, then built a hut in the cemetery. Those who understand said that the woman's act of going to the border to retrieve her father's remains and burying them together with her mother is both brave and filial, truly commendable. Building a hut over a grave is a recent custom, but it cannot be prohibited by the state, as it is not wrong. Extensively citing the rites to prove it.

    日本国王子棊
    　　唐宣宗朝日本国王子入贡善围棊帝令待诏顾师言与之对手王子出本国如楸玉局冷暖玉棊子盖玉之苍者如楸玉色其冷暖者言冬暖夏凉人或过说非也王子至三十三下师言惧辱君命汗手死心始敢落指王子亦凝目缩臂数四竟伏不胜逥谓礼宾曰此第防手答曰其第三手也王子愿见第一手礼宾曰胜第三可见第二胜第二可见第一王子抚局叹曰小国之
    一不及大国之三此日本人犹不可轻况中国之士乎葆光子曰蜀简州刺史安重霸黩货无厌部民有油客子者姓邓能棊其力粗赡安輙召与对敌只令立侍每落一子俾其退立于西北牖下俟我算路然后【一作始】进之终日不下十数子而已邓生倦立且饥殆不可堪次日又召或有讽邓生曰此侯好赂本不为棊何不献效而自求退邓生然之以中金十铤获免良可笑也

    Explanation

    7

    Go Game with the Japanese Prince

    During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty, a Japanese prince visited China and was skilled at playing Go. The emperor ordered the imperial advisor Gu Shiyan to play against him. The prince brought Go pieces made of cold and warm jade, with the green ones resembling the color of pine jade. The cold and warm jade pieces were said to be warm in winter and cool in summer, though some may have exaggerated this. The prince reached the 33rd move, and Gu Shiyan, fearing to dishonor the emperor's command, was sweating and trembling before finally making a move. The prince was also intensely focused and tense, and after several moves, he conceded defeat. He then said to the official in charge of foreign affairs, "This is just a defensive move." The official replied, "If you beat the third player, you can see the second. If you beat the second, you can see the first." The prince wished to see the strongest player. The official said, "If you beat the third, you can see the second. If you beat the second, you can see the first." The prince then said, "A small country like Japan cannot match a great country like China in three aspects, let alone the Chinese scholars."

    The Story of Deng

    Bao Guangzi said, "Governor An Zhongba of Jianzhou in Shu was greedy for wealth and called Deng, a skilled Go player, to play against him. He made Deng stand by and only allowed him to make a move after he had calculated his own moves, so that throughout the day, only a few moves were played. The next day, he called Deng again. Someone advised Deng, 'This governor likes bribes. He doesn't play Go; why don't you offer him something and ask to leave?' Deng agreed and paid ten ingots of gold to avoid further humiliation, which is truly laughable."

    駮杜预
    　　大中时工部尚书陈商立汉文帝废防议立春秋左传学议以孔圣修经褒贬善恶例分明法家流也左丘明为鲁史载述时政惜忠贤之泯灭恐善恶之失坠以日繋月修其职官本非扶助圣言縁饰经防盖太史氏之流也举其春秋则明白而有实合之左氏则丛杂而无征杜元凯曾不思夫子所以为经当与诗书周易等列丘明所以为史当与司马迁班固等列取二义乖剌不侔之语防而贯之故防防有所未周婉章有所未一文多不载又睹呉郡陆蒙亦引啖助赵匡为证正与陈工部义同葆光子同寮王公贞范精于春秋有駮正元凯之谬条绪甚多人咸【一作或】讶之独鄙夫尝以陈陆啖赵之论窃然之非茍合也唯义所在

    Explanation

    8

    Refutation of Du Yu

    During the Dazhong era, the Minister of Works Chen Shang established debates on Emperor Wen of Han's abolition of the guard and the Spring and Autumn Annals and Zuo Commentary scholarship. Confucius revised the classics, clearly distinguishing between praise and criticism, which is associated with Legalist thought. Zuo Qiuming, as the historian of Lu, recorded contemporary politics, lamenting the loss of loyal and virtuous individuals and fearing the decline of good and evil. He recorded events by days and months, detailing the roles of officials, which is fundamentally different from supporting the words of the sages or embellishing the classics. It is of the historian school. The Spring and Autumn Annals are clear and practical, while the Zuo Zhuan is complex and lacks evidence. Du Yu never considered that Confucius' work as the classics should be placed alongside the Shujing, Shijing, and Yijing, and that Zuo Qiuming's work as history should be placed alongside those of Sima Qian and Ban Gu. He combined these two distinct ideas in a way that is inconsistent and incomplete, leading to gaps in his explanations and a lack of coherence in his writings, with many passages omitted. Additionally, Lu Guimeng from Wu also cited the works of Dan Zhu and Zhao Kuang as evidence, aligning with Chen Shang's arguments. My colleague Wang Zhenfan, who specializes in the Spring and Autumn Annals, has refuted many of Du Yu's errors, presenting a well-organized and detailed critique that has surprised many. Only I, a humble person, have privately agreed with the arguments of Chen Shang, Lu Guimeng, Dan Zhu, and Zhao Kuang, not out of blind agreement, but because the matter is right.

    9

    李太尉抑白少傅
    　　白少傅居易文章冠世不跻大位先是刘禹锡太和中为宾客时李太尉徳裕同分司东都禹锡谒于徳裕曰近曾得白居易文集否徳裕曰累有相示别令贮然未一披今日为吾子览之及取看盈其箱笥没于尘坌既啓之而复卷之谓禹锡曰吾于此人不足久矣其文章精絶何必览焉但恐逥吾之心其见抑也如此衣冠之士【一作内】并皆忌之咸曰有学士才非宰臣器识者于其答制中见经纶之用为时所排此贾谊在汉文之朝不为卿相知人皆惜之葆光子曰李卫公之抑忌白少傅举而知也初文宗命徳裕朝中朋党首以杨虞卿牛僧孺为言杨牛即白公宻友也其不引翼义在于斯非抑文章也虑其朋比而掣肘也

    Explanation

    9

    Li Deyu Suppressed Bai Juyi

    Bai Juyi, the Right Minister, was renowned for his literary talent but did not attain a high official position. Before this, during the Taihe era, Liu Yuxi, serving as a guest official, visited Li Deyu, the Right Minister, and asked, "Have you recently received the collection of Bai Juyi's writings?" Li Deyu replied, "I have repeatedly shown it to you and stored it separately, but I have not yet opened it. Today, I will look through it for you." When he took it out, it was full of dust. After opening it and then rolling it up again, he said to Liu Yuxi, "I find this person unworthy of keeping for long. His writing is so exquisite, why bother to read it? I fear it will turn my heart." Thus, he was suppressed in this way. The gentlemen of the literati class all envied him, saying that he had the talent of a scholar but lacked the vision of a prime minister. In his responses to imperial edicts, one could see his ability to manage state affairs, but he was suppressed by the times. This is similar to Jia Yi, who served under Emperor Wen of Han but did not become a high-ranking official, and people felt sorry for him. Bao Guangzi said, "Li Deyu's suppression of Bai Juyi was based on this reason." Initially, Emperor Wenzong ordered Li Deyu to mention Yang Yuqing and Niu Sengru as leaders of factions in the court. Yang and Niu were close friends of Bai Juyi, and his reluctance to support them is due to this. It is not suppressing his writing; he feared that they would form alliances and hinder his actions.

    10

    牛僧孺竒士
    　　相国牛僧孺字思黯或言牛仙客之后居宛叶之间少单贫力学有倜傥之志唐永贞中擢进士第时与同辈过政事堂宰相谓曰扫防奉僧孺独出曰不敢众耸异之元和初登制科歴省郎中书舎人御史中书门下平章事扬州建州两镇东都留守左仆射先是撰周秦行记李徳裕切言短之大中初卒未赐諡后白敏中入相乃奏定諡曰简白居易曰文葆光子曰僧孺登庸在徳裕之先又非忌才所能掩抑今以牛之才术比李之功勲自然知其臧否也且周秦行记非所宜言徳裕著论而罪之正人览记而骇之勿谓卫公掩贤妬善牛相不罹大祸亦幸而免

    Explanation

    10

    Niu Sengru, a Remarkable Scholar

    The chancellor Niu Sengru, whose courtesy name was Sianan, was said to be descended from Niu Xianke. He lived in the region between Wan and Ye, where he was born into a poor family but dedicated himself to learning with great diligence and had bold and unconventional aspirations. During the Yongzhen period, he was selected as a Jinshi (imperial scholar). At the time, he and his peers passed through the Hall of State Affairs, where the prime minister said, "Cleanse and prepare for our arrival." Niu Sengru alone stepped forward and said, "I dare not." The others were astonished by his boldness. In the early Yuanhe period, he passed the imperial examinations for specialized positions and held various high-ranking offices, including those in the central government, such as the Office of the Imperial Censor, the Secretariat, and the position of Left Chancellor. He also served as the governor of Yangzhou and Jianzhou, and as the governor of the Eastern Capital (Luoyang). Before his death, he wrote the Zhouqin Xingji, a historical or travelogue-style account of the Zhou and Qin dynasties. Li Deyu sharply criticized this work. In the early Dazhong period, Niu Sengru died without receiving a posthumous title. Later, after Bai Minzhong became chancellor, he proposed the posthumous title "Jian" for Niu Sengru. Bai Juyi and Bao Guangzi commented, "Niu Sengru rose to prominence before Li Deyu, and his talents could not be suppressed. Comparing Niu's abilities and achievements with Li's, it is clear to see the merits and faults of both. Moreover, the Zhouqin Xingji was not appropriate, and Li Deyu's criticism of it was justified, while others found it shocking. Do not say that Li Deyu, the Duke of Wei, was jealous of talent and envious of goodness. Niu Sengru narrowly escaped a great calamity, which was fortunate indeed."

    11

    令狐滈预抜文解
    　　唐大中末相国令狐绹罢相其子滈应进士举在父未罢相前预拔文解及第谏议大夫崔宣上疏述滈弄父权势倾天下以举人文卷须十月前送纳岂可父身尚居于枢务男私拔其解名干挠主司侮弄文法恐奸欺得路孤直杜门云云请在御史台推勘疏留中不出葆光子曰令狐公在大中之初倾陷李太尉唯以附防李绅而杀呉湘又擅改元和史又言赂遗阉宦殊不似徳裕立功于国自俭立身掎其小瑕忘其大美洎身居岩庙别无所长谏官上章可见之矣与朱崖之终始殆难比焉
    　　刘三复记三生事

    Explanation

    11

    Pre-selection of Liu Huchao for the Imperial Examination

    At the end of the Dazhong era, the chancellor Lü Tuó resigned from his post, and his son Huchao was preparing to take the Jinshi examination before his father had stepped down. Huchao was prematurely selected for the examination and passed. The Counselor-in-Advisory, Cui Xuan, submitted a memorial stating that Huchao was abusing his father's power and influence, swaying the entire empire. He argued that the examination papers were required to be submitted by October, but how could it be acceptable for the son to privately select his father's name, interfering with the chief examiner, mocking and manipulating the legal procedures, allowing deceit and corruption to prevail? Huchao should isolate himself in seclusion, and the matter should be investigated by the Censorate. However, the memorial was not acted upon.

    The Preserver of Light commented: During the early Dazhong era, Lü Tuó was involved in the downfall of Li Taiwei, solely because he was aligned with Li Sen, who had killed Wu Xiang. He also altered the history of the Yuanhe period and accused officials of bribing eunuchs. This was far from the deeds of Deyu, who established his reputation through his contributions to the state and his frugal lifestyle. By focusing on minor flaws and ignoring his great virtues, when he held high office, he had no other merits. The advice from the censors is evident. Comparing his actions to those of Zhu Yaya, they are hardly comparable.

    Liu Sanfu's Account of Three Lifetimes

    12

    唐太和中李徳裕镇浙西有刘三复者少贫苦学有才思时中【一作王】人赍御书至以赐徳裕徳裕试其所为谓曰子可为我草表能立就【一作搆】或归以创之三复曰文理贵中不贵其速徳裕以为当言三复又请曰渔歌樵唱皆传公述作愿以文集见示徳裕出数轴与之三复乃体而为表徳裕嘉之因遣诣阙求试果登第歴任台阁三复能记三生事云曾为马常患渴望驿而嘶伤其蹄则心连痛后三复乗马过硗确之地必为缓辔有辙石必去之其家不施门限虑伤马蹄也其子邺勅赐及第登廊庙上表雪徳裕以朱崖神榇归洛中报其先恩也士大夫美之
    　　秃角犀
    　　杜邠公悰司徒佑之孙父曰从郁歴选补畿令悰尚宪宗岐阳公主累居大镇复居廊庙无他才未尝延接寒素甘食窃位而已有朝士贻书于悰曰公以硕大敦厐之徳生于文明之运矢厥谟猷出入隆显极言讥之文多不録时人号为秃角犀凡莅藩镇未尝断狱系囚死而不问宜其责之呜呼处髙位而妨贤享厚禄以丰己无功于国无徳于民富贵而终斯又何人也子孙不享何莫由斯

    Explanation

    12

    During the Tahe era of the Tang dynasty, Li De Yu was stationed in Zhe West, and there was a man named Liu San Fu who, despite growing up poor and hardworking in his studies, possessed remarkable talent and insight. At the time, a messenger carrying imperial edicts arrived to bestow upon Li De Yu. Li De Yu tested Liu San Fu's abilities and said, "You can draft a memorial for me. Can you complete it immediately?" Liu San Fu replied, "The essence of writing lies in precision, not speed." Li De Yu thought he had a point. Liu San Fu then asked, "The songs of fishermen and woodcutters are all said to be inspired by your writings. I wish to see your collection of writings." Li De Yu handed him several scrolls, and Liu San Fu then composed a memorial based on them. Li De Yu praised him and sent him to the imperial court to take the examination. Indeed, he passed the examination and served in various high-ranking positions. Liu San Fu could recall three lifetimes' worth of experiences. He once was a horse that often longed for the post station and neighed. If its hoof was hurt, it felt pain deeply. Later, when Liu San Fu rode a horse over rough terrain, he would slow down the pace. If there were stones on the road, he would remove them. His family did not install thresholds on their doors, out of concern for hurting the horse's hooves. His son Yi was granted the top rank in the imperial examination and served in the imperial court. He submitted a memorial to clear Li De Yu's name and returned the sacred coffin of Zhu Ya to be buried in Luoyang, to repay the kindness of his ancestors. Scholars and officials praised him.

    A Bald-Headed Rhinoceros

    Du Bin Gong Cong, the grandson of Duke You, whose father was named Cong Yu, served in various local administrative positions. He married Princess Qiyang of the Xianzong era and held many important positions. He served in the imperial court again but had no other talents. He never received poor and uneducated scholars and only enjoyed good food and held a position without doing much. A scholar wrote a letter to Cong, saying, "You have the virtue of being large and solid, living in a time of civilization. Direct your wise counsel, frequenting high-ranking positions. I strongly criticized him, but the text is too long to record." People called him a bald-headed rhinoceros. Whenever he governed a frontier region, he never punished or imprisoned anyone, not even inquiring about the dead. It is appropriate to blame him. Holding a high position and obstructing the talented, enjoying a generous salary to enrich oneself, having no merit for the country and no virtue for the people, to die in wealth and honor, what kind of person is this? His descendants did not enjoy the same, for what reason?

    13

    魏文贞公笏
    　　唐文宗皇帝谓宰相曰太宗得魏征采拾阙遗弼成圣政今我得魏謩于疑似之间必极匡谏虽不敢希及贞观之政庶防处无过之地今授謩右补阙委舎人善为之词又问謩曰卿家有何圗书謩曰家书悉无唯有文贞公笏在文宗令进来郑覃在侧曰在人不在笏文宗曰卿浑未晓但甘棠之义非要笏也

    　　北梦琐言卷一
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷二
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　皮日休献书
    　　咸通中进士皮日休进书两通其一请以孟子为学科其畧云臣闻圣人之道不过乎经经之降者不过乎史史之降者不过乎子不异道者孟子也舎是而子者必斥乎经史为圣人之贼也云云文多不载请废庄列之书以孟子为主有能通其义者其科选同明经也其二请以韩文公愈配飨太学其畧曰臣闻圣人之道不过乎求用用于生前则一时可知也用于死后则万世可知也云云又云孟子荀卿翼传孔道以至于文中子文中子之道旷矣其

    Explanation

    13

    The Emperor Wenzong of Tang, addressing the chancellors, said: "Emperor Taizong received Wei Zheng, who gathered and corrected omissions to perfect sage governance. Now I have gained Wei Mo, who will offer the strongest possible remonstrance in ambiguous situations. Though I dare not hope to reach the level of the Zhenguan era, I hope to avoid making mistakes. Today, I appoint Wei Mo as the Right Censor and instruct the Secretary to craft appropriate words for him. I then asked Wei Mo, 'What books do you have at home?' He replied, 'I have no books at all, only the tablet of the Right Censor Wei, the Marquis of Wen.' The Emperor ordered it brought in. Zheng Tan, standing nearby, said, 'It is in the person, not in the tablet.' The Emperor said, 'You do not understand at all. The meaning of the banyan tree is not dependent on the tablet.'

    North Dream Trifles, Volume One
    Imperially Approved Four Treasuries
    North Dream Trifles, Volume Two
    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Pi Rishou Submits a Written Proposal
    During the Xiantong era, the Jinshi Pi Rishou submitted two written proposals. The first proposed making Mencius a subject of study, stating: "I have heard that the principles of sage rulers do not exceed the classics. The principles of the classics do not exceed the histories, and the principles of the histories do not exceed the philosophical works. The one who does not diverge from the path is Mencius. Those who diverge from the path in their philosophical works are certainly to be condemned as enemies of the classics and histories." And so on. The text is too long to include here, but he proposed abolishing the works of Zhuangzi and Liezi in favor of Mencius, and making those who understand its meaning eligible for the same selection as those who pass the classics. The second proposal suggested enshrining Han Yu in the Imperial Academy, stating: "I have heard that the principles of sage rulers do not exceed the pursuit of usefulness. Their usefulness during their lifetime can be known at the time, and their usefulness after their death can be known for all time. And so on. He further said that Mencius and Xunzi helped to spread Confucius's teachings, and that the teachings of Wen Ziqi are vast and far-reaching."

    14

    防于室授者唯韩愈焉蹴及杨墨蹂践释老故得孔道炳然如日星焉吾唐以来一人而已茍不得在二十一贤之数列则典礼未为备也日休先字逸少后字袭美襄阳竟陵人也业文隐鹿门山中自号间气布衣大中榜未及第礼部侍郎郑愚以其貎不扬戏之曰子之才学甚富如一日何休对曰侍郎不可以一日废二日谓不以人废言也举子咸推伏之官至国子博士寓苏州与陆蒙为文友着文薮十卷皮子三卷黄冦中遇害其子为钱尚父呉越相
    　　宰相怙权【温庭筠附】
    　　宣宗时相国令狐绹最受恩遇而怙权尤忌胜已以其子滈不解而第为张云刘蜕崔瑄叠上疏防之宣宗优容绹出镇维扬上表诉子之寃其畧云一从先帝久次中书得臣恩者谓臣好不得臣恩者谓臣弱臣非美酒美肉安能啖众人之口时以执己之短取诮于人或云曽以故事访于温岐对以其事出南华且曰非僻书也或冀相公燮理之暇时宜览古绹

    Explanation

    14

    Only Han Yu was entrusted with the task of guarding and transmitting the teachings, trampling the teachings of Yang and Mo and the doctrines of Buddhism and Daoism, thus making Confucian teachings shine brightly like the sun and stars. Since the Tang dynasty, Han Yu alone has achieved this. If Han Yu is not included among the Twenty-One Sages, the ritual ceremonies are not complete. Li Yu was originally named Yi Shao and later named Xi Mei, from Xiangyang and Jingling. He devoted himself to literature, lived in seclusion in Lumen Mountain, and called himself "Jianqi" (a rare talent). During the Dazhong imperial examination, he did not pass, and the Minister of Rites Zheng Yu, mocking his appearance, said, "Your talent and learning are very rich, but why only one day?" Li Yu replied, "Minister, you cannot abandon me in one day; two days mean you should not discard my words because of my appearance." All scholars admired and respected him. He became a Doctor of the Imperial Academy, lived in Suzhou, and was a literary friend of Lu Guimeng. He wrote ten volumes of "Wen Su" and three volumes of "Pi Zi." His son was a chancellor under the King of Wu and Yue.

    During the reign of Emperor Xuānzōng, the Chancellor Lìng Hú Tóng received the most favor and held the highest power, especially jealous of those who surpassed him. Because his son Hào did not understand and failed the imperial examination, Zhang Yún, Liu Tuì, and Cui Xuān successively submitted memorials to protect him. Emperor Xuānzōng showed leniency towards Tóng and sent him to govern Weiyang. Tóng submitted a memorial to plead for his son's injustice, stating: "Since the previous emperor, I have been in the office of the Secretariat for a long time. Those who receive my favor say I am kind, while those who do not receive my favor say I am weak. I am not made of fine wine and meat, how could I satisfy everyone's mouths? At times, I am criticized for my shortcomings, and some say I once consulted Wēn Qí about historical matters. He replied that the matter originated from the Nanhua Jing (Tao Te Ching) and said it was not a rare book. Perhaps the chancellor should take the time to read ancient texts."

    15

    益怒之乃奏岐有才无行不宜与第防宣宗私行为温岐所忤乃授方城尉所以岐诗云因知此恨人多积悔读南华第二篇又李商隐绹父楚之故吏也殊不展分商隐憾之因题防阁落句云郎君官重施行马东阁无因许再窥亦怒之官只止使下贠外也江东罗隐亦受知于绹毕竟无成有诗哭相国云深恩无以报底事是柴荆以三才子怨望即知绹之遗贤也
    　　骆山人吿王庭凑
    　　唐田宏正之领镇州三军杀之而立王庭凑即王武俊支属也庭凑生于别墅尝有鸠数十只朝集庭树暮集檐下有里人骆徳播异之及长骈胁善隂符谷之书歴军职得士心曾使河阳囬在中路以酒困寝于路隅忽有一人荷防而过熟视之曰贵当列土非常人也仆者寤以告庭凑庭凑驰数里及之致敬而问自云济源骆山人也向见君鼻中之气左如

    Explanation

    15

    The emperor was increasingly angered by this and reported that Qi had talent but lacked proper conduct, making him unsuitable for promotion. He also mentioned that Emperor Xuānzōng's private actions offended Wen Qi, so Qi was appointed as the military officer in Fāngchéng. Therefore, in Qi's poem, he wrote: "I now understand this resentment; people accumulate regret from reading the second chapter of the Nánhuá." Li Shangyin, whose father was an old official of the state of Chu, was not shown favor by Táo, and Li Shangyin resented him. Therefore, he inscribed a poem in the guardhouse, the last line of which said: "Young man, despite your high status, you cannot enter the eastern pavilion again." The official position only allowed for a low rank. Luò Yǐn from Jiangdong was also known to Táo, but despite this, he achieved no success. He wrote a poem mourning the chancellor, saying: "Deep favor cannot be repaid; what matter is this humble dwelling?" Because of the resentment of the three talented scholars, it is known that Táo neglected talented people.

    Lù Shānrén informed Wang Tíngcuō. During the reign of Táng Tián Hóngzhèng, he led the three armies of Zhènzhōu, killed someone, and established Wang Tíngcuō. Wang Tíngcuō was a relative of Wáng Wǔjùn. He was born in a villa, and once several dozen birds gathered in the courtyard trees in the morning and under the eaves in the evening. A villager named Lù Débō found it strange. When he grew up, he had broad shoulders and was skilled in the books of Yin符 and Gu鬼. He served in military positions and gained the trust of the soldiers. Once, he was sent to Héyáng, returned on the way, got drunk, and slept in a corner of the road. Suddenly, a person carrying a basket passed by and looked at him carefully, saying: "He should be a fiefdom holder, not an ordinary person." The servant woke up and told Wang Tíngcuō. Wang Tíngcuō rode several miles to catch up with him, showed respect, and asked. The man introduced himself as Lù Shānrén from Jǐyuán, saying: "I saw that your nose breath was like this."

    16

    龙而右如虎龙虎气交王在今秋子孙相继满一百年又云家之庭合有大树树及于堂是其兆也是年果为三军扶立为留后归别墅而庭树婆娑暗北舎矣墅西飞龙山神庭凑往祭之将及祠百歩有人具冠冕折腰于庭凑及入庙神乃侧坐至今面东起宇尚存焉庭凑清俭公正忠于朝廷勤于军民子孙世嗣为镇帅至朱梁时王镕封赵王为部将张文礼灭之
    　　授任致冦
    　　唐马植相公曾镇安南安抚军民懐柔蛮獠废珠池尚俭素李琢后镇是用法大酷军城逺出而属南蛮六七年间劳动兵役咸通七年髙骈复之先是荆徐间征役拒蛮人甚苦之有举子闻许卒二千没于蛮乡有诗刺曰南荒不择吏致我交趾覆联绵三四年致我交趾辱懦者鬭则退武者兵益黩军容满天下战将多金玉刮得齐民疮分为猛士禄雄雄许昌师忠武冠其族去为万骑风住为一川肉时有践卒囬千门万户哭哀声动闾里怨气成山谷谁能听鼔声不忍看金镞念此堪泪流悠悠颍川緑吟此诗有以见【一作知】失于授任为国家生事大东之苦斯其乎

    Explanation

    16

    Final Translation

    The dragon on the right is like a tiger, the dragon and tiger qi (vital energy) intersect, and the king will reign in this autumn. The family courtyard should have a big tree, and the tree reaching the hall is a sign of this. That year, indeed, the three armies supported him as the acting governor, and he returned to his villa. The courtyard trees sway and darken the northern shed. In the west of the villa, the god of the Flying Dragon Mountain, Court Gather, went to worship it. As he was about to reach the temple, a hundred steps away, someone wearing a hat and robe bowed to him; when he entered the temple, the god was sitting sideways, facing east, and the structure still stands to this day. Court Gather was clear, thrifty, fair, loyal to the court, and diligent in serving the military and civilians. His descendants succeeded him as the commander of the garrison, and during the time of Zhu Liang, Wang Rong was enfeoffed as the Prince of Zhao, but was killed by his subordinate Zhang Wenli.

    Appointing officials leads to trouble.

    The Chancellor Ma Zhi of Tang once governed An Nan, pacified the military and civilians, treated the barbarians and savages kindly, abolished the pearl pool, and maintained frugality and simplicity. Li Zhuo later governed this region, using harsh laws, and the military city was far away and belonged to the southern barbarians, leading to labor and military service for six or seven years. In the seventh year of Xiantong, Gao Pian restored it; previously, between Jing and Xu, the conscription and resistance to the barbarians were very difficult. A candidate heard that two thousand soldiers had died in the barbarian territory, and wrote a poem to criticize, saying:

    The southern regions do not select officials properly, leading to the downfall of our troops. For three or four years, we have suffered humiliation. The weak retreat when they fight, and the brave become more brutal. Military forces fill the land, and generals amass wealth and jewels, carving the wounds of the common people into the salaries of the brave. The mighty army of Xu Chang, led by the loyal and valiant, departs like a thousand horses, stopping like a river of flesh. Sometimes, the foot soldiers return, and the gates and doors of a thousand households cry out, their lamentations echoing through the streets and alleys, filling the valleys with resentment. Who can bear to listen to the drumbeats, unable to look at the golden arrowheads? Thinking of this, tears flow endlessly. The green waters of the River Yi, reciting this poem, reveal the suffering caused by poor appointments, which is the cause of great hardship in the eastern regions.

    Final Translation

    The dragon on the right is like a tiger, the dragon and tiger qi (vital energy) intersect, and the king will reign in this autumn. The family courtyard should have a big tree, and the tree reaching the hall is a sign of this. That year, indeed, the three armies supported him as the acting governor, and he returned to his villa. The courtyard trees sway and darken the northern shed. In the west of the villa, the god of the Flying Dragon Mountain, Court Gather, went to worship it. As he was about to reach the temple, a hundred steps away, someone wearing a hat and robe bowed to him; when he entered the temple, the god was sitting sideways, facing east, and the structure still stands to this day. Court Gather was clear, thrifty, fair, loyal to the court, and diligent in serving the military and civilians. His descendants succeeded him as the commander of the garrison, and during the time of Zhu Liang, Wang Rong was enfeoffed as the Prince of Zhao, but was killed by his subordinate Zhang Wenli.

    Appointing officials leads to trouble.

    The Chancellor Ma Zhi of Tang once governed An Nan, pacified the military and civilians, treated the barbarians and savages kindly, abolished the pearl pool, and maintained frugality and simplicity. Li Zhuo later governed this region, using harsh laws, and the military city was far away and belonged to the southern barbarians, leading to labor and military service for six or seven years. In the seventh year of Xiantong, Gao Pian restored it; previously, between Jing and Xu, the conscription and resistance to the barbarians were very difficult. A candidate heard that two thousand soldiers had died in the barbarian territory, and wrote a poem to criticize, saying:

    The southern regions do not select officials properly, leading to the downfall of our troops. For three or four years, we have suffered humiliation. The weak retreat when they fight, and the brave become more brutal. Military forces fill the land, and generals amass wealth and jewels, carving the wounds of the common people into the salaries of the brave. The mighty army of Xu Chang, led by the loyal and valiant, departs like a thousand horses, stopping like a river of flesh. Sometimes, the foot soldiers return, and the gates and doors of a thousand households cry out, their lamentations echoing through the streets and alleys, filling the valleys with resentment. Who can bear to listen to the drumbeats, unable to look at the golden arrowheads? Thinking of this, tears flow endlessly. The green waters of the River Yi, reciting this poem, reveal the suffering caused by poor appointments, which is the cause of great hardship in the eastern regions.

    17

    髙骈开海路【王审知开海附】
    　　安南髙骈奏开本州海路初交趾以北距南海有水路多覆巨舟骈往视之乃有横石隐隐然在水中因奏请开凿以通南海之利其表畧云人牵利楫石限横津才登一去之舟便作九泉之计时有诏听之乃召工者啖以厚利竟削其石交广之利民至今赖之以济焉或言骈以术假雷电以开之未知其详葆光子尝闻闽王王审知患海畔石碕为舟楫之梗一夜梦呉安王【即伍子胥也】许以开导乃命判官刘山甫躬往祈祭三奠才毕风雷勃兴山甫凭髙观焉见海中有黄物可长千百丈奋跃攻击凡三日晴霁见石港通畅便于泛涉于时録奏赐名甘棠港即渤海假神之力又何怪焉亦号此地为天威路实神功也

    Explanation

    17

    High Pian Opened the Sea Route [Wang Shenji Also Opened the Sea Route]

    Initially, there was a sea route between Jiaozhi (in modern-day northern Vietnam) and the South China Sea, but many large ships sank in this area. High Pian, the governor of Annam, went to inspect the situation and discovered hidden rocks in the water. He then submitted a petition to the court requesting the excavation of the sea route to facilitate trade with the South China Sea. His memorial stated: "People are risking their lives to navigate these treacherous waters, and the rocks are a major obstacle. If we could clear these rocks, it would greatly benefit the people of the region." The emperor granted his request, and High Pian hired workers and offered them substantial rewards to clear the rocks. After the rocks were removed, the sea route became safe and navigable, benefiting the people of the region for generations.

    Some say that High Pian used his skills to summon lightning and thunder to clear the rocks, though the details are unclear. Bao Guangzi, a historian, once heard that Wang Shenji, the ruler of Min, was troubled by rocks along the coast that obstructed maritime traffic. One night, he dreamed of Wu Zixu (also known as Wu An Wang), who promised to help clear the rocks. Wang Shenji then ordered his official Liu Shanfu to perform a ritual to seek divine assistance. As soon as the ritual was completed, a fierce storm arose, and Liu Shanfu watched from a high place as a yellow object, measuring thousands of feet in length, attacked the rocks. After three days of intense activity, the storm subsided, and the rocks were cleared, revealing a clear and navigable channel. The area was then recorded and named "Gantang Port," and it was also called "Tianwei Road," signifying the divine intervention that had made it possible.

    18

    放孤寒三人及第【科松防花事附】
    　　咸通中礼部侍郎髙湜知举榜内孤贫【一作负】者公乗亿赋诗三【一作二】百首人多书于屋壁许棠有洞庭诗尤工时人谓之许洞庭最竒者有聂夷中河南中都人少贫苦精于古体有公子家诗云种花于西园花发青楼道花下一禾生去之为恶草又咏田家诗云父耕原上田子斸山下荒六月禾未秀官家已修仓又云锄禾【一作田】当日午汗滴禾下土谁念盘中飡粒粒皆辛苦又
    云二月卖新丝五月粜新谷医得眼前疮剜却心头肉我愿君王心化为光明烛不照绮罗筵只照逃亡屋所谓言近意逺合三百篇之防也盛得三人见湜之公道也葆光子尝有同寮示我调举时诗卷内一句云科松为防花因讥之曰贾浪仙云空庭唯有竹闲地拟栽松吾子与贾生春兰秋菊也他日赴逹官牡丹宴栏中有两松对植立命斧斫之以其防花此侯席上于愚有得色黙不敢答亦可知也

    Explanation

    18

    During the Xiantong era, the Minister of Rites, Gao Shi, was in charge of the imperial examination and promoted three isolated and poor scholars. Among them, Gong Cheng Yi composed three hundred poems, which many people wrote on the walls of houses. Xu Tang had a poem about Dongting Lake that was especially skillful, and people called him Xu Dongting. The most remarkable among them was Nie Yizhong, from Zhongdu in Henan, who was poor when young and excelled in ancient poetry. He wrote a poem about a nobleman's house that said, "Planting flowers in the west garden, the flowers bloom along the green pavilion road. Removing them to become weeds." He also wrote a poem about a farmer's family that said, "The father tills the fields on the plain, the son clears the mountains below. In June, the grain has not yet ripened, but the government has already built granaries." Another poem said, "Working the fields at noon, sweat drips onto the soil beneath the crops. Who thinks about the effort put into each grain on the plate?" Yet another poem said, "Selling new silk in February and new grain in May, healing a surface wound by cutting out the heart. I wish the king's heart could transform into a bright candle, not illuminating the luxurious banquets but only the houses of the fleeing." These poems are close in words but far in meaning, combining the essence of the Three Hundred Poems. Promoting three people showed Gao Shi's fairness. Bao Guangzi once had a colleague show him a line from a poem collection during the examination period, saying, "Pine trees are guarded by flowers." He criticized this by saying, "Jia Langxian said, 'In an empty courtyard, there are only bamboo; in idle land, pine trees are planted.' Your son and Jia Sheng are like spring orchids and autumn chrysanthemums." One day, attending a peony banquet for a high official, there were two pine trees planted opposite each other in the garden, and they were ordered to be cut down because they guarded the flowers. This official at the banquet had a smug look, and I remained silent and did not dare to answer, which can be understood.

    19

    文宗重王起
    　　王文懿公起三任节镇歴省寺赠守太尉文宗颇重之曾为诗写于太子之笏以扬之又画仪形于便殿师友目之曰当代仲尼虽歴外镇家无余财知其甚贫诏以仙韶院乐官逐月俸钱五百贯给之起昧于理家俸入其家尽为仆妾所有耄年寒馁故加给焉于时识者以起不能陈逊而与伶人分俸利其茍得此为短也葆光子曰士人之家唯耻【一作恐】货殖至于荷畚执耒灌园鬻蔬未有禄代耕岂空器而为养安可忘甘苦不迨晨昏今之世禄嚣薄不能撙节稍丰则饫其狗彘少【一作似】歉则困彼妻孥而云安贫吾无所取唯衣与食所谓切身傥德望名品未王相国者得不思俭而足用乎

    Explanation

    19

    Emperor Wenzong of Tang highly regarded Wang Qi. Wang Qi served three terms as a frontier governor and held various government positions. He was posthumously granted the title of Taifu (Grand Commandant). The emperor highly esteemed him, once writing a poem on the tablet of the Crown Prince to praise him. He had his portrait painted in a private hall, and teachers and friends regarded him as the contemporary Confucius. Although he served in frontier regions, his family had no surplus wealth. The emperor knew he was very poor and ordered that the monthly salary of 500 guan be given to him by the musicians of the Xianshao Academy. Wang Qi was ignorant in managing his household, and all his salary went to his servants and concubines. In his old age, he suffered from cold and hunger, so additional support was provided. At that time, those who understood the situation criticized Wang Qi for not expressing humility and for sharing his salary with musicians, criticizing him for his opportunistic gain, which was a flaw.

    Bao Guangzi said that scholars' families are ashamed of accumulating wealth. Down to carrying baskets, holding plows, tending gardens, and selling vegetables, there is no salary that can replace farming. How can one live without means? How can one forget the sweetness and bitterness and neglect morning and evening care? In today's society, salaries are small and people cannot be frugal. If they have a little more, they indulge their dogs and pigs. If they are a little short, they suffer their wives and children. And they claim to be content with poverty, but I find no value in that. Only clothing and food are essential for survival. If one does not aspire to be a high-ranking official, one should still think about being frugal and sufficient.

    北梦言卷二
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷三
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　卢肇为进士状元
    　　唐相国李太尉徳裕抑退浮薄奬拔孤寒于时朝贵朋党掌武破之由是结怨而絶于附防门无宾客唯进士卢肇宜春人有竒才每谒见许脱衫从容旧例礼部放牓先禀朝廷恐有亲属言荐防昌三年王相国起知举先白掌武乃曰某不荐人然奉贺今年牓中得一状元也起未喻其防复遣亲吏于相门侦问吏曰相公于举子中独有卢肇久接从容起相曰果在此也其年卢肇为状头及第时论曰卢虽受知于掌武无妨主司之公道也

    Explanation

    20

    Translation:

    Volume II of North Dream and Tales
    　　Part of the Four Treasuries
    　　Volume III of North Dream and Tales
    　　Compiled by Sun Guangxian of the Tang dynasty

    Lu Zhao as the Top Scorer in the Imperial Examination

    During the Tang dynasty, Chancellor Li Deyu, the Duke of Weiwu, suppressed superficial and shallow individuals while rewarding and promoting those who were poor and humble. At the time, powerful officials formed cliques, and the military officials broke their power. As a result, he made enemies and was cut off from the protection of powerful officials, leaving no guests. Only the scholar Lu Zhao, from Yichun, who had extraordinary talent, was allowed to take off his robe and be at ease during each meeting. According to the old custom, the Ministry of Rites first reported to the court before announcing the results of the imperial examination. Fearing that there might be relatives who would recommend candidates in the third year of Fanchang, Chancellor Wang was in charge of the imperial examination and first reported to the military officials. He said, "I do not recommend anyone, but I congratulate you on having a top scorer in this year's results." Wang did not understand the meaning of the phrase and sent a trusted official to inquire at the chancellor's residence. The official reported, "The chancellor has only had long and relaxed interactions with Lu Zhao among the candidates." Wang replied, "Indeed, he is here." That year, Lu Zhao became the top scorer and passed the examination. At the time, people said that although Lu was known by the military officials, it did not affect the fairness of the examiners.

    戏改毕諴相名
    　　唐相毕諴呉乡人词学器度冠于侪流擢进士未遂其志尝谒一受知朝士者希为改名以期亨逹此朝士讥其鹾贾之子请改为諴字相国忻然受而谢之竟以此名登第致位台辅前之朝士慙悔交集也
    　　段相踏金莲【夏侯相附】
    　　唐段相文昌家寓江陵少以贫窭修进常患口食不给每听曾口寺斋钟动輙诣谒飡为寺僧所厌自此乃斋后扣钟冀其晩屇而不逮食也后入登台座连出大镇拜荆南节度有诗题曽口寺云曽遇阇黎饭后钟盖为此也富贵后打金莲花盆盛水濯足徐相商致书规之邹平曰人生防何要酬平生不足也　夏侯孜相国未偶伶俜风尘蹇驴无故坠井每及朝士之门舎逆旅之馆多有龃龉时人号曰不利市秀才后登将相何先塞而后通也【或云王播相公未遇题扬州佛寺诗及荆南人云是段相亦两存之】

    Explanation

    21

    Translation

    Playful Name Change for Bi Xian
    During the Tang Dynasty, Bi Xian, a man from Wu Xiang, was renowned for his literary talent and noble bearing, surpassing his peers. He was selected as a Jinshi but did not achieve his aspirations. He once visited a respected official who was knowledgeable and influential, hoping for a name change to ensure success. This official mocked him for being the son of a salt merchant and suggested changing his name to "諴." The official, delighted, accepted and thanked him for the name. Bi Xian eventually passed the imperial examination and reached the position of prime minister. The previous official felt a mix of shame and regret.

    Duan Xiang Treads on the Golden Lotus (with Xiahou Xiang appended)
    Duan Xiang, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, resided in Jingling. In his youth, he was poor and struggled to find enough food. He often heard the bell of Zengkou Temple during temple services and would visit to eat. The temple monks grew tired of this and began ringing the bell after the service, hoping he would arrive too late to get food. Later, he rose to a high position, serving as the military governor of Jingnan. He wrote a poem titled "Zengkou Temple," which mentioned encountering a monk who rang the bell after the meal, alluding to his past experiences. After achieving wealth and status, he used a golden lotus-shaped basin to wash his feet. Xu Xiangshang wrote a letter advising him, saying, "Why should one block first and then open? What is the point of life if it does not fulfill one's aspirations?"

    Xiahou Zhi, another high-ranking official, was once a wandering scholar, traveling on a slow donkey that fell into a well. He often visited the homes of officials and stayed in inns, but frequently encountered disputes. People called him "Unlucky Scholar." Later, he rose to the rank of general and prime minister. Some say that Wang Bo, another high-ranking official, was similarly unlucky and wrote a poem about a temple in Yangzhou, which was also attributed to Duan Xiang. Both accounts are preserved.

    22

    李固言相国为栁表所误
    　　唐李固言生于凤翔庄墅雅【一作惟】性长厚未习防谒始应进士举舎于亲表栁氏京第诸栁昆仲率多戏谑以相国不谙人事俾习趋揖之仪俟其磬折密于乌巾上帖文字云此处有屋僦赁相国不及出朝士见而笑之许孟容守常侍朝中鄙此官号曰貂郤固不能为人延誉也相国始以所业求知谋于诸栁诸栁与导行卷去处先令投谒许常侍相国果诣骑省髙阳公慙谢曰某官绪极闲冷不足发君子声采虽然已藏之于心又覩乌巾上文字知其朴质无何来年许公知礼闱李相国居状头及第是知栁氏之戏侮足致陇西之速遇也

    Explanation

    22

    Chancellor Li Guan was misled by Liu Biao.

    During the Tang Dynasty, Li Guan, the chancellor, was born in a village near Fengxiang. He was of noble character and had not yet learned the customs of the court when he first took the imperial examinations. He stayed at the residence of his in-laws, the Liu family, in the capital. The various members of the Liu family, who were his in-laws, often teased him because he was unfamiliar with human affairs. They instructed him to learn the proper etiquette of bowing and kneeling, and waited until he bowed deeply. They secretly wrote words on his black headband, saying, "There is a house to rent here." The chancellor did not understand and left. The court officials saw and laughed at him.

    Xu Mengrong, who held the position of Attendant in Ordinary, looked down on this official title and called it a lowly official. He could not enhance Li Guan's reputation for others. The chancellor began to seek advice on his studies from the various members of the Liu family. The various members of the Liu family guided him to the right places for his studies and first instructed him to pay respects. Xu Mengrong, the chancellor, indeed went to the office of the Marquis of Gaoyang, who apologized with shame, saying, "My official position is extremely idle and cold, not worthy of enhancing a gentleman's reputation." Although it was already in his heart, and he saw the words on his black headband, knowing that he was simple and honest. Soon after, in the following year, Xu Mengrong knew the examination hall, and Li Guan, the chancellor, was the top scorer and passed the examination. Thus, it is known that the Liu family's teasing and mockery led to Li Guan's quick success.

    23

    杜邠公不恤亲戚
    　　杜邠公悰位极人臣富贵无比尝与同列言平生不称意有三其一为澧州刺史其二贬司农卿其三自西川移镇广陵舟次瞿塘左右为骇浪所惊呼唤不暇渴甚自泼汤茶吃也镇荆州日诸院姊妹多在渚宫寄寓贫困尤甚相国未尝拯济至于节腊一无沾遗有乗肩舆至衙门诟骂者亦不省问之凡莅方镇不理狱讼在鳯翔洎西川系囚毕政无轻无重任其殍殕人有从劒门拾得裹漆器文书乃成都具狱案牍畧不垂愍斯又何心哉【未尝荐贤时号秃角犀】

    Explanation

    23

    Du Bin Gong, reaching the highest rank among ministers and enjoying unparalleled wealth, once spoke with his colleagues about three things in life that did not go as he expected. The first was his appointment as Prefect of Lizhou, the second was his demotion to the position of Grand Minister of Agriculture, and the third was when he moved from the Western Circuit to Guangling, and his ship was anchored at Qutang Gorge, where he was surrounded by terrifying waves, too busy to call out, and extremely thirsty, he drank watered-down tea himself.

    When he was stationed in Jingzhou, many of his relatives and sisters-in-law stayed temporarily in the palace in Jingzhou, where they were extremely poor. The Duke never helped them and did not give them any gifts or favors during festivals and holidays. A person riding in a sedan chair arrived at the government office and scolded, but he did not inquire or investigate.

    Whenever he governed a military district, he did not deal with lawsuits. In Fengxiang and later in the Western Circuit, all prisoners were released or dealt with, whether they were punished lightly or severely, it was left to them to decide. Someone picked up a document wrapped in lacquerware at the Sword Gate, which was a complete record of court cases in Chengdu. He was completely indifferent or unmoved. What kind of heart does he have?

    [Note: "秃角犀" is a metaphorical term, possibly referring to a rhinoceros with no horns, symbolizing someone who is lacking in certain qualities. The exact meaning is uncertain, but it is retained in the translation with a brief note indicating the uncertainty.]

    24

    李光顔太师选佳壻
    　　李太师光顔以大勲康国品位穹崇爱女未聘幕僚谓其必选佳壻因从容语次盛誉一郑秀才词学门阀人韵风流异常冀太师以子妻之他日又言之太师谢幕僚曰李光顔一健儿也遭遇多【一作君】难偶立微功岂可妄求名族乎某已选得一佳壻诸贤未见乃召客司小将指之曰此即某女之匹也超三五阶军职厚与金帛而已从事许当曰李太师建定难之勲懐弓藏之虑武宁保境止务圗存而欲结援名家非其志也与夫侯景求婚王谢何其逺哉【王特尚书与太师宅重叠姻戚常语之】

    Explanation

    24

    Li Guangyan, the Grand Tutor, Selected a Suitable Son-in-Law

    Grand Tutor Li Guangyan, having achieved great feats that contributed to the stability and prosperity of the country, held a high rank and prestige. His daughter was still unmarried, and his advisors believed he would certainly select an excellent son-in-law. In casual conversation, they highly praised a scholar named Zheng, who was of noble family background, known for his elegance and charm, and hoped that the Grand Tutor would marry his daughter to him. On another occasion, they spoke of this again. The Grand Tutor thanked his advisors and said, "Li Guangyan is merely a soldier who has experienced many difficulties and achieved minor accomplishments. How could I unreasonably seek a prestigious family?" He had already selected an excellent son-in-law, whom none of the distinguished scholars had seen. He summoned a low-ranking officer from the guesthouse and pointed to him, saying, "This is the match for my daughter. He will be promoted to a higher military rank and given a generous amount of gold and silk." Xu Dang, an official, commented, "Grand Tutor Li has established a great achievement in stabilizing the country. He harbors concerns about being forgotten or betrayed after his success. Focusing solely on maintaining peace and security within the borders, he does not seek alliances with prestigious families. This is not his intention. How far removed this is from the case of Hou Jing, who sought to marry into the Wang and Xie families." [Note: The Wang and Xie families were close relatives of the Grand Tutor's family, and he often mentioned this.]

    王文公叉手睡【司空圗附】
    　　王文公凝清修重徳冠絶当时每就寝息必叉手而卧虑梦寐中见先灵也食防饦面不过十八片曾典绛州于时司空圗侍郎方应进士举自别墅到郡谒见后更不访亲知阍吏遽申司空秀才出郭矣或入郭访亲知即不造郡斋琅琊知之谓其专敬愈重之及知举日司空一防列第四人登科同年讶其名姓甚暗所圗太速有鄙薄者号为司徒空琅琊知有此说因召一牓人开筵宣言于众曰某叨忝文柄今年牓帖全为司空先辈一人而已由是声采益振尔后为御史分司旧相卢公携访之乃留诗曰氏族司空贵官班御史雄老夫如且在未可叹途穷其为名徳所重也如此
    　　河中饯刘相瞻
    　　唐相国刘公瞻其先人讳景本连州人少为汉南郑司徒掌牋劄因题商山驿侧泉石荥阳竒之勉以进修俾前驿换麻衣执贽之后致解荐擢进士第歴台省瞻相孤贫有艺虽登科第不预急流任大理评事日饘粥不给尝于安国寺相识僧处谒飡留所业文数轴置在僧几致仕刘军容游寺见此文卷甚竒之怜其贫窭厚有济恤又

    Explanation

    25

    Translation

    Wang Wen Gong Sleeping with Crossed Hands [Appendix: Sikong Tu]

    Wang Wen Gong Ning, a man of great moral integrity and ascetic practice, stood out among his contemporaries. He would always sleep with his hands crossed, fearing that he might encounter the spirits of his ancestors in his dreams. He ate no more than eighteen pieces of steamed bread, showing his frugality. Once, he served as the governor of Jiaozhou, and at that time, Sikong Tu, a serving scholar-official, was preparing for the imperial examination. Sikong Tu traveled from his villa to the prefecture to pay respects to Wang Wen Gong Ning. Afterward, he did not visit any relatives or acquaintances. The gatekeeper quickly informed Sikong Tu that he had left the city. If Sikong Tu entered the city to visit relatives or acquaintances, he would not enter the prefectural office. Wang Wen Gong Ning learned of this and praised Sikong Tu for his dedication and respect, which he found even more admirable. When it came time for the examination, Sikong Tu ranked fourth among those who passed. His contemporaries were surprised by his obscure name and rapid success, and some even mocked him, calling him "Sikong Kong." Wang Wen Gong Ning, aware of this, called together the top scholars and declared before them, "I have the honor of overseeing the examination this year, and the entire list is dedicated to Sikong Tu, a single individual." Thus, Sikong Tu's reputation grew even stronger. Later, he became a censor and served under the former prime minister Lu Xie, who visited him and left a poem: "The Sikong family is noble, and the office of censor is powerful. Old man, I am still here, but it is not yet time to lament the end of the road. His name and virtue are indeed highly esteemed."

    Farewell Feast for Duke Liu Zhan in Hezhong

    Duke Liu Zhan, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, had an ancestor named Liu Jing, who was from Lianzhou. In his youth, Liu Jing served as an official under a high-ranking official in Hennan, responsible for drafting documents. He inscribed his name on the stone and water features beside the Shangshan Post Station. The people of Xingyang found this remarkable and encouraged him to continue his studies, leading him to change into a simple robe and present himself as a humble scholar. Later, he was recommended and passed the imperial examination, serving in various high-ranking positions. Duke Liu Zhan, though poor and isolated, was talented. Although he passed the examination, he did not engage in the political intrigues of the time. As a judicial official, he often lacked even basic food. Once, he visited a temple where he met a monk and was invited to a meal. He left several scrolls of his writings with the monk. After retiring, a high-ranking official named Liu Junrong visited the temple and saw these writings, finding them remarkable and moved by Liu Zhan's poverty. He provided him with substantial assistance and support.

    26

    知其连州【一作山】人朝无强援谓僧曰某虽闲废能为此人致宰相尔后授河中少尹幕寮有贵族浮薄者蔑视之一旦有命征入蒲尹张筵而祖之浮薄幕客呼相国为尹公曰归朝作何官职相国对曰得路即作宰相此郎大笑之在席亦有异其言者自是以水部贠外知制诰相次入翰林以至大拜也【王屋匡一上人细话之】
    　　李氏瑞槐【赵令公櫺枣附】
    　　唐相国李公福河中永乐有宅庭槐一本抽三枝直过当舎屋一枝不及相国同堂昆弟三人曰石曰程皆登宰执唯福一人歴镇使相而已近者石晋朝赵令公莹家庭有檽树婆娑异常四逺俱见有望气者诣其邻里问人云此家合有登宰辅者里叟曰无之然赵令先徳小字相之儿得非此应乎术士曰王气方盛不在身当其子孙尔后中令由太原判官大拜出将入相则前言果效矣【一作也】凡士之宦逹非止一途或以才升或由命遇则盛衰之气亦随人而效之向者槐枣异常岂非王气先集耶不然何荣茂挺特拔耸之如是也【陇西事得于李载仁大夫天水事得于长阳宰康张甚详悉也】

    Explanation

    26

    Translation

    Knowing that the person from Lianzhou (or a mountain) had no powerful supporters in court, he told the monk that although he was idle, he could still make this person a chancellor. Later, when appointed as the Deputy Governor of Hedong, some arrogant and superficial nobles in his entourage despised him. One day, he was summoned to the capital, and the Deputy Governor of Pu held a farewell banquet for him. The superficial and arrogant entourage members called the chancellor 'Governor' and asked, 'What position will you hold upon returning to court?' The chancellor replied, 'As soon as I get a chance, I will become chancellor.' This man laughed at him, and there were also some who found his words unusual. From then on, he successively rose from Water Department Censor to Chief of Drafting Imperial Edicts, then into the Hanlin Academy, and finally received a high-ranking appointment. [As told by Master Wang Wukang.]

    The Lucky槐Tree of the Li Family [with an additional story about the枣Tree of Zhao Linggong]

    Duke Li Fu of the Tang Dynasty, who lived in Yongle, Hedong, had a courtyard with a槐tree that grew three branches, two of which reached over the house, but one did not. The chancellor had three brothers named Shi and Cheng, who all reached high positions, while Fu only held the position of military governor. Recently, during the Shizhou era, Zhao Linggong Ying had a枣tree in his family courtyard that was unusually graceful and visible from afar. A fortune-teller visited the neighborhood and asked people if this family would produce a chancellor. The elderly man said there was no such thing, but the fortune-teller suggested that Zhao Linggong's son, who was nicknamed 'Chancellor,' might fulfill this prophecy. The fortune-teller said that the auspicious signs were strong and would manifest in his descendants. Later, Zhao Linggong rose from a judge in Taiyuan to become a high-ranking official and a chancellor, proving the fortune-teller's prediction correct. [This version is also correct.]

    Scholars who achieve success do so through various paths, either through talent or fate. The rise and fall of fortunes also follow people, and the unusual growth of the槐and枣trees must be a sign of auspiciousness. Otherwise, why would they grow so luxuriantly and uniquely? [The story of the Li family was obtained from Grand Tutor Li Zairen, and the story of Zhao Linggong was obtained from the magistrate of Changyang, Kang Zhang, who provided detailed accounts.]

    髙太尉决礼佛僧
    　　唐渤海王太尉髙公骈镇蜀日因巡邉至资中郡舎于刺史衙对郡山顶有开元佛寺是夜黄昏僧礼赞螺呗间作渤海命军悉擒械之来晨笞背斥逐召将吏而谓之曰僧徒礼念亦无罪过但以此寺十年后当有秃丁数千作乱我以是厌之其后土人皆髠髪执兵号大髠小髠据此寺为寨陵胁州将果叶渤海之言【得于资中处士王迢】
    　　王中令铎拒黄巢

    Final Translation

    Gao Taiwei Decides the Fate of Buddhist Monks

    During the Tang Dynasty, Gao Pian, the Taiwei and Prince of Bohai, was stationed in Shu. While on a border inspection tour, he arrived at Zizhong Prefecture and stayed at the Prefectural Office. Across the mountain top from the prefectural office stood the Kaiyuan Buddhist Temple. One evening, as the sun set, the monks inside the temple were engaged in their ritual chants. Gao Pian, feeling repulsed by the sight, ordered his soldiers to capture and chain the monks. The next morning, he whipped them on the back and expelled them. He then summoned the generals and officials and told them, "These monks, though they have no fault in their devotion, will cause chaos in ten years. There will be thousands of tonsured men who will rebel, and I am repulsed by this." Indeed, later, the local people, all tonsured and armed, were called "Big Tonsured" and "Small Tonsured," and they used the temple as a base to threaten the prefectural officials, fulfilling Gao Pian's prophecy. [This account was obtained from Wang Tiao, a recluse from Zizhong.]

    Wang Zhongling Dodo Resists Huang Chao

    During the Tang Dynasty, Wang Zhongling, the Zhongling Military Governor, was highly respected and famous for his virtue. He held a prominent position and was known for his elegant demeanor, but he lacked the talent to quell rebellions. He was stationed at the Palace of Zhubing as the overall commander to defend against Huang Chao's rebel forces, which were gradually advancing southward. Before going to his post, he brought his concubines with him. His wife had not yet left the capital, and he was naturally jealous. Suddenly, he received news that his wife was leaving the capital and was on her way. He said to his attendants, "Huang Chao is gradually advancing southward, and my wife is coming from the north. How can I find peace in such a situation?" One of his attendants jokingly replied, "Why not surrender to Huang Chao?" Wang Zhongling laughed heartily at this. Later, when Jingzhou fell, he took control of Tongguan. Huang Chao sent someone to convey a message to him, saying, "Your Excellency, a scholar, is not my match. Please withdraw yourself."

    28

    避无汚锋刃于是弃闗随僖皇播迁于蜀再授都统复京都大勲不成竟罹非命时议曰黄巢过江髙太尉不能拒捍岂王中令儒懦所能应变乎落都统后有诗其要云勅【一作黜】诏已闻来阙下檄书犹未遍军前亦志在其中也【黄巢起广州自号义军百万都统上表先陈犯阙之意其词云傥便归降必有陞奬朝廷耻笑】
    　　路侍中巾裹
    　　唐路侍中岩风貎之美为世所闻镇成都日委执政于孔目吏邉咸日以妓乐自随宴于江津都人士女懐掷果之羡虽卫玠潘岳不足为比善巾裹蜀人见必效之后乃翦纱巾之脚以异于众也闾巷有袨服修容者人必讥之曰尔非路侍中耶尝过鬻豚之肆见侩豕者谓屠者【一作生】曰此豚端正路侍中不如用之比方良可笑也以官妓行云等十人侍宴移镇渚宫日于合江亭离筵赠行云等感恩多词有离魂何处断烟雨江南岸至今播于倡楼也
    　　李勲尚书发愤【赵文附】

    Explanation

    28

    To avoid defiling the sharp blade, he abandoned his post and followed Emperor Xian's retreat to Shu, where he was once again appointed as Grand Marshal. However, his great achievement was not accomplished, and he ultimately suffered an untimely fate. Contemporary opinion said: "When Huang Chao crossed the Yangtze River, General Gao could not resist or defend. Could Wang Zhongling, being a scholar, cope with the situation?" After being demoted from the position of Grand Marshal, there was a poem, and its main content was: "The imperial decree [or demotion] has been heard coming from the capital, but the military edict has not yet reached all the troops. He also had aspirations within it." [Huang Chao rose in Guangzhou and called himself the Grand Marshal of the Hundred Million Righteous Army, submitting a memorial first stating his intention to attack the capital, promising that if one were to surrender easily, there would certainly be promotion and reward, which was quite laughable for the court.]

    Lu Shizong's Headwear

    During the Tang Dynasty, Lu Shizong, known for his handsome appearance, was widely recognized. When he governed Chengdu, he entrusted administration to the official Bì Xián and accompanied himself with musicians and courtesans. He held banquets by the riverside, and the people and women of the city admired him as if they wanted to throw fruits at him, even though Wei Jie and Pan Yue could not compare to him. He was skilled in headwear, and the people of Shu followed his example; later, he cut the ends of his silk cap to distinguish himself from others. In the alleys, anyone who dressed up and combed their hair would be ridiculed, saying, "Are you not Lu Shizong?" Once, when passing a pork shop, he saw a pig dealer tell the butcher [or live pig] that this pig was well-formed and not inferior to Lu Shizong, which was quite laughable. He had ten official courtesans named Xingyun serving him at banquets. When he moved to Zhubiao Palace, he held farewell banquets at Hejiang Pavilion and gave gifts to Xingyun and others, who expressed gratitude with many poems, one of which said, "Where can the wandering soul be severed? At the misty banks of the Yangtze River in Jiangnan," which has since become popular in the entertainment circles.

    Li Xun, the Minister of Works, was filled with anger [with Zhao Wen's text attached].

    薛能尚书镇郓州见举进士者必加异礼李勲尚书先徳为衙前将校八座方为客司小子弟亦负文藻潜慕进脩因舎归田里未逾嵗服麻衣执所业于元戎左右具白其行止不请引见元戎曰此子慕善才与不才安可拒之某今自见其人质清秀复览其文卷深器重之乃出邮巡职牒一通与八座先徳俾罢职司闲居恐妨令子脩进尔后果防名第歴清显出为郓州节度也【八座事得王屋山僧匡一甚详近代进士赵观文及桂州小军杜状元及第乃才举也】
    　　郑愚尚书锦半臂
    　　唐郑愚尚书广州人雄才奥学擢进士第歴清显声称烜【一作赫】然而性本好华以锦为半臂崔魏公镇荆南荥阳除广南节制经过魏公以常礼延遇荥阳举进士时未尝以文章及魏公门此日于客次换麻衣先贽所业魏公览其卷首寻已赏叹至三四不曰真销得锦半臂也又以魏公故相合具军仪廷防不得已而授【一作使】之魏公曰文武之道备见之矣其钦服形于辞色也或曰荥阳因醉眠左右见一白猪盖杜征南蛇吐之

    Explanation

    29

    During his tenure as governor of Yuzhou, Xue Neng treated those who took the imperial examinations with special respect. Li Xun, a respected official, had an elder brother who served as a military officer at the government office. The younger brother, a talented but humble individual, aspired to improve himself through study and eventually retired to the countryside. Within a year, he wore mourning clothes and presented his work to the general, explaining his actions. The general praised him for his clear and handsome appearance and admired his writings, holding him in high regard. He then gave him a postal patrol certificate, allowing him to be relieved of his duties and live in seclusion, fearing it might hinder his son's advancement. Eventually, the younger brother achieved success in the imperial examinations, held high-ranking positions, and was appointed as the governor of Yuzhou.

    Zheng Yu, a high-ranking official, was known for his fondness for luxury and wore a half-sleeved brocade garment. During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong, Zheng Yu, a native of Guangzhou, was a man of great talent and scholarship. He was promoted to the rank of Jinshi and held high-ranking positions, earning a famous and illustrious reputation. However, by nature, he was fond of luxury and wore a half-sleeved garment made of brocade. Cui Wei, a high-ranking official, was stationed in Jingnan, and Xingyang was appointed as the governor of Guangnan. During his visit, Cui Wei treated Xingyang with normal courtesy, as he had never presented his writings to Hui Gong. On this occasion, Xingyang wore mourning clothes and presented his work in the guest quarters. Hui Gong read the beginning of his manuscript and praised him repeatedly without tiring, saying, "Truly, he is worthy of a half-sleeved brocade garment." Since Hui Gong was a former chancellor, he held a military ceremony in the palace and reluctantly granted him the position. Hui Gong said, "The way of both literature and martial arts is fully demonstrated," and expressed his admiration through words and expressions. Some say that Xingyang, while sleeping after drinking, saw a white pig, which is a legend about a snake spitting out a white pig, a metaphor for a good omen.

    韦宙相足翁
    　　唐相国韦公宙善治生江陵府东有别业良田美产最号膏腴而积稻如坻皆为滞穂大中初除广州节度使宣宗以番禺珠翠之地垂贪泉之戒京兆从容奏对曰江陵庄积谷尚有七十堆固无所贪宣皇曰此可谓之足谷翁也
    　　李当尚书竹笼【崔珏二子附】
    　　唐李当尚书镇南梁日境内多有朝士庄产子孙侨寓其间而不肖者相效为非前政以其各有阶縁弗克禁止闾巷苦之八座严明有断处分寛织篾笼召其尤者诘其家世谱第在朝姻亲乃曰郎君籍如是地望作如此行止无乃辱于存亡乎今日所惩贤亲眷闻之必赏老夫【一作安】勉旃遽命盛以竹笼沈于汉江由是其侪惕息各务戢敛也　崔珏侍御家寄荆州二子凶恶节度使刘都尉判之曰崔氏二男荆南三害不免行刑也

    Explanation

    30

    Wei Zong, the Man of Abundant Grain
    　　During the Tang Dynasty, Wei Zong, a high-ranking official, was skilled in managing wealth. He owned a large estate in the east of Jiangling Prefecture, with fertile land and valuable properties. The land was so rich that it was known as the most fertile in the region, and the rice piled up like small hills, all of which were surplus grain. In the early Dazhong era, he was appointed as the Governor of Guangzhou. Emperor Xuanzong warned him about the dangers of greed, mentioning the "greedy spring" (贪泉) in Fanyu. The Chancellor responded calmly, saying, "The estates in Jiangling still have seventy piles of grain, so there is no need for me to be greedy." The emperor replied, "This can be called a man of abundant grain."

    　　Li Dang, the Man in the Bamboo Cage [with Cui Jue's Two Sons Attached]
    　　During the Tang Dynasty, Li Dang, a high-ranking official, governed the region of Nanliang. There were many officials' estates within his jurisdiction, and their descendants lived as guests there. Some of these descendants were immoral and imitated each other in wrongdoing. Previous officials could not stop them because they had various excuses. Li Dang, known for his strictness and decisiveness, issued a lenient order to weave bamboo cages and summoned the worst offenders. He questioned their family backgrounds and connections in court, saying, "Your family lineage is so prestigious, yet your behavior is so disgraceful. Are you not bringing shame to your ancestors? Today, what I am punishing will surely be praised by your noble relatives. [Or, 'will surely be approved by your noble relatives.'] Be encouraged. I immediately ordered them to be placed in the bamboo cages and thrown into the Han River. From then on, the others were on guard and each tried to control themselves. Cui Jue, a high-ranking official, had two sons who were very wicked. The military officer Liu, holding the rank of duiwei, judged them, saying, "Cui's two sons are the three great evils of Jingnan and cannot escape punishment."

    呉行鲁温溲器【厉圗南附】
    　　唐呉行鲁尚书彭州人少年事内官西门军容小心畏慎每夜温溲溺器以奉之深得中尉之意或一日为洗足中尉以脚下文理示之曰如此文理争教不作十军容使行鲁拜曰此亦无凭某亦有之执厮仆之役乃脱屦呈之中尉嗟叹谓曰汝但忠孝我终为汝成之尔后假以军职除彭州刺史为卢耽相公西川行军司马御蛮有功歴东西川山南三镇节旄除西川制云为命代之英雄作人中之祥瑞讥之也　厉圗南为西川副使随府罢职行鲁欲延辟之圗南素薄行鲁闻之大笑曰不能翦头刺面而趋侍健儿乎自使院乗马不归私第直出北郭家人遽结束而追之张云起居为成都少尹常出轻言为行鲁酖杀之

    Explanation

    Wu Xinglu, Warming the Urinal [Lì Tú Nán Attached]

    During the Tang Dynasty, Wu Xinglu, a Shangshu (Minister) from Pengzhou, was a young man who served the eunuch Xi Men with caution and respect. Every night, he would warm the urinal and serve it to him, deeply pleasing the eunuch's intention. One day, when the eunuch was washing his feet, he showed Wu Xinglu the pattern on his feet and said, "With such a pattern, how could one not become a Ten Army Commander?" Wu Xinglu bowed and said, "This is not proof enough; I also have it." He performed the duties of a servant, removing his shoes and presenting them. The eunuch sighed and said, "You are just loyal and filial; I will eventually help you achieve this." Later, he was given a military position, appointed as the Governor of Pengzhou, and served as the Xunjun Sima (Military Governor) of Western Shu under Lu Dān, the Xianggong (Governor). He was successful in subduing the barbarians and served in the Western Shu, Eastern Shu, and three regions in the south. He was promoted to the position of Shangshu, and the imperial edict said, "He is the hero of the age, a harbinger of good fortune for the people." This was a criticism of him. Lì Tú Nán, as the Deputy Governor of Western Shu, was dismissed from office along with the governor. Wu Xinglu wanted to recruit him, but Lì Tú Nán had always despised Wu Xinglu. When he heard about this, he laughed and said, "I cannot shave my head and tattoo my face to serve as a bodyguard." He rode out of the government office directly to the northern suburb without returning to his private residence. His family hurriedly dressed him and chased after him. Zhang Yun, the resident magistrate of Chengdu, often spoke carelessly and was poisoned and killed by Wu Xinglu.

    崔侍中省刑狱
    　　唐崔侍中安潜崇奉释氏鲜茹荤血唯于刑辟常自躬亲虽僧人犯罪未尝屈法于防事前虑囚必温顔恤恻以尽其情有大辟者俾先示以判语赐以酒食而付于法镇西川三年唯多蔬食宴诸司以面及蒟蒻之染作顔色用象豚肩羊臑脍炙之属皆逼真也时人比于梁武而频于宅使堂前弄傀儡子军人百姓穿宅观看一无禁止而中壸预政以玷盛徳惜哉
    　　刘蜕舎人不祭先祖
    　　唐刘舎人蜕桐庐人早以文学应进士举其先徳戒之曰任汝进取穷之与逹不望于汝吾没后慎勿祭祀乃乗扁舟以渔钓自娯竟不知其所适【不审是隐者为复是渔师莫晓其端倪也】紫微歴登华贯出典商于霜露之思于是乎止临终亦戒其子如先考之命蜀礼部尚书纂即其息也尝与同列言之君子曰名教之家【一作中】重于丧祭刘氏先徳是何人斯茍同隐逸之流何伤菽水之礼紫微以儒而进爵比通侯遵乃父之绪言紊先王之旧制以时【一作报本】之敬能便废乎大彭通人抑有其说时未喻也

    Explanation
