    Final Translation

    Feng Shizhong Examines the Prison Records

    During the Tang Dynasty, Feng Shizhong, the Chancellor, revered Buddhism and rarely ate meat and blood. He personally handled the records of executions, never bending the law even for monks who committed crimes. Before the execution, he would consider the prisoners with a warm face and compassionate heart, fully understanding their situations. For those sentenced to death, he would first show them the judgment, give them wine and food, and then hand them over to the law. He governed Western Sichuan for three years, eating mostly vegetables. He feasted the officials with dumplings and other dishes made from taro, dyed to make colors, and used to imitate pork shoulder, lamb, and other delicacies, all very realistic. People compared him to Emperor Wu of Liang, but he frequently had puppet shows in his residence, allowing soldiers and civilians to watch without any restrictions. However, his involvement in palace politics tarnished his noble virtues, alas.

    Liu Tui, the Secretary, Did Not Worship His Ancestors

    Liu Tui, a Secretary from Tonglu, early in life entered the imperial examination through literature. His father advised him, saying, "Let you pursue your advancement, whether poor or rich. I do not expect anything from you. After I die, do not worship me." Then he took a small boat to fish and enjoy himself, finally unknown where he went. Purple Micro, as a high-ranking official, served in Shangyu, and his grief over the loss of parents was profound. On his deathbed, he also warned his son as his father had. Shu's Minister of Rites, Zuan, was his son. Once he spoke with his colleagues about it. Gentlemen say, "Families bound by the norms of propriety value funerals and ancestral worship." What kind of person was Liu's father? If he were a recluse, what harm would it do to the simple rites of filial piety? Purple Micro, as a Confucian scholar, advanced to a high rank, following his father's advice, but disrupted the old customs of the ancients. Could the respect due to ancestors be easily abandoned? Perhaps there is a reason, but people did not understand.

    33

    杜审权相斥冯防
    　　大中四年进士冯防登第牓中文誉最髙是嵗暹罗国起楼厚赍金帛奏请撰记时人荣之初官京兆府防军恩地即杜相审权也杜有江西之拜制书未行先召长乐公密话垂延辟之命欲以南昌牋奏任之戒令勿泄长乐公拜谢辞出宅速鞭而归于通衢遇友人郑賨见其喜形于色驻马恳诘长乐遽以恩地之辟吿之荥阳寻捧刺诣京兆门谒贺具言得于冯先辈也京兆嗟愤而鄙其浅露洎制下开幕冯不预焉心绪忧疑莫知所以亷车发日自防桥乗肩舆门生咸在长乐拜别京兆公长揖冯曰勉旃由是嚣浮之誉徧于搢绅竟不通显中间有涉交通中贵愈招清议官止祠部郎中眉州刺史仕蜀至御史大夫

    Explanation

    33

    During the fourth year of the Dazhong era, Feng Fang, a successful candidate in the imperial examinations, was the most renowned among his peers. That year, the Kingdom of Siam built a tower and presented valuable silk and cloth, requesting a record to be written, which brought him great honor. Initially, he served as a military officer in the capital region, where his benefactor was Du Shentuan, a prominent official. Du had been appointed to govern Jiangxi, and before the imperial decree was issued, he summoned Longle Gong privately to discuss the matter. Du promised him an appointment to serve in Nanchang and instructed him not to reveal the news. Longle Gong bowed and thanked Du before leaving hastily. On his way home, he met his friend Zheng Cong on a main road, who noticed his joyful expression and stopped to inquire. Longle Gong immediately revealed the promise of appointment from Du. Zheng Cong then went to the capital region to congratulate Du, stating that he had learned the news from Feng Fang. Du was deeply disappointed and disapproved of Feng Fang's lack of discretion. When the imperial decree was issued, Feng Fang was not included in the list of appointees, leaving him in a state of anxiety and doubt, unsure of what to do. On the day the decree was announced, Longle Gong traveled from Fang Bridge in a sedan chair, accompanied by his students. Longle Gong bowed to Du and said, "Be diligent." From then on, Feng Fang's reputation for being arrogant and superficial spread among the literati, and he never achieved prominence. Later, he became involved in dealings with influential eunuchs, which attracted more criticism. He held positions such as Minister of Rites, Governor of Meizhou, and eventually became a Grand Censor in Shu.

    34

    不肖子三变
    　　唐咸通中荆州有书生号唐五经者学识精博实曰鸿儒防趣甚髙人所师仰聚徒五百辈以束修自给优游卒嵗有西河济南之风幕寮多与之游常谓人曰不肖子弟有三变第一变为蝗虫谓鬻庄而食也第二变为蠧鱼谓鬻书而食也第三变为大虫谓卖奴婢而食也三食之辈何代无之
    　　薛保逊轻薄
    　　薛保逊名家子恃才与地凡所评品士子以之升降时号为浮薄相国夏侯孜【一作公】尤恶之其堂弟因名保厚以异之由是不睦内子卢氏与其良人操尚畧同因季父薛监来省卢新妇出防俟其去后命水涤门阈薛监知而大怒经宰相疏之保逊因谪授澧州司马凡七年不代夏侯孜【一作公】出镇魏相謩登庸方有征拜而殒于郡愚曽睹薛文数

    Explanation

    34

    The Three Transformations of Unworthy Sons
    In the Xiantong era of the Tang dynasty, in Jingzhou, there was a scholar named Tang Wujing, who was highly learned and well-versed in the Five Classics. He was truly a great scholar, and his interests were very high, earning him respect from others. He gathered five hundred disciples, supporting himself through teaching, and lived a leisurely life, enjoying the cultural atmosphere of Xihé and Jǐnán. Many of his associates were close friends, and he often said to others: "Unworthy sons undergo three transformations: the first is into locusts, meaning they sell their estates to eat; the second is into bookworms, meaning they sell their books to eat; the third is into tigers, meaning they sell their slaves and maidservants to eat. In every generation, there are those who fall into these three categories."

    Xue Baosun's Superficiality
    Xue Baosun was a son of a distinguished family, relying on his talent and family background. All evaluations of scholars were based on his opinions, and he was known for being superficial and shallow. Chancellor Xiahou Zi, particularly disliked him, and his younger brother was named Baohou to distinguish him. Because of this, they were not on good terms. His wife, Lu氏, shared similar character and values with him. When her uncle Xuejian came to visit, Lu氏 took precautions and waited until he left before ordering water to clean the threshold. Xuejian found out about this and became very angry. The chancellor criticized him, and as a result, Baosun was demoted to the position of司马 in Lǐzhou, where he remained for seven years without being replaced. When Xiahou Zi was appointed to govern Wei, the chancellor Mò was promoted, but Baosun died in the prefecture. I have seen some of Xue's writings.

    35

    幅其一云饯交亲于灞上止逆旅氏见数物象人诘之口輙动皆云江淮岭表州县官也呜呼天之生民为此辈笞挞又观优云绯胡折窣【一作推宰】莽转而出众人皆笑唯保逊不防其轻物皆此也卢防灌罢防州以其为姊妹夫径至澧州慰省回至邮亭回望而笑曰岂意薛保逊一旦接军事李判官打杨栁枝乎【澧州老军将周蔼旧曾服事备言之】
    　　陈防螳蜋赋
    　　蜀之士子莫不酤酒慕相如涤器之风也陈防郎中家以当垆为业为不埽街官吏殴之其母甚贤勉以进脩不许归乡以成名为期每嵗糇粮纸笔衣服仆马皆自成都赍致郎中业八韵唯螳蜋赋大行太和元年及第李相固言览报状处分厢界下酒斾阖其户家人犹拒之逡巡贺登第乃圣善奬训之力也后为白中令子壻西川副使连典彭汉两郡而终

    Explanation

    35

    One of the pieces says: "To see off friends at Bashi, I stayed at an inn and saw several objects resembling people. When I questioned them, their mouths moved, and they all said they were officials from the states and counties of Jianghuai and Lingnan. Alas, Heaven has created people to be beaten by these kinds. I also saw actors wearing red and black costumes performing a dance, and everyone laughed except for Baosun, who did not take it lightly; all these things are like this." Lu Fang, after finishing his term in Fangzhou, went directly to Lizhou to visit his sister-in-law and returned to a post office, looking back and laughing, saying, "Who would have thought that Xue Baosun would suddenly meet Military Judge Li and play with willow branches?" (As told by the old military officer Zhou Ai from Lizhou who once served there.)

    Chen Fang's Essay on the Mantis
    No scholar in Shu does not sell wine, admiring the example of Xiangru who sold pots. Chen Fang, the imperial physician, whose family sold wine, was beaten by officials who did not sweep the street. His mother was very virtuous and encouraged him to study, but he did not allow her to stop him from returning home to achieve fame. Every year, food, paper, pens, clothes, horses, and servants were sent from Chengdu. Chen Fang's eight-verse essay on the mantis became widely known, and he passed the imperial examination in the first year of Taihe. Prime Minister Li, upon seeing the announcement, ordered the removal of the wine sign and closed the door, but his family still refused, and eventually congratulated him on passing the examination, attributing it to his mother's encouragement. Later, he became the son-in-law of Bai Zhongling, served as a deputy governor of Xishu, and successively governed Peng and Han prefectures until his death.

    36

    刘仆射茘枝圗
    　　唐刘仆射崇以清俭自居甚招物论尝召同列餐苦荬【一作马】饆饠朝士有知其矫乃潜问小苍头曰仆射晨餐何物苍头曰泼生吃了也朝士闻而哂之又镇番禺效呉隐之为人京国亲知贫乏者颙俟濡救但画茘枝圗自作赋以遗之后薨于岭表扶防灵榇经渚宫家人鬻海珍珠翠于市时人讥之
    　　赵大夫号无字碑【张防附】
    　　唐赵大夫崇凝清介门无杂宾慕王蒙刘真长之风也标质堂堂不为文章号曰无字碑每遇转官旧例各举一人自代亚台未尝举人云朝中无可代己也世亦以此少之　梁相张防尝为僧返俗应举亚台鄙之或曰刘轲蔡京得非僧乎亚台曰刘蔡辈虽作僧未为人知翻然贡艺有何不可张防衣冠子弟无故出家不能防禅访道抗迹尘外乃于御前进诗希望恩泽如此行止岂掩人口某十度知举十度斥之清河公乃东依梁主而求际防盖为天水拒弃竟为梁相也

    Explanation

    36

    Liu Chonggui's Litchi Painting

    During the Tang Dynasty, Liu Chonggui, a high-ranking official, lived a life of simplicity and frugality, which greatly attracted public opinion. He once invited fellow officials to a meal of bitter kale [or horse] and steamed flatbread. Some court officials knew this was a show of humility and secretly asked a young servant, "What did the chancellor eat for breakfast?" The servant replied, "He ate it all up." The court officials laughed at this. Later, when Liu Chonggui was stationed in Fanyang, he emulated Wu Yin's integrity. His relatives and acquaintances in the capital who were poor awaited his help, but he only drew a painting of litchis and composed a poem to give as a gift. After his death in the southern regions, his family escorted his coffin through Zhuzhou Palace. His family members sold sea pearls and jade in the market, which was criticized by the public.

    Zhao Chongning, Called the Uninscribed Stele (with Zhang Fang attached)

    During the Tang Dynasty, Zhao Chongning, a high-ranking official, was clear and upright, and his household had no unworthy visitors. He admired the style of Wang Meng and Liu Zhenzhang. He was tall and dignified and did not write articles, so he was called the Uninscribed Stele. Each time he was promoted, the usual practice was to nominate someone to replace him, but he never nominated anyone, saying that there was no one in the court who could replace him. The world also criticized him for this. Liang Xiang Zhang Fang once became a monk and then returned to the secular world to take the imperial examinations. Zhao Chongning looked down on him. Someone asked, "Wasn't Liu Ke and Cai Jing monks?" Zhao Chongning replied, "Even if Liu Ke and Cai Jing became monks, they were not well-known. Suddenly presenting themselves in the imperial examinations, how could that be acceptable?" Zhang Fang was a member of the aristocracy who, for no reason, left the secular world and did not engage in meditation or seeking enlightenment, but instead presented himself in the imperial examinations in the hope of gaining favor. Such behavior could not be tolerated by the public. Zhang Fang, a member of the aristocracy, relied on the Eastern Prince to seek favor, because he was rejected by Tian Shui, and eventually became a high-ranking official in the Liang Dynasty.

    北梦琐言卷三
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷四
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　赵令公红拂子
    　　唐襄州赵康凝令公世勲嗣袭人质甚伟酷好修容前后垂镜以整冠栉往往以家讳刑人相国崔公允出镇湖南由岘首赵令逢迎开宴崔相从容而防之曰闻令公以文字刑人甚无谓也闻名心瞿但有颦蹙岂可笞责及人耶俄而近侍以红拂子于乌巾上拂之相国又曰此尤不可也陪寮俛首而已天水其后汉南失守已而奔呉路由夏口杜洪念公郊迓以主座逊之遽尸其位其不识去就皆此也竟罹祸于淮甸宜乎

    Explanation

    Scattered Notes of the Northern Dream, Volume Three
    　　Imperially Approved Complete Library of the Four Treasuries
    　　Scattered Notes of the Northern Dream, Volume Four
    　　By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty
    　　Governor Zhao Kangning's Red Brush
    　　During the Tang dynasty, Governor Zhao Kangning of Xiang Prefecture, a man of great merit and title, was renowned for his handsome appearance and his meticulous grooming. He would hang a mirror to adjust his hat and comb, often using a family taboo to punish someone. When Prime Minister Cui Gong Rong was transferred to govern Hunan, he met Zhao Kangning at Xianshou and hosted a banquet. The prime minister casually and subtly intervened, saying, "I have heard that Lord Gong punishes people with words, which is very meaningless. Upon hearing this, I felt uneasy and only showed frowns. How can one beat or scold others?" Soon after, a courtier used a red brush to sweep over the black hat. The prime minister then said, "This is especially unacceptable," and the attendants only bowed their heads. Later, in the land of Tianshui, after the loss of Han South, Zhao Kangning fled to Wu, passing through Xiakou where Du Hong met him at the outskirts and yielded the main seat. Zhao Kangning quickly occupied the position, not knowing how to act appropriately, as shown in this example. He ultimately suffered misfortune in Huai Prefecture, and it is appropriate.

    薛氏子具军仪
    　　唐薛尚书能以文章自负累出戎镇常郁郁叹惜因有诗谢淮南寄天柱茶其落句云麄官乞与真抛却赖有诗名合得尝意以节将为麄官也镇许昌日幕吏咸集令其子具櫜鞬防诸幕客幕客怪惊八座曰俾渠消灾时人以为轻薄盖不得本分官矫此以见志非轻薄也
    　　孙偓相通简
    　　唐相国孙公偓寛裕通简不事矫异常语于亲友曰凡人持己务在得中但士行无不必太苦以我之长彰彼之短以我之清彰彼之浊幸勿为之后谪居衡山情抱坦然不以放逐而懐戚戚每对客座而厮仆辈纷诟殴曳仆于面前相国凝然似无所睹谓客曰以怒心逢彼即方寸自挠矣其性度皆此也相国曽乗轺至蜀诣杜光庭先生受箓乃曰尝遇至人话及时事每有髙栖之约尔后虽登台辅竟出官于南岳有诗寄杜先生其要句云蜀国信难遇楚乡心更愁我行同范蠡师举效浮丘他日相逢处多应在十洲唐末朝逹罹谷水白马驿之祸唯相国获免焉

    Explanation

    38

    The Son of the Xue Family Prepared Military Attire
    The Tang dynasty official Xue, known for his literary talent, was frequently posted to military garrisons and often sighed with regret. He once wrote a poem thanking Huainan for sending him Tianzhu tea, with the lines: "A lower-ranking official is given something; truly discarded, relying on my poetic reputation to receive it." He meant that as a military commander, he was considered a low-ranking official. When he was stationed in Xuchang, all the officials gathered, and he ordered his son to prepare military attire to protect the guests. The guests were surprised and alarmed, and the Eighth Seat (a high-ranking official) said, "Make him avoid disaster." At the time, people thought he was superficial, but it was because he did not hold a proper official position and used this as a way to express his intentions, not because he was superficial.

    The Right Minister Sun Wò Was Open and Simple
    The Right Minister Sun Wò was open and simple, not engaging in artificial or exaggerated behavior. He once said to his friends and relatives, "When one holds oneself, one must strive for moderation. Though one's conduct may not be perfect, it does not need to be overly strict. Use one's strengths to highlight others' shortcomings, and one's clarity to highlight others' obscurity. It is best not to do this." After being exiled to Hengshan, he had a calm and open heart and did not feel sorrow because of his exile. Whenever he met guests, the servants and laborers would quarrel and fight in front of him, but he remained calm as if seeing nothing. He said to the guests, "If one meets such people with anger, one's own mind will be disturbed." His character and demeanor were all like this. Once, he traveled to Shu and visited Master Du Guangting to receive a talisman. He said, "I once met a sage who spoke of current affairs and often made plans for a high retreat. Afterward, even though I reached a high position, I was eventually exiled to Nanyue. I wrote a poem to Master Du, with the key lines: 'It is indeed difficult to meet in Shu; the heart in Chu is even more sorrowful. My journey is like that of Fan Li, and my teacher is like Xu Fu. Someday, our meeting place will be in the Ten Isles.'" In the late Tang dynasty, many officials suffered the disaster at Gushui and Baima Pavilion, but only Right Minister Sun Wò was spared.

    栁玭大夫赏牟黁
    　　唐栁大夫玭直清重徳中外惮之谪授泸州郡守先诣东川庭防具櫜鞬元戎顾相彦朗坚却之亚台曰朝廷本用见责此乃军府旧仪顾公不得已而受之赴任路由渝州有牟黁秀才者即都校牟居厚之子文采不髙执所业谒见亚台奬饰甚勤甥侄从行以为牟子卷轴不消见遇亚台曰巴蜀多故土豪倔起斯乃押衙之子独能慕善茍不诱进渠即退志以吾称之人必荣之由此减三五贠草贼不亦善乎子弟窃笑而服之

    Explanation

    39

    Liu Pin, the Tang Dynasty Official, Honors Mou Xun

    During the Tang Dynasty, Liu Pin, an official known for his upright, clear, and virtuous character, was feared both inside and outside the court. He was demoted to serve as the governor of Luzhou. Before taking up his new post, he visited the Eastern Shu court with his ceremonial weapons. The chief general, Gu Xiang Yanlang, firmly refused to receive him. A high-ranking official, referred to as "subordinate," said, "The regions of Ba and Shu are troubled, and local strongmen are rising up. This is the son of a military officer, but he alone is able to admire virtue. If not encouraged to advance, he will then withdraw his ambition. By my praise, people will certainly honor him. This could benefit the region by reducing the number of bandits, which would be good." The younger generation secretly laughed but respected him.

    孙揆尚书锯解【刘知俊附】
    　　唐末朝廷围太原不克以宰相张濬为都统华帅韩建为副使泽潞孙揆尚书以本道兵防伐军容使杨复恭与张相不叶逗挠其师因而自溃由是贬张相为绣州牧孙尚书为太原所执诟骂元戎李公克用以狗猪代之李公大怒俾以锯解虽加苦楚而锯齿不行八座乃谓曰死狗猪解人须用板夹然后可得行汝何以知之由此施板而锯方行未絶间骂声不歇何乃壮而不怖斯则君子之儒必有勇也近者刘知俊自梁奔秦自秦奔蜀骁暴之声天下咸闻焉蜀先主坐其惨酷而诛之受戮日章皇万端乞命不暇行刑者嗟而笑之比孙帅何勇怯之不侔也【孙揆尚书少年不慧涕泪狼籍蒙然而已十五嵗适然一变非唯时俊乃烈士也】

    Explanation

    40

    In the late Tang Dynasty, the imperial court failed to capture Taiyuan, so Chancellor Zhang Jun was appointed as the supreme commander, with Han Jian as his deputy. Sun Kui, the Shangshu of Zelü, led the campaign with troops from his region. Yang Fugong, the military commander, did not agree with Zhang Jun and delayed his troops, causing them to溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃溃

    崔允相腋文
    　　唐崔相国慎猷亷察浙西日有瓦棺寺持法华经僧为门徒或有术士言相国面上气色有贵子问其姙娠之所在夫人洎妾媵间皆无所见相国徐思之乃召曾侍更衣官妓而示术士曰果在此也及载诞日腋下有文相次分明即瓦棺僧名也因命其小字缁郎年七嵗尚不食肉一日有僧请见乃掌其颊谓曰既爱官爵何不食肉自此方味荤血即相国允也崔事一说云是终南山僧两存之

    Explanation

    41

    Cui Yun's Armpit Mark

    During the Tang Dynasty, when Cui Yun, the prime minister, was conducting an inspection in Zhe West, there was a monk from Waguan Temple who held the Lotus Sutra and had disciples. A fortune-teller told Cui Yun that his facial expression indicated he would have a noble child. When asked where the child would be, neither his wife nor his concubines could see any sign. Cui Yun pondered slowly and then summoned a former attendant who had once served as a court entertainer and showed her to the fortune-teller, saying, "Indeed, it is here." On the day of the child's birth, there was a mark on the child's armpit, clearly resembling the name of the monk from Waguan Temple. Cui Yun then named the child "Zi Lang." At seven years old, the child still did not eat meat. One day, a monk came to see him, and Cui Yun slapped the child's cheek and said, "Since you love the position of official, why don't you eat meat?" From then on, the child began to eat meat. This child was none other than Cui Yun. Another account suggests that the monk was from Mount Zhongnan, and both accounts exist.

    诸重徳好尚
    　　唐朱崖李太尉与同列欵曲或有征其所好者掌武曰喜见未闻言新书防崔魏公好食新防头以为珍美从事开筵先一夕前必到使院索新煑防头也杜豳公每早食饙饭干脯崔侍郎安潜好看鬭牛虽各有所美而非近利与夫牙筹金埒钱癖谷堆不亦逺乎
    　　毕舅知分【蜀杨会附】
    　　唐毕相諴家本寒微其渭阳为太湖县伍伯【伍伯即今号杂职行杖者】相国耻之俾罢此役为除一官累遣致意竟不承命特除选人杨载宰此邑防辞特于私第延坐与语期为落此猥籍津送入京杨令到任具逹台旨伍伯曰某下贱岂有外甥为宰相耶杨令坚勉之乃曰某每嵗公税享六十緍事例钱茍无败阙终身优渥不审相公欲为致何官职

    Explanation

    42

    The Preferences of Respected Individuals

    During the Tang Dynasty, Li Jing, the Grand Councillor of Zhu崖, was known for his close relationships with his colleagues. When someone inquired about his preferences, he replied, "I enjoy hearing something new," and mentioned a new book by Cui Wei, a high-ranking official, which he particularly liked for its fresh content. He also enjoyed eating new cakes, considering them delicious and precious. Before a banquet, he would ensure that new cakes were prepared by arriving at the office the day before to request them.

    Du You, another high-ranking official, preferred to have steamed rice and dried meat for breakfast. Cui Anqian, a high-ranking official, enjoyed watching bullfights. Despite their individual preferences, none of these officials were driven by immediate gain, unlike those who were obsessed with gambling tokens, betting on horses, or accumulating wealth.

    Bi Xian, a high-ranking official, came from a humble background. His family in the region near the Wei River was originally poor, and he himself had been a low-ranking official in Wuxi County, often referred to as a "伍伯" (a guard or low-ranking official). The Grand Councillor was ashamed of this and wanted him to quit his menial duties. He repeatedly sent messages to improve his position but received no response. Finally, he appointed Yang Zai, a local official, to govern the county. Bi Xian personally invited Yang Zai to his private residence, sat down with him, and discussed the matter, hoping to elevate his nephew's status. He promised to ensure that Yang Zai would receive favorable treatment and generous conditions if he could secure a government position for his nephew. Upon arriving in the county, Yang Zai informed the low-ranking official of Bi Xian's intentions. The official, however, was surprised and asked, "How could I, a lowly person, have a nephew who is a high-ranking official?" Yang Zai encouraged him, saying, "Each year, you receive sixty units of currency and customary fees. If you perform your duties well, you will receive favorable treatment for life. What specific position does the Grand Councillor wish to secure for you?"

    杨令具以闻相国叹赏亦然其说竟不夺其志也近者蜀相庾公傅素与其从弟凝绩曾宰蜀州唐兴县郎【一作良】吏有杨防者庾氏之昆弟深念之洎迭秉蜀政为杨防除长马以酬之杨防曰某之吏役逺近皆知忝冒为官宁掩人口岂可将数千【一作子】家供待而博【一作簿】一虚名长马乎虽强假军职除授检校官竟不舎县役亦毕舅之次也
    　　杨蔚使君三典洋源
    　　唐杨蔚使君典洋州道者陈休复每到州多止于紫极宫宏农甚思一见而颍川輙便他适乃谓道士曰此度更来便须申报或一日再至遽令申白俄而州将拥斾而至方遂披揖宏农曰向风久矣幸获祗奉敢以将来禄算为请勿讶造次颍川呼人为卿乃谓州牧曰卿三为刺史了更无言州牧不怿以其曾典两郡至此三也自是常以见任为终焉之所尔后秩满无恙不喻其言无何又授此州亦终考限罢后又除是郡凡三任竟殒于是三为刺史之说果在于此乎杨公季弟玭为愚话之

    Explanation

    43

    Yang Lingsheng reported all this to the Chancellor, who admired and praised him, and found his words to be true, ultimately not changing his mind. Recently, Governor Fu Su of Shu and his younger brother, Ning Ji, who had once served as the magistrate of Tangxing County in Shuzhou, deeply missed a local official named Yang Fang, who was a close relative of the Yu family. When they repeatedly held power in Shu, they appointed Yang Fang to a high-ranking position as a reward. Yang Fang said, "My service as an official is known far and wide; I humbly accept this post, but would not hide the truth from the people. How could I take on the responsibility of thousands of households to gain a mere title?" Even if forced to take a military position, he was appointed as a temporary official but finally did not leave his post in the county, completing his duties as a relative.

    Yang Wei, the governor of Yangzhou, served three terms in the region. Daoist Chen Xiufu, who often stayed at the Purple Extreme Palace, greatly desired to meet him, but Yu Hongnong always left for other places. Yu Hongnong then told the道士, "If he comes again, please report it to me." One day, Chen Xiufu arrived twice in quick succession, and soon the state official arrived with his banner. Yu Hongnong finally greeted him, saying, "I have long admired you from afar. I am happy to serve you. May I ask about your future career?" Yu Hongnong called him "卿" and said to the prefect, "You have served three terms as a prefect; what more can you say?" The prefect was displeased, thinking that he had previously governed two counties and now served three terms in the same region. From then on, he considered his current position as his final resting place. After completing his term without incident, he did not understand his words. Shortly after, he was appointed to this county again, serving his term until he died. Thus, the saying that he served three terms as a prefect was indeed true. Yang Gong's younger brother, Pin, told me about this.

    妖人为称陈帝师
    　　唐军容使田令孜擅权有囬天之力尝致书于许昌为其兄陈敬瑄求兵马使职节将崔侍中安潜不允尔后崔公移镇西川敬瑄与师立牛勉罗元果以打毬争三川敬瑄获头筹制授右蜀节旄以代崔公中外惊骇报状云陈仆射之命莫知谁何青城县弥勒防妖人【弥勒会北中金刚禅也】窥此声势乃伪作陈仆射行李云山
    东盗起车驾必谋幸蜀先以陈公走马赴任乃树一魁妖共翼佐之军府未喻亦差迎至近驿有指挥索白马四匹察事者其非常乃羁縻之未供承间而真陈仆射亦连辔而至其妖人等悉擒缚而俟命颍川俾隐而诛之识者曰陈帝师【一作仆射】由阉官之力无防尘之效盗处方镇始为妖物所凭终以自贻诛灭非不幸也

    Explanation

    44

    A False Claim to Imperial Authority

    During the Tang Dynasty, the powerful eunuch Tian Lingzi, who held the title of Army Commander, wielded immense influence and power. He once wrote to Xu Chang, requesting that his brother Chen Jingxuan be appointed to the position of Commander of Cavalry. The high-ranking official Cui Shizhong, serving as Secretary of State, refused the request. Later, Cui was transferred to govern the western region (Sichuan). Chen Jingxuan, along with generals Shili, Niuan, and Luo Yuan, competed for control of the three major rivers (symbolizing power and influence). Chen emerged victorious and was appointed as the Governor of the Western Region, succeeding Cui. This news shocked the court and the people. A report was circulated claiming that Chen had been appointed by the Chancellor, but no one knew who had issued the order.

    In Qingcheng County, a group of followers of the Maitreya sect (a Buddhist millenarian movement) saw an opportunity in the chaos and began to spread false claims, pretending to be the Chancellor's emissaries. They claimed that a rebellion had broken out in the east, and the emperor was planning to flee to Sichuan. They urged Chen to ride swiftly to take up his new post and even set up a false leader to assist him. The military authorities were confused and sent officials to greet Chen at a nearby inn. These officials were instructed to provide four white horses, which they suspected were unusual. They detained the officials and kept them under surveillance. Soon after, the real Chen, accompanied by his entourage, arrived at the inn. The false leaders were then captured and bound, awaiting further orders. They were secretly executed in Yingchuan. Knowledgeable people remarked that Chen's claim to the title of "Imperial Teacher" (or "Chancellor") was a fabrication, achieved through the influence of eunuchs, and had no positive impact. Those who sought power through such means were ultimately doomed to self-destruction, a fate that was not entirely unexpected.

    哭麻刘舎人事
    　　唐李相磎髙才奥学冠絶羣彦为朋党所排洎登岩廊似涉由径虽然亦才授也制下之日刘舎人崇抱麻而哭之李相斥其祖祢条上其事具表论之又以彭城先徳受贿饮酖乃作鹦鹉杯赋丑词讦切人为寒心朝士有识者阅其表曰何必多言但不云倒防侧于君前有诛彭城子何所逃刑时以为然
    　　蔡京尚书拔顾氏昆弟
    　　唐蔡京尚书为天徳军使衙前小将顾彦朗彦晖知使宅市买八座有知人之鉴或一日俾其子叔向巳下备酒馔于山亭召二顾赐宴八座俄而即席约令勿起二顾惶惑莫喻其意八座勉之曰公弟兄俱有封侯之相善自保爱他年愿以子孙相依因迁其职级洎黄冦犯阙顾彦朗领本军立复功除东川加使相蔡叔向兄弟往依之请叔向为节度副使仍以丈人行拜之军府大事皆谘谋焉顾相薨其弟彦晖嗣之亦至使相

    Explanation

    45

    Translation

    Crying for Ma and the Matter of Liu Shèrén

    During the Tang Dynasty, Li Shi, the chancellor, was a man of extraordinary talent and profound learning, surpassing all his peers. However, he was slandered by political factions and eventually promoted to a high position, which seemed to be achieved through improper means. Although his promotion was ostensibly based on his talent and merit, it was widely seen as a result of political maneuvering. On the day the edict was issued, Liu Shèrén, a scribe, cried upon hearing the news. Chancellor Li Shi criticized Liu Shèrén's ancestors for their corruption and submitted a detailed memorial to the emperor, accusing them of accepting bribes and drinking poison. He wrote a poem titled "Parrot Cup," filled with harsh and critical words that deeply offended the court. Knowledgeable officials read his memorial and said, "Why say so much? If only you had not mentioned the disrespectful actions in front of the emperor, there would be no need to punish the son of the Pei family." At the time, this view was generally accepted.

    The Promotion of the Gu Brothers by Cai Jing

    During the Tang Dynasty, Cai Jing, a high-ranking official, served as the military governor of Tian De. He had a keen eye for talent and often recognized the potential of those around him. One day, he invited his son, Shu Xiang, and other officials to a banquet at a mountain pavilion, where he called upon two young men named Gu Yanlang and Gu Yanhui, who were known for their integrity. He instructed them not to stand up and asked them to remain seated. The two young men were confused and did not understand his intentions. Cai Jing encouraged them, saying, "Both of you have the appearance of future marquises. Take good care of yourselves, and in the future, I hope to rely on your descendants." He then promoted their ranks. When the Yellow Turban rebels invaded the capital, Gu Yanlang led his troops and restored order, earning the title of governor of Dongchuan and being appointed as an imperial envoy. Shu Xiang and his brothers went to rely on him and requested that Shu Xiang be appointed as the deputy military governor. They treated him with great respect, as if he were a father figure, and all major military and administrative matters were discussed with him. After Gu Yanlang's death, his brother Gu Yanhui succeeded him and also reached the rank of imperial envoy.

    46

    陆扆相六月及第【卢光启附】
    　　唐陆相扆举进士属僖宗再幸梁洋随驾至行在于时奔避劳止又时当六月而相国防名尔后在翰林暑月苦于蒸溽同列讥之曰今日好造天牓以其进取非时也然相国文才重徳名冠一时朝中陆氏三人号曰三陆即相国洎希声及威乃三人也　卢相光启先人伏刑尔后兄弟脩饰赴举因谓亲知曰此乃开荒也然其立性周谨进取多涂初举子一卷即进
    取诸事皆此也防名后歴台省受知于租庸张濬清河出征并汾卢每致书疏凡一事别为一幅朝士至今效之盖八行重叠别纸自公始也唐末举人不问士行文艺但勤于请谒号曰精切亦楷法于范阳公尔其族弟汝弼尝为张相【一作濬】出征判官传檄四方其畧云致赤子之流离自朱邪之版荡自谓人曰天生朱邪赤子供我之笔也俊迈亦有族昆之风

    Explanation

    46

    Lu Yi, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, passed the imperial examination in the sixth month. During the reign of Emperor Xizong, he followed the emperor to Liangyang and stayed at his temporary residence during the time of fleeing and laboring. At that time, it was the sixth month, and after passing the examination, he became a high-ranking official. He later served in the Hanlin Academy, where he suffered from the heat and humidity during the summer months. His colleagues mocked him, saying, "It's a good day to make the imperial list," implying that his success was untimely. However, the official was renowned for his literary talent and noble character, and he was one of the three prominent Lus in the court, known as the "Three Lus." The other two were Lu Xi and Lu Wei.

    Lu Guangqi, the son of Lu Yi, was executed, and his brothers prepared themselves to take the examination. They told their close friends, "This is our first attempt," indicating their initial effort. Lu Guangqi was known for his cautious and meticulous nature, and he pursued various paths to success. He submitted a single scroll of his work and achieved success in many endeavors. After passing the examination, he served in various positions in the imperial court and was known for his ability to write detailed and separate documents for each matter. This style of writing, with eight lines of text and separate sheets of paper, became a model for officials to follow, and it was Lu Guangqi who first established this practice.

    During the late Tang Dynasty, candidates for the imperial examination did not focus on their moral conduct or literary skills but rather on diligently visiting and networking with influential people, a practice known as "jingqie." This was also the model set by the Prince of Fanyang. Lu Guangqi's nephew, Junmai, also had the spirit of his clan, known for their prominence and influence.

    呉融侍郎文笔
    　　唐呉融侍郎防名后曾依相国太尉韦公昭度以文笔求知每起草先呈皆不称旨呉乃祈掌武亲密俾逹其诚且曰某幸得齿在宾次唯以文字受眷虽愧荒拙敢不着功未闻惬当反甚忧惧掌武笑曰呉校书诚是艺士每有见请自是呉家文字非干老夫由是改之果惬上公之意也散版出官寓于江陵为僧贯休撰诗序以唐来唯元白休师而已又祭陆蒙文即云海内文章止鲁望而已自相矛盾于时不免识者所讥
    　　破天荒解
    　　唐荆州衣冠薮泽每嵗解送举人多不成名号曰天荒解刘蜕舎人以荆解及第号为破天荒尔来余知古关圗常脩乃荆州之居人也率有髙文连登上科闗即衙前将校之子也及第归乡都押已下为其张筵乃指盘上酱瓯戏老校曰要校【一作拔】卒为者其人以醋樽进之曰此亦校【一作拔】卒为者也席人大噱闗圗妻即常脩妹才思妇也有祭夫文行于世

    Explanation

    47

    Wú Róng's Literary Ability

    After gaining some reputation, the Tang official Wú Róng, serving as a侍郎 (attendant official), once sought recognition through his literary talent by attaching himself to Wéi Zhāodù, the Prime Minister and Grand General. Every time he drafted a document, he would first present it to Wéi, but it never met his approval. Wú then sought the help of his close associate Zhang Wu to convey his sincerity, saying, "I am fortunate to be among the guests of your court, and I have only ever gained your favor through my writings. Though I feel ashamed of my crude and unrefined skills, I dare not fail to strive for merit. Yet I have heard no word of approval, and I am instead filled with fear." Zhang Wu laughed and said, "Wú the compiler (校书) is indeed a talented scholar. Whenever he is invited to contribute, it is his own writing, not mine. Therefore, you should change your style." He did so, and it finally met the approval of the high-ranking official.

    Later, he was demoted from office and took residence in Jiangling. There, he composed a preface to a collection of poems by the Buddhist monk Guàn Xiū, stating that since the Tang dynasty, only Yuan and Bai (the famous poets Yuan Zhen and Bai Juyi) and Guàn Xiū himself had been worthy of praise. In his eulogy for Lù Guīmēng, he wrote, "Within the realm, literary talent is only Lǔ Wàng (Lu Guimeng)." These contradictory statements did not go unnoticed and were inevitably criticized by those who understood the matter.

    Breaking the "Tianhuang" Examination

    In the Tang dynasty, Jingzhou was a region known for its gentry and scholars. Each year, candidates from the area were sent to take the imperial examinations, but few succeeded. This region was known as the "tianhuang" (unbroken wilderness), a term for a place that had never produced a successful examinee. Liu Tuì, the Secretary (舎人), was the first to pass the examination from Jingzhou, and thus was called the one who "broke the tianhuang."

    Since then, I have known of Gǔ Guāntú and Cháng Xiū, who were residents of Jingzhou. Cháng Xiū was known for his high literary talent and had repeatedly passed the highest-level examinations. Guāntú was the son of a military officer stationed before the government office (衙前将校). After passing the examination and returning to his hometown, the local military commander and his subordinates hosted a banquet in his honor. During the feast, he pointed to a sauce bowl on the table and joked with the old officer, saying, "The one who is in charge [or: the one who is promoted] is the one who does it." The person serving the sauce replied, "This is also the one who is in charge [or: promoted] who does it." The guests at the table laughed heartily.

    Gǔ Guāntú's wife was Cháng Xiū's sister, a woman of literary talent. She composed a eulogy for her husband, which became known in the world.

    成令公为蛇绕身
    　　唐荆州成令公汭领蔡州军戍江陵为节度使张璝谋害之遂率本都奔于秭归一夜为巨蛇绕身防至于殒乃曰茍有所负死生唯命逡巡蛇亦亡去尔后招辑户口训练士卒防流而镇渚宫寻授节旄抚绥凋残励精为理初年居民唯一十七家末年至万户勤王奉国通商务农有足称焉朝廷号北韩南郭【韩即华州韩建成令初姓郭后归本姓】有孔目官贺隐者亦返俗僧也端贞俭约始为腹心凡有阙政赖其防赞自贺物故率由胸加以骋辨陵人又多矜伐为识者所鄙妇翁竺知章乃饼匠也言多不逊又元子微过皆手刃之竟无系嗣楼船之役幕僚结舌终致鄂渚之败惜哉

    Explanation

    48

    Cheng Linggong was suddenly surrounded by a giant snake. During the Tang Dynasty, Cheng Linggong, the Commander-in-Chief of Jingzhou, led troops from Cai Prefecture to garrison Jingling. He was targeted for assassination by the military governor Zhang Qian and fled with his troops to Zigui County. One night, a large snake wrapped around his body, preventing him from dying. He said, "If there is something owed, life and death are determined by fate." He hesitated, and the snake also disappeared. Afterward, he recruited and settled households, trained soldiers, and stabilized the region at Zhu Gong. He was soon granted a ceremonial staff, comforted and supported the devastated, and strove diligently for good governance. In the early years, the population was only seventeen households, but by the end of his tenure, it had grown to ten thousand. He served the king and the state diligently, facilitating trade and agriculture, earning praise from the court. He was known as "North Han and South Guo" (Han refers to the surname of the official from Huazhou, originally surnamed Guo, who later returned to his original surname). There was a registrar named He Yin, who was also a former monk, and was upright, sincere, thrifty, and frugal. He became a trusted advisor, and all administrative shortcomings relied on his prevention and assistance. After He Yin's death, Cheng Linggong became more assertive and boastful, often challenging others, and was criticized by those who knew him. His father-in-law, Zhu Zhizhang, a baker, often spoke disrespectfully. Cheng Linggong even killed his eldest son for a minor fault, leaving no heir. During the naval campaign, his advisors remained silent, leading to the defeat at the Battle of Ezh渚, a regrettable outcome.

    张濬相破贼
    　　唐黄巢犯阙僖宗幸蜀张相国濬白身未有名第时在河中永乐庄居里有一道士或麻衣或羽帔不可亲狎一日张在村路前行后有唤张三十四郎驾前待尔破贼囬顾乃是此道士【一作人】相国曰某一布衣耳何阶縁而能破贼乎道士勉其入蜀适遇相国圣善疾苦未果南行道者乃遗两粒丹曰服此可十年无恙相国得药奉亲所疾痊复后歴登台辅道者亦不复见破贼之说何其騐哉

    Explanation

    49

    The Chancellor Zhang Jun's Defeat of the Rebels

    During the Tang Dynasty, Huang Chao's forces attacked the imperial capital, and Emperor Xizong took refuge in Shu. At the time, Zhang Jun, who was still a commoner without official rank, lived in Yongle Village in Hedong. One day, while walking along a village road, he encountered a Daoist priest who appeared in different guises—sometimes wearing a coarse linen garment and other times a Daoist robe. This Daoist was not easily approachable. Suddenly, the Daoist called out to Zhang, saying, "Zhang San Shi Si Lang, await me in the imperial court to defeat the rebels." Zhang turned around and saw that it was the same Daoist. He said, "I am just a commoner; how could I possibly defeat the rebels?" The Daoist encouraged him to go to Shu, where he would meet with the emperor. However, Zhang was unable to make the journey south due to his mother's illness. The Daoist then gave him two pills and said, "By taking these, you can remain healthy for ten years." Zhang took the medicine, and his mother's illness was cured. Later, Zhang Jun rose to become a chancellor and successfully defeated the rebels. The Daoist, however, was never seen again, and the prophecy of Zhang's victory proved to be remarkably accurate.

    薛澄州弄笏【罗九臯附】
    　　唐薛澄州昭纬即保逊之子也恃才傲物亦有父风每入朝省弄笏而行旁无人好唱浣溪纱词知举后有一门生辞归乡里临岐献防曰侍郎重徳某乃受恩尔后请不弄笏与唱浣溪纱即某幸也时人谓之至言有小吏常学其行步揖逊公知之乃召谓曰试于庭前学得似则恕尔罪于是下亷拥姬妾而观之小吏安详傲然举动酷似笑而舎之　路侍中岩在西蜀尝夏日纳凉于毬场防中使院小吏罗九臯巾裹步履有似裴条郎中大貂遥见促召衫带遍视方知其非因笞之
    　　西岳神毙张簴
    　　唐张防早为僧败道归俗后为梁相先在华山云台观修业观侧有庄其弟簴亦轻易道教因脱防服挂于天尊臂上云借此公为我掌之须臾精神恍忽似遭殴撃痛呌狼狈或顿或起如有人拖曵之状归至别业而卒斯人也必党于释氏而轻侮道尊人之无礼自贻隂殛非不幸也与嘉州崔使君开尹真君石函事同【开石函为防官所録夺算见宣室志】李载仁郎中目睹为愚话之

    Explanation

    50

    薛澄州弄笏【罗九臯附】
    　　唐薛澄州昭纬，即薛保逊之子，恃才傲物，亦有父风。每入朝省，弄笏而行，旁若无人。好唱浣溪纱词。知举后，有一门生辞归乡里，临岐献防曰：“侍郎重德，某乃受恩，尔后请不弄笏与唱浣溪纱，即某幸也。”时人谓之至言。有小吏常学其行步揖逊，公知之，乃召谓曰：“试于庭前学得似，则恕尔罪。”于是下亷拥姬妾而观之，小吏安详傲然，举动酷似，笑而舎之。路侍中岩在西蜀，尝夏日纳凉于毬场防中使院。小吏罗九臯巾裹步履，有似裴条郎中，大貂遥见，促召衫带，遍视方知其非，因笞之。
    　　西岳神毙张簴
    　　唐张防早为僧，败道归俗，后为梁相。先在华山云台观修业，观侧有庄。其弟簴亦轻易道教，因脱防服挂于天尊臂上，云：“借此公为我掌之。”须臾，精神恍忽，似遭殴撃，痛呌狼狈，或顿或起，如有人拖曵之状，归至别业而卒。斯人也，必党于释氏而轻侮道尊，人之无礼，自贻隂殛，非不幸也。与嘉州崔使君开尹真君石函事同【开石函为防官所録夺算见宣室志】。李载仁郎中目睹为愚话之。

    栁婢讥盖巨源
    　　唐栁仆射仲郢【一作贤】镇郪城有一婢失意将婢于成都鬻之盖巨源使君乃西川大校累典雄郡【一作大郡】宅在苦竹溪女侩具以栁婢言导盖公欲之乃取归其家女工之具悉随之日夕赏其巧技或一日盖公临街窥窓栁婢在侍通衢有鬻绫罗者从窓下过召婢就宅盖公于束缣内选择邉幅舒卷揲之第其厚薄酬酢可否栁婢失声而仆似中风恙命扶之而去一无言语但令舆还女侩家翌日而瘳诘其所苦青衣曰某虽贱人曾为栁家细婢死则死矣安能事卖绢牙郎乎蜀都闻之皆嗟叹也清族之家率由礼门盖公暴贵未知士风为婢仆所讥宜矣哉

    Explanation

    51

    Liu Zhongying, the high-ranking official, was governing Qiancheng when one of his maids, disappointed and out of favor, was sold to Chengdu by a female intermediary. Gai Juyuan, a prominent military leader in the Western Shu region, repeatedly governed powerful prefectures and had his residence in Kuzhuxi. The female intermediary described the maid to Gai Juyuan, who decided to take her into his household. The tools and materials for women's work followed her. Every day and night, Gai Juyuan admired her skills and craftsmanship. One day, while Gai Juyuan was looking out of his street-facing window, the maid was attending to him. On the street below, a silk peddler passed by. Gai Juyuan called the maid to his residence and, among the silk bolts, unfolded, rolled, and examined them, assessing their thickness and bargaining with the peddler. The maid suddenly lost her voice and collapsed, as if suffering from a stroke. She was ordered to be carried away and taken back to the female intermediary's home. The next day, she recovered. When questioned about her suffering, the maid, a low-ranking servant, said, "I once was a fine maid of the Liu family. If I die, I die, but how could I serve a silk peddler?" The people of Shu heard of this and all sighed in admiration. Families of high status generally follow the path of propriety, but Gai Juyuan, suddenly becoming wealthy, did not know the customs of scholars and was mocked by maids and servants. It is appropriate.

    赵师儒与栁大夫唱和
    　　唐栁玭大夫之任泸州泝舟经马骁镇土豪赵师儒率乡兵数千凭髙立寨刑讼生杀得以自专本道署以军职闻五马经过乃棹扁舟被褐衫把杖子迎接防状云百姓赵师儒亚台以其有职非属邑怪而辞之师儒曰巴蜀乱离某懐集乡人拒他盗非敢僭幸妄徼戎职亚台欣而接之乃驻旌斾馆于寨中供亿丰备钦礼弥勤师儒亦有诗句皆陈素心亚台悉为和之睹其清俭不嗟叹曰我他年登廊庙必为斯人而致节察盖赏其知分任真也

    Explanation

    52

    Zhao Shishu and Liu Bin's Mutual Poetry
    During the Tang Dynasty, Liu Bin, the governor of Luzhou, was traveling upstream when his boat passed through Ma Xiao Town. A local leader named Zhao Shishu, who had established a camp on high ground and had the authority to decide on crimes, lawsuits, and life or death matters, was granted a military position by the local authority. When the governor's entourage passed by, Zhao Shishu rowed a small boat, wearing a rough cloth robe and holding a cane, and presented a petition stating, "The commoner Zhao Shishu, deputy governor, is not under the jurisdiction of the local area." Liu Bin found this strange and refused to accept it. Zhao Shishu explained, "I am a deputy governor and not under the jurisdiction of the local area." Liu Bin was pleased and received him happily, staying in the camp and setting up a residence, providing abundant supplies and becoming even more respectful and courteous. Zhao Shishu also composed poems expressing his true intentions, which Liu Bin responded to in kind. Liu Bin praised Zhao Shishu for understanding his limits and being sincere.

    祖系圗进士牓
    　　禅门有祖系圗得佛心印者皆次列之进士有登科记懐将相才者咸编缀之而名实相违玉石混杂疑误后人良可怪也唐进士宇文翃虽士族子无文藻酷爱上科有女及笄真国色也朝之令子弟求之不得时窦璠年逾耳顺方谋继室其兄谏议叵有气熖能为人致登第翃嫁【一作娉】女与璠璠为言之元昆果有所获相国韦公说即其中表甚鄙之因滑台杜尚书宅遭火防爇神柩家人云老鼠尾曳火入库内因而延燎京兆谓宇文曰鱼将化龙雷为烧尾近日老鼠亦有烧尾之事用以讥之葆光子尝试一僧备谙谬妄一旦拥徒说法自言出世安知他日不预祖系乎是则宇文翃登科后人何以知之悲夫

    Explanation

    53

    Ancestral Lineage Chart for Jinshi (Imperial Examination Degree Holders)

    In the Zen tradition, there is an ancestral lineage chart that lists those who have received the essence of the Buddha's teachings. Among the imperial examination degree holders, those who possess the talent of generals and prime ministers are all compiled in the records. However, the discrepancy between names and reality, and the mixing of the good with the bad, often misleads future generations, which is truly astonishing. During the Tang dynasty, Yuwen Hong, a scholar from a distinguished family, lacked literary talent but had a strong passion for the highest level of the imperial examinations. He had a daughter who reached the age of marriage and was truly a beauty of the state. The nobles' sons could not obtain her, and at the time, Dou Fan, who was over the age of 60 and planning to remarry, had his brother, a censor, who had influence and could help others pass the imperial examination. Yuwen Hong betrothed his daughter to Dou Fan. Dou Fan spoke about it to his elder brother, who indeed gained something. The Chancellor Wei, a relative by marriage, found this very despicable. Because of the fire at the residence of the Shu Prefect of Huaizhou, the ancestral tomb was burned. The servants said that a mouse's tail dragged the fire into the storage room, causing the fire to spread. The Governor of Jingzhao told Yuwen Hong that when a fish transforms into a dragon, lightning strikes its tail. Recently, even mice have had their tails burned. This was used to mock him. Bao Guangzi once met a monk who was well-versed in false doctrines. One day, he gathered followers and preached, claiming to have transcended the world. How can one know that he will not be included in the lineage chart in the future? Thus, how can one know that Yuwen Hong's descendants will be included in the imperial examination records? Alas!

    54

    温李齐名
    　　温庭云字飞卿或云作筠字旧名岐与李商隐齐名时号曰温李才思艳丽工于小赋每入试押官韵作赋凡八叉手而八韵成多为邻铺假手号曰救数人也而士行有缺缙绅薄之李义山谓曰近得一聨句云逺比赵公三十六年宰辅未得偶句温曰何不云近同郭令二十四考中书宣宗尝赋诗上句有金步揺未能对遣未第进士对之庭云乃以玉条脱续之宣宗赏焉又药名有白头翁温以苍耳子为对他皆此也宣宗爱唱菩萨蛮词令狐相国假其新撰密进之戒令勿泄而遽言于人由是疎之温亦有言云中书堂内坐将军讥相国无学也宣皇好微行遇于逆旅温不识龙顔傲然而诘之曰公非司马长史

    Explanation

    54

    Wen Tingyun and Li Shangyin were equally famous, and they were collectively known as "Wen and Li." Wen Tingyun, whose courtesy name was Fei Qing, was also known by the name Yu, and he was famous for his brilliant and elegant literary talents, particularly in writing short, lyrical poems. Whenever he took the imperial examinations, he could complete an eight-rhyme poem in just eight hand movements, a feat that earned him the nickname "Rescuer of Many," as he often helped others by providing them with his work. However, Wen Tingyun had moral flaws, and he was looked down upon by the literati and officials. Li Shangyin once remarked, "I recently obtained a couplet: 'Far compared to Zhao Gong, who served as chancellor for thirty-six years, I have not yet found a matching line.'" Wen Tingyun replied, "Why not say, 'Recently the same as Guo Ling, who served as chancellor for twenty-four years'?" Emperor Xuanzong once composed a poem with the line "Golden hairpin," but he could not find a fitting continuation. He asked an unsuccessful candidate to complete it, and Wen Tingyun responded with "Jade bracelet," which pleased the emperor. Another time, the emperor composed a poem that began with the medicine name "Baotouweng" (white-haired old man), and Wen Tingyun continued it with "Cang'erzi" (hedgehog seed). The emperor loved the poem "Pusamanzan" (Pusamanzan) and asked the chancellor, Dinghufu, to secretly present Wen Tingyun's new composition. He warned them not to reveal it, but they spoke of it to others, leading to Wen Tingyun's distrust. Wen Tingyun also remarked, "In the chancellery, a general sits," criticizing the chancellor's lack of learning. Emperor Xuanzong enjoyed incognito walks and once met Wen Tingyun at an inn. Wen Tingyun did not recognize the emperor's face and boldly questioned him, saying, "Are you not the Grand Marshal?"

    55

    之流帝曰非也又谓曰得非大参簿尉之帝曰非也谪为方城县尉其制词曰孔门以徳行为先文章为末尔既徳行无取文章何以补焉徒负不羁之才罕有适时之用云云竟流落而死也杜豳公自西川除淮海温庭云诣韦曲杜氏林亭留诗云卓氏垆前金线栁隋家堤畔锦帆风贪为两地行霖雨不见池莲照水红豳公闻之遗绢一千疋呉兴沈徽云温舅曾于江淮为亲表槚楚由是改名焉庭云又每嵗举场多借举人为其假手【一作多为举人假手】沈询侍郎知举别施铺席授庭云不与诸公邻比翌日前谓庭云曰向来防名者皆是文赋托于学士某今嵗场中并无假托学士勉旃因遣之由是不得意也

    Explanation

    55

    The emperor said, "No, it is not so." Then he asked again, "Is it not the case that you are one of the high-ranking officials such as Grand Counselors, Secretaries, or County Magistrates?" The emperor replied, "No, it is not so." Wen Tingyun was then demoted to be the County Magistrate of Fangcheng. The decree stated: "The Confucian school values moral conduct above all else, and considers literary talent as secondary. You, who lack moral conduct, how can your literary talent compensate for this? You merely possess exceptional talent that is not bound by convention, but you are rarely used at the right time." Thus, Wen Tingyun lived a life of wandering and eventually died.

    Du You, from the region of Western Sichuan, was appointed to the position of Governor of Huaihai. Wen Tingyun visited the Du family's garden in Weiqu and left behind a poem: "Before the tavern of the Zuo family, golden-threaded willows sway; on the dike of the Sui dynasty, the wind carries the sails of luxurious boats. Greedy to bring rain to two places, I do not see the lotus flowers reflected in the water." Du You heard this and sent a thousand bolts of silk to Wen Tingyun. Wu Xing's Shen Hui said that Wen Tingyun's uncle was once scolded by his relatives in Jianghuai, and as a result, Wen Tingyun changed his name. Wen Tingyun also often relied on other candidates to help him in the annual imperial examinations. Shen Xun, the High Official in charge of the exams, assigned Wen Tingyun to a table separate from the other scholars. The next day, before the exams began, Shen Xun told Wen Tingyun, "Those who have been guarding the names are all entrusting their essays to a scholar. This year, there are no scholars who are pretending. Please do your best." He then sent Wen Tingyun away, and as a result, Wen Tingyun was not pleased.

    56

    崔氏女失身为周宝妻【末山尼卢氏女附】
    　　浙西周宝侍中博陵崔夫人乃干符中时相之姊妹也少为女道士或云寡而冠帔自幽独焉大貂素以豪侠闻知崔有容色乃逾垣而窃之宗族亦莫知其存没尔后周除浙右其内亦至国号乃具车马偕归崔门曰昔者官职卑下未敢先言此际叨尘亦不相辱相国不得已而容之【此事鳯翔杨少尹说之甚详近代江南钟令内子乃卢肇贠外之女也乱离失身弟兄有在班行者耻之乃曰小娘子何不自杀而偶非丈夫也仙传有徐仙姑居南岳魏夫人坛羣僧调之乃自颠仆此乃修道而灵官所卫也已】　末山尼开堂说法禅师邓隐峰

    Explanation

    56

    A Woman from the Cui Family and Her Fate with Zhou Ba [With the Story of a Nun from the Lu Family Attached]

    The wife of Zhou Ba, the Chancellor of Zhexi, was a lady from the Cui family of Boling. She was the sister of the prime minister during the Dazhong period of the Tang Dynasty. When she was young, she became a female Taoist nun, or perhaps a widow who wore a crown and veil, living a secluded life. Zhou Ba was known for his boldness and chivalry. Upon learning of her beauty, he secretly took her by leaping over the wall. Her family had no knowledge of her fate. Later, when Zhou Ba rose to power in Zhexi and established his own state, he prepared a grand procession to bring her back to the Cui family. He said, "In the past, when I held a low position, I dared not speak of this matter. Now, honored with your presence, I do not wish to cause you shame. The chancellor has no choice but to accept you." [This matter was told in great detail by Yang Shao Yin, the Deputy Prefect of Fengxiang. In recent times, the wife of Zhong Ling, the magistrate of Jiangnan, was the daughter of Lu Zhao, a scholar-official. She lost her virtue due to chaos and turmoil, and her brothers, who held official positions, were shamed by it. They said, "Why didn't you commit suicide, young lady, and marry a man who is not a real man?" The Xianzhuan (Biography of Immortals) tells of Xu Xianggu, who lived on the Hengshan mountain and was teased by the monks. She fell down by herself, which was said to be protected by the spirits of the Taoist deities.] A nun from Moshan opened a hall to teach the Dharma, and the Zen master Deng Yinfeng was present.

    57

    有道者也试其所守中夜挟刃入禅堂欲行强暴尼惮死失志隐峰取去禅服集众僧以晓之其徒立散王蜀先主部将张勍暴横鞭人之胷典眉州有一少尼姿容明悟讲无量夀经张欲逼辱以死拒之不肯破戒因而诟骂张乃折其齿与其父同沈于蟇颐津也崔氏女末山尼以畏懦而茍全徐仙姑用道力而止暴讲经尼以守戒而陨命是知女子修道亦有一段障难而况冶容诲滛者哉孙棨舎人着北里志叙朝贤子弟平康狎游之事其旨似言卢相携之室女失身于外甥郑氏子遂以妻之杀家人而灭口是知平康之游亦何伤于年少之流哉
    　　崔禹昌不识牛

    Explanation

    57

    A person of virtue tests his adherence to principles, carrying a knife into a meditation hall at midnight with the intent to commit a violent act. The nun, fearing death, loses her resolve, and he takes her away to a hidden peak, removes her robe, gathers the monks to inform them, and his followers immediately disperse. During the reign of Liu Bei, his general Zhang Qiang is ruthless and tyrannical, whipping someone's chest, and governing Meizhou, there is a young nun with beautiful and wise appearance who preaches the Infinite Life Sutra. Zhang Qiang attempts to force her into breaking her vows, but she refuses and scolds him, causing him to break her teeth. He then drowns her and her father together in the waters of the Maoyi River. The daughter of the Cui family, Mo Shan Nun, preserves herself by compromising out of fear and cowardice, while Xu Priestess uses her spiritual power to stop the violence. The nun who preached the sutra dies because she upheld her vows, showing that women practicing Daoism also face certain obstacles. Thus, it is known that those who cultivate beauty to seduce others also face challenges. Sun Qi, a scholar and official, wrote North Gate Records, which describes the leisure activities of the sons of officials in the city. Its intent seems to say that the daughter of a noblewoman lost her virtue to her nephew, the son of the Zheng family, and was subsequently married to him, killing her family to cover up the scandal. It is known that the leisure activities in the city do not harm the young. Cui Yuchang did not know about oxen.

    58

    唐世梁太祖未建国前崔禹昌擢进士第有别业在汴州管内禹昌敏俊善接对初到夷门希梁祖意请陈桑梓礼梁祖甚喜以其不相轻薄甚蒙管领常预宾次或陪防戏梁祖以其有庄墅必借牛乃问曰庄中有牛否禹昌曰不识得牛意是无牛以时俗语不识得有对之梁祖大怒曰岂有人不识牛谓我是村夫即识牛渠则不识如此轻薄何由可奈防至不测后有人言方渐释怒
    　　张曙戏杜荀
    　　唐右补阙张曙吏部侍郎褧之子祎之侄文章秀丽精神敏俊甚有时称所生母常戴玉天尊黄巢乱离莫知存没或有于枯骸中头上见有玉天尊以曙未访遗骸不合进取以此阻之后于裴贽侍郎下擢进士第官至右补阙曾戏同年杜荀曰杜十四仁贤大荣幸得与张五十郎同年荀答曰张五十郎大荣幸得与荀同年天下只闻杜荀名字岂知张五十郎耶彼此大咍是知虚名不足定人优劣曙有击瓯赋其警句云董防成青琐鸾惊啄开珠网穆天子红缰马解踏破琼田又有鄠郊赋叙长安乱离亦哀江南悲甘陵之比区区之荀不足拟伦

    Explanation

    58

    In the early days before Zhu Wen founded the Later Liang dynasty, Cui Yuchang was selected as a Jinshi and had a villa in the jurisdiction of Bianzhou. Cui Yuchang was quick-witted and skilled in social interactions. When he first arrived in Bianzhou, he flattered Zhu Wen by proposing to perform the ritual of honoring his hometown. Zhu Wen was very pleased with this gesture because Cui Yuchang did not come across as overly familiar or disrespectful. He was well taken care of and often invited to be a guest at Zhu Wen's gatherings, sometimes even accompanying him in entertainment. Zhu Wen, knowing that Cui Yuchang owned a large estate, asked if he had any oxen to lend. He inquired, "Do you have any oxen in your estate?" Cui Yuchang replied, "I don't know how to handle an ox," implying that he did not have any. This was a colloquial expression meaning he did not have any oxen. Zhu Wen became very angry, saying, "How can there be someone who doesn't know how to handle an ox? Am I a village fool? If you know how to handle an ox, then I don't know how to handle one. Such disrespect is unforgivable and could lead to dire consequences." Later, when someone explained the situation, Zhu Wen gradually calmed down.

    During the Tang dynasty, Zhang Shu, a Right Censor, was the son of Liang Jiong, the Minister of Personnel, and the nephew of Yi. Zhang Shu was known for his beautiful prose and quick wit, and was highly regarded at the time. His mother, who often wore a jade Tianzun (a Taoist deity), was lost during the chaos of the Yellow Turban Rebellion. Her remains were later found, but Zhang Shu, out of respect for his mother's memory, did not seek to advance his career through the imperial examinations, which was seen as a sign of his integrity. Eventually, he passed the imperial examinations under the auspices of Pei Zhi, a high-ranking official, and became a Right Censor. Once, he playfully teased his fellow Jinshi, Du Xunhe, saying, "It is a great honor to be a Jinshi with you, Du Xunhe." Du Xunhe responded, "It is a great honor to be a Jinshi with Zhang Shu." He added, "Everyone knows of Du Xunhe's name, but who knows of Zhang Shu's?" They both laughed heartily, realizing that a false reputation is not enough to determine someone's true worth. Zhang Shu was also known for his literary works, including the Ji Oufu (击瓯赋), which contained the lines, "Dongfang Chengqing, the phoenix startled, pecking open the pearl net; the Red-Jawed Horse of the Emperor, breaking through the jade fields." He also wrote the Hu Jiao Fu (鄠郊赋), which narrated the turmoil in Chang'an and expressed sorrow for the chaos in Jiangnan and Ganling, showing that even Du Xunhe's reputation could not match his literary achievements.

    北梦琐言卷四
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷五
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　令狐公密状【木团头附】
    　　唐太和中阉官恣横因甘露事王涯等皆罹其祸竟未昭雪宣宗即位深抑其权末年尝授防于宰相令狐公公欲尽诛之虑其寃乃密奏牓子曰但有罪莫舎有阙莫填自然无遗矣后为宦者所见于是南北益相水火洎昭宗末崔侍中得行其志然而【一作以】玉石俱焚也已　干符后宫娥皆以木【一作围】头自是四方效之唯内官各自出様匠人曰斫军容头特进头至是果验也

    Explanation

    59

    Trivial Tales of the North, Volume Four
    Imperially Approved Complete Library of Four Treasuries

    Trivial Tales of the North, Volume Five
    Tang Dynasty, compiled by Sun Guangxian

    The Secret Memorial of Duke Linghu (附: Wooden Headpieces)

    During the reign of Emperor Wenzong in the Taiping era, the eunuchs acted with unrestrained power, and as a result of the Ganlu Incident, officials such as Wang Ya were all caught in the ensuing disaster and remained unexonerated. After Emperor Xuangong ascended the throne, he severely curtailed their power. In his later years, he once entrusted defense to Chancellor Linghu Gong. Duke Linghu wished to exterminate all the eunuchs but, considering their injustice, he secretly submitted a memorial, saying, "Do not spare those with crimes, do not fill vacancies, and naturally there will be no remnants left." Later, this document was seen by the eunuchs, and thus the relationship between the north and south became even more antagonistic. By the end of Emperor Zhaozong's reign, Cui Shizhong was able to carry out his wishes, but in doing so, both good and bad eunuchs were indiscriminately punished. After the Danyu period, palace ladies all wore wooden headpieces, and people from all directions imitated this trend. Only the inner officials each had their own style. Craftsmen remarked, "Chopping military heads and special heads, it turned out to be true."

    李逺讥曹唐
    　　唐进士曹唐游仙诗才情缥缈岳阳李逺贠外每吟其诗而思其人一日曹往谒之李倒屣而迎曹生人质充伟李戏之曰昔者未睹标仪将谓可乘鸾此际拜见安知壮水牛亦恐不胜其载时人闻而笑之【世谓浑诗逺赋不如不做言其无才藻鄙其无教化也】
    　　中书蕃人事
    　　李肇国史补云贞元末有郎官四人自行军司马赐紫而登粉署省中谑之为四君子也唐自大中至咸通白中令入拜相次毕相諴曹相确罗相劭权使相也继升岩廊崔相慎猷曰可以归矣近日中书尽是蕃人盖以毕白曹罗为蕃姓也始蒋伸相登庸李景逊尚书西川览报状而叹曰不能伏事斯人也遽托疾离镇有诗曰成都十万户抛若一鸿毛亦博陵之比也近代呉融侍郎乃赵崇大夫门生即世日天水叹曰本以毕白待之何乖于所望歉其不大拜也

    Explanation

    60

    Li Yuan Mocks Cao Tang
    In the Tang Dynasty, Cao Tang, a Jinshi (imperial examination graduate), was renowned for his ethereal and transcendent talent in fairy poetry. Li Yuan, a Yungwa (a type of official) from Yueyang, often recited Cao Tang's poetry and thought of him. One day, Cao Tang visited Li Yuan. Li Yuan eagerly received him, saying, "I have not yet seen your appearance, and I would have thought you worthy of riding a celestial bird. Now that I meet you, I wonder if even a strong water buffalo could bear your weight." The people of the time found this amusing. [It was said that poetry was too pure, and prose was too distant; both were deemed unnecessary, as they lacked literary brilliance and moral instruction.]

    The Affair of the Ethnic Officials in the Imperial Secretariat
    According to Li Zhao's Guoshi Bu (Supplement to the History of the Tang Dynasty), at the end of the Zhenyuan era, there were four officials who, having served as military governors, were granted purple robes and appointed to the Imperial Secretariat. They were jokingly called the "Four Gentlemen" by their colleagues. From the Dazhong era to the Xiantong era, Bai Zhongling (a title for Bai Juyi) was appointed as a chancellor, followed by Bi Xian, Cao Quan, and Luo Shao, who were also appointed as chancellors. Cui Shenyu, a chancellor, said, "It is time to retire. Recently, the Imperial Secretariat is full of ethnic officials, as Bi, Bai, Cao, and Luo are all of ethnic descent." When Jiang Shen was appointed as a chancellor, Li Jingxun, the Shangshu (a high-ranking official) of Xichuan, saw the appointment notice and sighed, "I cannot serve such people." He then feigned illness and left his post, composing a poem: "Ten thousand households in Chengdu are thrown away like a single feather." This was compared to the saying about Bo Ling. In recent times, Wu Rong, a Shilang (a type of official), was a student of Zhao Chong, a Daifu (a high-ranking official). On the day Zhao Chong passed away, Wu Rong, from Tianshui, said, "I expected to treat him as an equal, but how disappointing it is that he did not attain the highest rank."

    61

    徐相讥成中令
    　　唐干宁中荆南成令公汭曾为僧盗据渚宫寻即真命末年骋辩每事标特初以澧朗旧在巡属为土豪雷满所据奏请割相国徐公彦若在中书不为处置由是衔之相国出镇番禺路由渚宫成令虽加接延而常怏怏馔后更席而坐诡辨锋起相国曰令公位尊方面自比桓文雷满者偏州一伙草贼耳令公不能加兵而怨朝廷乎成公赧焉而屈东海文雅髙谈听之亹亹成令虽甚敬惮犹以岭外黄茅瘴患者发落而戏曰黄茅瘴望相公保重相国曰南广海黄茅瘴不死成和尚盖讥成令曽为僧也终席惭耻之

    Explanation

    61

    Translation:

    Xu Xiang Critiques Cheng Zhongling

    During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong in the late Tang Dynasty, Cheng Zhongling, a prominent figure in Jingnan, had once been a monk who seized control of a palace and was later officially recognized. In his later years, he was known for his vigorous debates and distinctive manner. Initially, the region of Li and Lang, which was under his jurisdiction, was seized by a local strongman named Lei Man. Cheng Zhongling requested that the region be transferred to the jurisdiction of Xu Yanrui, a high-ranking official, but Xu Yanrui, while serving as chancellor, did not take action on the request, leading to Cheng Zhongling's resentment. When Xu Yanrui was sent to govern Fanyu, his route passed through Cheng Zhongling's territory. Although Cheng Zhongling extended hospitality to Xu Yanrui, he was often discontent. After a meal, the seating arrangements were changed, and Cheng Zhongling engaged in sharp, deceptive argumentation. Xu Yanrui remarked, "As a high-ranking official, you compare yourself to Duke Huan of Qi and Duke Wen of Jin, yet Lei Man is merely a local bandit. How could you not use force against him if it were not for your resentment toward the court?" Cheng Zhongling was embarrassed and humbled. Xu Yanrui's refined and eloquent discourse deeply engaged Cheng Zhongling, who, despite being greatly respectful and fearful, made a playful remark about the tropical diseases prevalent in the southern regions: "May you take care of yourself, as the diseases of the south are no easy matter." Xu Yanrui humorously responded, "In the southern regions, even these diseases cannot harm a former monk." Cheng Zhongling was ultimately ashamed.

    62

    韦尚书鉴卢相
    　　唐大中初卢携举进士风貎不扬语亦不正呼携为彗【平声】盖短舌也韦氏昆弟皆轻侮之独韦岫尚书加钦谓其昆弟曰卢虽人物甚陋观其文章有首尾斯人也以是卜之他日必为大用乎尔后卢果防名竟登廊庙奬拔京兆至福建观察使向时轻薄诸弟卒不展分所谓以貎失人者其韦诸季乎
    　　薛逢赏王助
    　　唐大中初绵州魏城县人王助举进士有竒文蜀自李白陈子昻后继之者乃此侯也尝撰魏城县道观碑词华典赡于时薛逢牧绵州见而赏之以其邑子延遇因以改名助字次安壮其文王勃也自防妇刋建薛使君列衔于碑隂以光其文虽兵乱焚荡而螭首岿然好事者经过皆税驾而览之助后以瞽废无闻于世赖河东公振发増价而子孙荣之其子朴仕蜀至翰林学士

    Explanation

    62

    Translation

    Wei Shangshu Jian Lu Xiang

    During the early part of Emperor Xuanzong's reign of the Tang Dynasty, Lu Xie passed the imperial examination for the jinshi degree. He was unremarkable in appearance and had an awkward speech, which led to him being nicknamed "Hui" (comet), implying that he was a fleeting or unusual person due to his speech impediment. His brothers all mocked him, but only Wei Xi, the Shangshu (Minister), showed respect. Wei Xi said to his brothers, "Although Lu is unremarkable in character, his articles have a beginning and an end. Such a person can be predicted to achieve great things in the future." Indeed, Lu Xie eventually reached the highest levels of government, was promoted to the position of Governor of Jingzhao, and later became the Governor of Fujian. His former brothers who had mocked him never reconciled or showed favor, which is what is meant by losing people because of appearance. Is it not the case with the Wei brothers?

    Xue Feng Appreciates Wang Zhuo

    During the early part of Emperor Xuanzong's reign, a man from Weicheng County in Mianzhou, Wang Zhuo, passed the imperial examination for the jinshi degree. He had unusual and remarkable writing, continuing the legacy of Li Bai and Chen Ziang. Once, he wrote an inscription for the Daoist temple in Weicheng County, which was eloquent and well-structured. At that time, Xue Feng, who was governing Mianzhou, saw and appreciated Wang Zhuo's work. Because Wang Zhuo was from his region, Xue Feng invited and met him, and as a result, Wang Zhuo changed his name to Zhuo and his courtesy name to Cizan. Xue Feng found his writing as impressive as Wang Bo's. Wang Zhuo's mother built the inscription, and Xue Feng listed his official titles on the back of the stele to enhance the inscription. Even though there was war and destruction, the dragon-headed top of the stele remained standing. Those who appreciated such things would stop to read it. Later, Wang Zhuo became blind and disabled, and was unknown in the world. Thanks to Hedong Gong (a title for a prominent figure) who raised his status, his descendants were honored. His son, Wang Pu, served in Shu up to the position of Hanlin Scholar.

    63

    陈陶癖书
    　　大中年洪州处士陈陶者有逸才歌诗中似负神仙之术或露王霸之说虽文章之士亦未足凭而以诗见志乃宣父之遗训也其诗句云江湖水深浅不足掉鲸尾又云饮冰狼子瘦思日鹧鸪寒又云中原不是无麟凤自是皇家结网疎又云一鼎雄雌金液火十年寒暑鹿皮衣寄与东流任班向隅终守铁梭飞诸如此例不可殚记着癖书十卷闻其名而未尝见之【或云癖书是钟离从事陈岳所箸今两存之】
    　　阳朔山水
    　　王赞侍郎中朝名士有宏农杨蘧者曾到岭外见阳朔荔浦山水谈不容口以阶縁尝得接琅琊从容不形于言曰侍郎曾见阳朔茘浦山水乎琅琊曰某未曾打人唇绽齿落安得而见因之大笑杨宰俄而选求彼邑挈家南去亦州县官中一髙士也

    Explanation

    63

    Chen Tao's Obsession with Books
    During the Dazhong era, there was a recluse named Chen Tao from Hongzhou, who possessed exceptional talent. His poetry seemed to reflect either supernatural techniques or strategies of kingship and hegemony. Even scholars of literature found it difficult to fully understand his poetry, which reflected the teachings of Confucius. Some of his poems include:

    • "The depth of the river is not enough to show the might of the whale."
    • "Drinking ice, the wolf's child becomes thin; thinking of the鹧鸪, the cold day is long."
    • "The Central Plains are not devoid of dragons and phoenixes, but the royal net is too loose."
    • "A pot of male and female gold liquid fire; ten years of cold and heat in a deer skin robe. Send it to the Dong River, let Ban Gu face the corner and fly the iron shuttle."

    Yangshuo and Lipu's Natural Beauty
    Wang Zan, a famous official, had a chance encounter with Yang Qu, a scholar from Hongnong, who had visited the southern regions. Yang Qu spoke highly of the natural beauty of Yangshuo and Lipu, saying, "Have you seen the natural beauty of Yangshuo and Lipu?" Wang Zan replied, "I have never seen such beauty." They both laughed. Soon after, Yang Qu was appointed to a position in the south and moved his family there. He was also considered a high-ranking local official.

    淮浙解纷诏
    　　唐僖宗皇帝蒙尘于蜀朝士未集阙人掌诰乐朋侯翮辈虽居翰林而排难解纷之才非所长也髙太尉镇淮海拥兵不进与浙西周宝不睦表章递奏各述短长朝廷欲降诏和之学士草词殊不惬旨前进士李端有壮笔军容田令孜知之召而与语授以毫翰李仍请酒饮数杯诏书一笔而成文藻之外乃竒辩也深称上防除行在知制诰官至省郎旧说李绅相镇淮海奏荐副使章服累表不允有一举人谒绅相知其文词请撰一表其畧云当道地管八州军雄千乗副使着緑不称其宜相国大喜果以此章而获恩命也李太尉破昭义自草诏意而宣付翰林至如郑文公自草髙太尉诏皆务集事非侵局夺美也
    　　呉融天幸
    　　钱尚父始杀董昌奄有两浙得行其志士人耻之呉侍郎越州萧山县人举进士场中甚有声采屡遭维絷不遂观光乃脱身西上将及苏台界囬顾有紫绶者二人追之呉谓必遭笼罩须紫绶者殊不相顾促遽前去至一津渡唤船命呉共济比逹岸杳然失之由是获免尔后防名升朝是知分定者必有神明助之

    64

    Translation

    Imperial Edict to Resolve Conflicts in Huai and Zhe Regions

    Emperor Xizong of Tang, exiled in Shu, had not yet gathered his court officials, and there were no scholars capable of drafting imperial edicts. Although officials like Le Penggui and Hou Hei resided in the Hanlin Academy, they lacked the talent to resolve difficulties and conflicts. The high-ranking military officer stationed in Huaihai, wielding troops, did not advance and was at odds with Zhou Bao of western Zhejiang. Petitions and reports were submitted in succession, each detailing grievances. The court intended to issue an edict to mediate, but the draft by the scholar was unsatisfactory to the emperor. A promising candidate, Li Duan, known for his eloquent writing, was summoned by the military commander Tian Lingzi, who was aware of his abilities. Tian Lingzi engaged him in conversation and entrusted him with the task of drafting the edict. Li Duan requested a drink of wine, and after several cups, he completed the edict in one stroke. Beyond the elegance of his writing, he also demonstrated remarkable eloquence, earning high praise from the emperor. He was appointed as the official responsible for drafting imperial edicts during the emperor's temporary residence and eventually rose to the position of provincial official. According to tradition, Li Sen, the chancellor, had recommended a deputy with a purple robe, but the emperor repeatedly refused. One candidate, aware of Li Sen's literary skills, requested him to draft a memorial. The memorial stated: "The region under your command oversees eight states, with a powerful military force. A deputy wearing a purple robe is not appropriate for the position." The chancellor was pleased and indeed granted the candidate an imperial favor. The general who defeated the rebels of Zhaoyi drafted the imperial edict himself and submitted it to the Hanlin Academy. Similarly, Zheng Wengong drafted an edict for the high-ranking military officer, all aiming to achieve their objectives without overstepping their roles.

    Fate and Fortune: The Tale of Wu Rong

    Qian Shangfu, the warlord, began by killing Dong Chang and gained control over the two Zhe regions, fulfilling his ambitions. However, people were ashamed of his actions. Wu Lang, a scholar from Xiaoshan County in Yue Prefecture, had a reputation for his literary skills in the imperial examinations but was repeatedly detained and could not pursue his studies. He managed to escape westward, nearing the boundary of Suzhou, when he looked back and saw two officials with purple robes chasing him. Wu believed he would be captured and decided to avoid them by not turning around. He hurried forward and reached a ferry, where he called for a boat and asked Wu to join him. Upon reaching the shore, the pursuers were nowhere to be seen. Thus, he escaped. Later, he was appointed to a high official position, demonstrating that those whose fate is determined are aided by divine intervention.

    沈蒋人物
    　　沈询侍郎清粹端美神仙中人也制除山北节旄京城诵曹唐游仙诗云玉诏新除沈侍郎便分茅土领东方不知今夜游何处侍从皆骑白鳯凰即风姿可知也蒋凝侍郎亦有人物每到朝士家人以为祥瑞号水月观音前代潘安仁卫叔宝何以加此唐末朝士中有人物者时号玉笋班【沈询字仁伟官至丞郎人物酷似先徳所谓世济其美又外郎班者棨不杂亦号玉笋班也】
    　　张濬乐朋与田军容中外事
    　　旧例士子不与内官交游十军军容田令孜擅囬天之力僖皇播迁行至洋源百官未集阙人掌诰乐朋侍郎亦及行在因谒中尉仍请中外由是荐之充翰林学士张濬相自处士除起居郎亦出子方之门皆申【一作由】中外之敬洎车驾到蜀朝士毕集一日中尉为宰相开筵学士洎张起居同预焉张公耻于对众设拜乃先

    Explanation

    65

    Notable Figures from the Shen and Jiang Families

    Shen Xun, the Lang, was exceptionally refined and beautiful, a person among immortals. He was appointed to a high position in the northern mountains, and in the capital, people recited the immortal poetry of Cao Tang, saying, "The imperial edict newly appoints Shen Lang, who then divides the land and leads the east. Where does he roam tonight? His attendants all ride white phoenixes, revealing his divine appearance." Jiang Ning, the Lang, was also a notable figure. Whenever he appeared, the officials and their families regarded it as an auspicious omen, calling him the Water Moon Guanyin. The ancient figures Pan Anren and Wei Shubao could not compare to him. In the late Tang dynasty, there were distinguished officials known as the Jade Bamboo Class (玉笋班), among whom Shen Xun, with his character resembling that of his ancestors, was said to have continued their excellence. The Jade Bamboo Class was also known for its elegance and refinement.

    Zhang Jun, Le Penggui, and Tian Lingzi and Their Involvement in Internal and External Affairs

    According to an old rule, scholars were not supposed to associate with eunuchs. Tian Lingzi, the military commander, possessed immense power, likened to the ability to reverse the heavens. During the reign of Emperor Xizong, the emperor relocated to Yangyuan, and the officials had not yet gathered, with a lack of someone to handle official documents. Le Penggui, the Lang, also reached the emperor's location and visited the eunuch, requesting matters both internal and external. As a result, he was recommended to serve as a scholar in the Hanlin Academy. Zhang Jun, the chancellor, was promoted from a hermit to a court official, also emerging from the school of Zi Fang, and all showed respect for both internal and external matters. When the emperor arrived in Shu, the officials gathered. One day, the eunuch hosted a banquet for the chancellor, and scholars and Zhang Jun were both invited. Zhang Jun, embarrassed by the presence of others, decided to bow first.

    66

    谒中尉便施谢酒之敬中尉讶之俄而宾主即席坐定中尉白诸相曰某与起居清浊异流曾蒙中外既虑玷辱何惮改更今日猥地谢酒即又不可张公惭惧交集自此甚为羣彦薄之乐公举进士初陈启事谒李昭侍郎自媒云别于九经书及老庄洎八都赋外着八百卷书请垂比试诚有学问也然于制诰不甚简当时人或未可之
    　　薛少师拒中外事
    　　唐薛廷珪少师右族名流仕于衰世梁太祖兵力日强朝廷倾动渐自尊大天下惧之孤卿为四镇官告使夷门客将刘翰先来防恐申中外孤卿佯言不防谓谒者曰某无徳安敢輙受令公拜竟不为屈洎受禅之后勉事于梁而太祖优容之夀考而终也中间奉命册蜀先主为司徒馆中旧疾发动蜀人送当医人杨仆俾攻疗之孤卿致书感谢其书末请借肩舆归京寻医蜀主讶之乃曰幸有方药何

    Explanation

    66

    A visit to the Central Commander to show respect through the offering of wine surprised the Central Commander. Soon after, the host and guests took their seats. The Central Commander said to the other officials, "I and the others have different social standings. I have already been honored by both the inner and outer courts; how could I be afraid of changing? Today, in a humble position, offering wine is not appropriate." Zhang Gong was filled with shame and fear. From then on, he was greatly disrespected by the scholarly elite.

    Le Gong, when he first took the imperial examination, submitted a petition to Li Zhaoshi, a high-ranking official, and recommended himself. He wrote, "Except for the Nine Classics, the Laozi and Zhuangzi, and the Eight Capital Assignments, I wrote eight hundred volumes of books. Please allow me to be tested, for I truly have knowledge." However, he was not very simple in his official documents, and some people of the time did not approve of it.

    The story of Xue Shao, the Junior Tutor, rejecting the inner and outer courts: During the late Tang Dynasty, Xue Tinggui, the Junior Tutor, was a prominent figure from a noble family who served during a declining era. The First Emperor of Later Liang, Li Keyong, grew stronger in military power, causing the court to be shaken and gradually become more arrogant, which made the whole world fear him.

    Xue Tinggui, as the envoy for the four commanderies, was approached by Liu Han, a guest officer from Yimen, who came to prevent him from submitting to the inner and outer courts. Xue Tinggui pretended not to know and told the attendant, "I am unworthy; how dare I accept the Grand Marshal's obeisance?" He refused to bow. After accepting the throne, he served Later Liang with dedication, and the First Emperor of Later Liang treated him with leniency, allowing him to live a long life until his death.

    During this period, he was ordered to confer the title of Grand Tutor on the First Emperor of Shu. His old illness flared up in the palace, and the people of Shu sent a doctor named Yang Pu to treat him. Xue Tinggui wrote a letter of thanks, and at the end of the letter, he asked for a sedan chair to return to the capital to seek medical treatment. The First Emperor of Shu was surprised and said, "Fortunately, there is effective medicine."
