    不俟愈而行坚请且驻行轩公谓客将曰夜来问此医官殊不识字安可以性命委之乎竟不服药而北归后唐相国韦公说仕梁为中书舎人倅轺于钱塘先是钱尚父自据一方每要姑息梁主以河北关西悉为勍敌又频失利于淮海甚借两浙牵掎之其次又资贡赋凡命使臣逺泛沧溟一则希其丰遗二则惧不周旋悉皆拜之钱公亦自尊大唯京兆公长揖而已既不辱命识者异之竟有岩廊之拜也
    　　杨晟义母【安师建附】
    　　唐杨晟始事凤翔节度李昌符累立军功因而疑之潜欲加害昌符爱妾周氏愍其无辜密告之由是亡去而获免也后为驾前五十四军都指挥使除威胜军节度使建节于彭州抚绥士民延敬宾客洎僧道辈各得其所厚于礼敬人甚懐之李昌符之败因令求访周氏既至以义母事之周氏自以少年复有美色恐有好合之请宏农

    Explanation

    67

    Without waiting for recovery, he firmly requested and stopped the carriage. The official said to the envoy, "Last night, when I asked this doctor, he was completely illiterate. How can I entrust my life to him?" Eventually, he did not take medicine and returned north.

    Wang Jian served in the Later Liang as a Censor of the Secretariat and served as an assistant to the governor in Qiantang (Hangzhou). Before that, Wang Jian had established himself in one region. He often had to tolerate the Later Liang ruler because the regions north of the Yellow River and west of the pass were powerful enemies. He also frequently suffered defeats in the Huai River and Yangtze River area, which greatly relied on the Two Zhe regions for support and tribute. Whenever envoys were sent far across the vast sea, they hoped for generous gifts and feared not being treated properly, so they all bowed to him. Those who understood it found it remarkable. Eventually, he received a high-ranking position in the imperial court.

    Yang Sheng, the Adopted Mother [An Shi Jian Attached]

    During the Tang Dynasty, Yang Sheng initially served under Li Changfu, the military governor of Fengxiang, and repeatedly established military achievements. However, Li Changfu began to suspect him and secretly intended to harm him. Li Changfu's beloved concubine, Zhou, pitied Yang Sheng's innocence and secretly informed him. Thus, Yang Sheng managed to escape and was saved. Later, he became the commander of the Fifty-Fourth Army and was appointed as the military governor of Weisheng Commandery, establishing his command in Pengzhou. He governed the people with kindness and invited respected guests, including monks and Taoists, treating them with great courtesy. The people deeply revered him. After Li Changfu's defeat, he ordered the search for Zhou, who was then treated as a mother figure. Zhou, being young and beautiful, feared that there might be inappropriate requests, so she remained cautious.

    68

    告誓天地终不以非礼偶之每旦未视事前必伸问安之礼虽厄在重围未尝废也新理之所兵力未完遽为王蜀先主攻围保守孤城救兵不至十日而为西川所破而害焉有马步使安师建者杨氏之腹心也城克执之蜀先主知其忠烈冀为其用欲寛之师建曰某受杨司徒提拔不敢惜死先主叹【一作嗟】赏而行戮为设祭而之
    　　成令公和州载
    　　唐天祐中淮师围武昌不解杜洪令公乞师于梁王梁王与荆方睦乃讽成令帅兵救之于是禀奉霸主欲亲征乃以巡属五州事力造巨舰一艘三年而成号曰和州载舰上列防事洎司局有衙府之制又有齐山截海之名其于华壮即可知也饰非拒谏断自其意幕寮俛仰不措一词唯孔目官杨厚赞成之舟次破军山下为呉师纵燎而焚之中令溺死兵士溃散先是改名曰汭汭字即水内也水内之死岂非前兆乎湖南及朗州军入江陵俘载军人百姓职掌伎巧僧道伶官并归长沙改汭之名和州之说盖前定也

    Explanation

    68

    Translation:

    He swore to heaven and earth that he would never enter into an improper match. Every morning before attending to his duties, he would perform the ritual of asking for well-being. Even when besieged, he never neglected these rituals. The newly established regime's military forces were not yet fully prepared, and it was suddenly attacked by the ruler of Shu (Liu Bei) on a besieged city. The rescue forces did not arrive in time, and the city was destroyed within ten days, leading to the death of the commander. There was a horse and foot officer named An Shijian, who was a trusted advisor to Yang. When the city was captured, he was taken prisoner. The ruler of Shu, knowing his loyalty and valor, hoped to use him and wished to treat him leniently. An Shijian said, "I have been promoted by Yang, the Grand Tutor, and dare not hesitate to die." The ruler sighed and executed him, setting up a memorial service and burying him.

    Cheng Lingong and the Hezhou Zai

    During the Tianyou period of the Tang Dynasty, the Huai army besieged Wuchang without relief. Du Hong, the official, requested assistance from the King of Liang. The King of Liang, being friendly with Jingzhou, advised Cheng to lead troops to rescue. Following the hegemon's desire to personally lead the campaign, he ordered the construction of a large ship using resources from five prefectures. It took three years to complete, and it was named "Hezhou Zai." The ship was equipped with defensive measures and had a structure resembling a government office, and it was also named "Qishan Jiehai," meaning "Cutting through the Sea." Its splendor and grandeur can be imagined. He concealed faults and rejected advice, making decisions based on his own will. The officials in the government were unable to speak up, and only the clerk Yang Hou supported him. The ship was attacked and burned by Wu forces at Pujun Mountain, leading to the drowning of the commander and the scattering of the soldiers. Previously, the name was changed to "Rui," which means "inside the water," and his death in the water was seen as a premonition. The armies of Hunan and Langzhou entered Jingzhou, capturing soldiers, civilians, and various officials, leading them to Changsha. Changing the name "Rui" and the story of "Hezhou Zai" were all predestined.

    69

    韦太尉伐西川
    　　唐陈敬瑄据成都府拒命韦太尉昭度充招讨使率东川兵以伐之王蜀先主时为草贼剽掠诸县乃拥守下兵投掌武署为衙内指挥使资其爪牙也因奏请割西川数州就临邛建节以授之蜀主卑谦多智事韦公甚谨掌武量其事势终不能驾御况军旅之事又非所长每欲攻城请戎服临阵虑矢石所及不敢近前掌武曰军人安敢无礼东川都显有唐吃人者呼而戒之曰人肉何如猪羊乃赐一缗俾充肉价他皆仿此重围二年蜀城已困不日将下一旦门外諠哗以军粮阙乏兵士擒曳掌武亲吏骆别驾【忘名】者脔而噉之由是惧罹其祸遽托疾以西川牌印付蜀主而归朝虽曰不武斯亦用智自免也

    Explanation

    69

    Wei Zhaodu, the Imperial High Commissioner, led an expedition against Western Shu. During the Tang Dynasty, Chen Jingxuan occupied Chengdu and defied the central government. Wei Zhaodu was appointed as the Imperial High Commissioner to lead the campaign against him, mobilizing troops from Eastern Shu. At that time, Wang Shu, the future founder of the Shu Kingdom, was a bandit leader who had been plundering various counties. He rallied his troops and submitted to Wei Zhaodu, becoming the Commander of the Inner Guard and serving as one of Wei Zhaodu's key lieutenants. Wang Shu then petitioned to be granted control over several states in Western Shu, with authority established in the region of Linjiang.

    Wang Shu was known for his humility and wisdom, and he served Wei Zhaodu with great caution. However, Wei Zhaodu realized that Wang Shu could not effectively manage military affairs, as this was not his strength. Whenever Wei Zhaodu planned to attack a city, he would request to wear military attire and lead the troops into battle, but he feared being hit by arrows or stones and would not approach the front lines. Wei Zhaodu would then say, "How could soldiers dare to be disrespectful?" He would call out to a notorious figure from Eastern Shu known as "Tang the Human-Eater" and warn him, saying, "How is human flesh different from pork or mutton?" He would then give the figure one thousand coins to compensate for the "meat price," and others would follow this example.

    After two years of siege, the city of Shu was already in dire straits and would soon fall. One day, there was a commotion outside the city gates, as the troops were running out of food. A soldier seized and dragged one of Wei Zhaodu's close aides, Cao the Magistrate, and cut him into pieces, eating him. Fearing that he would suffer the same fate, Wei Zhaodu feigned illness and handed over the banner of Western Shu to Wang Shu, returning to the imperial court. Although he was not known for his bravery, he had used his intelligence to save himself.

    70

    章鲁封不幸
    　　屯难之世君子遭遇不幸往往有之唐进士章鲁封与罗隐齐名皆浙中人频举不第声采甚着钱尚父土豪倔起号钱塘八都洎破董昌奄有杭越于是章罗二士罹其笼罩然其出于草莱未谙事体重县宰而轻郎官尝曰某人非才只可作郎官不堪作县令即可知也以章鲁封为表奏孔目官章拒而见笞差罗隐宰钱塘皆畏死禀命也章罗以之为耻钱公用之为荣【一作禁】玉石俱焚吁可惜也或云章鲁封后典苏州着章子三卷行于世罗隐为中朝所重钱公寻倍加钦官至给事中享夀考温饱而卒
    　　裴氏再行【归登尚书附】
    　　唐裴司徒璩性靳啬亷问江西日凡什器圗障皆新其制闭屋缄贮未尝施用每有宴防即于朝士家借之在番禺时钟爱一女选荥阳郑进士以壻之才过礼期遽属秋荐不免随计无何到京寻报物故五教念女及壻不胜悲痛而郑偶笑之盖夫妇之爱未深不解思虑非有他故也大凡士族女郎无改醮之礼五教念女早寡不能忘情乃召门

    Explanation

    70

    Translation

    Zhang Lufeng's Misfortune

    In times of great difficulty, it is often the case that gentlemen encounter misfortune. During the late Tang Dynasty, the Jinshi Zhang Lufeng, who was renowned alongside Luo Yin, both from Zhejiang, frequently failed the imperial examinations despite their fame. The powerful warlord Qian Chu, known as "Qian Shangfu," rose to prominence and controlled the eight districts of Qiantang. After defeating Dong Chang, he completely occupied Hangzhou and Yue. Thus, Zhang and Luo were caught in his net. However, they came from humble origins and were not familiar with the affairs of the world. They valued county magistrates more than imperial court officials, once saying, "Such a person is not capable of being a county magistrate, only fit to be an imperial court official." Consequently, Zhang Lufeng was appointed as a low-ranking official responsible for drafting and managing official documents. He refused and was beaten. Luo Yin was appointed as the magistrate of Qiantang and obeyed orders out of fear of death. Zhang and Luo considered this a disgrace, while Qian Chu took pride in it. Both good and bad were destroyed together; alas, how pitiful! It is said that later, Zhang Lufeng served as the governor of Suzhou and wrote three volumes titled Zhangzi, which circulated in the world. Luo Yin was highly regarded by the imperial court, and Qian Chu eventually appointed him as a high-ranking official, the Grand Secretary, and he lived a comfortable life until his death.

    The Second Marriage of the Pei Family (with the addition of Guī Dēng Shàngshū)

    Pei Qiu, the Duke of Jin, was frugal and meticulous. During his time in Jiangxi, he kept all household items and books sealed and stored, never using them. Whenever there was a banquet, he would borrow them from officials' homes. In Fanyu, he had a daughter whom he deeply loved and chose Zheng Jinshi of荥yang as her husband. However, due to the urgency of the autumn recommendation, he could not avoid the examination. Soon after arriving in the capital, he received news of his father's death. The five teachings (five moral principles) dictated that his daughter and her husband were overwhelmed with grief, but Zheng, the husband, laughed, indicating a lack of deep affection. Generally, women from noble families do not remarry after their husbands' deaths. The daughter, being young and unable to forget her feelings, summoned the doorkeeper to arrange a second marriage.

    71

    生故吏而告之因【一作曰】别适人乱伦再醮自河东始也元祯【一作顽】少监苏涯中丞赐紫杨玭少尹与五教亲吏别驾说皆同　归登尚书每浴皆屏左右自于浴斛中坐移时或有窥者见一巨吹水也性甚鄙啬尝烂一羊脾旋割旋噉封其残者一旦内子于封处割食八座不见元封大怒其内由是没身不食肉斯亦愈于和峤之流也
    　　闭门避蛮【王先主附】
    　　西川自唐刘辟搆逆后久无干戈人不习战每嵗诸道差兵屯戍大渡河蛮旗才举望风而溃咸通中长驱直抵府城居人有扃户而拒之蛮亦不敢扣门也尝有一蛮迷路入广都县村墅里人相率数百辈呌噪而逐之蛮一囬顾却走如堵墙崩焉自昼及暝终不能擒致其怯懦如此　王蜀先主时云南冦蜀蜀军勇锐欲吞之俘擒噉食不以为敌与向前之兵百倍其勇也
    　　髙太尉机诈

    Explanation

    71

    A Former Official Informed Him [or: A Former Official Told Him] that Remarriage Involving Incestuous Relations Began in Hedong (河东). Yuán Zhēn (元祯), a Junior Supervisor (少监), Sū Yá (苏涯), a Middle Chancellor (中丞) granted purple robes, Yáng Pín (杨玭), a Junior County Magistrate (少尹), and the Five Teachings' close officials, including the Chief of the County (别驾), all agreed. Guī Dēng (归登), a Grand Secretary (尚书), always cleared the area around him when bathing and sat in a large basin for a while. Sometimes, someone peeping saw a giant turtle blowing water. He was very stingy in nature. Once he spoiled a lamb's liver, cut it, and ate it immediately, sealing the leftovers. One day, his wife cut and ate the sealed leftovers, and he became very angry, leading him to never eat meat again. This is better than the likes of He Qiao.

    Closing Doors to Avoid Barbarians [Wang Xianzhu Attached]

    Western Sichuan (西川) has been free from war since the rebellion of Liu Pi (刘辟) after the Tang dynasty. People are not accustomed to fighting. Each year, troops are sent to garrison at the Dadu River (大渡河). As soon as the barbarian flag is raised, they flee at the sight of it. During the Xiantong period (咸通), the barbarians advanced directly to the city, and the residents closed their doors to resist, and the barbarians did not dare to knock on the doors. Once, a barbarian got lost and entered Guangdu County (广都县). Hundreds of villagers chased him, and as soon as he turned back, he fled like a collapsing wall. From morning till night, they could not capture him, showing how cowardly he was. During the reign of Wang Xianzhu (王先主), the Yunnan barbarians invaded Sichuan. The Sichuan army was brave and eager to conquer them, capturing and eating them without regarding them as enemies, showing a hundredfold increase in courage compared to before.

    High Magistrate's Cunning Deceit

    72

    咸通中南蛮围西川朝廷命太尉渤海髙公骈自天平军移镇成都戎车未届乃先以帛书军号其上仍画一符于邮亭递之以壮军声蛮酋惩交趾之败望驿【一作铎】而遁先是府无罗郭南冦才临遂成煨烬士民无久安之计渤海规画地势圗版筑焉虑畚锸将施亭堠有警乃命山僧景山【此僧多为掌武决防人谓是厐勋漏网而变名也】奉使入南诏宣言骈自巡邉自下手筑城日举烽直至大渡河凡九十三日楼橹矗然旌斾竟不行而骠信詟栗不暇兵以诈胜斯之谓也
    　　张道古题墓
    　　唐天复中张道古沧州蒲台县人擢进士第拜左补阙文学甚富介僻不羣因上五危二乱表左授施掾尔后入蜀先是所陈二乱疏云只今刘备孙权已生于世矣惧为蜀主所憾无路栖托洎逢开创诚思征召为幕寮排摈卒不齿録竟罹非命也尝自筮遇凶卦预造一穴题表云唐左补阙张道古墓后果遇害而瘗之人有获其上蜀主书遗藁极言幕寮掩其才学不为延誉又非违【一作逹】时变盘桓取祸之流也【补阙深于彖象著书号易题数卷行于世】

    Explanation

    72

    During the Xiantong period, the southern barbarians surrounded the Western Shu region. The court ordered Grand Marshal Gao Pian, Duke of Bohai, to move from Tianping Army to govern Chengdu. Before the military vehicles arrived, he first wrote military orders on silk banners, drew a symbol on them, and posted them at post stations to boost morale. The Nanzhao chieftain, having been punished by the defeat at Jiaozhi, fled upon seeing the post station. Previously, the city had no outer walls; when the southern invaders arrived, it was quickly reduced to ashes. The common people had no long-term plan for safety. Duke Gao planned the layout, drew maps, and began construction. Worried that the construction would be disrupted, he ordered the monk Jingshan to enter Nanzhao on a mission. He declared that Gao was personally inspecting the border and personally overseeing the construction of the city, raising beacons all the way to the Dadu River. In 93 days, the city walls rose, and the flags did not move; the Nanzhao army was too frightened to act. This is what it means to win through deception.

    Zhang Daogu's Epitaph

    During the Tianfu period of the Tang dynasty, Zhang Daogu from Putaixian, Cangzhou, was promoted to the position of Left Censor after passing the imperial examination. He was highly learned but eccentric and aloof. He submitted a memorial on five dangers and two disorders and was demoted to serve as a magistrate in Shizhou. Afterward, he went to Shu (modern Sichuan). In his earlier memorial, he said that Liu Bei and Sun Quan have already been born in this world. He feared being resented by the Shu ruler and had no place to settle. When the new dynasty began, he hoped to be summoned to serve in the court but was rejected and ultimately met a tragic fate. He once divined an ominous hexagram and prepared a tomb, inscribing it as the grave of Zhang Daogu, Left Censor of the Tang dynasty. Indeed, he was later killed and buried. Someone found a letter from the Shu ruler, criticizing the officials for concealing his talents and not recommending him, and saying that he was a person who clung to the past and brought disaster upon himself. (The Left Censor was deeply knowledgeable in the I Ching and wrote several volumes titled Yi Ti, which were circulated in the world.)

    叙巢居子
    　　唐贞元中秭归人覃正夫顷栖庐岳帅符载征召为文竟汨没于巴巫也或有以其文数篇示愚辞韵挺特风调凛然真得武都之刀尺也号巢居子有二十卷愚因致书于归州之衙校李玩俾搜访之书未逹前三日里人有家藏全集者适遇延爇而煨烬之嗟乎鄙于覃生异时也茍得缮写流布振彼声光而焚如之酷何不幸之甚也
    　　罗衮不就西川辟【李频黄匪躬附】
    　　唐罗贠外衮成都临邛人应进士举文学优赡操尚甚髙唐大顺中防名不归故乡时属丧乱朝廷多故契濶兵难备歴饥寒蜀先主致书于翰林令狐学士呉侍郎选书记一贠欲以桂阳应聘外郎谓知己曰誓拥马通衢服弊布衣以俟外朝无复西归为鲁国东家丘也【一作乎】竟通朝籍终于梁礼部贠外郎也蜀人有志者唯外郎乎扬子云二息亡遗体于蜀与夫延陵季子何相逺哉近代李频黄匪躬皆岭表人频即遗其糟糠别婚士族黄即三十年不返乡里于时妻母俱在又何心乎

    73

    Translation

    Preface to the Collection of Chaogujizi

    During the Zhenyuan period of the Tang Dynasty, there was a man from Zigui named Tan Zhengfu, who lived in the mountains of Lushan. He was summoned by a high-ranking official, Fu Zai, to write for him, but he eventually disappeared in the regions of Ba and Wu. Someone once showed me a few of his writings, which had a unique style and a severe yet dignified tone, truly embodying the craftsmanship of Wudu's knife and ruler. He was given the title "Chaogujizi," and his collection consisted of twenty volumes. I wrote to Li Wan, an official in the prefectural administration of Guizhou, asking him to search for the collection. However, three days before the letter reached him, a local resident who had a complete set of his works accidentally set fire to them, burning them to ashes. Alas, if I had been able to transcribe and disseminate them, it would have brought glory to his reputation. What a great misfortune!

    Luo Gun's Refusal of the Appointment in Western Sichuan [with Appendices on Li Pin and Huang Fegong]

    Luo Gun, an official from Chengdu, was a native of Linqiong. He took the imperial examination for the jinshi degree and was known for his excellent literary skills and high moral character. During the Dashi period of the Tang Dynasty, after passing the examination, he did not return home. At a time of chaos and disorder, the court was full of troubles, and he faced military hardships, enduring all kinds of poverty and cold. The ruler of Shu sent a letter to the Hanlin Academy, asking the scholar-official Lühu and the junior minister Wu to select one person to serve as a secretary and appoint him as a junior minister in the region of Guiyang. Luo Gun, addressing his close friend, said, "I swear to block the main road with horses, wear ragged clothes, and wait for the imperial court. I will no longer return west; I will be like the Eastern neighbor of Confucius." Eventually, he became a member of the imperial court and died as a junior minister of the Rites Department in the Later Liang Dynasty. In Shu, the only person with ambition was this junior minister. Yang Xiong's two sons died, leaving no heir, and he was buried in Shu. How far is this from the example of Master Ji of Yanling? In recent times, Li Pin and Huang Fegong were both from the southern regions. Li Pin abandoned his wife and married into a noble family, while Huang did not return home for thirty years, during which his wife and mother were still alive. How could he have the heart to do so?

    74

    髙测启事【韩昭附】
    　　唐髙测彭州人聪明博识文翰纵横至于天文厯数琴棊书画长笛胡琴率皆精巧乃梁朝朱异之流尝谒髙燕公上启事自序其要云读书万卷饮酒百杯燕公曰万卷书不易征诘【一作不暇征召】百杯酒得以奉试乃饮以酒果如所言僖皇帝幸蜀因进所著书除秘校卒于威胜军节度判官也　韩昭仕蜀至礼部尚书文思殿大学士粗有文章至于琴棊书算射法悉皆涉猎以此承恩于后主时有朝士李台嘏曰韩八座事艺如拆袜线无一条长时人韪之

    Explanation

    74

    Gao Ce's Memorial [with Han Zhao's Commentary]

    Gao Ce of Pengzhou was a man of great intelligence and broad knowledge, his literary skills extensive and versatile. He was skilled in astronomy and calendar calculations, as well as the four traditional arts: playing the zither, chess, painting, and calligraphy. He was also adept at playing the flute and the huqin. He was compared to Zhu Yi of the Liang dynasty. Once, he paid homage to Gao Yan and presented a memorial, in which he summarized his abilities: "I have read ten thousand volumes and can drink a hundred cups." Gao Yan said, "Ten thousand volumes are not easily verified [or, 'one does not have time to verify']; but a hundred cups of wine can be tested." He then offered Gao Ce wine, and indeed, Gao Ce drank a hundred cups as he claimed. Later, when Emperor Xian of the Han dynasty fled to Shu, Gao Ce presented his writings to the court and was appointed to the position of Secretarial Officer. He died while serving as the Military Governor's Secretary in Weisheng.

    Han Zhao, who served in Shu, reached the rank of Minister of Rites and Grand Master of the Palace of Literary Thought. He had some literary talent, but his skills were varied and not particularly strong, like a sock's thread that has no single strong strand. At the time, a court official named Li Taigao said, "Han the Eighth Seat's skills and arts are like the threads of a sock—none of them are particularly strong." Contemporaries agreed with this assessment.

    75

    符载侯翮归隐【赵防附】
    　　唐武都符载字厚之本蜀人有竒才始与杨衡宋济栖青城山以习业杨衡擢进士第宋济老死无成唯符公以王霸自许耻于常调懐防之望韦南康镇蜀辟为支使虽曰受知尚多偃蹇韦公于二十四化设醮请撰斋词于时陪饮于摩诃之池符公离席盥潄命使院小吏十二人捧砚人分两题绕【一作缓】步池滨各授口占其敏速如此刘辟时为金吾仓曹参军依栖韦公特与譔真赞其词云矫矫化初气杰文雄灵螭出水秋鹗乗风行义则固辅仁乃通他年良觌麟阁之中洎京兆变故彭城知留务起雄据之意符为其

    Explanation

    75

    Fu Zai (符载), originally from Shu, was a man of extraordinary talent. He initially associated with Yang Heng and Song Ji, residing in Qingcheng Mountain to study. Yang Heng was promoted to the rank of Jinshi (进士), while Song Ji died old without achieving anything. Only Fu Gong (符公) considered himself capable of great achievements and was ashamed of routine appointments, holding high aspirations. Wei Nankang (韦南康), while governing Shu, appointed him as a deputy officer. Although he was recognized, he still behaved haughtily. Wei Gong set up an alchemical ritual to invite him to write a斋词 (斋词) at the Maha Pool. Fu Gong accompanied by drinking at the Maha Pool, left the table to wash his hands and mouth, and ordered twelve clerks to hold the inkstone. Each person took turns walking around the pool and recited poetry on the spot, praising his quick and agile nature. Liu Pi (刘辟) was a military officer at the time and relied on Wei Gong. He especially asked Fu Gong to write a true praise, which read: "Majestic and powerful, with a noble and heroic spirit, like a dragon emerging from the water and an eagle riding the wind. Acting with righteousness is firm, assisting benevolence is smooth. In the future, meeting in the Hall of the Unicorns. When the troubles in Jingzhao occurred, Pengcheng appointed him to a temporary post, arising the intention to dominate. Fu Gong for him."

    76

    所縻凡有代奏愈更恭顺刘辟之败也幕寮多罹其祸唯符生以牋奏藁草一箧呈髙崇文相公长揖东下栖于庐山即前之真赞可谓有先鉴也居浔阳二林间优游卒嵗南昌军奏请为副倅授奉礼郎不赴命小僮持一幅上于襄阳乞百万钱买山四方交辟羔鴈盈于山门草堂中以女妓二十人娯侍声名籍甚于时守道循常者号曰凶人【曾览符公全集其文简举清便入其堂奥者唯建平覃正夫耳至宋济虽有词学其文冗泛非符之流湛贲卒于彭山宰墓铭即宋文也】唐光啓中成都人侯翮风仪端秀有若氷壶以拔

    Explanation

    76

    In all the matters he handled, he was even more submissive and respectful, especially during Liu Pi's defeat. Many officials in the office suffered the disaster, but only Fu Sheng presented a box of rough drafts of his memorials to Gao Chongwen, the chancellor, and then respectfully departed. He lived in seclusion on Mount Lu, and it can be said that he had foresight, as evidenced by the previous true praise. He lived comfortably in the two forests of Jixian and passed the year there. The army of Nanchang requested him to serve as a deputy and be appointed as a ritual official, but he did not accept the appointment. A young servant carried a scroll and presented it to Xiangyang, asking for a million coins to buy a mountain. People from all directions invited him, and his door was filled with offerings. In his thatched cottage, he had twenty female entertainers to serve and entertain him. His reputation was very famous at the time, and those who adhered to the right path and followed conventions were called wicked people. [I once read the complete works of Fu Gong. His writing is concise and elegant, entering the inner chambers of his art. Only Jianping Tan Zhengfu could truly appreciate it. As for Song Ji, though he had literary talent, his writing was verbose and superficial, not in the same league as Fu's. Zhan Ben died in the tomb inscription of Pengshan, which is written in the style of Song.] During the Guangqi period of the Tang Dynasty, there was a man named Hou He from Chengdu. He had a dignified and beautiful appearance, like an ice pot, and was selected or promoted.

    77

    萃出身为邠宁从事僖皇播迁擢拜中书舎人翰林学士内试数题目其词立就旧族朝士潜推服之僖宗归阙除郡不赴归隐导江别墅号卧龙馆王蜀先主圗霸屈致幕府先俾节度判官冯防【一作俟】其可否冯有文章大名除眉州刺史田令孜拒朝命不放之任羇寓成都为侯公轸防甚徳之其辞【一作辟】书即冯防极笔也侯有谢上王先主其自负云可以行脩牋表坐了檄书【其先人蜀之小将也】　赵防者梓州盐亭县人也博学韬钤长于经世夫妇俱有节操不受交辟撰长短经十卷王霸之道见行于世

    Explanation

    77

    Cui, who came from a family of officials in Binning, served as a subordinate during the displacement of Emperor Xian. He was later promoted to the positions of Zhongshu Shèrén and Hanlin Xueshi, and was able to complete several test questions immediately during an imperial examination. The old aristocratic scholars secretly admired him. After Emperor Xian returned to the capital, he was appointed to a prefecture but did not take up the post. Instead, he retired to a villa in Daojiang and named it "Wulong Pavilion." When Wang Jian, who sought to establish a base in Sichuan, wanted to invite Cui to join his entourage, he first sent his chief secretary Feng Fang to assess Cui's suitability. Feng Fang, known for his literary talent, wrote the letter inviting Cui. Cui stayed in Chengdu and was highly respected by Hou Gong Zhen. Hou Gong Zhen wrote a letter of thanks to Wang Jian, expressing his confidence in his ability to draft official documents and memorials.

    Zhao Fang, from Yanting County in Zizhou, was well-versed in military strategy and practical governance. Both he and his wife had strong moral principles and did not accept invitations from other officials. He wrote ten volumes of "The Long and Short Strategies," which discussed the principles of kingship and hegemony and were widely circulated.

    78

    北梦琐言卷五
    <子部,小说家类,杂事之属,北梦琐言>
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷六

    　　吴湘事【刘汉宏附】

    Trivial Records of the Northern Dream, Volume Five
    <Subsection, Novel Class, Miscellaneous Records, Trivial Records of the Northern Dream>

    　　Trivial Records of the Northern Dream, Volume Six
    　　By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty
    　　The Affair of Wu Xiang [with Liu Hanhong attached]
    　　Tang Dynasty's Li Shen was known for his integrity and straightforwardness. In the central government, he was close with Li Deyu, and those who opposed them were deeply resentful. When Li Shen governed Huaihai, Wu Xiang was the Magistrate of Jiangdu. At that time, there was a fallen noblewoman of the Yan family living in Guangling, who was known for her beauty. The chancellor wanted to take her as a concubine, and Wu Xiang forcibly betrothed her. This angered him greatly. Taking advantage of the lavish dowry during the wedding, he fabricated charges and investigated, finding that Wu Xiang had additional decorative items beyond his salary. He was charged with embezzlement and executed, supposedly as punishment for disrespect. When Emperor Xuanzong was still a commoner, he fully understood Wu Xiang's injustice. After ascending the throne, those who were not in harmony with the two Lis led them to file a petition for redress. Li Deyu was exiled to Zhu Ya for this. Passing through Lishui, he told the officials residing in the capital, "Li Twenty wronged me." Ma Zhi, who was once feared by Li Deyu, was sent out as an external official. The matter of Wu Xiang was investigated by the Censorate, and when Fuwu was serving as the Censor-in-Chief, he was able to carry out his intentions. Wu Xiang was from Lishui, and the woman from the Yan family returned to Lishui, dying a widow. The old saying that Zhe Dong is difficult to govern holds true. Li Shen understood five or six parts of public affairs, while Liu Hanhong understood seven parts. Others understood three or four parts. Because his talent was rare.

    The Story of Pei Xiang Gong's Birth in the Kingdom of Yutian [with Master Shuangfeng, Daoist Wen Ruhai]

    During the Tang Dynasty, Pei Xiang Gong devoted his attention to Buddhism and was proficient in Zen and monastic rules. He wrote the preface for the "Chán Quán" (Zen Commentary on the Dharmadhātu) by Master Mi of Gui Peak, who attained the direct transmission of Dharma from Bodhidharma. Pei Xiang Gong often wore a robe made of coarse wool and held a begging bowl, begging for alms in a place where singers and courtesans performed. He claimed that he was not tainted by worldly desires and could teach the Dharma to others. He often made vows to be a king in future lives and to promote and protect Buddhism. Later, a son was born to the king of Yutian, and the boy had the name of Pei Xiang Gong written on his hands. This news reached the imperial court, and his descendants wanted to bring him back to China, but the king of Yutian refused.

    Master Shuangfeng gathered a thousand disciples, and the depth of his discussions on metaphysics was unparalleled. However, he became entangled with a common woman and thus lost his way, confirming that lust is indeed a great punishment. Initially, Li Gong Wei had a good relationship with the master and only appointed him as a minor official. Daoist Wen Ruhai wrote extensive commentaries on the Zhuangzi, earnestly requesting a minor official position, just like Tang Huixiu and Liao Guangxuan, whose aspirations and status were equally humble. Alas!

    The Story of Wei Shi's Daughter Marrying Liu Qian

    Chancellor Wei Gong Zhou was stationed in the South Sea and had a subordinate named Liu Qian, who was of low rank but had a distinguished appearance. Wei Gong Zhou married his daughter to Liu Qian as a concubine. His wife, fearing that this would bring criticism, advised against it, but Wei Gong Zhou said, "This man is not an ordinary person. In the future, my descendants may rely on him." Liu Qian was later promoted to the position of governor of Fengzhou due to his military achievements. Wei Gong Zhou's wife gave birth to two sons, Liu Fang and Liu Yan. Liu Fang became the governor of Guangzhou, and Liu Yan succeeded him, ruling over the four prefectures of the Lingnan region. They established the Kingdom of Han, changed their name to Fang, and reigned for 24 years before Liu Fang's younger son succeeded him. The governor of Jingzhao's ability to recognize talent was indeed accurate.

    Translation:

    The Biography of Tian Bu, Minister

    When the Duke of Wei, Cui Wei, the Prime Minister of the Tang Dynasty, was stationed in Huaiyang, Lu Dan, the Chancellor, and Zhang Duo, the Langzhong, both of whom had been dismissed from their posts in Zhe West and Changzhou respectively, passed through Huaiyang to pay homage to the Duke. On a leisurely day, the Duke privately entertained the two guests while playing chess. At this time, a woman carrying a report stated that a female sorceress had arrived with Minister Tian Bu and was staying at an inn near a certain pavilion. The Duke was greatly surprised by the sorceress's arrival, as it was unusual. Soon after, the sorceress said that her manifestation was different from that of other sorceresses and requested to be moved to the Duke's residence. The Duke then hurriedly summoned the sorceress, who met with the spirit and bowed, saying, "Thank you, Minister." The Duke asked, "Why do you thank me?" The spirit replied, "Tian has an unworthy son who is corrupt and insatiable, causing the affairs of the prefecture to be in disarray. He should be punished with death, but thanks to your hidden virtue, he has been spared. It is your grace that allows the ancestral temple of Tian's family to continue receiving offerings." The Duke was startled and said, "Strange indeed! While I have been a minister, I have never used confidential matters to benefit my family."

    One day, the military governor of Xia Prefecture reported that Tian Kuang, the governor of Yin Prefecture, had committed embezzlement and privately forged armor to exchange for border horses and cloth. The emperor was furious and said, "Embezzlement is a separate matter, but he was entrusted with a border prefecture where he should have been guarding against theft. Using armor to aid the enemy is tantamount to rebellion. I have ordered the chancellor to punish him according to the law, which may even lead to the extermination of his entire clan." The next day, the Duke calmly said to the emperor, "Tian Kuang's embezzlement is already subject to the law, but he is the grandson of Tian Hongzheng and the son of Tian Bu. Tian Hongzheng was the first to request to pay homage to the emperor from the region north of the Yellow River and served as an official. Tian Bu also followed his father's example and was later summoned to fight in Huai West, where he died with loyalty and filial piety. If we now punish him according to the law to strengthen the borders, it would be better to show leniency and encourage loyalty and valor." The emperor's anger subsided, and he only demoted Tian Kuang to be a magistrate in a distant prefecture, without any intervention from the Duke's relatives or close friends.

    Having almost forgotten it, now the spirit's words are indeed the truth of the matter, he then ordered it to be inscribed on a tablet and displayed. The official said to the spirit, "You died for righteousness and valor, how can you be so influenced by a foolish woman?" The spirit replied in a mournful tone, "I often owe this old woman eighty thousand coins, and now I am enduring shame to repay her; it is just an old debt." The official, along with two guests and the military governor's staff, jointly repaid the remaining amount, paying it on their behalf. He claimed that the matter was not verified, and the spirit then departed. The chancellor Li Gong Qi of the Liang dynasty recorded this matter and said, "Alas, a remarkable man, dying for the debt owed to a woman is already like this; how much more so for a great national debt? Stealing the ruler's salary without reporting, stealing the ruler's authority and being disloyal, is it appropriate? And Chancellor Cui served as a general and prime minister for nearly thirty years, it is indeed appropriate."

    The Request to Repair the Temple of Duke Liang of Di

    Li Deyu, the Grand Vizier, had not yet left the academy when he was renowned for his eloquence and literary talent but was not fond of taking the imperial examinations. Ji Fu, the chancellor, urged his relatives to encourage him, and Zhang Wu said, "Enjoying fine horses and not entering the ranks of officials, one can still advance in rank through merit." Ji Fu and Wu Yuanheng, the chancellor, were colleagues, and their affairs often did not align. Whenever they retired from court, Ji Fu's demeanor was displeased. Zhang Wu then said, "What is difficult about this? Why not ask to repair the Temple of Duke Liang of Di?" Thus, Wu Yuanheng gradually sought to leave the capital and take up a military governorship, and his plans were known early on. I once read the Grand Vizier's record of his three court submissions and rejections, which truly shows his remarkable talent, yet he ultimately suffered from factional strife, a result of his exceptional qualities.

    　　宣宗希兾遐龄无储嗣宰臣多有忤防者懿宗藩邸常怀危栗后郭美人诞育一女未逾月卒适值懿皇伤忧之际皇女忽言得活登极后钟爱之封同昌公主降韦保衡恩泽无比因有疾汤药不效而殒医官韩宗昭康守商等数家皆族诛刘相国瞻上谏懿皇不聴懿皇尝幸左军见观音像陷地四尺问左右对曰陛下中国之天子菩萨即边地之道人上悦之冦入京郭妃不及奔赴行在乞食于都城时人乃嗟之【同昌公主奢华事见苏鹗杜阳杂编】

    Princess Tongchang's Story

    Emperor Xuanzong hoped for a long life without an heir, and many high-ranking officials were disobedient or rebellious. Emperor Yizong, while living in his princely mansion, often felt fear or anxiety. Later, a concubine named Guo gave birth to a daughter who died within a month, just as Emperor Yizong was in a state of sorrow. The imperial princess, who had survived, was treasured by Emperor Yizong after he ascended the throne. She was bestowed the title of Princess Tongchang and received incomparable favor from Wei Baocheng. However, due to her illness, the medicinal treatments were ineffective, and she died. Several families of medical officials, including Han Zongzhao, Kang Shoushang, and others, were all exterminated. Chancellor Liu submitted a petition to admonish Emperor Yizong, but he did not listen. Emperor Yizong once visited the left army and saw a Bodhisattva Guanyin statue that sank into the ground four feet. He asked those around him, and they replied that he was the emperor of China, while the Bodhisattva was a monk from the borderlands. The emperor was pleased. When bandits invaded the capital, Concubine Guo did not manage to rush to the imperial residence and had to beg for food in the capital city, and people at the time mourned her. [The lavish life of Princess Tongchang is described in Su E's Du Yang Za Bian]

    Memorial by Hou Changye

    After the Guangming era, eunuchs gained power, setting up positions for the north and south, and the military commander Tian Lingzi had the power to reverse the heavens. The court was filled with fear, and while Wang Xianzhi and Huang Chao were plundering the Jianghuai region, the court was deeply concerned. Left Censor Hou Changye submitted a memorial, strongly criticizing the current situation, but it was not presented to the emperor. He was ordered to be executed within the palace. Later, it was said that the content of Hou Changye's memorial was inappropriate, particularly the phrase "please open the Dati Daochang to dissipate the military threat," which seemed to be written by a mediocre monk. If Hou Changye had made such a statement, it was fitting that he should have been punished.

    道之每拂曙出寺为脩功徳因縁也仰常侍徳岂敢秘惜小貂辞逊再三竟得其术尔后最受三峯胡相国及崔相恩知每遇二公载诞之辰乃献银药盂子此外虽家屡空终不自奉亦不传于子孙遂平宰李璩乃嫡孙也尝为愚话之广成杜光庭先生常云未有不脩道而希得仙术茍得之必致祸矣唯名行谨洁者往往得之即李貂之谓也

    Li Changshi's Encounter with Daoist Arts

    Li Fu, the son of Li Changshi, the Grand Attendant from Longxi, was known for his simple and tranquil nature. During the Guanghua period, he fled to Liangchuan with other officials to escape the turmoil. Known as "Xiaodie," he often visited a neighboring temple to relieve his worries. There, he met a monk named Shuang Gong, who, due to their karmic connection, became acquainted with Li Fu. Every morning, the monk would leave the temple, either to attend a meal or to practice his spiritual duties. If Li Fu was in the temple, the monk would not lock his room, allowing Li Fu to stay and rest. Over time, their friendship deepened, and the monk said, "How could I, being in the temple, close the door on Li Changshi?"

    One day, the monk calmly asked Li Fu, "The world speaks of the 'yellow-white arts.' Do you believe in them? Do you desire them?" Li Fu replied, "Though I have never paid much attention, how could I doubt their existence? Yet, how could I dare to desire them?" The monk, who was known as "Pendao," explained that he left the temple every dawn to cultivate virtue, and his respect for Li Changshi's virtue made him unwilling to keep such knowledge secret. Despite Li Fu's repeated polite refusals, the monk eventually shared his Daoist arts with him.

    Afterward, Li Fu was most favored by Prince Sanfeng Hu and Chancellor Cui. Whenever these two officials celebrated their birthdays, Li Fu would present them with silver medicinal vessels. Despite his family's frequent financial struggles, Li Fu never indulged himself and never passed on these Daoist arts to his descendants. Li Qu, the Grand Administrator and Li Fu's direct descendant, once told me about this story. Master Du Guangting of Guangcheng often said, "There is no one who has not cultivated Dao and yet hoped to obtain Daoist arts. If one obtains them, disaster will surely follow. Only those renowned for their integrity and purity often attain them." This is precisely what Li Fu exemplified.

    陆相公劝酒事【朱进士酒狂东臯子刘虚白附】
    　　陆相扆出典夷陵时有士子脩谒相国与之从容因命酒劝此子辞曰天性不饮酒相国曰诚如所言已校五分矣盖平生悔吝若有十分不为酒困自然减半也朱秀才庆余遂宁府人举进士有杨贵妃别明皇赋最佳然狂于酒陇州防御使巩咸乃蜀将也朱生以乡人下第谒之巩亦使酒新铸一劒乃曰如何得一汉试之朱便引颈俄而身首异处惜哉死非其所即陆公之戏诚哉善言也　东臯子王勣字无功有杜康庙碑醉乡记备言酒徳竟陵人刘虚白擢进士第嗜酒有诗云知道醉乡无户税任他荒却下丹田世之嗜酒者茍为孔门之徒得无违吿诫乎

    Lu Xiang's Experience with Drinking [With Zhu Xiucai, the Drunken Scholar, and Liu Xubai of Donggao Attached]

    When Lu Xiang was serving as an official in Yiling, a scholar came to pay respects to the chancellor. They conversed in a relaxed manner, and Lu Xiang then ordered wine and urged the scholar to drink. The scholar replied, "By nature, I do not drink alcohol." Lu Xiang said, "If indeed as you say, then you have already reduced your weaknesses by half." He meant that if one has a lifelong aversion to drinking, it is as if one has ten parts of regret, and being troubled by alcohol would naturally reduce it by half.

    Zhu Xiucai, from Suining, passed the imperial examinations. He loved drinking and wrote a poem that was considered the best, especially his Farewell to Yang Guifei from the Bright Emperor. However, he was also known for his drunkenness. When he failed the examination, he went to pay respects to Gong Xian, the governor of Longzhou, who was a general from Shu. Gong Xian, who was also fond of drinking, had recently cast a new sword and said, "How can I find someone to test it?" Zhu Xiucai, being a fellow villager, was invited to try it. Zhu Xiucai stretched his neck, and soon his head and body were separated. Alas, he died in a place not befitting his talents. This was indeed a playful remark by Lu Xiang, but it was also wise words.

    **Liu Xubai of Donggao, whose name was Wang Ji, with the courtesy name Wugong, wrote a Memorial to the Du Kang Temple and a Record of the Drunken Land, both of which elaborately praised the virtues of wine. Liu Xubai, from Jingling, passed the imperial examinations and loved drinking. He wrote a poem that said, "Knowing that in the land of drunkenness there is no tax on households, let him indulge in it and neglect his lower dantian." Those who love drinking, if they are followers of Confucius, would not go against the warnings?"

    The Story of Pei and Zheng Supporting the Prince

    During the reign of Emperor Xizong of Tang, when he visited Liangyang again, Zhu Mei supported the prince. Chancellors Xiao Guo, Pei Che, and Zheng Kuangtu, among others, supported him as well. When the false ruler was defeated and Emperor Xizong was restored, Pei and Zheng, among others, all suffered the death penalty. Initially equipped with guards, surrounded by spears and halberds, Chancellor Pei still joked, "The emperor's defenses are formidable, even though they may seem weak or ineffective." Chancellor Xiao Guo was given poison in Hezhong, held in hand, hoping for a reduced punishment due to the emperor's past favor. The poison caused his hand to rot, and he eventually drank it and died.

    田军容檄韦太尉
    　　唐太尉韦公昭度旧族名人位非忝窃而沙门僧澈承恩为人潜结中禁京兆与一二时相皆因之大拜悟达国师知元乃澈之师也尝鄙之诸相在西川行在每谒悟达皆申跪礼国师揖之请于僧澈处吃茶后掌武伐成都田军容致檄书曰伏以太尉相国顷因和尚方始登庸在中书则开铺卖官居翰苑则借人把笔盖谓此也
    　　朱李骤进
    　　唐李师望乃诸宗属也自负才术欲以方面为己任因旅游邛蜀备知南蛮之勇怯遂上书希割西川数州于临邛郡建定边军节度诏防允之乃自凤翔少尹擢领此任于时西川大将嫉其分裂巡属乃隂通【一作致意】南诏于是蛮军为近界乡豪所导侵轶蜀川元戎窦滂不能遏截师望亦寻受贬黜陇西【又云因任华阳捕贼】　光化中朱朴自毛诗博士登庸恃其口辩可以立致太平由藩邸引导闻于

    Explanation

    85

    田军容檄韦太尉

    唐太尉韦昭度出身于显赫世家，名位非同小可，然而沙门僧澈因其承蒙皇恩而暗中结交宫廷。京兆尹与几位当时宰相皆因他而被提拔。悟达国师知元是僧澈的师父，曾被诸宰相轻视，每当在西川行宫谒见悟达国师时，他们皆行大礼。国师以礼相待，并邀请僧澈共饮。后来，田军容掌管军事事务，讨伐成都，他发布了一封檄文说：“太尉相国韦昭度，近日因和尚僧澈才得以显达。他在中书省开设官职买卖，在翰林院则借他人之笔。此即所指也。”

    朱李骤进

    唐李师望是皇族成员，自负才华，欲以一方为己任。他游历邛蜀，了解南蛮的勇怯。于是上书请求分割西川数州，在临邛郡建立定边军节度使。诏书批准了他的请求，他从凤翔少尹被提拔担任此职。当时西川大将嫉妒他分割自己的辖区，于是暗中与南诏通信。因此，蛮军在附近乡绅的引导下侵犯了蜀川。元戎窦滂未能阻止，李师望不久也被贬谪。陇西（又说是因为在华阳捕贼）。光化年间，朱朴从毛诗博士升为宰相，依仗其口才，认为可以迅速实现太平，由藩邸推荐而闻名。

    86

    昭宗遂有此拜对敭之日面陈时事数条每言臣为陛下致之洎操大柄无以施展自是恩泽日衰中外腾沸内优曰俳优穆刀陵作念经行者至御【一作狮】前曰若是朱相即是非相翌日出官时人曰拔士为相自古有也君子【一作此】不耻其言之不出耻躬之不逮况唐末防乱天下阻兵虽负奇才不能谋画而朱公一儒生以区区辩给欲整其乱祗自取辱焉涓缕未申而教乐僮吹筚篥甚为识者所责也
    　　李羣玉轻薄事【韦沆李璩附】
    　　唐李羣玉校书字文山澧州人有诗名散逸不乐应举亲友强之一上而已尝受知于相国河东裴公休为其延誉因进诗授文馆校书终于荆襄间然多狎酒徒疑其为张祜之流李少逢善夷谪官澧阳备知其行止因为纪之乃清介髙节之人非轻率之士疑为同人所谤或曰曽为荆之幕下假书题谒澧吏艾使君李谓艾侯曰小子困甚

    Explanation

    86

    Emperor Zhaozong was appointed to this position and, on the day of his appointment, he personally presented several matters of state. Each time he said that he would bring it to the Emperor. When he took on great power, he could not implement his plans. From then on, the emperor's favor gradually diminished, and there was turmoil both inside and outside the court. The eunuchs said that the performer Mu Dao Ling was reciting scriptures. When he reached the emperor's presence, he said, "If Zhu is a prime minister, then he is not a prime minister." The next day, when he was dismissed from office, people said, "It has always been possible for a scholar to be made prime minister." A gentleman does not despise words that are not spoken, but despises actions that fall short. Especially in the late Tang, when the country was in turmoil and everyone was armed, even with extraordinary talent, one could not plan effectively. Zhu Gong, a mere scholar, tried to restore order with his limited eloquence and only brought himself disgrace. Before he could fully express his ideas, he was criticized by knowledgeable people for having his young attendants play the hululu.

    The Frivolous Affairs of Li Qunyu [with references to Wei Hang and Li Qu]

    Li Qunyu, a scholar from Lizhou, had a reputation for poetry and was not fond of taking the imperial examinations. His friends and relatives forced him to take it once. He was known to the chancellor of Hedong, Pei Gongxiu, who promoted his reputation. He presented poems and was appointed as a scholar in the Hall of Imperial Literature, and he died in Jing and Xiang regions. However, he often associated with drunkards, and it was suspected that he was like Zhang Hu. Li Shao, who was exiled to Lizyang, knew all about his behavior. He recorded it, saying that he was a person of high moral integrity and not a reckless one. It was suspected that he was slandered by his peers, or it was said that he had served as an officer in Jing and had borrowed books to present to the magistrate of Lizhou, Ai Shi. Li said to Ai, "I am in dire straits."

    87

    幸使君痛救之州将以【一作戒】其轻脱所济不厚也又近年京兆韦沆者衣缨旧族亦攻古文流落不偶而没于世陇西李璩乃福相之曽孙也常宰襄州乡乐县京兆侨于是邑常来干扰李亦祗奉不厌一旦谓李宰曰客有相勉且求一邑以救饥寒室人闻之大怒曰人唤郎为长官即得唤我作长官夫人即不可陇西闻而鄙薄亦笑亦怒也
    　　以歌词自娱【蜀相韦庄晋相和凝附】
    　　先是李逺以曽有诗云人事三杯酒流年一局棊唐宣宗以其非牧人之才不与郡守宰相为言然始俞允蜀相韦庄应举时遇黄冦犯阙着秦妇吟一篇内一联云内库烧为锦绣灰天街踏尽公卿骨尔后公卿亦多垂讶庄乃讳之时人号秦妇吟秀才他日撰家戒内不许垂秦妇吟障子以此止谤亦无及也　晋相和凝少年时好为曲子词布于汴洛洎入相专托人収拾焚毁不暇然相国厚重有徳终为艶词玷之契丹入夷门号为曲子相公所谓好事不出门恶事行千里士君子得不戒之乎【又云长日唯消一局棊两存之】

    Explanation

    87

    May the governor kindly rescue it, the governor should admonish for its recklessness, the benefit is not great. In recent years, Wei Hang from Jingzhao, a member of an old, prestigious family, also studied classical literature but was unsuccessful and died without achieving much. Li Qu from Longxi, a great-grandson of someone with a good fortune, often served as the magistrate of Xiangzhou Xiangle County, and people from Jingzhao frequently disturbed him. Li Qu would always serve them with respect and patience. One day, a guest said to Li Qu, "There is someone who encourages you to seek a position to save yourself from poverty and hunger." His wife heard this and became very angry, saying, "If they call you 'Lord,' then they can call me 'Lady.' That is unacceptable." Li Qu heard this and felt both amused and disdainful.

    Using lyrics for entertainment [with references to Wei Zhuang and He Ning].

    Before this, Li Yuan once wrote a poem: "Human affairs are settled over three cups of wine, and a lifetime is played out in one game of chess." Emperor Xuanzong of Tang believed that he lacked the talent to govern and did not discuss it with the prefects or chancellors. However, he eventually agreed. When Wei Zhuang took the imperial exams, he encountered a bandit attack and wrote "Qin Woman's Lament," which includes the lines, "The inner treasury burned to ashes, and the bones of the nobles were trodden underfoot on the imperial street." After this, many nobles were surprised and criticized him. Wei Zhuang then avoided mentioning it, and people called him "Qin Woman's Lament Scholar." Later, in his family precepts, he forbade hanging screens with "Qin Woman's Lament" on them, but this was too late to stop the criticism. He Ning, when young, enjoyed writing lyrics and distributed them in Bian and Luo. When he became chancellor, he entrusted others to collect and burn them. However, the chancellor was heavy and virtuous, and he was ultimately tainted by his love for elegant poetry. When the Khitans entered Yimen, he was called "Lyric Chancellor." The saying goes, "Good deeds don't spread far, but bad deeds travel a thousand miles." Scholars and gentlemen should be cautious about this [another version says, "Long days are spent playing one game of chess, both versions are kept"].

    88

    刘蜕奏令狐相
    　　宣宗以政事委相国令狐公君臣道契人无间然刘舍人每讦其短密奏之宣宗留中但以其事规于相国而不言其人姓名其间以丞相子拔解就试疏略云号曰无解进士其实有耳未闻云云又以子弟纳财贿疏云白日之下见金而不见人云云丞相憾之乃俾一人为其书吏谨事之紫防托以腹心都不疑虑乃为一经业举人致名第受赂十万为此吏所吿由是贬之君子曰彭城公将欲律人先须洁已安有自负赃汚而发人之短乎宜其不跻大位也先是令狐相自以单族每欲繁其宗党与崔卢抗衡凡是富家率皆引进皇籍有不得官者欲进状请改姓令狐时以此少之

    Explanation

    88

    In the reign of Emperor Xuanzong, the administration of state affairs was entrusted to Prime Minister Linghu Gong, and the relationship between the ruler and minister was harmonious, with no gap between them. Dong Shiren, a court official, frequently criticized Linghu Gong's shortcomings and submitted secret reports to the emperor, who kept the reports and only instructed the Prime Minister about the matters without mentioning the names of the individuals involved.

    During this period, the son of the Chancellor was selected for an examination, but the process was loosely handled, and it was said that he was called 'the unsolvable jinshi' (a degree candidate), though in reality, he had something to be heard about. He also submitted a report about his sons and nephews accepting bribes, stating that they were seen taking gold but not people in broad daylight.

    The Chancellor resented Dong Shiren and appointed a man to be his secretary, treating him with great care. The purple robe (a symbol of high office) was entrusted to him as a trusted advisor, and the Chancellor had no doubts about him. The official who was supposed to be a model of integrity received a bribe of ten thousand coins, and this was reported by the secretary, leading to his demotion.

    The gentleman said, 'The Duke of Pengcheng intends to discipline others but must first cleanse himself. How can he criticize others for corruption when he himself is corrupt? It is appropriate that he did not reach a high position.'

    Before this, Linghu, the Chancellor, being of a single lineage, often tried to expand his clan to rival the powerful families of Cui and Lu. He often introduced wealthy families into the imperial register, and those who could not obtain official positions wanted to submit petitions to change their surname to Linghu. At the time, people criticized him for this.

    89

    陆蒙追赠【薛许州附】
    　　唐吴郡陆蒙字鲁望旧名族也其父賔虞进士甲科浙东从事侍御史家于苏台防精六籍弱冠攻文与顔荛皮日休罗吴融为益友性髙洁家贫思养亲之禄与张博为吴兴庐江二郡倅着吴兴实録四十卷松陵集十卷笠泽丛书五卷丞相李公蔚卢公携景重之罗给事寄陆诗云龙楼李丞相昔嵗仰髙文黄阁今无主青山竟不焚盖尝有征聘之意唐末以左拾遗授之诏下

    Explanation

    89

    Lu Guimeng, posthumously honored as Lu Wàng, was of an old and distinguished family. His father, Bīn Yú, passed the highest imperial examination and served as an imperial censor in Zhejiang East. Lu Guimeng lived in Suzhou, where he dedicated himself to the Six Classics and began studying literature at the age of twenty. He formed close friendships with scholars such as Yan Rao, Pi Rihou, Luo Yin, and Wu Rong. Known for his high moral integrity, he was poor at home and thought about earning a salary to support his parents. He served as deputy governor of Wu and Lujiang prefectures with Zhang Bo and compiled works such as Fuxing Shilu (40 volumes), Songling Ji (10 volumes), and Lizhe Congshu (5 volumes). Chancellor Li Wei and Grand Tutor Lu Xie highly respected him. Luo the Censor sent a poem to Lu Guimeng, which read, "The Dragon Pavilion Chancellor once admired your lofty writings; now the Yellow Gate has no master, and the green mountains remain unburned." This indicates that he had been considered for a position of honor. At the end of the Tang dynasty, he was appointed as Left Censor by imperial decree.

    90

    之日疾终光化三年赠右补阙吴侍郎融传贻史右补阙韦庄撰诔文相国陆希声撰碑文给事中顔荛书皮日休博士为诗皮冦死浙中方干诗名著于吴中陆未许之一旦顿作诗五十首装为方干新制时辈吟赏降仰陆谓曰此乃下官效方干之作也方诗在模范中尔奇意精识者亦然之　薛许州能以诗道为己任还刘徳仁卷有诗云百首如一首卷初如卷终讥刘不能变态乃陆之比也
    　　顔给事墓铭
    　　顔给事荛谪官没于湖外尝自草墓志性躁急不能容物其志词云寓于东吴与吴郡陆为诗论之交一纪无逾卒为其就木至穴情礼不缺其后即故谏议大夫髙公丞之故丞相陆公扆二君于荛至死不变其余面交皆如携手过市见利即解携而去莫我知也复有吏部尚书薛公贻矩兵部侍郎于公兢中书舍人郑公撰三君子者余今日已前不变不知异日见余骨肉孤防复如何哉

    Explanation

    90

    On that day, Wu Rong, the Right Censor, died suddenly. In the third year of Guanghua, he was posthumously granted the title of Right Censor. Wei Zhuang composed an epitaph for him, and Lu Xisheng wrote an epitaph. Yan Rao wrote the inscription on his tombstone. Pi Rihou, the Doctor, composed a poem. When Pi Rihou died in Zhejiang, Fang Gan's poetry was famous in Wu region, but Lu Xisheng did not approve of it. One day, he suddenly composed fifty poems, arranged as new works by Fang Gan. Contemporaries praised and admired them. Lu Xisheng said, "These are the works of the underling imitating Fang Gan." Fang Gan's poems were in the model, and those with a keen eye and discernment also agreed.

    Shi Ji, the Minister of Personnel, was able to take poetry as his own responsibility. He returned Liu Deren's scroll with a poem that said, "A hundred poems are like one; the beginning is like the end." He criticized Liu for not being able to change his style, which was similar to Lu Xisheng.

    Yan Jifu's Tombstone Inscription
    Yan Jifu Rao was exiled and died outside Lake. He once wrote his own tombstone inscription. He was impatient and could not tolerate others. His inscription said, "He resided in the East Wu region and had a friendship with Lu Guimeng of Wu Prefecture based on poetry and discourse. A decade without exceeding. When Lu Guimeng died, he helped him to the grave, and emotional and ceremonial respect remained intact. After that, the former Adviser to the Imperial Council, Gao Gong, and the former Chancellor, Lu Gong Yi, two gentlemen, remained unchanged with Rao until his death. The rest of his face-to-face friends were like hands being held while passing through the market, and upon seeing profit, they would release their hands and go their separate ways. Nobody understands me. There are also the Minister of Personnel, Shi Ji, the Deputy Minister of War, Yu Jing, and the Secretary of the Central Secretariat, Zheng Gong, who wrote it. These three gentlemen have not changed since today, but I do not know what will happen in the future when I see my lonely and unprotected family."

    91

    李磎行状【梁补阙附】
    　　司空图侍郎撰李公磎行状以公有出伦之才为时辈妬忌罹于非横其平生着文有百家着诸心要文集三十卷品流志五卷易之心要三卷注论语一部明无为上下二【一作三】篇义説一篇仓卒之辰焚于贼火时人无所闻也惜哉阳春白雪世人寡和岂虚言也葆光子曰唐代韩愈栁宗元洎李翺李观皇甫湜数君子之文陵轹荀孟穅秕顔谢其所宗仰者唯梁浩补阙而已乃诸人之鉴而梁之声采寂寂岂阳春白雪之流乎是知俗誉喧喧者宜鉴其滥吹也
    　　白太傅墓志【卢郑二相附】
    　　白太傅与元相国友善以诗道著名时号元白其集内有诗挽元相云相看掩泪俱无语别后伤心事岂知想得咸阳原上树已抽三丈白杨枝洎自撰墓志云与彭城刘梦得为诗友殊不言元公时人疑其隙终也　郑文公畋与卢相携亲表也阀阅相齐词学相均同在中书因公事不叶挥霍间言语相挤诟不觉砚瓦翻泼谓宰相鬭击亦不然也竟以此出官矣

    Explanation

    91

    Biography of Li Qi [with Liang Buqu Attached]
    　　Sikong Tu, the Attendant in the Secretariat, composed the biography of Li Qi, noting that he possessed exceptional talent which was envied by his contemporaries, leading to unjust misfortune. Throughout his life, he wrote extensively, producing a collection of writings that distilled the essence of various schools of thought, a thirty-volume anthology, a five-volume work on social ranks and classifications, a three-volume work on the essence of the I Ching, a commentary on the Analects, and a two-part work on the concept of "wu wei," along with a single work on the interpretation of principles. In a moment of crisis, his works were destroyed in a fire, and as a result, they are no longer accessible to the public. Alas! "Yang Chun Bai Xue" (highbrow art) is appreciated by only a few; is this not a true statement? Bao Guangzi said: The writings of Tang Dynasty figures such as Han Yu, Liu Zongyuan, Li Ao, Li Guan, and Huangfu Shi surpassed Xunzi and Mencius, and were superior to the works of Yan and Xie. The only figure they revered was Liang Buqu, who served as their mirror. Yet Liang's reputation was silent and unacknowledged, was he not of the same caliber as those who created "Yang Chun Bai Xue"? Thus, one should be wary of the empty praise bestowed upon popular figures.

    　　Tombstone Inscription for Bai Juyi [with Lu and Zheng Attached]
    　　Bai Juyi, the Attendant in the Secretariat, was close friends with Yuan Zhen, and both were famous for their poetry, earning them the nickname "Yuan Bai." In his collection, there is a poem mourning Yuan Zhen, in which he writes: "We both shed tears, unable to speak, and I wonder about the sorrowful events that have transpired since our parting. I imagine the trees on the original plains of Xianyang have already grown three zhang tall, with white willow branches." In his own tombstone inscription, Bai Juyi mentions his friendship with Liu Yuxi of Pengcheng but does not mention Yuan Zhen, leading people to suspect that there was a rift between them. Zheng Wengong Tian and Lu Xiang were related by family ties, sharing similar family backgrounds and literary accomplishments. They served together in the central government, but due to a disagreement over official matters, they engaged in a verbal altercation, accidentally spilling ink from an inkstone. It was said that this was a conflict between prime ministers, but it was not serious enough to warrant such an accusation. Ultimately, one of them was dismissed from office as a result.

    92

    内官改创职事【窦给事附】
    　　古者阉官擅权专制者多矣其间不无忠孝亦存简编唐自安史已来兵难荐臻天子播越亲卫戎柄皆付大阉鱼朝恩窦文塲乃其魁也尔后置左右军十二卫观军容处置枢密宣徽四院使拟于四相也十六宫使皆宦者为之分卿寺之职以权为班行备员而已供奉官紫绶入侍后军容使杨复恭俾其襴笏宣导自农改作也严遵美内谒之最良也
    尝典戎唐末致仕居蜀郡鄙叟庸夫时得亲狎其子仕蜀至閤门使曾为一僧致紫袈裟僧来感谢书记所谢之语于掌中方属炎天手汗模糊文字莫辨折腰【一作行膝】而趋汗流喘乏只云伏以军容寂无所道抵掌视之良久云貌寝人微凡事无能严公曰不敢退而大咍严公物故蜀朝册赠命给事中窦雍坚不承命虽偏霸之世亦不茍且士人多之

    Explanation

    92

    Eunuchs Reforming Their Duties [With Dou the Censor Attached]
    In ancient times, there were many eunuchs who usurped power and ruled autocratically, yet some also exhibited loyalty and filial piety, which are recorded in historical annals. Since the An Lushan Rebellion, military disasters repeatedly occurred, forcing the emperor to flee. The command of the emperor's personal guard was entrusted to powerful eunuchs such as Yu Chao'en and Dou Wentang, who were the most prominent among them. Later, positions such as the Left Army, Twelve Guards, Military Inspectorate, Chancellery, and Palace Secretariat were established, comparable to the four chancellors. Sixteen palace officials, all eunuchs, were appointed to perform the duties of the ministries, acting as formal members of the bureaucracy. Officials with purple belts, who served in the imperial court as military commanders, were under the command of Yang Fugong, who allowed them to announce or guide using ceremonial robes and tablets, a role that was changed from the original. Yan Zunmei was the best eunuch for internal court affairs.

    He once commanded the military and retired at the end of the Tang Dynasty, living in Shu Prefecture as a common old man. Occasionally, he was approached or befriended. His son served in Shu as a Gatekeeper, and once, a monk presented him with a purple robe. When the monk came to thank him, the words of thanks recorded in the official documents were unclear due to the heat and sweat. He bowed and said nothing about the military commander, slapping his palm and looking at it for a long time. He said, "Ugly and of low status, I am unable to do anything." The eunuch replied, "Not dare." He laughed loudly after stepping back. After Yan's death, the Shu court bestowed posthumous honors upon him, appointing him as a Censor. Dou Yong refused to accept the posthumous appointment, even during the era of divided rule, he did not compromise. Many scholars admired him.

    93

    罗顾升降【方干附】
    　　唐罗给事顾博士云俱受知于相国令狐公顾虽鹾商之子而风韵详整罗亦钱塘人乡音乖剌相国子弟每有宴防顾独与之丰韵谈谐莫辨其寒素之士也顾文赋为时所称而切于成名尝有启事陈于所知只望丙科尽处竟列名于尾株之前也【令狐召学士话于梁震先辈愚于梁公处闻之】罗既频不得意未免怨望竟为贵子弟所排契濶东归黄冦事平朝贤议欲召之韦贻范沮之曰某曽与之同舟而载虽未相识舟人吿云此有朝官罗曰是何朝官我脚夹笔可以敌得数辈必若登科通籍吾徒为秕穅也由是不果召　诗人方干亦吴人也王大夫重之既延入内乃连下两拜亚相安详以答之未起间方又致一拜时号方三拜也

    Explanation

    93

    The Rise and Fall of Luo and Gu [with Fang Gan appended]

    During the Tang dynasty, Luo Geshizhong and Gu Boshi were both favored by Chancellor Liang Hui. Although Gu was the son of a salt merchant, he possessed a refined and dignified demeanor. Luo, also from Qiantang, had a strange accent. Whenever the chancellor's children hosted banquets, Gu alone could engage in graceful and harmonious conversation, making it hard to distinguish him as a person of humble origin. Gu's literary works were highly regarded in his time, and he was eager for fame. He once submitted a request to his patrons, hoping to rank just above the lowest candidate in the civil service examination. [Liang Hui mentioned this to Xue Shi, who passed on the story to Liang Gong. I heard it from Liang Gong.] Luo, however, frequently faced setbacks and grew resentful. Eventually, he was ostracized by the aristocratic youth and, after a falling out, returned eastward. After the Yellow Turban Rebellion was quelled, court officials discussed recalling Luo, but Wei Yifan opposed it, saying, "I once shared a boat with him, though we were not acquainted. The boatman told me, 'There is a government official on board.' I asked, 'What kind of official?' Luo replied, 'What kind of official? I can hold my pen between my feet and match several of you.' If he were to pass the examination and enter officialdom, we would be mere chaff." Thus, Luo was not recalled.

    The poet Fang Gan was also from Wu. Wang Gui, a high-ranking official, valued his talent and invited him into his inner chambers. Fang bowed twice in succession, and the vice-premier responded calmly. Before Fang could rise, he offered another bow. At the time, he was nicknamed "Fang Sanbai" (Fang Three Bows).

    94

    李琪书树叶
    　　梁李相国琪唐末以文学策名仕至御史昭宗播迁衣冠荡析因与农杨玢藏迹于荆楚间杨即蜀琪相盘桓于夷道之清江自晦其迹号华原李长官其堂兄光符宰宜都尝厌薄之琪相寂寞每临流踞石摘树叶而试草制词吁嗟怏怅而投于水中梁祖受禅征入拜翰林学士寻登廊庙尔后宜都之子彬羇旅渚宫因省相国乃数厥父之所短而遣之矣

    Explanation

    94

    Li Qiqiang, the chancellor of the Later Liang dynasty, gained fame through his literary talent and served as a censor during the late Tang dynasty. During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong, when the imperial court was relocated and the literati dispersed, he and Yang Bin from Hongnong also sought refuge in the regions of Jing and Chu. Yang Bin later became the ruler of Shu. Li Qiqiang lingered in Qingjiang of Yidao, concealing his identity and calling himself Li Changguan of Huayuan. His elder brother Guangfu served as the governor of Yidu and often despised him, leaving Li Qiqiang feeling lonely. He often sat by the water, picking leaves and trying to draft imperial edicts, exclaiming with disappointment and frustration before throwing them into the water. When Zhu Wen, the founder of the Later Liang dynasty, accepted the imperial throne, Li Qiqiang was summoned to serve as a翰林学士 and soon entered the imperial court. Later, Yidu's son Bin, a traveler in Zhubu, visited the chancellor and counted the shortcomings of his father, eventually sending him away.

    杜荀入翰林【平曽贾岛附】
    　　唐杜荀尝游梁献太祖诗三十章皆易晓也因厚遇之洎受禅拜翰林学士五日而卒朱崖李太尉奬拔寒俊至于掌诰率用子弟乃曰以其谙练故事以济缓急也如京兆者一篇一咏而已经国大手非其所能幸而殂逝免贻伊耻也制贬平曽贾岛以其僻涩之才无所采用皆此类也
    　　乐工关小红【石潨附】
    　　唐昭宗刼迁百官荡析名娼伎儿皆为强诸侯有之供奉弹琵琶乐工号关别驾小红者小名也梁太祖求之既至谓曰尔解弹阳下采桑乎关伶俛而奏之及出又为亲近者俾其弹而送酒由是失意不久而殂复有琵琶石潨者号石司马自言早为相国令狐公见赏俾与诸子涣湚连水边作名也乱后入蜀不乐籍多防诸大官家皆以宾客待之一日防军校数员饮酒石潨以胡琴擅塲在坐非别音者諠哗语笑殊不倾聴潨乃扑槽而诟曰某曽为中朝宰相供奉今日与健儿弹而不蒙我听何其苦哉于时识者亦叹讶之防乱以来冠履颠倒不幸之事何可胜道岂独贱伶云乎哉

    Explanation

    95

    Du Xunhe entered the Hanlin Academy [with Ping Zeng and Jia Dao attached].
    During the Tang Dynasty, Du Xunhe once traveled to Li Xian, the first emperor of the Later Liang Dynasty, and presented him with thirty poems, all of which were easy to understand. Because of this, Li Xian treated him generously. Upon receiving the throne, Du Xunhe was appointed as a翰林学士 and died five days later. Li Yiji, the military governor of Zhuang, promoted talented individuals from humble backgrounds, often using his own sons for the role of掌诰. He said, "They are knowledgeable about historical stories and can be useful in emergencies." For example, someone like Jingzhao could write a single poem or essay that would be considered a national masterpiece, which was beyond the capabilities of others. Fortunately, Du Xunhe passed away, sparing him from bringing shame to Li Yiji. Ping Zeng and Jia Dao were demoted for their obscure and difficult talents, which were deemed useless, and this was typical of the situation.

    The musician Guan Xiaohong [with Shi Cong attached].
    During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong of Tang, when the court officials were forcibly relocated, many famous courtesans and musicians fell into the hands of powerful feudal lords. Guan Xiaohong, a female musician known for playing the pipa, was called "Guan Biejia" and was a nickname. Zhu Wen, the founder of the Later Liang Dynasty, sought her out. When she arrived, he asked, "Can you play 'Yangxia Saisang'?" Guan Xiaohong bowed and played it. When she left, he ordered those close to him to make her play and serve wine. As a result, she lost her favor and soon died. There was also a pipa player named Shi Cong, known as "Shi Sima," who claimed that he had been praised by Linghu Chu, the chancellor of the Tang Dynasty, and was allowed to perform with his sons, including Huanshen and Lian. After the chaos, he entered Shu and was not listed in the music registry. He was often invited by high-ranking officials and treated as a guest. One day, several military officers were drinking, and Shi Cong played the huqin, dominating the scene. Those present, who were not playing different instruments, were noisy and laughing, paying no attention to him. Shi Cong then struck the instrument and cursed, saying, "I was once a court official serving as a chancellor. Today, I am playing with these soldiers and am not being listened to. How bitter is this!" At the time, those who recognized him also expressed their surprise. Since the chaos, the social order has been inverted, and there are countless unfortunate events. Is it only the lowly musicians who suffer such misfortunes?

    96

    孙内子【萧惟香附】
    　　唐乐安孙氏进士孟昌期之内子善为诗一旦并焚其集以为才思非妇人之事自是专以妇道内治孙有代夫诗赠人白蜡烛曰景胜银釭香比兰【一作自古清香胜蕙兰】一条白玉逼人寒他时紫禁春风夜醉草天书仔细看又闻琴诗曰玉指朱轧复清湘妃愁怨最难聴初疑飒飒凉风动又似萧萧暮雨零近若流泉来碧嶂逺如下青
    防夜深弹罢堪惆怅雾湿丛兰月满庭又代谢崔家郎君酒诗曰谢将清酒寄愁人澄澈甘香气味真好是緑窓明月夜一杯摇荡满怀春又台州盘村有一妇人萧惟香有才思未嫁于所居牕下与进士王元宴相对因奔琅琊复淫冶不禁王舍于逆旅而去遂私接行客托身无所自经而死店有数百首诗所谓才思非妇人之事诚然也哉闻于刘山甫

    Explanation

    96

    孙内子【萧惟香附】

    The wife of Meng Changqi, a scholar from the Tang dynasty, was skilled in composing poetry. One day, she burned all her collections, thinking that poetic talent was not a woman's business. From then on, she dedicated herself solely to fulfilling her role as a wife and managing the household. She wrote a poem about a candle, which read:

    "The light surpasses silver candle and the fragrance compares to orchids. A piece of white jade that makes one feel cold. On a spring night in the imperial palace, carefully read the heavenly script after being drunk."

    She also wrote a poem about a zither, which read:

    "The fingers of jade pluck the strings with a clear sound. The sad and resentful feelings of Xiangfei are the hardest to listen to. At first, it sounds like a cool breeze blowing. It seems like a drizzling evening rain. It sounds like a stream flowing from a green mountain. It sounds like a stream flowing down a blue cliff from afar. After playing at night, one feels melancholic. The dew moistens the clusters of orchids, and the moon fills the courtyard."

    She wrote another poem about receiving clear wine, which read:

    "Thank you for sending clear wine to a sorrowful person. Clear, sweet, and fragrant, the scent is true. It is best on a moonlit night in a green window. A cup of wine stirs up the spring in one's heart."

    In the village of Pan Nian in Taizhou, there was a woman named Xiao Weixiang, who had talent and creativity. Before marriage, she often conversed with the scholar Wang Yuanyan through the window. She ran to Langya and indulged in unrestrained behavior. Wang left her in an inn and went away. She secretly met travelers and, having nowhere to turn, hanged herself. There were hundreds of poems in the inn. It is indeed true that poetic talent is not a woman's business. This story was heard from Liu Shanfu.

    北梦琐言卷六

    　　北梦琐言卷七
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　孟浩然赵嘏以诗失意
    　　唐襄阳孟浩然与李太白交防宗征李入翰林孟以故人之分有弹冠之望久无消息乃入京谒之一日宗召李入对因从容説及孟浩然李奏曰臣故人也见在臣私第上令急召赐对俾口进佳句孟浩然诵诗曰北阙休上书南山归敝庐不才明主弃多病故人疎上意不悦乃曰未曽见浩然进书朝廷退黜何不云气蒸云梦泽波撼岳阳城縁是不降恩泽终于布衣而已宣宗索赵嘏诗其卷首有题秦皇诗其略云徒知六国随斤斧莫有羣儒定是非上不悦【或云孟郊王维于翰林今两存之】

    Random Notes of the Northern Dream, Volume Six
    　　Imperially Sanctioned Complete Library
    　　Random Notes of the Northern Dream, Volume Seven
    　　Compiled by Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty
    　　Meng Haoran and Zhao Guo Lost Their Way in Poetry

    During the Tang Dynasty, Meng Haoran of Xiangyang was a close friend of Li Bai. When Emperor Xuanzong summoned Li Bai to join the Hanlin Academy, Meng Haoran, hoping to be recommended by his friend, waited for news in the capital for a long time. One day, Emperor Xuanzong summoned Li Bai for a private audience. Li Bai took the opportunity to mention Meng Haoran, saying, "Your Majesty, I have a good friend, Meng Haoran, who is currently staying at my residence. I humbly request that he be summoned to present his poetry." The emperor agreed and summoned Meng Haoran to present his verses. Meng Haoran recited his poem:

    "Stop submitting petitions at the northern gate,
    Return to my humble home in the south.
    An unworthy person is abandoned by a wise ruler,
    Due to illness, old friends have become distant."

    The emperor was displeased and said, "I have never seen Meng Haoran present his poetry to the court. Why did he not say something like 'The mist rises over the Yunmeng Marsh, the waves shake the walls of Yueyang City'? Because of this, he did not receive any favor, and he remained a commoner until the end."

    Later, Emperor Xuanzong requested Zhao Guo's poetry. The first poem in Zhao Guo's collection was titled "On Qin Shi Huang" and contained the lines:

    "Only knowing that the six states fell to the axe,
    No scholars were able to determine right from wrong."

    The emperor was displeased with this. [Some say that the passage refers to Meng Jiao and Wang Wei in the Hanlin Academy, and both interpretations are preserved here.]

    郑綮相诗【李程附】
    　　唐相国郑綮虽有诗名本无廊庙之望常典庐州吴王杨行密为本州步奏官因有遗阙而笞责之然其儒懦清慎农常重之昭宗时吴雄据淮海朝廷务行姑息因【一作恩】盛言郑公之徳由是登庸中外惊骇于时皇纲已紊四方多故相国既无施展事必依违太原兵至渭北天子震恐渴于攘却之术相国奏对请于文宣王諡号中加一哲字其不究时病率此类也同列以其忝窃每讥侮之相国乃题诗于中书壁上其词曰侧坡蛆昆仑蚁子竞来拖一朝白雨下无钝无喽啰意者以时运将衰

    Explanation

    98

    Vang Qi's Poem as Chancellor [with Li Cheng attached]

    Although Vang Qi, the chancellor of the Tang Dynasty, had a reputation as a poet, he had no aspirations for high office. He often served as the governor of Lu Prefecture, where he was a low-ranking official under Yang Xingmi, the Wu King. Because of an oversight, he was punished with a beating. However, he was valued for his scholarly, mild-mannered, and cautious nature. During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong, when Wu Xiong controlled the Huaihai region, the court indulged in leniency and spoke highly of Vang Qi's virtues, leading to his appointment, which shocked both inside and outside the court. At the time, the imperial order had been disrupted, and there were many troubles throughout the land. The chancellor had no room to act and was indecisive in his decisions. When the troops from Taiyuan arrived near the Wei River, the emperor was terrified and eager for a way to repel the enemy. The chancellor proposed adding the character "哲" (meaning "wise") to Confucius' posthumous name. His failure to address the current problems was typical of such situations. His colleagues, who felt he held his position undeservedly, often mocked him. The chancellor then wrote a poem on the wall of the Secretariat. The poem read: "Side slopes, tiny worms, Kunlun ants, all competing to drag; one day, white rain falls, no dull, no weak, it seems the times are declining."

    99

    纵有才智亦不能康济当有玉石俱焚之虑也时亦然之相国题老僧诗云日照西山雪老僧门未开冻缾粘柱础宿火焰炉灰童子病归去鹿麑寒入来常云此诗属对可以称衡重轻不偏也或曰相国近有新诗否对曰诗思在灀桥风雪中驴背上此处何以得之盖言平生苦心也　李程以日五色赋擢第为河南尹日试举人有浩虚舟行卷中日五色赋程相大惊虑掩其美伸览之次服其才丽至末韵侵晩水以芒动俯寒山而秀发程相大咍曰李程赋且在瑞日何为到夜秀发由是浩赋不能陵迈

    Explanation

    99

    Even with talent and intelligence, one cannot achieve prosperity or rescue; there must be concern for the possibility of both good and bad being destroyed together. The chancellor agreed and commented on the poem of the old monk: "The sun illuminates the snow on the western mountains, the old monk's door is not open. A frozen bottle sticks to the pillar base, the ashes of the overnight fire remain. The child is sick and returns home, a young deer enters in the cold." It is often said that this poem's couplets can weigh heavy and light equally, without bias. Someone asked the chancellor if he had recently written new poetry. The chancellor replied, "My poetic inspiration comes from a snowy bridge while riding a donkey. How did I come to this insight? This is what I say about my lifelong effort." Li Cheng was promoted for his essay on the five colors of the sun and became the governor of Henan. He tested candidates daily, and among them was Hao, whose scroll contained the poem on the five colors of the sun. The chancellor was greatly surprised, fearing that his own excellence would be overshadowed. Upon further examination, he admired his talent and beauty. In the final lines of the poem, it invades the late water with a sharp movement, looking down at the cold mountain and revealing its beauty. The chancellor laughed loudly and said, "Li Cheng's poem is already in the auspicious sun; why is its beauty revealed at night?" Therefore, Hao's poem could not surpass it.
