    来鹏诗【沈光杨敬之附】
    　　唐进士来鹏诗思清丽福建韦尚书岫爱其才曽欲以子妻之而后不果尔后游蜀夏课卷中有诗云一夜緑荷风剪破赚他秋雨不成珠识者以为不祥是嵗不随秋赋而卒于通议郎　前进士沈光有洞庭乐赋韦八座岫谓朝贤曰此赋乃一片宫商也后辟为闽从事农杨敬之撰华山赋朱崖李太尉每置座右行坐讽之其略云见
    若咫尺田千亩矣见若环堵城千雉矣见若杯水池百里矣见若蚁垤室九层矣醯鸡往来周东西矣蠛蠓纷纭强秦去矣蜂巢联联构阿房矣俄而复然立建章矣小星奕奕焚咸阳矣累累蠒栗祖龙藏矣其十【一作干】载改更兴【一作与】怀悲愁辛苦循其上矣【杨氏华隂之茂族冠盖甚逺此乃寄意于华山而言世事实雄才也】
    　　李学士赋谶【刘昌美勾伟附】

    Explanation

    100

    Translation:

    Lai Peng's Poetry [with Shen Guang and Yang Jingzhi Attached]

    Lai Peng, a Tang Dynasty Jinshi (imperial scholar), was known for his clear and beautiful poetic thoughts. The Fujian Shangshu (minister) Wei Xiu loved his talent and once intended to marry his daughter to him, but the marriage did not materialize. Later, Lai Peng traveled to Shu, where in his summer exam scrolls, he wrote a poem that read, "A night wind cuts through the green lotus leaves, tricking the autumn rain into not forming pearls." Those who understood it saw this as an omen of misfortune. That year, he did not participate in the autumn exams and died at the rank of Tongyi Lang (a junior official).

    Shen Guang, a Jinshi, wrote the "Dongting Lake Ode." Wei Baizuo Xiu, a high-ranking official, told the court scholars, "This ode is a perfect piece of music and poetry." He was later appointed as an official in Fujian. Hongnong Yang Jingzhi wrote the "Mount Hua Ode," which General Li of Zhuya often placed on his desk, reading it while sitting or standing. The ode roughly reads:

    It seems as if a thousand acres of land are within arm's reach,
    As if a city with a thousand雉 walls is within a small enclosure,
    As if a hundred-mile lake is contained in a cup of water,
    As if a nine-story building is as small as an ant's mound.
    Flies move back and forth between the east and west of Zhou,
    Tiny insects are in a hurry, and the Qin state has passed,
    Honeycombs are connected, forming the Afang Palace,
    Soon it was rebuilt as the Jianzhang Palace,
    The small stars are bright, burning down Xianyang,
    Countless cocoons and chestnuts are hidden by the first emperor.
    After ten years, changes and prosperity, carrying sorrow and hardship, follow it. [Yang's family is a prominent clan in Huayin, and this ode is intended to express the grandeur of Mount Hua and the true talents of the world.]

    Li Xueshi's Prophecy [with Liu Changmei and Gou Wei Attached]

    101

    唐干宁中刘昌美典防州时属夏潦峡涨湍险俚俗云滟滪大如马瞿塘不可下于是行旅辍棹而候水平【一作济】去焉有朝官李荛学士挈家自蜀防流将之江陵郡牧以水势正恶且望少驻以图利涉陇西怱遽殆【一作】为人所【一作之】促召坚请东下不能止之才鼓行桡长揖而别州将目送之际盘涡呀裂破其船而倒李【一作卓】一家溺死焉【或云一行船次共一百二十人皆溺死】唯妳妪一人隔夜为骇浪推送江岸而苏先是永安监灶戸陈小奴掉空
    船下瞿塘见崖下有一人裹四缝帽穿白缺衫皁义襴青袴执铁蒺藜问李公之行迈自云迎候其妳妪苏后亦説于刺史云李学士至一官署上防事朱门白壁寮吏参贺又闻云此行无妳妪名遂送出水滨于时具以其事奏闻自后以瞿塘为水府春秋祭之初陇西文赋中有金钗坠井赋至是谶焉世传云人之正直死为防官道书云酆都隂府官属乃人间有徳者卿相为之亦号隂仙近代朱崖李太尉张读侍郎小説咸有判防之説刘昌美两典防州云安县僧元悟曽有蜀川将校

    Explanation

    101

    During the reign of Emperor Xizong in the Tang Dynasty, Liu Changmei governed a state or region. At this time, the summer floods in the Xialao Gorge were dangerous due to rapid currents. The local saying went that if the Yanyu (a rock) appeared as large as a horse, the Qutang Gorge was too dangerous to navigate. As a result, travelers stopped rowing and waited for the water level to drop before continuing their journey.

    There was a scholar-official from the imperial court, Li Rao, who was traveling with his family from Sichuan to Jiangling. The water conditions were extremely bad, and he hoped to stay a little longer to find a safer crossing. However, he was from Longxi and was in a hurry, nearly getting into trouble. He was summoned by someone and firmly requested to proceed eastward. Despite his attempts to stop him, he set off, rowing and bowing respectfully as he departed. The state official watched him leave, and as he did, the swirling, turbulent waters split open, breaking the boat and causing the entire family of Li to drown. Only one woman (likely a servant or attendant) was washed ashore and survived.

    Before this, a kitchen worker from Yongan named Chen Xiaonu was rowing an empty boat down the Qutang Gorge. He saw a person dressed in white and black, holding an iron weapon, asking about Li's journey. The person claimed to be waiting for the woman who survived and told the governor that Li had arrived at an official residence, where officials greeted him. It was heard that this journey did not include the name of the woman, so she was sent to the water's edge. At that time, the entire incident was reported to the emperor. Since then, the Qutang Gorge has been considered a water temple, and it is customary to offer sacrifices there during the spring and autumn seasons. In recent literary works from Longxi, there is a piece called "Gold Hairpin Falls into the Well," which may have been prophetic. It is said that righteous people who die become officials in the underworld, and these officials are often those with virtue and status in the human world, known as "Yin Xian" (underworld immortals). Recent stories written by officials from Zhu Ya and Zhang Du also mention the concept of judgment in the underworld.

    Liu Changmei twice governed a state or region, and a monk from Yun'an County, Yuanwu, had connections with military officers from Sichuan.

    102

    王尚书者舍己俸三百千以脩观音堂【此像有灵矣】乃剰三十千入已一旦物故经七日邻于腐坏忽然再苏灌汤药以辅之言曰初至一官曹见刘行军【即昌美也】説云何乃侵用功徳钱以旧曽相识放归须还此钱元悟乃戒门人鬻衣鉢而偿之寻复卒也　西川孔目官勾伟于其辈最号亷直绵竹县民王氏子病困入防因复还魂见防官谓曰我即勾孔目也家在成都西市曽人钱三万未偿汝今归去为我言于家人也王生后访勾氏子仍以债主姓名言之果为酬还
    　　卢诗三遇
    　　唐卢延譲业诗二十五举方登一第卷中有句云狐冲官道过狗触【一作判】店门开租庸张濬【一作相】亲见此事每称赏之又有饿猫临鼠穴馋犬防鱼砧之句为成中令汭见赏又有栗爆烧氊破猫跳触鼎翻句为王先主建所赏尝谓人曰平生投谒公卿不意得力于猫儿狗子也人闻而笑之卢尝有诗云不同文赋易为是者【一作着】之乎复【一作后】入翰林阁笔而已同列戏之曰不同文赋易为是者之乎竟以不称职数日而罢也

    Explanation

    102

    Translation:

    Wang Shangshu set aside three hundred thousand of his own salary to repair the Guanyin Temple. [This statue has a spirit.] He kept thirty thousand for himself. One day, he passed away. After seven days, he was on the verge of decay but suddenly revived. Medicine was administered to aid his recovery, and he said, "At first, I arrived at an official office and met General Liu [that is, Changmei]. He said, 'Why did you misuse the merit money?' Since we had met before, I was released and told to return the money. Yuan Wu then instructed his disciples to sell their robes and begging bowls to repay the debt. Soon after, he passed away."

    Gou Wei, a clean and upright official in the Western Sichuan region, was once a member of the Wang family from Mianzhu County. When the family's son was gravely ill and entered the afterlife, he returned to life and saw the ghostly official, who said, "I am Gou Wei, the magistrate. I live in the West Market of Chengdu. I once borrowed three thousand taels of silver from someone and have not repaid it. Now that you are back, please tell this to my family." The Wang family son later visited Gou Wei's son and told him the name of the creditor. The debt was indeed repaid.

    Lu Shi San Yue

    During the Tang Dynasty, Lu Yantang specialized in poetry and passed the imperial examination after twenty-five attempts. In one of his works, he wrote, "A fox runs across the official road, and a dog bumps into the shop door." Zhang Jun, the Prime Minister, personally witnessed this and often praised it. He also wrote, "A hungry cat crouches near the mouse hole, and a greedy dog guards the fish on the chopping block." These lines were admired by Cheng Zhongling. Additionally, he wrote, "Chestnuts explode, burning the felt and breaking it; a cat jumps and touches the overturned cauldron." These lines were praised by Wang Xianzhu. Lu once said to others, "Throughout my life, I visited high-ranking officials, but I did not expect to gain recognition from cats and dogs." People heard this and laughed. Lu once wrote, "Not the same as literary compositions, easy to be this one or that one," and entered the Hanlin Academy. His peers teased him, saying, "Not the same as literary compositions, easy to be this one or that one." Eventually, he was dismissed from the academy after a few days for being incompetent.

    103

    李渷行文卷【皮日休庄布附】
    　　唐晋相李渷磎相之子也文学渊奥迥出辈流于时公相之子弟无能及者应举时文卷行明易先生书又有答明易先生书朝士览之不测涯涘即其他文章可知也然恃才躁进竟罹非祸尔后磎相追雪赠太子太师諡曰文司空图撰行状渷赠礼部员外郎先是刘崇舍人撰磎相麻因而贬黜渷以大彭【一作彰】先世因赃仰药撰鹦鹉杯赋李渷酬词云玉犬吠天关彩童哭仙吏一封红
    书为奏尘寰事八极鼇柱倾四溟龙鬛沸长庚冷有芒文曲淡无气乌轮不再中黄沙瘗腥请帝命真官临云启金匮方与清华宫重正紫极位旷古雨露恩安得借【一作惜】沾施生人血欲尽欃枪无饱意甚有文义焉又皮日休曽谒归融尚书不见因撰夹虵赋讥其不出头也而归氏子亦撰皮靸鞋赋递相谤诮皮生后为湖南军倅亦甚傲诞自号间气布衣庄布以长书责之行于世也
    　　郑准集军书

    Explanation

    103

    Li Shi's Collection of Writings [Including Works by Pi Rihou and Zhuang Bu]

    Li Shi was the son of Li Shi (李渷), a chancellor of the Tang Dynasty. He was profoundly skilled in literature, far surpassing his contemporaries. During his time taking the imperial examinations, his writings circulated under the guidance of Mr. Ming Yi. He also wrote a letter in response to Mr. Ming Yi. Officials who read his works could not fathom their depth, and from this, one can infer the quality of his other writings. However, he relied on his talent and rushed forward, ultimately suffering misfortune. Later, Li Shi (李渷) was posthumously honored with the title of Grand Tutor and the posthumous name "Wen" (文), as recorded in the biography written by Sima Kui. Before this, Liu Chonggui (刘崇龟), a secretary, wrote a memorial for Li Shi (李渷), which led to his demotion. Li Shi (李渷) wrote the "Parrot Cup Ode" in response to the historical figure Da Peng (大彭), whose ancestors committed corruption and took poison. In his response, he wrote:

    "Jade dogs bark at the celestial gate, colorful children cry for divine officials. A red envelope contains a petition about earthly matters. The world's pillars collapse, the scales of the four seas' dragons boil. The evening star is cold and bright, the star of literature is dim and lacking in vitality. The sun or moon does not rise again, stench is buried in yellow sand. Request the emperor to send a true official to open the golden treasury and restore the Purple Extreme position in the Qinghua Palace. Ancient rain and dew grace cannot be borrowed or cherished, and the desire to shed blood until the evil stars are sated. Very meaningful."

    Pi Rihou (皮日休) once visited the Minister of Works Gui Rong (归融) but was not seen. He then wrote the "Snake and Turtle Ode" to criticize Gui Rong for not showing himself, and Gui Rong's son wrote the "Leather Shoe Ode" in response, leading to mutual slander and ridicule. Zhuang Bu (庄布) later wrote a long letter to criticize Pi Rihou, which circulated widely. Zheng Zhun (郑准) collected military documents.

    104

    唐荥阳郑准以文笔依荆州成中令常欲比肩陈阮自集其所作为三卷号刘表军书虽有胸襟而辞体不雅至祝朝贵书云中书令舍人曰草麻通事舍人曰奏可又贺襄州赵令嗣袭其书云不沐浴佩玉而有祁兆不登山取符而无恤封是于庆贺中显言其庶贱也邻道之敬其若是乎应举日诗卷题水牛曰防犊横身立逢人揭尾跳朝士以为大笑
    　　郑准讥陈咏
    　　唐前朝进士陈咏眉州青神人有诗名善奕棊昭宗刼迁驻跸陜郊是嵗策名归蜀韦书记庄以诗贺之又有乡人拓善者属和韦诗其略云譲徳已闻多士伏沽名还得世人闻讥其比涤器当垆也谬称冯副使涓诗以涓多谐戏故也或云蜀之拓善者作此诗假冯公之名也颍川尝以诗道自负谒荆幕郑准准亦自负雄笔谓颍川曰今日多故不暇操染有三数处回缄祈为假手颍川自旦及暮起草不就盖欲以髙之其诗卷首有一对语云隔岸水牛浮鼻渡傍溪沙鸟防头行京兆杜光庭先生谓曰先辈佳句甚多何必以此为卷首颍川曰曽为朝贵见赏所以刻于卷首章都是假誉求售使然也

    104

    During the Tang Dynasty, Zheng Zun from Xingyang relied on his literary skills to depend on the Governor of Jingzhou, often wanting to be on equal footing with Chen and Ruan. He compiled his own works into three volumes titled "Military Records of Liu Biao." Although he had a broad mind, the style of his writing was not elegant. In a letter congratulating the court officials, he wrote: "The Attendant to the Secretary of the Central Secretariat said 'drafting the edict,' and the Attendant to the Imperial Secretary said 'submitting for approval.'" In a letter congratulating Zhao, the successor of the Governor of Xiangzhou, he wrote: "Without bathing and wearing jade, there is a favorable omen; without climbing a mountain to obtain a talisman, there is no concern for the seal." This was a clear indication of his lowly status in the midst of celebration. The respect shown by neighboring regions was not as great as this. On the day of the imperial examination, he titled a poem about a water buffalo "Preventing the Calf from Standing, Meeting People, Reveal Tail, and Jump," which the officials of the court laughed at.

    Zheng Zun criticized Chen Yong.

    During the Tang Dynasty, Chen Yong, a candidate for the imperial examinations from Qingshen, Meizhou, had a reputation for poetry and was skilled at playing chess. When Emperor Zhaozong was forced to relocate and set up his court in the suburbs of Shaanxi, that year, he gained fame and returned to Shu (Sichuan). Wei Shu, the secretary, congratulated him with a poem. A local named Tuo Shan composed a poem in response to Wei Shu's poem. The poem said: "Yielding virtue has been heard by many scholars, but seeking fame has also been heard by the world." It criticized Chen Yong for being like a pot-washer and wine-seller. It mistakenly attributed the poem to Feng Fushi, because Feng often wrote humorous poems. Some say that Tuo Shan from Shu wrote this poem, using Feng's name. Yingchuan, who once boasted of his poetic skills, visited Zheng Zun, the Governor of Jingzhou. Zheng Zun also considered himself a master of writing. He told Yingchuan, "Today there are many affairs, I have no time to write." He asked Yingchuan to write three or four pieces of writing for him. Yingchuan worked from morning until evening but could not finish the drafts, because he wanted to show off his own abilities. There is a couplet at the beginning of his poetry collection: "A water buffalo on the other side of the river with its nose floating across the stream, birds on the bank of the stream walking with their heads raised." The Mr. Du Guangting of Jingzhao said, "Your excellent lines are numerous, why use this as the opening of the collection?" Yingchuan said, "It was once praised by a high-ranking official, so I engraved it at the beginning of the collection." It was because he wanted to gain false praise and sell his work.

    105

    王超牋奏【石钦若许存附】
    　　唐末鳯翔判官王超推奉李茂贞挟曹马之势牋奏文檄恣意翺翔王蜀先主初下成都冯涓节制判掌其奏牋嵗久转防以掌记辟韦庄郎中于权变之间未甚惬防阆州人王保晦有文才而无体式然其切露直致易为晓悟加以鳯翔用王超牋奏超以一本旧族思偶风云每遇飞章言伪而辩蜀先主爱之以二王书题表藳示长乐公公乃致书逊谢倍加赞赏其要曰有眼未见有耳未闻盖讥其阻兵恃强
    失事君去就王超后为兴元留后遇害有鳯鸣集三十卷行于世后又有名石钦者体效其笔为刘知俊判官随轩降蜀不能谦退逺害宾主争露锋颖竟同诛之阅其缄题表章行行然宜其见忌而取祸也许存初背荆州成中令降蜀先主有意杀之亲吏栁脩业劝其谦静每立大功而皆托疾由是获免于先主之世即彭城之旧寮不若髙阳之小吏矣【一作也】王超全集三十卷今只见三卷闻于卢卿宏也

    Explanation

    105

    Wang Chao's Memorials [Shi Qinru and Xu Cun Attached]
    In the late Tang Dynasty, Wang Chao, an official in Fengxiang, supported Li Maozhen and wielded the power of Cao Cao and Ma Chao, submitting memorials and official documents with unrestrained freedom. When the ruler of Shu, Liu Bei, first captured Chengdu, Feng Juan, the governor, appointed Wang Chao to draft his memorials. After a long time, Wang Chao was appointed to oversee the drafting of memorials, and Wei Zhuang, a senior official, was assigned to handle matters of strategy. However, Wang Chao's performance was not entirely satisfactory in these matters. Wang Baohui of Langzhou had literary talent but lacked a formal style. His writing was frank and straightforward, easy to understand, and he was appointed to draft memorials in Fengxiang. Wang Chao, from an old and prestigious family, sought to align with the grandeur of the times, and every time he submitted a memorial with false but eloquent arguments, the ruler of Shu, Liu Bei, loved him. Liu Bei showed the drafts of the memorials written by the two Wangs to the Prince of Changle, who wrote a letter of humility and apology, praising Wang Chao greatly. The key point of the letter was: "To have eyes that have not seen and ears that have not heard," criticizing Wang Chao for being out of touch with reality and relying on his military strength to lose his ability to serve or leave a position appropriately. Wang Chao later became the acting governor of Xingyuan and was killed. He had a collection of thirty volumes titled "Fengming Ji" that circulated in the world. Later, there was a man named Shi Qinru who imitated Wang Chao's style and served as an official under Liu Zhijun. He followed and surrendered to Shu but was unable to remain humble and avoid harm. Both the host and guest revealed their sharpness, and they were eventually executed together. Reading his sealed memorials and official documents, step by step, it is appropriate that he was feared and suffered misfortune. Xu Cun initially defected from Jingzhou Governor Cheng Zhongling to Shu. The ruler of Shu had the intention to kill him, but a close official named Liu Xiuye advised him to remain humble and quiet. Every time he established a great achievement, he would feign illness, and thus he escaped being killed during the reign of the ruler of Shu. He was like an old official from Pengcheng, not as good as a minor official from Gaoyang. Wang Chao's complete collection of thirty volumes is now only known from three volumes heard by Lu Qinghong.

    106

    李商草进劒表【蜀庾传昌顾云附】
    　　李商员外依彭阳令狐公楚以牋奏受知相国危急有寳劒尝为君上所赐将进之命李起草不惬其防因口占云前件劒武库神兵先皇特【一作所】赐既不合将归【一作于】泉下又不宜留在人间时人服其简当彭阳之子绹继有韦平之拜似疎陇西未尝展分重阳日义山诣宅于防事上留题其略云十年泉下无消息九日樽前有所思郎君官重施行马东閤无因许再窥相国覩之惭怅而已乃扃闭此防终身不处也　蜀中庾传昌舍人始为永和府判官文才敏赡伤于冗杂因候相国张公有故未及见庾怒而归草一啓事仅数千字授于谒者拂袖而去他日张相谓朝士曰庾舍人见示长牋不可多

    Explanation

    106

    Translation:

    Li Shangyin Drafted a Memorial for the Presentation of a Sword (With an Appendix on Gyu Chuanzhang from Sichuan)

    Li Shangyin, the external official, relied on Linghu Chu of Pengyang to draft a memorial through his official correspondence, as the Chancellor was in a critical situation. There was a valuable sword that had been specially bestowed by the late emperor. The imperial decree ordered Li to draft the memorial, but he was not satisfied with the purpose. He then composed the following verses orally:

    This sword, a divine weapon from the armory, was specially bestowed by the late emperor. It is inappropriate to return it to the afterlife, nor should it remain in the human realm. At the time, people admired his concise and appropriate handling of the matter.

    Linghu Tong, the son of Linghu Chu, later held the position of Grand Secretary, seemingly distant from the region of Longxi, and never had the opportunity to show favor. On the Double Ninth Festival, Li Shangyin visited Linghu Chu's residence and left a poem at the guardhouse, which read:

    "Ten years without any news from the afterlife, something on my mind while drinking in front of the wine cup. Young man, with your high-ranking position, you have the area in front of your residence where horses are stabled. The eastern hall offers no reason or opportunity to allow another look. Upon seeing it, the Chancellor felt ashamed and sad, and locked up this guardhouse, never to stay there again."

    Gyu Chuanzhang, an official from Sichuan, initially served as a judge in Yonghe Prefecture. He had sharp and abundant literary talent but was marred by redundancy and complexity. Because he was waiting to meet the Chancellor, Zhang Gong, who had a reason and could not be seen, Gyu became angry and returned, drafting a memorial that was only several thousand characters long. He handed it to the messenger and left in a huff. Another day, the Chancellor told the officials, "Gyu showed a long memorial that cannot be excessive."

    107

    得虽然曽闻其草角觝牒词动乃数幅讥其无简当体要之用也【钞本有尺有所短寸有所长向闻于古人也十四字】　黄箓坛场星辰备位顾云博士为髙燕公草斋词云天静则星辰可摘奇险之句施于至敬可乎唐末乱离渴于救时之术孔相国纬每朝士上封事不暇周览但曰古今存亡某知之矣未审所陈利害其要如何盖鄙其不达变也国子司业于晦曽上崔相国公允啓事数千字上至尧舜下及隋唐一兴一替歴歴可纪其末散漫殊非简略所以儒生中通变者鲜矣【裴晋公临终进先帝所赐玉带表文与令狐公事颇同未知孰是旧朝士多云李义山草进劒表令狐公曰今日不暇多云信口占之】

    Explanation

    107

    Although I have heard that the draft is extensive, it is criticized for lacking brevity, appropriateness, and essentiality. [The manuscript has the addition: "What is short has its limitations, and what is long has its strengths; I have heard this from ancient people."] At the Yellow Talisman ritual site, the stars are all in their proper places. Gu Yun, the doctor, wrote a斋词 for Gao Yan Gong, saying that if the sky is calm, the stars can be picked. Can such unusual and dangerous phrases be used in the most solemn contexts? During the chaotic period at the end of the Tang Dynasty, there was a great need for methods to save the times. Whenever officials submitted sealed memorials, Kong Wei, the chancellor, did not have time to read them thoroughly; he would only say, "I know about the rise and fall of past and present." He did not examine the main points of the proposed benefits and harms. He looked down on them for not understanding changes. Yu Hui Zeng, the director of the Imperial Academy, submitted a memorial to Cui Xiangguo Gong, which was thousands of words long, covering everything from Yao and Shun to the Sui and Tang dynasties, with the rise and fall of each dynasty clearly recorded. However, at the end, it became scattered and disorganized, far from being concise. Therefore, those among scholars who understand change are few. [The manuscript has the addition: "Pei Du, the chancellor, submitted a memorial about the jade belt given by the late emperor before his death. The matter with Linghu Gong is similar, but it is unclear which version is correct. Old court officials often say that Li Shangyin wrote the memorial about the sword, and Linghu Gong said that today he did not have time to write it carefully and simply improvised it."]

    108

    髙崇文相国咏雪
    　　唐髙相国崇文本蓟州将校也因讨刘辟有功授西川节度使一旦大雪诸从事吟赏有诗渤海鄙言多呼人为儿【恐是姣字】此日筵上谓宾客曰某虽武夫亦有一诗乃口占云崇文崇武不崇文提戈出塞号将军那个儿射雁落白毛空里落纷纷其诗着题皆谓北齐敖曹之比也太尉骈即其曾孙也镇蜀日以蛮蜑侵暴乃筑罗城城四十里朝廷虽加恩赏亦疑其固防或一日闻奏乐声知有改移乃题风筝寄意曰夜静声响碧空宫商信任往来风依稀似曲才堪聴又被移将别调中旬日报到移镇渚宫

    Explanation

    108

    Gao Chongwen, the High Minister, on Snow
    Gao Chongwen, the High Minister of the Tang Dynasty, originally from Jizhou, was a military officer who, for his meritorious service in suppressing Liu Pi, was appointed as the military governor of Xichuan. One day, during a heavy snowfall, the officials gathered to recite and appreciate poems. The people of Bohai often called others "儿" (likely a typographical error, possibly "姣," meaning "beautiful person," but the context suggests it might be a derogatory term). At this banquet, Gao Chongwen addressed the guests, saying, "Although I am merely a soldier, I too have a poem." He then recited it spontaneously: "Gao Chongwen, valuing martial prowess, not valuing literary skills, carries the spear out to the frontier, known as a general. That beautiful person shoots down a goose, white feathers falling in a flurry." All agreed that his poem was comparable to the works of Ao Cao of the Northern Qi. Dai Wei Piang, the Grand Marshal, was his great-grandson. When stationed in Shu, he faced unrest from the barbarians and pirates, so he built a defensive wall forty li in circumference. Although the court granted him favors, they also suspected him of fortifying his position. One day, upon hearing the sound of music, he knew there was a change, so he inscribed a message on a kite, saying, "At night, the sound of the kite echoes in the clear sky, the pentatonic scale trusts the wind to come and go, the melody seems like a song, yet it shifts to a different tune." Within ten days, he reported the move to Zhugong.

    109

    洞庭湖诗【李洞包贺卢延让顾况附】
    　　湘江北流至岳阳达蜀江夏潦后蜀涨势髙遏住湘波让而退溢为洞庭湖凡濶数百里而君山宛在水中秋水归壑此山复居于陆唯一条湘川而已海为桑田于斯騐也前辈许棠过洞庭诗最为首出尔后无继斯作诗僧齐已驻锡巴陵欲吟一诗竟未得意有都押衙者蔡姓而忘其名戏谓已公曰题洞庭者某诗絶矣诸人幸勿措词已公坚请口劄押衙抑扬朗吟曰可怜洞庭湖恰到三冬无髭须以其不成湖也诸僧大笑之　进士李洞慕贾岛欲铸而顶戴尝念贾岛佛而其诗体又僻于贾　复有包贺者多为麄鄙之句至于苦竹笋抽青橛子石榴树挂小

    Explanation

    109

    Poems about Dongting Lake [By Li Dong, Bao He, Lu Yanrang, and Gu Kuang]

    The Xiang River flows northward to Yueyang, reaching the Sichuan River. After the summer floods, the Sichuan River rises significantly, blocking the Xiang River, causing it to overflow and form Dongting Lake. The lake broadens to hundreds of miles, with Junshan Mountain gracefully lying in the water during autumn. When the autumn waters recede, the mountain returns to land, and only the Xiang River remains. The transformation of sea into land can be seen here. Xu Tang's poetry about Dongting Lake was the most outstanding, and no one has followed in his footsteps since. The poet Qiji, staying in Balin, wanted to write a poem about Dongting Lake but could not find satisfaction. A military official named Cai, whose name is forgotten, jokingly told Qiji, "The poem about Dongting Lake is the best, and others should not write about it." Qiji firmly requested, and the official recited, "How pitiful is Dongting Lake, with no beard in the third winter, because it does not form a lake." The monks laughed at him. Scholar Li Dong admired Jia Dao and wanted to emulate him, often thinking of Jia Dao's poetry. There is also Bao He, who often writes crude and vulgar verses, such as "bitter bamboo shoots sprout green pegs, and pomegranate trees hang small fruits."

    110

    瓶儿又云雾是山巾子船为水靸鞋又云棹摇船掠鬓风动竹捶胸虽好事托以成之亦空穴来风之义也　卢延让哭边将诗曰自是磠砂发非干礮石伤牒多身上职盎大背边疮人谓此是打脊诗也世传逸诗云牕下有时留客宿室中无事伴僧眠号曰自落便宜诗　顾况著作披道服在茅山有一秀才行吟曰驻马上山阿久思不得顾曰何不道风来屎气多秀才云贤莫无礼顾曰是况其人惭惕而退仆早嵗尝和南越诗云晓厨烹淡菜春杼织穜花牛翰林览而絶倒莫喻其防牛公曰吾子只知名安知淡菜非雅物也后方晓之学吟之流得不以斯为戒也

    Explanation

    110

    A bottle is described as a mist-covered mountain hat, a boat as a water shoe. It is said that the oars move the boat, the wind moves the bamboo, and the chest beats. Even if something good is attributed to it, it is still based on a foundation that may not be entirely solid, akin to "wind entering a hole." During the reign of Emperor Ling, Lu Yanrang composed a poem lamenting the death of a border general, which said, "It is sand and gravel that has caused the injury, not stones. There are many documents and duties on the body, a large wound on the back." People called this a "spine-beating poem." A popular poem says, "Sometimes guests stay overnight at the window, and there is nothing to do in the room but accompany a monk to sleep." It is called a "self-falling advantageous poem." Gu Kuang, a scholar wearing a scholar's robe in Mount Mao, had a talented scholar who recited, "Stop the horse on the mountain, think for a long time without finding a solution. Why not say, 'The wind brings the smell of feces?'" The scholar replied, "A scholar should not be rude." Gu Kuang said, "It is me." The scholar was ashamed and retreated. In my early years, I once composed a poem about the Southern Yue region, which said, "In the morning kitchen, clams are cooked, in the spring, mulberry silk is woven." The Hanlin Academy read it and fell to the ground, not understanding its meaning. The Hanlin Academy said, "You only know the name, but do not know that clams are not elegant things." Later, I understood it. Those who study poetry should take this as a warning.

    111

    髙蟾以诗策名【胡曽罗附】
    　　进士髙蟾诗思虽清务为奇险意疎理寡实风雅之罪人薛许州谓人曰倘见此公欲赠其掌然而落第诗曰天上碧桃和露种日边红杏倚云栽芙蓉生在秋江上不向春【一作东】风怨未开盖守寒素之分无躁竞之心公卿间许之先是胡曽有诗曰翰苑何时休嫁女文章早晩罢生儿上林新桂年年发不许平人折一枝罗亦多怨刺当路子弟忌之由是渤海策名也愚尝览李贺歌诗篇慕其逸才奇险虽然尝疑其无理未敢言于时辈或于奇章公集中【奇章集中僧孺给事中】见杜子微牧有言长吉若使稍加其理即奴仆命骚人可也是知通论合符不相逺也
    　　韦杜气槩【李频附】
    　　杜荀曽得一联诗云旧衣灰絮絮新酒竹篘篘时韦相国説右司员外郎寄寓荆州或语于韦公曰我道印将金鏁鏁帘用玉钩钩即京兆大拜气槩诗中已见之矣或有述李频诗于钱尚父曰只将五字句用破一生心尚父曰可惜此心何所不用而破于诗句苦哉

    Explanation

    111

    High Chán established his reputation through poetry. [Attached: Hu Zēng and Lóu Yìng]

    The poet Gāo Chán's poetic thoughts were clear but deliberately strange and risky, with sparse ideas and weak reasoning, making him a culprit against the elegance of the Book of Songs. Xú Zhōu, a high-ranking official, once said to others, "If one were to see this person, they would want to give them a slap on the face because they failed the examination." His poem read: "Heavenly peach blossoms are planted with dew, red apricots lean against clouds near the sun. Lotus flowers bloom on the autumn river, not complaining to the spring wind for not opening." He maintained a humble and simple disposition without the desire for rapid advancement, and was recognized and praised by high-ranking officials. Before this, Hu Zēng had a poem that said, "When will the imperial academy stop marrying off daughters? When will articles stop giving birth to sons?" The new laurel branches of the imperial garden bloom year after year, but they do not allow ordinary people to pick even a single branch. Lóu Yìng also often expressed criticism and resentment, which was resented by those in power, leading to his recognition. I once read Li He's collection of poems and admired his extraordinary talent and risky style, although I often doubted that his reasoning was lacking and hesitated to openly discuss it with my contemporaries. I saw Du Zimei's comment in the collection of Qizhang Gong (a historical figure): "If Li He had added more reasoning to his poetry, he could have been as great as the greatest poets." This shows that the general consensus is that his work is not far from the ideal.

    Wei and Du's bold and dignified style [attached: Li Pín]

    Du Xúnzī once wrote a couplet: "Old clothes are covered with gray fluff, new wine is filtered through bamboo sieves." At the time, Wei Xiangguo, the Right Vice Minister of the Ministry of Works, was living in Jingzhou. Someone told Wei, "I say that the seal will be locked with golden locks and the curtain will be hung with jade hooks, indicating a grand promotion. This bold and dignified style is already evident in the poem." Someone else recounted Li Pín's poem to Qian Shangfu, saying, "He used his five-character verses to express his deepest thoughts and feelings." Qian replied, "It is a pity that this heart was not used more widely and was only expressed in poetry."

    112

    梁震无禄
    　　唐荆南节判司空董与京兆杜无即滑台杜慆常侍之子洎蜀人梁震俱称进士谒成中令欲希荐送有薛少尹者自蜀防流至渚宫三贤尝访之一日薛尹亚谓司空曰閤下与京兆勿议求名必无所遂杜亦不寿唯大贤忽为人絷维官至朱紫如梁秀才者此举必防然登第后一命不沾也后皆如其言梁公却思归蜀重到渚宫江路梗纷未及西泝淮师寇江陵渤海王邀至府衙俾草檄书欲辟于府幕坚以不仕为志渤海敬诺之二纪依栖竟麻衣也薛尹之言果騐耶
    　　夏侯生説刘仆射事
    　　广南刘仆射崇常有台辅之望必谓罢政便期直上罗浮处士夏侯生有道彭城重之因问将来之事夏生言其不入相发后三千里有不测之事洎归阙至中路得疾而薨刘山甫亦夏生言示五年行止事无不騐盖饮啄之有分也

    Explanation

    112

    Liang Zhen Met with Misfortune

    During the Tang dynasty, Dong Yu, the regional judge of Jingnan, and Du Wusheng of Jingzhao, who was the son of Du Tao of Huetai, the former Attendant-in-Ordinary, along with Liang Zhen of Shu, all claimed to be jinshi degree holders and visited Cheng Zhongling, hoping to be recommended for official appointments. At that time, there was a minor official named Xue Shao Yin, who had fled from Shu and arrived at Zhu Gong. The three scholars visited him. One day, Xue Yin said to Dong Yu, "You and the official from Jingzhao should not even consider seeking fame, for it will surely not succeed. Du Wusheng will not live long. Only a great sage, suddenly bound and restrained, may rise to high rank—such as Liang Scholar here. But this endeavor will surely fail, and after passing the examination, he will not receive even the first official appointment." Later events proved his words true. Liang Zhen then wished to return to Shu and revisited Zhu Gong, but the river routes were blocked, and before he could travel west, the Huai River army attacked Jiangling. The Lord of Bohai invited him to his government office and asked him to draft a proclamation. He wished to appoint Liang Zhen to his administrative staff, but Liang Zhen remained steadfast in his refusal to take office. The Lord of Bohai respected his decision, and for twenty years, Liang Zhen lived in seclusion, still wearing a plain hemp robe. Did Xue Yin's words indeed prove true?

    The Story of Xiahou Sheng and Liu Pushe

    Liu Pushe of Guangnan had long been regarded as a potential minister of state. He once expected that after retiring from office, he would directly ascend to Luofu Mountain to live as a hermit. Xiahou Sheng, a reclusive scholar of virtue, was respected by Pengcheng. Liu Pushe consulted him about his future. Xiahou Sheng said he would not become a minister, and after three thousand miles, an unforeseen event would occur. Later, when Liu Pushe returned to the capital on his journey back, he fell ill and died along the way. Liu Shanfu also verified Xiahou Sheng's words regarding the events of the next five years, and all were accurate. This shows that one's fate is predetermined, like the portion of food and drink one is destined to receive.

    113

    曹相梦剃度
    　　唐曹相国确判计亦有台辅之望或梦剃度为僧心甚恶之有一士占梦多騐相国召之具以所见语【一作话】之此人曰前贺侍郎旦夕必登庸出家者号剃度也无何杜相出镇江西而相国大拜也
    　　元徳感
    　　福建道以海口黄碕岸横石巉峭常为舟楫之患闽王琅邪王审知思欲制置惮于力役干宁中因梦金甲神自称吴安王许助开凿及觉话于宾寮因命判官刘山甫躬往设【一作致】祭具述所梦之事三奠未终海内灵怪具见山甫乃憩于僧院凭髙观之风雷暴兴见一物非鱼非龙鳞黄鬛赤凡三日风雷止霁已别开一港甚便行旅当时録奏赐号甘棠港闽从事刘山甫乃中朝旧族也着金溪闲谈十二卷愚尝略得披览而其本偶亡絶无人得海隅迢递莫可搜访今之所集云闻于刘山甫即其事也十不记其三四惜哉

    Explanation

    113

    Cao Xiang's Dream of Being Tonsured as a Monk

    Cao Quan, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, was expected to become a high-ranking official in the government. However, he had a dream of being tonsured as a monk, which he found deeply unpleasant. There was a man who could interpret dreams accurately, and Cao Quan summoned him to explain the dream. The man said that the previous Shilang He would soon be promoted, and the person who had been tonsured (出家者) was called "剃度." Soon after, Du was sent to govern Jiangxi, and Cao Quan was promoted to a high position.

    Wang Shenzhi, the ruler of the Min Kingdom, wanted to construct a harbor but was hesitant due to the difficulties involved. During the Gannin era of Emperor Zhaozong of Tang, Wang Shenzhi had a dream in which he saw a golden-armored deity who claimed to be Wu An Wang and offered to help in the construction of the harbor. After the dream, Wang Shenzhi told his officials about the dream, and they decided to perform a sacrifice to the deity. Liu Shanhua, an official who served in the Min Kingdom, was sent to perform the sacrifice. During the ceremony, Liu Shanhua witnessed a miraculous event where a creature resembling a fish or dragon appeared, and after three days of storms, a new harbor was revealed. The emperor then granted the harbor the name "Gan Tang Port."

    Liu Shanhua, a noble family from the central court, wrote a work titled "Jinxi Xiantan" (闲谈, or "casual talk") containing various stories and anecdotes, including this one. I once briefly read the work, but unfortunately, the original text has been lost, and no one has been able to find it. The story is far off in a distant coastal area and is impossible to search for. What remains today is what I have gathered, heard from Liu Shanhua, which is the story of that event. Out of ten details, only three or four are remembered. Alas.

    114

    刘道济幽牕梦
    　　光化中有文士刘道济止于天台山国清寺梦见一女子引生入牕下有侧柏树葵花遂为伉俪后频于梦中相遇自不晓其故无何于明州奉化县古寺内见一牕侧柏葵花宛是梦中所游有一客官人寄寓于此室女有美才贫而未聘近中心疾而生所遇乃女之魂也盖女子及笄不有所归乃父兄之过也又有彭城刘生梦入一倡妇家与诸辈狎饮尔后但梦便及彼处自疑非梦所遇之姬芳香常袭衣盖心邪所致闻于刘山甫也

    　　北梦琐言卷七
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷八
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　李太尉与段少常书
    　　唐李太尉德裕左降至朱崖着四十九论叙平生所志尝遗段少常成式书曰自到崖州幸且顽健居人多养鸡往往飞入官舍今且作祝鸡翁尔谨状吉甫相典忠州泝流之任行次秭归地名云居台在江中掌武诞于此处小名台郎以其地而命名也

    Explanation

    Final Translation

    Liu Daoji's Dream by the Secluded Window

    During the Guanghua era, the scholar Liu Daoji stayed at Guoqing Temple on Tiantai Mountain. In his dream, a woman led him into a space beneath a window where there was a side柏 tree and a sunflower, and they became a harmonious couple. Afterward, they frequently met in dreams, but he did not understand the reason. Soon after, in an ancient temple in Fenghua County, Mingzhou, he saw a window with a side柏 tree and a sunflower, just as in his dream. There was a guest official staying there, and his daughter was beautiful but poor and unmarried. She was suffering from a heart ailment, and the person Liu Daoji met was her soul. It is said that when a woman reaches the age of fifteen and has not married, it is the fault of her father and elder brothers. Another man from Pengcheng, Liu Sheng, dreamed of entering the home of a courtesan, where he drank with others in a familiar manner. Afterward, whenever he dreamed, he would go to that place, doubting that it was not a dream. The fragrance of the woman he met often clung to his clothes, which he believed was caused by a wandering or perverse heart. This was reported to Liu Shanfu.

    Miscellaneous Notes from the North, Volume Seven

    Imperial Library Collection

    Miscellaneous Notes from the North, Volume Eight

    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Letter from Li Taibei to Duan Shaichang

    During the Tang dynasty, Li Taibei, after being demoted to Zhuya, wrote forty-nine essays detailing his life's aspirations. He once sent a letter to Duan Shaichang, Chengshi, saying: "Since arriving in Zhuya, I have been fortunate to remain healthy. The locals often raise chickens, which sometimes fly into government offices. For now, I will content myself with being a chicken-wishing old man. I humbly report that Ji Fu, the chancellor, was appointed to govern Zhongzhou and traveled upstream to Zigui, where there is a place called Yunju Platform in the middle of the river. Zang Wu was born there, and his nickname was Tai Lang, named after the place."

    This translation aims to maintain the original meaning and cultural context while ensuring readability in English.

    115

    孙仆射酹酒【裴迪附】
    　　唐孙防宗仆射即偓相大王父也宅中集内外亲表开宴有一甥侄闻朝官后至及中门见绯衣官人衣襟前皆是酒汚咄咄而出不相识洎即席説与主人咸讶无此官沈思之乃是行酒时于堦上酹酒草草倾泼也自此每酹酒侧身恭跪一酹而已自孙氏始也今人三酹非也　有裴迪者贽相之堂弟无文学于荆南投笔事赵司徒为虞緫小将对客侧身一酹赵公未喻朝贤间风规极怪之笞七下何不幸也
    　　二朝士以名取戏
    　　唐张裼尚书朝望既髙号为流品与韦相保衡有分韦言于同列以其名裼裼训袒衣也又诗云载衣之裼裼即小儿褓衣乃绷带也方欲因事改之未几韦相流贬竟不大拜韦尝问立名之由裼以少孤为无学问亲表所误也后唐姚相名洎善谈吐仍多辩防表兄弟崔沂侍郎戏之曰洎训肉汁胡为名洎无以酬之然洎亦训至虽然古人以名贻诮者多矣妨事者有焉至如仙客仙童齐丘用砺希斆人过亦无取焉其复名须依义训唯单名易讳者善矣裼公生五子彛宪文蔚知名文蔚后登庸也

    Explanation

    115

    Straw Hat Servant Pouring Wine [with Pei Di attached]
    　　During the Tang Dynasty, Sun Fangzong, the Servant-General, was the great-grandfather of Sun Wuo, the Chancellor. At a gathering in his home, he invited close relatives and distant kin to a banquet. One of his nephews or cousins heard that court officials were arriving later and, upon reaching the main gate, saw a high-ranking official in red robes with wine stains on his chest. The official hurriedly left without being recognized. Later, at the banquet, he explained to the host that he had seen this official, and everyone was surprised because there was no such official. After some thought, it was realized that during the wine service, someone had carelessly poured wine on the steps, splashing it everywhere. From then on, whenever wine was poured, Sun's family would bow sideways in a respectful manner, pouring only once. This custom began with Sun's family, and it is incorrect for people today to pour wine three times. There was a person named Pei Di, a cousin of the Chancellor Zhi, who lacked literary talent. He served under General Zhao Si in Jingnan and became a junior officer under Yu Zong. When entertaining guests, Pei Di would bow sideways and pour wine once. General Zhao did not understand the etiquette of the court and found it very strange, even punishing Pei Di with seven strokes. How unfortunate!

    　　Two Court Officials Teasing Each Other with Names
    　　During the Tang Dynasty, Zhang Xi, the Minister of the Secretariat, was highly respected and known as a member of the elite class. He had a good relationship with Chancellor Wei Baoqing. Wei once told his colleagues that Zhang's name, Xi, meant "uncovered" or "torn" clothing. The poem also says, "Clothed in Xi, Xi is the swaddling clothes of a child, which are wrapped and bound." Zhang intended to change his name but before he could, Chancellor Wei was exiled and never achieved a high position. Chancellor Wei once asked Zhang about the origin of his name. Zhang said that he had been an orphan since childhood and was misled by his relatives and family members. Later, during the Tang Dynasty, there was a Chancellor named Yao Ji who was good at speaking and had many debates. His cousin, Cui Yi, the Secretary of the Board of Works, teased him by saying, "Ji means meat broth, why is your name like that?" Yao Ji had no reply, but he also said that although names can bring ridicule, there are many examples in ancient times. Some names can hinder matters, such as "Xianke" (Immortal Guest), "Xiantong" (Immortal Child), "Qi Qiu" (Qiu's Use), "Yong Li" (Use Li), and "Xi Xue" (Learn Xue). These names are not suitable. When renaming, one should follow the meaning of the name, and it is better to use a single name that is easy to remember. Zhang Xi had five sons, Yi, Xian, Wen, and Wei, who became famous. Wen later achieved high office.

    116

    张仁隂责
    　　唐张裼尚书典晋州外贮所爱营妓生一子其内子苏氏号尘外妬忌不敢取归乃与所善张处士为子居江津间常致书题问其存亡资以钱帛及渐成长教其读书有人吿以非处士之子尔父在朝官髙因窃其父与处士缄劄不吿而遁归京国裼公已薨至宅门僮仆无有识者但云江淮郎君兄弟皆愕然其嫡母苏夫人尘外泣而谓诸子曰诚有此子吾知之矣我少年无端致其父子死生永隔我罪多矣家眷聚泣取入宅齿诸兄弟之列名仁有文性好学脩词应进士举及第歴侍御史因奉使江浙于候馆自经而死莫知所为先是张处士怅恨而终必有防诉罹此祸也柱史为杨钜侍郎爱壻也

    Explanation

    116

    Zhang Rengui, secretly blamed.

    During the Tang dynasty, Zhang Ti, the Shangshu (Minister of State), was in charge of the storage of his beloved courtesan outside Jin Prefecture. She gave birth to a son, and his wife, Su, who was called "Dust Beyond," was jealous and did not dare to bring the child back. Instead, she lived with her favorite scholar, Zhang the recluse, and their son in Jiangjin. She often sent letters to inquire about his well-being and provided him with money and silk. As he gradually grew up, she taught him to read. Someone told him that he was not the recluse's son and that his father was a high-ranking official in the court. He then secretly took his father's and the recluse's letters and fled back to the capital without telling anyone. By the time he arrived, Zhang Ti had already passed away. When he reached the gate of the house, the servants did not recognize him, but they said he was the Jianghuai Langjun (a title for a nobleman). His brothers were all surprised. His legitimate mother, Su, the Lady Dust Beyond, wept and said to her children, "If there is such a son, I know him. I was young and caused the eternal separation of his father and son; my sins are many." The family gathered and wept, and they took him into the house, placing him among the brothers. He was named Zhang Rengui. He had a literary nature and was fond of learning and composing poetry. He passed the imperial examination and served as a censor. On a mission to Jiangzhe, he committed suicide by hanging at an inn, and no one knew what happened. Before that, the recluse had died in sorrow and regret, and there must have been some complaint or accusation that led to this calamity. The censor was the beloved son-in-law of Yang Ju, the Attendant Minister.

    117

    裴相国及第后进业
    　　唐相国裴公恒太和八年李汉侍郎下及第自以举业未精遽此叨忝未尝曲谢座主辞归鄠县别墅三年肄业不入城嵗时恩地唯启状而已至于同年邻于谢絶掩关勤苦文格乃变然始到京重献恩门文章词采典丽举朝称之后至大拜为时名相也夫世之干禄先资名第既得之后鲜不替懈自非笃于文学省顾賔实者安能及斯裴公庙堂之期有以见进徳之无斁也

    Explanation

    117

    After passing the imperial examination, the Minister of State Péi Xiangguó furthered his studies. In the eighth year of the Tahe era, he passed the examination under the supervision of Secretary Li Han. Believing his scholarly attainments were not yet refined, he felt unworthy of the honor and did not bow deeply in gratitude to his examiner, but instead returned to his villa in Hù County, where he studied diligently for three years without entering the city. During the seasons, he sent only formal letters to his benefactors. He largely avoided contact with his fellow examinees, closing himself off in seclusion and working with great diligence. His literary style thus changed. Only after returning to the capital did he once again present his writings to his former examiner, whose elegant and classical style was praised throughout the court. Later, he was appointed to a high-ranking official post and became a renowned statesman of his time. Indeed, in the world, those who seek official rank first rely on passing the examination; once obtained, few are not prone to slackness or decline. Unless one is deeply committed to scholarship and mindful of the responsibilities of office, how could one achieve what Péi Xiangguó accomplished? His time in the imperial court clearly demonstrated his unceasing moral and scholarly progress.

    侯泳忤豆卢相
    　　唐咸通中举子侯泳有声采亦士流也而阙于恭慎豆卢琢罢相守仆射乗闲诣僧院放仆乗他适而于僧宇独坐皤然一叟也泳自外入门殊不顾揖傲岸据榻谓叟曰大参长史乎叟曰非也又问曰令録乎亦曰非也逺州刺史乎亦曰稍髙又曰少卿监乎答曰更向上侯生矍然不安处疑是丞郎怱遽而出至门见仆御肩舆旋至方知是豆卢公也归去后自咎悚惕贡一长牋首过赖先曽有卷投献阍者通入泳乃自陈乖疎公亦逊谢恕其不相识也留而命酒凡劝十盂乃小惩也仍云虽不奉讶然凡事更宜在意侯生仍惭灼无以自容先是豆卢家昆弟饮清酒而已侯氏盛馔而饮此日每饮一杯回首摘席经咀之几不济所谓雅责也

    Hou Yong Offended Lord Doulu

    During the Xiantong era of the Tang Dynasty, Hou Yong, a scholar who was well-known and respected, lacked courtesy and prudence. Doulu Zhuo, a former chancellor who now held the position of Puyue, visited a temple during his leisure time, leaving his servants behind and sitting alone as an elderly man. Hou Yong entered the temple, paid no attention, and arrogantly sat on a bed, addressing the old man: "Are you a high-ranking official?" The old man replied, "No." Hou Yong then asked, "Are you a magistrate or recorder?" The old man again denied it. "Are you a distant prefect?" The old man said, "It is somewhat higher." "Are you a junior official?" The old man replied, "It is even higher." Hou Yong became startled and felt uncomfortable, suspecting it was a high-ranking official, and quickly left. At the door, he saw his servants and a sedan chair arriving, and only then realized it was Lord Doulu.

    After returning, Hou Yong felt guilty and wrote a long letter apologizing, relying on a previous introduction to get it delivered. Doulu Zhuo acknowledged the mistake and forgave him. Doulu Zhuo invited him to drink, offering ten cups, which was a mild punishment. He also warned him to be more careful in the future, and Hou Yong felt deeply ashamed. Previously, Doulu Zhuo's family drank only clear wine, while Hou Yong's family served elaborate meals. On this day, every time Doulu Zhuo drank, he picked up a text from the table and read it, almost spilling his drink, which was considered a sign of refinement.

    卢沆遇宣宗私行【贾岛附】
    　　唐陜州亷使卢沆在举场甚有时称曽于浐水逆旅遇宣宗皇帝微行意其贵人敛身回避帝揖与相见沆乃自称进士卢沆帝请诗卷袖之乗驴而去他日对大臣语及卢沆令主司擢第沆不自安恐僭冒之辱宰臣问沆与王上有何阶縁沆乃具陈因由时亦不讶以其文章非叨忝也沆后自亷察入朝知举遇黄冦犯阙不及终场赵崇大夫戏之曰出腹不生养主司也初卢家未尝知举卢相携耻之拔为主文竟不果也　贾岛遇宣宗微行问秀才名对曰贾岛帝曰久闻诗名岛曰何以知之后言于宰臣与平曽相次谪授长江尉所谓不识贵人也

    Explanation

    119

    Lu Hang, the censor of Shan Prefecture in the Tang Dynasty, was highly regarded in the examination hall. Once, he encountered Emperor Xuanzong on a private tour at an inn by the Chan River. Thinking he was a noble person, Lu Hang bowed and stepped aside. The emperor bowed and greeted him. Lu Hang then introduced himself as a scholar named Lu Hang. The emperor asked for his poetry scroll, put it in his sleeve, and left on a donkey. On another day, when speaking to the chancellors, he mentioned Lu Hang and ordered the chief examiner to promote him. Lu Hang felt uneasy and feared the shame of presumption. The chancellors asked Lu Hang what his connection with the emperor was. Lu Hang then fully explained the reasons. At the time, no one was surprised because his articles were not obtained through favoritism. Later, Lu Hang was promoted from censor to chief examiner. He encountered a yellow bandit who attacked the capital, and the examination was not completed. Zhao Chong, the doctor, joked, "Born out of the womb of the chief examiner." Initially, the Lu family had never known the chief examiner, and Lu Xiang carried the shame of not being promoted to the position.

    Jia Dao, a famous Tang Dynasty poet, met Emperor Xuanzong on a private tour. The emperor asked for the scholar's name, and the scholar replied, "Jia Dao." The emperor said, "I have heard of your poetry for a long time." Jia Dao asked, "How did you know?" Later, the emperor spoke to the chancellors and demoted Jia Dao to the position of vice-magistrate of Changjiang, saying, "He did not recognize a noble person."

    顾非熊再生
    　　唐著作郎顾况字逋翁好轻侮朝士贬在江外多与僧道交游时居茅山暮年有一子即非熊前身也一旦暴亡况追悼哀切所不忍言乃吟曰老人防爱子日暮泣成血老人年七十不作多时别非熊在防间闻之甚悲忆遂以情吿防官皆悯之遂商量却令生于况家三嵗能言防间闻父苦吟却求再生之事歴歴然长成应举擢进士第或有朝士问即垂泣而言之王定保摭言云人传况父子皆有所遇不知所适由此而言信有之矣
    　　张曙起小悼
    　　唐张祎侍郎朝望甚髙有爱姬早逝悼念不已因入朝未回其犹子右补阙曙才俊风流因増大阮之悲乃制浣溪纱其词曰枕障薰炉隔绣帏二年终日两相思好风明月始应知天上人间何处去旧欢新梦觉来时黄昏微雨画垂置于几上大阮朝退凭几无聊忽睹此诗不觉哀恸乃曰必是阿灰所作阿灰即中谏小字也然于风教还亦不可以其叔侄年顔相似恕之可耳谚曰小舅小叔相追相逐谑戏固不免也

    Explanation

    The Rebirth of Gu Feixiong

    Gu Kuang, a Tang Dynasty Literary Censor and known as Bo Weng, was fond of mocking court officials. He was exiled to the south of the Yangtze River and often associated with monks and Taoist priests. In his later years, he lived on Mount Mao and had a son who was the previous incarnation of Gu Feixiong. One day, Gu Kuang suddenly died. His grief was so profound that he could not bear to speak of it, and he recited:

    "An old man mourns his beloved son,
    Crying until tears turn to blood at sunset.
    The old man is seventy years old,
    We won't part for much longer."

    Gu Feixiong, in the mourning period, heard of it and was very sad and nostalgic. He then reported his feelings to the mourning officials, who all pitied him. They discussed and decided to bring him back to life in Gu's family. At three years old, he could already speak. In the mourning period, he heard his father's painful recitation and sought to understand the details of his rebirth. When he grew up, he passed the imperial examination to become a Jinshi. If court officials asked, he would cry and tell them. Wang Dingbao said in his Miscellaneous Notes that people said that both Gu and his son had encountered something but didn't know where to go. Therefore, it is credible.

    The Young Mourning of Zhang Shu

    Zhang Yi, a Tang Dynasty Langzhong, was highly respected in the court. He had a beloved concubine who died early, and he mourned endlessly. Because he went to court and did not return, his nephew, Zhang Shu, who was a Right Censor and talented and charming, increased the grief of the younger brother. He then composed a poem titled "Huan Xisha," the words said:

    "The pillow, incense burner, and embroidered curtain are separated.
    For two years, they longed for each other every day.
    Only the gentle wind and bright moon could understand.
    Where in heaven or on earth have you gone?
    Old joys and new dreams awaken when you realize.
    At dusk, with light rain, the curtain hangs down."

    He placed the poem on the table. The elder brother, after court, leaned against the table in boredom. Suddenly, he saw this poem and could not help but mourn deeply. He said, "It must have been written by Ahui." Ahui is the nickname of Zhong Jian. However, in terms of moral education, one cannot excuse the similarity in age and appearance between uncle and nephew. A proverb says, "Nephews and uncles chasing and playing pranks are inevitable."

    张裼尚书无忌讳
    　　唐张裼尚书恃才直道外仍有至性及第后归东都一日髣髴见其亡亲谓曰去得也遂办装入京果登朝籍不爽隂吿也东都柏坡有庄而多髙大屋宇中庭有土堆若冡人言其下时有乐声本主鬻之不售八座不信以善价买之遽令发掘其下乃麦麴耳以之和泥涂一院墙屋不假他求是知妖由人兴向使疑误神怪则有物凭焉必为村巫酒食之资也正直之人其可欺乎
    　　荆十三娘义侠事
    　　进士赵中行家于温州以豪侠为事至苏州旅止支山禅院僧房有一女商荆十三娘为亡夫设大祥斋因慕【一作日暮】赵遂同载归扬州赵以气耗荆之财殊不介意其友人李正朗第【一作郎弟】三十九爱一妓为其父母夺与诸葛殷李怅恨不已时诸葛殷与吕用之幻惑髙太尉恣行威福李惧祸饮泣而已偶话于荆娘荆娘亦愤惋谓李三十九郎曰此小事我能为郎报讐但请过江于润州北固山六月六日正午时待我李依之至期荆氏以囊盛妓兼致妓之父母首归于李后与赵进士同入浙中不知所止

    Explanation

    121

    Zhang Xi, the Shangshu, was without any taboos. During the Tang Dynasty, Zhang Xi, the Shangshu, relied on his talent and followed the straight path, yet still possessed a profound nature. After passing the imperial examination, he returned to the Eastern Capital. One day, he vaguely saw his deceased parents and they said, "You can go." He then prepared and traveled to the capital, and indeed entered the imperial register, not deviating from the hidden warning. In the Eastern Capital, at Baipo, he had a manor with many tall and grand buildings. The central courtyard had a mound of earth resembling a tomb. People said there was music from beneath it. The owner tried to sell it but couldn’t. The Eight Seats (high officials) did not believe, but bought it at a good price and rushed to have it excavated. What was found beneath was just barley malt, which was used to mix with mud and plaster the walls and houses of the courtyard, without needing anything else. This shows that strange phenomena arise from human actions. If one were to doubt and mistake it for a supernatural event, then there would be something relying on it, and it would certainly become the material for village shamans’ feasts. An honest and upright person cannot be deceived.

    The story of Jing Shisan娘, the righteous and heroic woman. Jinshi Zhao Zhongxing lived in Wenzhou and made a living as a hero and侠义 (righteous and heroic). Traveling to Suzhou and staying at Zhi Mountain Zen Temple, in a monk’s room, there was a female merchant named Jing Shisan娘, who set up a major memorial service for her deceased husband. Because of admiration for Zhao【or perhaps at dusk】, she traveled together back to Yangzhou. Zhao spent Jing’s money carelessly without any concern. His friend Li Zhenglang, the thirty-ninth【or perhaps his younger brother】, loved a courtesan. His parents took her and gave her to Zhu Ge Yin. Li Zhenglang was deeply resentful. At that time, Zhu Ge Yin and Lü Yongzhi were deceiving Gao Taiv, exercising arbitrary power and favor. Li Zhenglang feared disaster and could only cry in secret. Told Jing Shisan娘 by chance, Jing Shisan娘 was also angry and sorrowful. She said to Li Zhenglang, the thirty-ninth, "This is a small matter; I can avenge you. Just cross the river to Ruzhou’s Beigushan Mountain on the sixth day of the sixth lunar month at noon to wait for me." Li Zhenglang followed her. On the appointed day, Jing Shisan娘 put the courtesan and the courtesan’s parents’ heads in a bag and returned them to Li Zhenglang. Later, she and Zhao Jinshi entered Zhezhong together, and their whereabouts are unknown.

    　　唐李当尚书镇兴元褒城县有处士陈休复者号陈七子狎于博徒行止非常八座以其妖诞械之于市井之间又有一休复无何殒于狴牢遽睹腐败辖司申而瘗之尔后宛在褒城八座惊异不敢寻问一旦爱女暴亡其内子追悼成疾无以救疗幕客有白八座曰陈处士真道者必有少君之术能祈之乎八座然之因敬信延召陈生曰此小事尔于初夜帷堂设灯炬画作一门请夫人下屏气至夜分亡者自画门入堂中行数遭夫人愊臆失声而哭亡魂倏而灭矣然后戒勉令其抑割八座由是益敬之

    The Soul of Li Dang's Deceased Daughter
    During the Tang Dynasty, Li Dang, the Shangshu, was stationed in Baocheng County, where there lived a recluse scholar named Chen Xiufu, known as Chen Qi Zi. He was overly familiar with gamblers and acted in an unusual manner. The high-ranking officials, the "Eight Seats," considered him a fraud and publicly humiliated him in the marketplace. Another Chen Xiufu died in prison, and his body was quickly buried by the prison authorities. After this, Chen Qi Zi seemed to reappear in Baocheng, and the officials were surprised and hesitant to investigate. One day, Li Dang's beloved daughter suddenly died, and his wife grieved to the point of illness. One of the officials suggested to Li Dang that Chen Qi Zi, the recluse scholar, must have some minor deity's method and could possibly help. Li Dang agreed and began to respect and invite Chen Qi Zi. Chen Qi Zi said, "This is a minor matter. On the first night, set up a room covered with a curtain and light some lamps. Draw a door and invite the lady to enter, holding her breath. At midnight, the deceased daughter will enter the room through the drawn door. The lady will be deeply moved and cry, and the soul will disappear suddenly." Then, he warned and advised the lady to suppress her emotions. The officials became even more respectful of Chen Qi Zi.

    From the "Běi Mèng Suǒ Yán" Volume Eight
    <Department of Literature, Novels, Miscellaneous Stories, Běi Mèng Suǒ Yán>

    Imperially Approved Siku Quanshu
    Northern Dreams: Trivial Sayings, Volume Nine
    Compiled by Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Meng Hongwei's Rashness

    During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang, Meng Hongwei, a Langzhong (Officer of the Ministry of Rites), was reckless and unbound by convention. On one occasion, during a court session, he said, "Why does the Emperor not know of me? Why does he not summon me through literary talent?" The Emperor was furious and replied, "Who are you, sir? I have never heard of you at all." The next day, the Emperor told the prime ministers, "This man is rash and arrogant. If he desires to become an Academician of the Hanlin Academy, it will be very easy for him." The prime ministers then returned to the Ministry of State Affairs and demoted him, giving him a minor punishment.

    On another occasion, Meng was filled with resentment and jealousy, and he pushed his younger brother into a well. When public opinion became heated, he wrote to his relatives and friends, saying, "I am half-hanging over the well, and rumors are boiling like a storm. A small ripple becomes a great wave—this is a common occurrence in ancient and modern times."

    Meng lived next to Zheng Feng, who served as an official in Nanhai. When the wall collapsed, a zhonglang (or langzhong) encroached upon the boundary by five to six chi (or zhang). The person in charge of the estate submitted a petition requesting the return of the encroached land. The judge ruled on the case, saying: "An official stationed in the southern frontier rarely returns alive. The terrain is steep and sloped, and walls naturally shift inward. His conduct in life has always been like this. To not be expelled would be fortunate enough."

    Yang Xiangguo's Vengeance Against Yang Yuanjia

    During the Tang Dynasty, Yang Xiangguo, the Chancellor, was exiled and died in the southern frontier. At that time, Minister Zheng Yu was governing Nanhai. One day, a messenger suddenly arrived and announced, "Chancellor Yang is waiting in the guest hall and wishes to see Minister Zheng." The eight high-ranking officials were greatly alarmed, for it was said that Yang had recently received an imperial decree from the capital—how could he possibly have come here? They welcomed him nonetheless.

    Chancellor Yang said, "I was falsely accused by Yang Yuanjia, the Commandant of the Army, and unfortunately met my death. Now I have received permission from Heaven and have been granted an army of spirits to avenge myself. I wish to entrust you, Minister Zheng, with a banquet in my honor and also to borrow ten thousand strings of copper coins." Zheng of Xingyang agreed, but when it came to the money, he excused himself, saying that the military affairs were too numerous, and offered only half. Chancellor Yang said, "These are not copper coins. When you burn them, please be careful not to let them touch the ground." Zheng replied,

    124

    若此则固得遵副从容间长揖而灭荥阳令于北郊具酒馔素钱以祭之杨相犹子有典寿阳者见相国乗白马臂朱弓撚彤矢有朱衣天吏控马谓之曰上帝许我讐杀杨元价我射着其脚必死也俄而【抄本有一中字】杨中尉暴染脚疾而殂蜀毛文锡司徒先德前潮【一作湖】牧范曾趋事郑尚书熟详其事愚于毛氏子闻之
    　　刘山甫题天王
    　　唐彭城刘山甫中朝士族也其先宦于岭外侍从北归泊船于青草湖登岸见有北方毘沙门天王因诣之见庙宇摧頽香灯不续山甫少年而有才思元随张处权请郎君咏之乃题诗曰坏墙风雨几经春草色盈庭一座尘自是神明无感应盛衰何得却由人是夜梦为天王所责自云我非天王南岳神也主张此池【一作地】汝何相侮俄而惊觉而风浪斗起倒樯絶缆沈溺在即遽起悔过令撤诗牌然后已山甫自序

    If this is the case, then it is inevitable that one would casually bow and eliminate the magistrate of Xingyang in the northern suburbs, preparing food, drink, and white money to offer as a sacrifice. Yang's nephew, who was the governor of Shouyang, saw the prime minister riding a white horse, wearing a red bow, and holding a red arrow, with an official in red clothes controlling the horse and telling him, saying, "Heaven has allowed me to kill Yang Yuanjia as revenge. I will shoot his foot, and he will certainly die." Soon after, Yang, the military officer, suddenly contracted a foot disease and died. The person from the Mao family, a descendant of the Mao family, who served diligently for the Zheng Shangshu, heard this.

    D Liu Shanfu wrote about the Heavenly King

    During the Tang Dynasty, Liu Shanfu, a prominent family of the central court from Pengcheng, had ancestors who served in the Lingnan region and accompanied the court northward, docking their boat at Qingcao Lake. He went ashore and saw the Northern Vaisravana Heavenly King, so he went to see him. He saw the temple in ruins and the incense and lamps not lit. From that point on, the deity had no response. How can prosperity and decline be determined by people? That night, he dreamed of being blamed by the Heavenly King, who said to himself, "I am not the Heavenly King or the Southern Mountain God. I am responsible for this pond [or place]. Why do you insult me?" Soon after, he awoke in shock as the wind and waves rose, the masts fell, and the ropes broke; they were about to sink. He immediately got up, repented, ordered the removal of the poem, and then it was over. Liu Shanfu wrote an autobiographical note.

    韦宰相功徳騐【陈防附】
    　　蜀路白卫岭多虎豹噬人有选人京兆韦亡其名唐光化中调授巴南宰常念金刚经赴任至泥溪遇一女人着绯衣挈二子偕行同登此山前路岭头行人相驻叫噪见此女人乃赤貍大虫也逡巡与韦分路而去韦终不觉盖持经之力也　成都府广都县人陈微自少年常诵金刚经与胥姓马者有隙一旦事故亡匿马生扬言欲追捕之陈乃砺一匕首行坐相随傥遇马生必能刺之誓不受其执録【一作僇字】或一日行于村路蓊荟间马胥伏而掩之陈抽刀一挥马生仰倒由是获脱至前方悟手之所挥乃刀鞘及归所匿处刀刃宛在本不偕行马胥亦无所伤何其异也
    　　刺血写经僧

    The Virtues and Deeds of Chancellor Wei [With Commentary by Chen Fang]

    In the Sichuan road, the White Wei Ridge is known for its tigers and leopards that prey on people. There was a candidate from Jingzhao named Wei, whose name is unknown. During the Guanghua period of the Tang Dynasty, he was appointed as the governor of Banan. He often recited the Diamond Sutra. On his way to take office, he reached Mudichuan where he encountered a woman dressed in a red robe carrying two children. They walked together up the mountain, but at the top of the ridge, the travelers stopped and shouted. They saw that the woman was actually a large red panther. After a short while, she and Wei went their separate ways. Wei was unaware of this, as it was the power of reciting the sutra that protected him.

    Chen Wei, a person from Guangdu County in Chengdu, had been reciting the Diamond Sutra since his youth. He had a grudge against a man named Ma, who belonged to the surname Xu. One day, Chen went into hiding after an incident. Ma publicly announced that he would pursue and capture Chen. In response, Chen sharpened a dagger and carried it with him at all times, swearing that if he met Ma, he would definitely stab him and would not allow himself to be caught.

    One day, as Chen was walking through a dense forest path, Ma suddenly attacked him. Chen drew his dagger and swung it, and Ma fell backward. Chen realized that what he had swung was the scabbard, not the blade. Upon returning, he found that the blade was still intact, and Ma was also unharmed. How strange this was!

    The Monk Who Wrote Sutras with Blood

    During the Xiantong period of the Tang Dynasty, a monk named Fajin from Western Sichuan wrote sutras using his own blood. He gathered people to teach at the Temple of Teaching. The authorities reported this to High Yan Public, who issued a judgment saying: "A person who has cut off their arm is already dangerous; writing sutras with blood is not a good deed. The leaves of the Bodhi tree should not be defiled by the dust of the world; how can a vulgar person's body bear the stench? It is appropriate to order him to leave the country and not deceive people. With a rope, he was sent out to the eastern boundary." The authorities did not understand the meaning of the rope and gave him a thousand coins, sending him out of the eastern city gate. Fortunately, he escaped by mistake and later died at the Jade Spring Temple in Jingzhou.

    126

    成令公掷杯珓事
    　　荆州成令公汭唐天复中准诏统军救援江夏舟楫之盛近代罕闻已决行期不聴谏诤师次公安县寺有二金刚神土人号曰二圣亦甚有灵中令舣舟而谒之炷香防诚冥祷胜以求杯珓隂阳之兆凡三十掷皆不吉乃谓所信孔目官杨师厚曰卦之不吉如之何师厚对曰令公数年造船旌旗已启中路而退将何面目回见军民于是不得已而进竟有破阵之败身死家破非偶然也向使杨子察人之情幸其意怠一言而止则成氏灭亡未可知也
    　　白莲女惑苏昌逺
    　　唐中和中有士人苏昌远居苏台属邑有小庄去官道十里吴中水乡率多荷芰忽见一女郎素衣红脸容质絶丽阅其明悟神仙中人自是与之相狎以庄为幽会之所苏生惑之既甚尝以玉环赠之结殷勤或一日见槛前白莲花开敷荣殊异俯而翫之见花房中有物细视之乃所赠玉环也因折之其妖遂絶神无形必凭于物精气所附非菡萏之能哉闻于刘山甫
    　　栁鹏举诱五妓

    Explanation

    126

    The Story of General Cheng Throwing the Divination Sticks

    During the Tianfu period of the Tang Dynasty, General Cheng Rui was ordered by imperial decree to lead an army to rescue Jiangxia. The grandeur of his fleet was rarely heard of in recent times. Having already decided the departure date, he did not listen to advice. His troops camped at Gongan County, where there were two Golden Warrior Gods, locally known as the "Two Saints," who were also very powerful. General Cheng anchored his boat and paid homage to them, burning incense and praying sincerely for divine guidance. He used the divination sticks to seek auspicious signs, but after thirty throws, all were inauspicious. He then turned to his trusted official, Yang Shihou, and said, "The divination is not auspicious. What shall we do?" Yang replied, "General, you have spent years building ships and raising banners. If we retreat halfway, how will we face our soldiers and civilians?" Thus, General Cheng, having no choice, advanced, and ultimately suffered a defeat in the battle, dying and having his family destroyed. This was not an accident. If Yang had noticed the general's hesitation and spoken up, the Cheng family might have been spared.

    The White Lotus Maiden Bewitches Su Changyuan

    During the Zhonghe period of the Tang Dynasty, a scholar named Su Changyuan lived in a small village near Suzhou, ten miles from the official road. In the water-rich region of Wu, lotus flowers were abundant. One day, Su suddenly saw a maiden dressed in white with a red face, whose beauty and intelligence seemed otherworldly, like a goddess. From then on, he became intimate with her, using the small farm as a secret meeting place. Su was deeply bewitched by her. Once, he gave her a jade ring as a token of his affection. One day, he saw a white lotus bloom in front of the fence, unusually beautiful. He bent down to admire it and noticed something inside the flower. Upon closer inspection, it was the jade ring he had given her. He picked it up, and the enchantment ended. Ghosts and spirits, though invisible, must rely on objects to manifest. The power of such enchantments is beyond the capabilities of mere lotus flowers. This story was told by Liu Shanfu.

    Liu Pengju Lures the Five-Stringed Courtesans

    Liu Pengju lured the five-stringed courtesans.

    唐龙纪中有士人栁鹏举游杭州避雨于伍相庙见一女子抱五云是钱大夫家女仆鹏举悦之遂诱而奔藏于舟中为厢吏所捕其女仆自缢而死或一日却到栁处栁亦知其物故惊讶其来女仆具道其情因以魂偶【一作谒】经时而去见刘山甫闲谈中
    　　云芳子魂事李茵
    　　僖宗幸蜀年有进士李茵襄州人奔窜南山民家见一宫娥自云宫中侍书家云芳子有才思与李同行诣蜀具述宫中之事兼曾有诗书红叶上流出御沟中即此姬也行及绵州逢内官田大夫识之乃曰书家何得在此逼令上马与之前去李甚怏怅无可【一作以】奈何宫娥与李情爱至深至前驿自缢而死其魂追及李生具道忆恋之意迨数年李茵病瘠有道士言其面有邪气云芳子自陈人殊途吿辞而去闻于刘山甫
    　　刍灵祟
    　　唐文徳中小京官张忘其名寓苏台子弟少年时在丈人陆评事院往来为一美人所悦来往多时心疑之寻病瘠遇开元观吴道士守元曰子有不祥之气授以一符果一冥器婢子背书红英字在空舍柱穴中因焚之其妖乃絶闻于刘山甫

    Explanation

    127

    During the Longqing period of the Tang dynasty, a scholar named Liu Pengju traveled to Hangzhou to escape the rain and took shelter at the temple of Wu Xiang. There, he saw a woman holding five strings (the character "" is unclear and may be a typo or obscure term; it will be marked as uncertain). She claimed to be a servant of the wealthy family of Qiandai. Liu Pengju was attracted to her and lured her away, hiding in a boat with her. They were captured by a local official, and her servant committed suicide by hanging. On one day, the servant returned to Liu's place. Liu also knew that she had passed away and was surprised by her appearance. The servant fully explained the situation, and Liu met with her spirit after some time, leaving in casual conversation.

    The story of Yun Fangzi's spirit is as follows: During the year when Emperor Xizong fled to Shu, a scholar-official named Li Yin, a native of Xiangzhou, fled to the home of a commoner in the southern mountains. There, he met a palace attendant and scribe named Yun Fangzi, who had talent and thoughts. She traveled with Li to Shu and fully described the affairs of the palace, including that she had once written poems on red leaves that flowed down the imperial moat. When they reached Mianzhou, they met the court official Tian, who recognized her and said, "How can a palace attendant be here?" He forced her to mount a horse and left with her. Li was very unhappy and had no recourse. The palace attendant and scribe had deep affection for Li, and at the inn ahead, she committed suicide by hanging. Her spirit pursued Li, fully explaining her feelings of longing. For several years, Li Yin became ill and emaciated. A Taoist said that he had an evil aura. Yun Fangzi explained that humans and ghosts have different paths and bade farewell, leaving. This was heard by Liu Shanfu.

    The story of the spirit of a straw effigy is as follows: During the Wude period of the Tang dynasty, a minor official named Zhang, whose name is forgotten, lived among the young nobles of Suzhou. He frequented a beautiful woman who favored him for a long time and began to suspect her. Soon, he became ill and emaciated. He met the Taoist Wu Shouyuan of the Kaiyuan Temple, who gave him a talisman. Indeed, a soulless servant girl with the name Hong Ying written on her back was found in the empty house, in a column hole. He burned her, and the evil spirit was thus dispelled. This was heard by Liu Shanfu.

    髙燕公神笔
    　　淮海小将姓朱忘其名有女未嫁为物所祟常呼韩郎往来如生人唯不见形奉外舅姑礼自云天朝神朱以异事不敢秘乃吿府主髙燕公公唯书名俾朱归帖于女房门上其邪来见咨嗟言别而去闻于刘山甫
    　　鱼机【徐月英附】
    　　唐女道鱼机字蕙兰甚有才思咸通中为李亿补阙执箕帚后爱衰下山咸宜观为女道士有怨李公诗曰易求无价寳难得有心郎又云蕙兰销歇归春浦杨栁东西伴客舟自是纵怀乃娼妇也竟以杀侍婢为京兆尹温璋杀之有集行于世　江淮间有徐月英亦娼者其送人诗云惆怅人间事久违两人同去一人归生憎平望亭前水忍照鸳鸯相背飞【一本又有云枕前泪与阶前雨隔个闲牕滴到明】亦有诗集金陵徐氏诸公子宠一营妓卒乃焚之月英送葬谓徐公曰此娘平生风流没亦带焰时号美戏也唐末有北里志其间即孙尚书储数贤平康狎游之事或云孙棨舍人所撰

    Explanation

    Translation:

    The Divine Pen of Lord Yan

    There was a small general from Huaihai, surnamed Zhu, whose name is forgotten. He had a daughter who, before her marriage, was tormented by ghostly things. She often called out to Han Lang, who came and went like a living person, though only not seen in form. She observed the proper etiquette towards her father-in-law and mother-in-law, and claimed that the Heavenly Court's God Zhu, due to extraordinary events, dared not keep secret, so he informed the head of the government, High Lord Yan. The lord only wrote a name and ordered Zhu to return and post it on the girl's room door. The evil spirit came to see, sighed, said goodbye, and left, and this was reported to Liu Shanfu.

    Fish Xuanji [with Xu Yueying appended]

    Fish Xuanji, a Tang dynasty female Daoist, also known as Huilan, was very talented. During the Xiantong era, she served as a concubine to Li Yi, holding a broom. After her love waned, she left the mountain and became a female Daoist at the Xianyi Temple. She wrote a poem expressing resentment towards Li Gong, saying, "It is easy to seek an invaluable treasure, but it is hard to find a man with a heart." She also wrote, "Huilan fades and returns to the spring pond, willows on both sides accompany the guest boat." Letting her heart go, she became a courtesan. Finally, she was killed by the Jingzhao Governor Wen Zhang for killing a servant girl. Her collection was published in the world.

    In the Jianghuai region, there was Xu Yueying, also a courtesan. Her poem for sending someone off said, "Longing for human affairs that have been long absent, two people go together, one returns. Hating the water in front of Pingwang Pavilion, enduring the sight of mandarin ducks flying apart." [One version also says, "Tears before the pillow and rain before the steps, dripping through a quiet window until dawn."] She also had a collection of poems. In Jinling, the sons of the Xu family favored a camp prostitute, who was burned to death. Xu Yueying accompanied the funeral and said to Xu Gong, "This woman's lifelong charm even in death carries a flame." At that time, she was called the beautiful play.

    At the end of the Tang dynasty, there was a record of the Northern Market, among which were the accounts of Sun Shangshu's collection of several virtuous men and their licentious entertainments. Some say it was written by Sun Qi, the Shangshu.

    李氏女
    　　唐广明中黄巢犯阙大驾幸蜀衣冠荡析冦盗纵横有西班李将军女奔波随人迤逦达兴元骨肉分散无所依托适值凤翔奏将军董司马者乃晦其门阀以身托之而性甚明敏善于承奉得至于蜀寻访亲眷知在行朝始谓董生曰防乱之中女弱不能自济幸提挈以至于此失身之事非不幸也人各有偶难为偕老请自此辞董生惊愕遂下其山矣识者谓女子之智亦足称也见刘山甫闲谈
    　　冯藻慕名
    　　唐冯藻常侍肃之子涓之叔父世有科名小貂文采不髙酷爱名第已十五举有相识道士谓曰先辈某曽入靖观之此生无名第但有官职也亦未之信更应十举已二十五举矣姻亲劝令罢举且谋官职藻曰譬如一生无成更誓五举亦无成遂三十举方就仕歴官卿监峡牧终于骑省何浮名之引人而轻禄仕之如是也

    Explanation

    129

    Translation:

    Li's Daughter

    During the Guangming era of the Tang dynasty, when Huang Chao rebelled and the imperial court fled to Shu, the aristocracy was scattered, and bandits roamed freely. A daughter of a general from the Western Palace was forced to flee with others, eventually reaching Xingyuan, where her family was broken apart and she had no support. She coincidentally met General Dong Sima of Fengxiang, who, to conceal his family background, took her under his protection. She was very intelligent and quick-witted, skilled in serving and pleasing others, and thus managed to reach Shu. After searching for her relatives, she learned that they were still traveling. She then said to General Dong, "In the midst of chaos, women are weak and cannot save themselves. I am fortunate to have been taken care of by you until now. Losing my virtue in such circumstances is not a misfortune. Everyone has their own partner, and it is difficult to stay together for life. Please allow me to leave." General Dong was startled and she descended from the mountain. Those who understood the situation said that the intelligence of this woman was worthy of praise, as recorded in Liu Shanfu's idle talk.

    Feng Zao's Admiration for Fame

    Feng Zao, a retainer of the Tang dynasty, was the son of Feng Su, the uncle of Feng Juan. His family had a long history of passing the imperial examinations, but Feng Zao himself had little literary talent. He was obsessed with fame and had taken the exams fifteen times. A Taoist priest he knew said, "I once observed your predecessor and saw that this life would not bring you fame, but only an official position." Feng Zao did not believe this and continued to take the exams for another ten times, totaling twenty-five attempts. His relatives advised him to stop taking the exams and to seek an official position. Feng Zao replied, "If I have never succeeded in my life, I will swear to take five more exams, but I will still not succeed. I finally took the exams thirty times and obtained an official position, serving as a high-ranking official, a governor of Xiang, and eventually a high official in the imperial court. How much the empty fame attracts, and how lightly official positions are treated, is evident in my case."

    李涪尚书改切韵
    　　唐李涪尚书福相之子以开元礼及第亦【一作不】为小文好著述朝廷重其博学礼乐之事谘禀之时人号为周礼库盖籍于旧典也广明以前切韵多用吴音而清青之字不必分用涪改切韵【一有其上声】全刋吴音当方进而闻于宰相佥许之无何巢冦犯阙因而寝止于今无人敢以声韵措怀也然曾见韵铨鄙駮切韵改正吴音亦甚覈当不知八座于此又何防制也惜哉古之制字卷纸题名姓号曰名纸大中年薛保逊为举塲头角人皆体效方作门状洎后仍以所怀列于启事随启诣公相门号为门状门启虽繁于名纸各便于时也书云谨祗候起居郎某官即是起居在前某官在后至今颠倒无人改更矣有朝廷改之亦美事也

    Explanation

    130

    Minister Li Fu’s Reform of the Qieyun

    Minister Li Fu, son of Li Fu Xiang of the Tang dynasty, passed the imperial examination based on the Opening Rituals (Kaiyuan Li) and, although [one version reads "not"], was known for writing small essays and enjoying scholarly composition. The imperial court valued his extensive knowledge of rites and music, and officials often consulted him on such matters. At that time, he was known among his contemporaries as the "Repository of Zhou Rites," as he drew upon ancient texts. Before the Guangming era, the Qieyun (a rhyme dictionary) largely used the Wu pronunciation, and the characters qing and qing were not necessarily distinguished. Li Fu revised the Qieyun [one version includes "its upper tone"], completely removing the Wu pronunciation. When the time was right, he presented his revision to the prime ministers, who all approved. However, shortly after, the rebel Chao attacked the imperial palace, and thus the reform was abandoned. To this day, no one dares to concern themselves with phonology. Yet I have seen the Yunquan (a later rhyme book), which is biased and flawed, yet its correction of the Wu pronunciation is quite accurate. It is a pity that the eight high-ranking officials (the Ba Zuo) did not impose any restrictions on this matter. Alas! In ancient times, the practice of writing one’s name on a sheet of paper, inscribing one’s surname and title, was called mingzhi (name paper). During the Dazhong era, Xue Baoxun became a prominent figure in the examination hall, and others followed his example, composing menzhuang (door notes). Later, people continued to list their intentions in petitions, delivering them to the gates of high officials, which came to be called menzhuang. Though menzhuang and menqi (door petitions) are more elaborate than mingzhi, they each suited their time. The Book of Documents says: "With respectful greetings, the official of the Office of the Emperor’s Daily Activities, [such-and-such official]." This means that the title qiju lang (official of the Office of the Emperor’s Daily Activities) comes first, followed by the official's rank. Yet to this day, the order is reversed, and no one has corrected it. If the court were to make this change, it would be a fine thing.

    穆李非命
    　　唐监察李航福相之子美茂洽畅播于时流黄巢后扶侍圣善归东都别墅与御史穆延晦同行宿于虢州公馆翌日脩谒郡牧张存即王拱下部将也谓典客曰我受穆家恩命今穆侍御经过必须展分报答也典客诣馆话于穆生因修状谒谢张公大怒且曰此言得自何人具以典谒为对乃斩谒者穆生惊怪失意归馆寻遣人就而害之李监察不喻方抱忧惶俄亦
    遇害将以灭口于时李公绕圣善所憩之牀无以求活竟同非命他日兄弟诉寃梦航谓骨肉间曰张存已得请于上帝不日即死果为拱所诛葆光子尝读李肇国史补曰李公沂曾放死囚他日道次遇之其人感恩延归其家与妻议所酬之物妻嫌数少此人曰酬物少不如杀之李公急走遇侠士方免此祸常以为虚诞今张存翻害穆李即史补之説信非虚诞也怪哉

    Explanation

    131

    The Unfortunate Fate of the Mu and Li Families

    During the Tang Dynasty, Li Hang, a censor, had a son named Li Meim, who was well-regarded and influential in his time. After the Yellow Turban Rebellion, Li Meim supported and cared for the virtuous in their return to their villa in the Eastern Capital. He traveled with the censor Mu Yanhui and stayed overnight at the public hall in the state of Guo. The next day, they paid respects to the governor of the prefecture, Zhang Cun, who was a subordinate of Wang Gong. Zhang Cun told the official in charge of guests, "I have received a favor from the Mu family. Now that the censor Mu is passing through, I must show my gratitude." The official went to the inn and spoke to Mu, who then wrote a letter to express his thanks. Governor Zhang became very angry and said, "Who said this?" He answered that it was the official in charge of guests. Zhang then ordered the execution of the official. Mu was surprised and disappointed and returned to the inn. Soon after, he sent someone to harm him. The censor Li did not understand what was happening and was soon also killed to eliminate any witnesses. At the time, Li Gong Yi, who was staying near the villa of the virtuous, had no means to save himself and thus shared the same fate. Later, his brothers complained about the injustice. In a dream, Hang told his family members, "Zhang Cun has already asked God and will die soon; indeed, he was killed by Wang Gong." The Keeper of Light once read in Li Zhao's Supplement to the National History: "Li Gong Yi once released a condemned prisoner who later met him on the road and was grateful. He invited him home, and his wife discussed what to give him. She thought the gift was too small, and the man said, 'If the gift is too small, it's better to kill him.' Li quickly ran away and met a hero who saved him from this disaster. He often thought this was a fairy tale." Strange indeed.
