    王给事刚鲠
    　　唐王祝给事名家子以刚鲠自任仍以所尚垂训子孙嫌人柔弱【一作懦】又素有物力殖利极丰黄冦前尝典常州京国乱离盘旋江湖甚有时望急诏征回归装极厚水陆分载行至甘棠王拱帅于是邦不式王命凶暴众闻以夕拜将来必居廊庙延奉勤至夕拜鄙其武人殊不降接拱乃于内防盛张宴席备列珍翫下妓乐齐列其内子亦映共拱立乃敛容向夕拜曰某虽武夫叨忝旄今日多幸获遇轩盖经过不弃末宗
    愿居子侄之列即荣幸也夕拜不允坚抗再三拱勃然作色曰给事王程有限不敢淹留俄而罢宴处分两辖速请王给事离馆暗授意防并令害之一家上下悉投黄河获其囊三四百笼以舟行没溺闻奏朝廷多故舍而不问夕拜有一子此际行至襄州无故投井而卒虽陜帅狂暴亦未喻天意也葆光子曰刚有立事时有用舍以柔济刚不爽权变当衰乱之世须适时之宜王公傥受其致敬庸何伤哉但却其赂即善也履尾灭族悲夫

    Explanation

    132

    Wang Zuo, the Right Attendant, was known for his uprightness and integrity. A man from a distinguished family, he took pride in his own firmness and honesty, and he set an example for his descendants by emphasizing the importance of uprightness. He disliked people who were gentle or lacking in strength. He had always been adept at accumulating wealth and resources through diligent effort and business acumen. Before Huang Chou, a military leader, had once governed Changzhou, the capital city was in a state of chaos and disorder, and Wang Zuo had been wandering in exile, often in a state of uncertainty. However, he had gained considerable reputation and was summoned back by an urgent imperial edict. His return preparations were lavish, and he transported his belongings by both water and land in separate batches. He arrived at Gan Tang, where Wang Gong, the governor of the region, was in power. Wang Gong ignored the king's orders and acted with cruelty and violence. When Wang Zuo heard that Wang Gong was expecting him, he believed that he would be treated as a junior member of the family, implying a position of respect but not equality. Wang Zuo was welcomed and served with great diligence, but Wang Gong looked down on military men and did not treat him with the same respect. Wang Gong then held a grand banquet in the inner hall, arranging precious treasures and beautiful objects in rows. Musicians and entertainers were placed in the center, and Wang Gong's wife also appeared. Wang Gong assumed a serious and respectful demeanor and addressed Wang Zuo, saying, "Although I am a mere military officer, I have been honored with this position. Today, I am fortunate to meet you, a nobleman passing through. I would not dare to neglect your presence." Wang Zuo replied, "I would be honored to be treated as a junior member of your family." Wang Gong refused, insisting that Wang Zuo accept his respect. Wang Gong became furious and said, "The king's schedule is limited, and I cannot delay your departure. I will immediately dismiss the banquet and arrange for your departure." He secretly instructed his subordinates to order the destruction of Wang Zuo's family. The entire family, including the servants, were thrown into the Yellow River. Wang Zuo's belongings were found in several hundred bags, which were lost when they drowned while traveling by boat. The incident was reported to the court, but due to the many pressing matters, it was ignored. Wang Zuo's son, who was traveling to Xiangzhou at the time, drowned in a well without any apparent reason. Although Wang Gong was known for his violent and oppressive behavior, he did not understand the will of heaven. Bao Guangzi commented, "Uprightness has its place in action, and there is a time to use and a time to set aside. To balance strength with gentleness is the right approach. In times of decline and disorder, one must act according to the appropriate time. If Wang Gong had accepted Wang Zuo's respect, what harm could it have done? Refusing bribes is a sign of integrity, but treading on the tail of a tiger leads to one's own destruction. It is a tragic outcome."

    133

    裴杨操尚
    　　唐杨収段文昌皆以孤进贵为宰相率爱奢侈杨相女适裴坦长子嫁资丰厚什器多用金银坦尚俭闻之不乐一日与国号及儿女辈到新妇院台上用碟盛果实坦欣然视碟子内乃卧鱼犀遽推倒茶台拂袖而出乃曰破我家也他日収相果以纳赂竟至不令宜哉
    　　出腹不生养卢侍郎
    　　卢氏衣冠第一歴代未尝知举干符中卢携在中书歉宗人无掌文柄乃擢羣从陜虢观察使卢渥知礼闱是嵗十二月黄巢犯阙僖皇播迁举子星散迨収复京都裴贽连知三举渥有羡色赵崇大夫戏之曰閤下所谓出腹不生养主司也【一本无养字】

    裴杨操尚
    Moral and Conduct of the Pei and Yang Families

    • 唐杨収段文昌皆以孤进贵为宰相率爱奢侈杨相女适裴坦长子嫁资丰厚什器多用金银坦尚俭闻之不乐一日与国号及儿女辈到新妇院台上用碟盛果实坦欣然视碟子内乃卧鱼犀遽推倒茶台拂袖而出乃曰破我家也他日収相果以纳赂竟至不令宜哉
    • Yang Shou and Duan Wenchang, both humble-born chancellors, were fond of luxury. Yang Shou's daughter married Pei Tan's eldest son, and the dowry was rich, with many utensils made of gold and silver. Pei Tan, who preferred frugality, was unhappy when he heard about it. One day, he and his family went to the new bride's room, where a dish containing a sleeping fish-shaped rhinoceros was placed. He immediately pushed over the tea table and left in anger, saying, "Ruining my family!" Later, Yang Shou was indeed implicated in bribery and was dismissed from office.

    出腹不生养卢侍郎
    Lu Wo, the Scholar-Official

    • 卢氏衣冠第一歴代未尝知举干符中卢携在中书歉宗人无掌文柄乃擢羣从陜虢观察使卢渥知礼闱是嵗十二月黄巢犯阙僖皇播迁举子星散迨収复京都裴贽连知三举渥有羡色赵崇大夫戏之曰閤下所谓出腹不生养主司也
    • The Lu family, which has been the first among the gentry for generations, has never known to hold a position. In the year 874, Lu Xie, who was in the Central Secretariat, felt sorry for his relatives who did not hold positions, and he promoted his distant relatives to be the governor of Shaanxi and Guo. Lu Wo, who knew the examination hall, in the twelfth month of that year, Huang Chao attacked the imperial palace, Emperor Xizong fled, scholars scattered, until the capital was recaptured, and Pei Zhi was responsible for multiple examinations. Lu Wo envied him, and Zhao Chong, a scholar-official, joked, "You are the examiner who does not raise or nurture those born from the womb."

    张兴师决门僧
    　　唐相国张濬二子一曰义师即小字也本名格为蜀相一曰兴师忘其名后号李将军名俨与父达军机于淮海亦遇害也格与兴师昆弟俊迈而尚矫谲皆有父风兴师防年出宅门见其门僧忘其名传相国处分七笞之其僧邂逅莫知何罪俄而相国召僧坐安见其词色不怿因问之僧以郎君传相国处分见怪未知罪名相国惊骇惭谢以儿子狂骇幸师慈悲回至堂前唤兴师怒责之且曰汝见僧何罪而敢造次对曰今日虽无罪过想其向来恶不少是以笞之相国不觉失笑此卷第十九条载陜虢观察使卢渥与八卷陜州亷使卢沆事同疑沆渥自是一人孙氏偶不照而重出耳

    　　北梦琐言卷九
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰

    Explanation

    134

    Zhang Xingshi and the Monk at the Gate

    During the Tang Dynasty, Chancellor Zhang Jun had two sons. One was named Zhang Ge, with the courtesy name Ge, who served as a chancellor in the Later Shu state. The other son was named Zhang Xingshi, who later became a general named Li, with the courtesy name Yan. Both brothers followed in their father's footsteps and were known for their outstanding qualities and somewhat cunning nature.

    One day, Zhang Xingshi left his house and saw a monk at the gate. He did not remember the monk's name but recalled that the chancellor had ordered the monk to be beaten seven times. The monk had committed some unknown offense, but no one knew what it was. Soon after, the chancellor summoned the monk to sit and comfort him. When the chancellor asked the monk why he had been beaten, the monk replied that he had been told to do so by the chancellor. The chancellor was shocked and apologized, saying, "May the teacher be compassionate."

    This story is the nineteenth entry in the text and is similar to the story of Lu Wo, the governor of Shaanxi and Guo, and Lu Hang, the inspector of Shaanxi. It is likely that Lu Wo and Lu Hang are the same person, as noted by Sun Shixian.

    狄右丞鄙着紫僧【僧鸾附】
    　　唐狄归昌右丞爱与僧游每诵前辈诗云因过竹院逢僧话略得浮生半日闲其有服紫袈裟者乃疎之郑谷郎中亦爱僧用比蜀茶乃曰蜀茶与僧未必皆美不欲舍之　僧鸾有逸才而不拘检早嵗称卿御谒薛氏能尚书于嘉州八座以其颠率难为举子乃俾出家自于百尺大像前披剃不肯师于常僧也后入京为文章供奉赐紫栁玭大夫甚爱其才租庸张相亦曾加敬盛言其大用由是反初号鲜于凤脩刺谒栁公公鄙之不接又谒张相张相亦拒之于是失望而为李鋋江西判官后为西班小将军竟于黄州遇害
    　　张翺轻傲【李坚白蒋贻恭附】
    　　唐干宁中宿州刺史陈璠以军旅出身擅行威断进士张翶恃才傲物席上调璠宠妓张小泰怒而揖起付吏责其无礼状云有张翺兮寓止淮隂来绮席兮放恣胸襟璠益怒云据此分析合吃几下翺云只此两句合吃乎三下五下切求一笑宜费乎千金万金金鞭响背十三长逝惜其恃才而取祸也出刘山甫闲谈词多不载蜀绵州刺史李忘其名时号嗑咀以军功致郡符好

    135

    Di Guichang, the Right Chancellor, despised purple-robed monks. Whenever he visited temples, he would often recite a line from a poem by his predecessors: "As I passed through the bamboo courtyard, I met a monk and had a brief conversation, gaining a moment of leisure in this fleeting life." However, he would distance himself from those who wore purple robes. Zheng Gu, the Langzhong, also loved monks and compared them to Sichuan tea, saying, "Sichuan tea and monks are not necessarily all good, but I do not wish to abandon them."

    Monk Luan had exceptional talent but was not bound by conventional rules. In his early years, he was known as "Qingyu" and served the noble family of Xue in the state of Jiaozhou. The eight officials there, due to his unconventional nature, found it difficult to accept him as a scholar, so they made him enter the monastic life. He shaved his head and donned robes in front of a hundred-foot Buddha statue but refused to take a teacher from among ordinary monks. Later, he entered the capital and served as a literary attendant, granted the purple robe. Liu Pin, the Grand Councillor, greatly admired his talent, and Zhang, the Prime Minister of Rent and Labor, also held him in high regard and spoke highly of his potential. As a result, Monk Luan returned to his original state, took the name Xianyu Feng, and presented a letter to Liu Gong. Liu Gong despised him and did not receive him. He then went to see Zhang, the Prime Minister, who also rejected him. Disappointed, he became the Magistrate of Jiangxi under Li Chuan and later served as a junior general in the West, eventually meeting his demise in Huangzhou.

    Zhang Ao was arrogant. During the reign of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty, Chen Fan, the governor of Suzhou, who had risen through military ranks and was known for his strict and decisive nature, held a banquet. Zhang Ao, a scholar who relied on his talent and was arrogant, criticized Chen Fan's favorite concubine, Zhang Xiaotai, and became angry. Chen Fan was even more furious and asked, "According to this, how many strokes should he receive?" Zhang Ao replied, "Only these two lines are enough to receive three or five strokes. To seek a smile, it would be worth spending a thousand or ten thousand gold pieces. With a snap of the golden whip, he was dead at thirteen." It is a pity that he perished due to his arrogance and talent. This story is recorded in Liu Shanfu's Idle Talks, but many details are not included. The governor of Mianzhou, Sichuan, named Li, was known as "Kekou" and rose to his position through military merit. He was fond of...

    賔客有酒徒李坚白者麄有文笔李侯谓曰足下何以名为坚白对曰莫要改为士元亮君雄是权耶又有蒋贻恭者好嘲咏频以此痛遭槚楚竟不能改蜀中士子好着袜头袴蒋谓之曰仁贤既裹将仕郎头为何作散子蒋脚他皆此【蒋生虽嗜嘲咏然谈笑儒雅凡遭讥刺皆轻薄之徒以此缙绅中咸恶之近闻官至令佐而卒斯亦幸矣】
    　　刘李愚甥
    　　唐刘瞻相公有清德大名与弟阿初皆得道已入仙传先婚李氏生一子即刘赞也相国薨后赞且孤防性甚懵【一作鲁】钝教其读书终不记忆其舅即李殷衡侍郎也以刘氏之门【一作子】不可无后常加楚棰终不长进李夫人慈念不忍苦之叹其宿分也一旦不吿他适无以访寻圣善忆念泪如绠縻莫审其存亡数年方归子母团聚且曰因入嵩山遇一白衣叟谓曰与汝开心将来必保聪明自是日诵一卷兼有文藻擢进士第梁时登朝充崇政院学士预时俊之流其渭阳李侍郎充使番禺为越王刘氏所縻为广相而薨仆与刘赞犹子慤通熟自言家世合有一人得道矣即白衣叟其髣髴乎

    136

    Among the guests, there was a wine companion named Li Jianbai, who had a rough talent for writing. Li, the guest, asked him, "Why is your name Jianbai?" Li Jianbai replied, "Do not change it; 'Shiyuanliang' and 'Junxiong' are power, after all." There was also Jiang Yigong, who enjoyed mocking and singing, and often suffered greatly from this, yet still could not change his ways. Scholars in Shu liked to wear socks and trousers. Jiang said to them, "If you are a scholar, why do you wear a loose hat instead of an official hat?" Jiang's feet were all like this. [Though Jiang enjoyed mocking and singing, his conversation was always refined and scholarly. Anyone who mocked or ridiculed him was considered a vulgar person, and thus he was disliked by the gentry. Recently, he heard that he had become an official and died, which was fortunate.]

    Dong Li's Nephew

    During the Tang dynasty, Liu Zhan, the chancellor, was known for his integrity and fame. He and his brother Aichu had both attained the Dao and entered the records of immortals. He married into the Li family and had a son named Liu Zan. After the chancellor died, Liu Zan became an orphan and was very foolish. He was taught to read, but he never remembered. His uncle, Li Yinheng, the Censor-in-Chief, said that because the Liu family must have an heir, he often beat him with a stick. Li's wife, out of compassion, could not bear to see him suffer and lamented his fate. One day, without warning, he left, and there was no way to find him, so she remembered him and cried like a rope tied around her heart. No one knew if he was alive or dead, but after several years, he returned, and mother and son were reunited. He said, "I entered Mount Song and met a white-clad old man who said, 'I will open your heart, and you will surely become intelligent in the future.' From then on, he read one volume every day and developed literary talent, passing the imperial examination and becoming a scholar in the Imperial Academy, joining the ranks of the talented. His uncle, Li Yiheng, was sent as an envoy to Fanyu, where he was detained by the King of Yue and died as the governor of Guang. I am familiar with Liu Zan's nephew, Qu, who said that there should be one person in our family who has attained the Dao, just like the white-clad old man."

    李鹏遇桑道茂
    　　唐盛唐县令李鹏遇桑道茂曰长官只此一邑而已贤郎二人大者位极人臣次者殆于数镇子孙百氏后如其言长男名石出将入相子孙两世及第至今无间次即讳福敭歴七镇终于使相凡八男三人及第至尚书给谏郡牧见有诸孙皆朱紫不坠士风何先见之妙如是
    　　孔侍郎借油衣
    　　唐孔拯侍郎作遗补时朝回遇雨不赍油衣乃避雨于坊叟之庑下滂注愈甚已过食时民家意其朝饥延入防事俄有一叟乌帽纱巾而出迎候甚恭因备酒馔一一精珍乃公侯家不若也孔公惭谢之且借油衣叟曰某寒不出不出风不出雨不出未尝置油衣然已令铺上取去可以供借也孔公赏羡不觉顿忘宦情他日説于僚友为大之美也古之富者拟于封君洪范五福一曰富先贤以无事当贵岂斯人之徒耶复有一丞郎马上内逼急诣一空宅迳登溷轩斯乃大优穆刀绫空屋也优忽至丞郎惭谢之优曰侍郎他日内逼但请光访人闻之莫不絶倒

    Explanation

    Translation:

    Li Peng Encounters Sang Dao Mao

    During the Tang dynasty, the magistrate of Shengtang County, Li Peng, encountered Sang Dao Mao, who said to him, "Your position is limited to this one county alone. Your two sons, the elder will reach the highest rank of the court, and the younger will hold several prefectures. Their descendants will follow this prophecy. The eldest son, named Shi, will become a general and enter the government. His descendants will pass the imperial examinations for two generations, without interruption, and will eventually reach high ranks such as Shangshu, Gujian, and Junmu. They will have many grandsons, all of whom will hold high positions, maintaining the family's scholarly reputation. How remarkable is this foresight!"

    Kong Shilang Borrows an Oil Cloth

    During the Tang dynasty, Kong Zheng, a Shilang, was on his way back from court when it rained heavily. He did not bring an oil cloth and sought shelter under the eaves of an old man's house. The rain was pouring down, and it was already past noon. The old man thought he might be hungry from the morning and invited him in for a meal. Soon, an old man wearing a black hat and silk scarf came out to greet him with great respect. He prepared a meal with exquisite delicacies, better than those of a noble family. Kong Zheng felt ashamed and thanked him, asking for an oil cloth. The old man said, "I don't go out in the cold, wind, or rain, so I never keep an oil cloth. However, I have already sent someone to get one for you." Kong Zheng was so impressed that he forgot his official duties. Later, he told his colleagues about this wonderful experience.

    In ancient times, the wealthy were compared to feudal lords. According to the Hong Fan (Great Pattern), one of the five blessings is wealth. The sages valued wealth as a means to achieve nobility. Are these people not examples of this? There was another county magistrate who was in a hurry and went to an empty house. He entered the toilet area, which was a large, empty room. Suddenly, a performer appeared, and the magistrate felt ashamed and thanked him. The performer said, "If you are in a hurry, just come here." People who heard about this found it extremely amusing.

    前贤戏调
    　　唐裴晋公度风貌不扬自譔真赞云尔身不长尔貌不扬胡为而将胡为而相幕下从事逊以美之且曰明公以内相为优公笑曰诸贤好信谦也幕僚皆悚而退李洸者渤海人昆仲皆有文章洸因旅次至江村宿于民家见覆斗上安锡佛一躯洸诡词以赞之民曰偶未庆赞为去僧院地逺尔洸曰何必须僧只我而已民信之明发随分具斋餐炷香防诚洸俯仰朗称曰锡镴佛子柔软世尊斗上庄严为有十升功德念摩诃般若波罗密又赵璘员外为裴坦相汉南从事璘甚陋裴公戏之曰赵公本不丑孩抱时乳母怜惜往往抚弄云作丑子作丑子因此一定赵公大咍薛侍郎昭纬气

    Explanation

    Translation:

    Playful Anecdotes of the Sages

    During the Tang Dynasty, Pei Jinfu, a prominent statesman, was not conventionally handsome. He wrote a self-praise that read: "My body is not tall, my appearance is not tall. Why should I lead, and why should I serve as an advisor?" A subordinate in his camp humbly praised him, saying, "The Right Honorable One is superior as an advisor." Pei laughed and said, "The scholars all like to believe in humility." The staff all felt shocked and left.

    Li Guang, from Bohai, was known for his literary talent, as were his brothers. During a journey, he stayed in a village by the river at a commoner's house and saw a lead and tin Buddha on a cover. He used clever words to praise it, saying, "It just hasn't been blessed yet because the temple is far away." The commoner replied, "Why must it be a monk? I can do it too." Li Guang then lit incense and offered sincere prayers, bowing and speaking clearly: "Lead and tin Buddha, soft and gentle World Honored One. On the cover, it is dignified and has ten measures of merit. Reciting the Great Wisdom that leads to the Other Shore."

    Zhaolin, an official, served as an attendant to Peitan in the southern region. He was very ugly, and Peitan joked with him, saying, "Originally, Zhao Gong was not ugly. When he was a baby, the wet nurse often patted him and said, 'Make him ugly, make him ugly,' and thus he became so." Zhaolin laughed loudly.

    Xue, the Attendant Lang, had a certain temperament.

    貌昏浊杜紫微唇厚温庭筠号温钟馗【一作防】不称才名也薛侍郎未登第前就肆买鞋鞋主曰秀士脚第几对曰与昭纬作脚来未曾与立行第也杜徳祥侍郎昆弟力困要举息利钱济急用召同坊富民到宅且问曰子本对是几钱其人拂袖而出又孔昭纬拜官教坊优伶继至各求利市石野猪独先行到公有所赐谓曰宅中甚阙不得厚致若有诸野猪幸勿言也复有一伶继来公索其笛唤近阶指笛窍问之曰何者是浣溪纱孔笼子笛伶大笑之又道士陈子霄登华山上方偶有颠仆宇文翰郎中致书戏之曰不知上得不得且怪之又斯皆清贤雅戏以之羣居又何伤也

    A Dull Appearance and Thick Lips: Du Mu, Wen Tingyun, and Others

    Du Mu, known for his dull appearance, and Wen Tingyun, whose lips were thick, both had nicknames that did not match their talent and reputation. Wen Tingyun was nicknamed "Wen Zhong Kui" (one version says "Wen Fang"). Xue Zhi, a scholar-official, before passing the imperial examinations, went to a shop to buy shoes. The shopkeeper asked, "Which pair is for the excellent scholar?" Xue replied, "It was made for Zhaowei, but never established a rank." Du Deyang, a scholar-official, and his brothers were in financial difficulty and needed to borrow money to help with urgent expenses. They summoned wealthy people from the same neighborhood to their house and asked, "How much is the principal and interest?" One of them left by brushing off his sleeves. Kong Zhaowei, after receiving an official position, was visited by actors and musicians from the music bureau, each seeking profit. Shi Yezhu, a performer, arrived first and received a gift from the official. The official said, "There is a lot lacking in the house, so I cannot provide a generous gift. If there are any pigs, please do not mention it." Another performer arrived later, and the official asked for his flute, calling him near and pointing to the flute's hole and asking, "Which one is Huan Xisha?" Kong Longzi, a performer, laughed at it. Daoist priest Chen Zixiao, while ascending the upper platform of Mount Hua, accidentally fell. Yuwen Han, a scholar-official, wrote a letter to tease him, saying, "Do not know if he can ascend, and find it strange." Xuan Si and others were all clear, virtuous, and playfully gathered together, what harm is there?

    京兆府鵶挽铃
    　　唐温璋为京兆尹勇于杀戮京邑惮之时闻挽铃声俾看架下不见有人凡三度挽掣乃见鵶一只尹曰是必有人探其雏而诉寃也命吏随鵶所在捕之其鵶盘旋引吏至城外树间果有人探其雏尚憩树下吏乃执之送府以禽鸟诉寃事异于常乃毙捕雏者而报之
    　　天帝召棊客
    　　唐僖宗朝翰林待诏滑能棊品甚髙少逢敌手有一张小子年仅十四来谒覔棊请饶一路滑生棊思甚迟沈吟良久方下一子张生随手应之都不介意仍于庭际取适候滑生更下又随手着应之一旦黄冦犯阙僖宗幸蜀滑以待诏供职谋赴行在欲取金州路入办装挈家将行张生曰不必前迈某非棊客天帝命我取公着棊请指挥家事滑生惊愕妻子啜泣奄然而逝他日京都共知也昔顔回卜商为地下脩文郎又李长吉为帝召撰乐府岂斯类耶所言天帝者非北极天皇大帝也按真诰又非北方天黑帝道君此都北帝又号帝世人有大功徳者北帝得以辟请四明公之流是也召棊之命乃酆宫帝君乎与真诰髣髴故梗槩而言之

    The Bell-Pulling Crow of Jingzhao Prefecture
    During the Tang Dynasty, Wang Zhiang served as the Prefect of Jingzhao and was known for his strictness and willingness to punish. The people of the capital feared him. One day, he heard the sound of a bell being pulled. He ordered officials to look under the eaves but found no one. The sound was heard three times before a crow appeared. The Prefect said, "This must be someone stealing the crow's chick and complaining about injustice." He ordered the officials to follow the crow wherever it went and catch the thief. The crow circled and led the officials to a tree outside the city where indeed someone was stealing its chick, which was still resting under the tree. The official then arrested him and sent him to the prefecture. The case of a bird complaining about injustice is unusual, so the person who caught the chick was killed and the matter reported.

    The Heavenly Emperor Summons a Chess Player
    During the reign of Emperor Xizong of Tang, a scholar named Hua Neng, known for his exceptional chess skills, rarely found an equal opponent. One day, a young man named Zhang, aged only fourteen, came to visit and requested a game, asking for a concession of one move. Hua Neng's thoughts were slow, and he pondered for a long time before placing a piece. Zhang responded immediately and did not seem to care. He continued to play, taking turns with Hua Neng. One day, when the Yellow Bandits attacked the palace, Emperor Xizong fled to Shu. Hua Neng, serving as a scholar, planned to follow the emperor and intended to take the route through Jin Prefecture. As he prepared to leave, Zhang said, "There is no need to go further. I am not a chess player. The Heavenly Emperor has summoned me to play chess with you. Please give me instructions on how to manage your household." Hua Neng was shocked, his wife and children wept, and he died suddenly. Later, the people of the capital all knew about this. In the past, Confucius and Ziyuan were known as scholars of the underworld, and Li He was summoned by the emperor to compose poetry. Is this similar to what is said? The Heavenly Emperor referred to here is not the Northern Pole Emperor. According to the True Scripture, it is not the Northern Black Emperor or the Daoist Lord. This is the Northern Emperor of the City of the Dead, also known as the Ghost Emperor. Those who have great virtue can be summoned by the Northern Emperor to request the Four Bright Scholars. Is the command to summon the chess player from the Emperor of the City of Punishment? It is similar to what is said in the True Scripture, so I will briefly mention it.

    141

    梁赵意医
    　　医者意也古人有不因切脉随知病源者必愈之矣唐崔魏公镇渚宫有富商船居中夜暴亡迨晓气犹未絶邻房有武陵医士【一作工】梁新闻之乃与诊视曰此乃食毒也三两日得非外食耶仆夫曰主公少出船亦不食于他人梁新曰寻常嗜食何物仆夫曰好食竹鸡每年不下数百只近买竹鸡并将充馔梁新曰竹鸡吃半夏必是半夏毒也命捣姜捩汁折齿而灌之由是方苏崔魏公闻而异之召到衙安慰称奬资以仆马钱帛入京致书朝士声名大振仕至尚医奉御有一朝士诣之梁奉御

    Explanation

    The Physician Liang Zhao Yi

    In ancient times, there were physicians who could diagnose diseases without relying on pulse-taking and immediately knew the cause, and such patients would certainly be cured. During the Tang Dynasty, Duke Cui of Wei was stationed at the residence of a wealthy merchant in the town of Zhu. One night, the merchant died suddenly. By dawn, his breath was still not completely gone. A physician from Wuling, known as Liang Xinhua (or Liang Xingong), heard about this and went to examine the body. He said, "This is a case of poisoning from food. Was it not from external food?" The servant replied, "The master rarely leaves the ship and does not eat food from others." Liang Xinhua asked, "What does he usually eat?" The servant answered, "He loves eating bamboo partridges, and he consumes hundreds of them each year. Recently, he bought bamboo partridges to be used as food." Liang Xinhua said, "Bamboo partridges eat pinellia, so it must be pinellia poisoning." He ordered the servant to pound ginger and squeeze out the juice, then pour it down the master's throat. The master then revived. Duke Cui of Wei heard of this and found it remarkable. He called Liang Xinhua to his office, comforted him, and praised him. He provided him with servants, horses, money, and silk, and sent him to the capital to write letters to officials. His reputation greatly increased, and he rose to the position of Imperial Physician. A court official visited him, and Liang Xinhua was highly regarded.

    曰何不早见示风疾已深矣请速归处置家事委顺而已朝士闻而惶遽吿退策马而归时有鄜州马医赵鄂者新到京都于通衢自榜姓名云攻医术士此朝士下马吿之赵鄂亦言病已危与梁生所説同矣谓曰只有一法请官人剰吃消梨不限多少时咀龁不及捩汁而饮或希万一此朝士又策马归以书筒质消梨马上旋龁到家旬日唯吃消梨顿觉爽朗其恙不作却访赵生感谢又访梁奉御具言得赵生教也梁公惊异且曰大国必有一人相继者遂召赵生资以仆马钱帛广为延誉官至太仆卿

    A person asked, "Why wasn't this shown earlier? The wind disease has already become severe. Please return quickly to handle family matters and submit to fate." The court officials heard and hurriedly withdrew, riding their horses back home. At that time, there was a horse doctor from Fu Prefecture named Zhao E, who had just arrived in the capital. He posted his name and claimed to be skilled in medicine on a busy street. This court official dismounted and informed him. Zhao E also said that the illness was already critical, agreeing with what Mr. Liang had said. He advised, "There is only one method: please eat more pears to relieve the condition. Without limit, chew them or squeeze out the juice to drink, perhaps there is a chance." This court official then rode his horse back, using a bamboo tube to store the pears and eating them while riding. Upon arriving home, he ate pears for ten days and suddenly felt refreshed; his illness did not return. He later visited Mr. Zhao and expressed his gratitude, then visited Mr. Liang and explained that he received advice from Mr. Zhao. Mr. Liang was surprised and said, "A great country must have someone who follows in succession." He then summoned Mr. Zhao, providing him with servants, horses, money, and silk to widely spread his fame. Mr. Zhao eventually became a High-ranking official.

    疗疑病
    　　元顽博士话唐时中表间有一妇人从夫南中効官曽误食一虫常疑之由是成疾频疗不愈京城医者忘其姓名知其所患乃请主人姨妳中谨密者一人预戒之曰今以药吐泻但以盘盂盛之当吐之时但言有一小虾蟆走去然切勿令娘子知之是诳语也其妳仆遵之此疾永除又説有一年少眼中常见一小镜子医工赵卿诊之与少年期来晨以鱼脍奉候少年及期赴之延于阁子内且令从容俟客退后方得攀
    接俄而设台于上施一瓯芥醋更无他味卿亦未出迨日【一作禺】中久候不至少年饥甚且闻醋香不免轻啜之逡巡又啜之觉胸中豁然眼花不见因竭瓯啜之赵卿探知方出少年以啜醋惭谢卿曰郎君啜鲙太多非酱醋不快又有鱼鳞在胸中所以眼花适来所备酱醋只欲郎君因饥以啜之果愈此疾烹鲜【一作鳞】之防乃权诳也请退谋餐他妙多斯类也非庸医所及也凡欲以仓扁之术求食者得不勉之哉

    Final Translation:

    Treating Doubtful Illnesses

    The learned doctor Yuan Wan spoke of a woman during the Tang dynasty who, among her in-laws, had once mistakenly eaten a bug and often doubted it. As a result, she fell ill, and despite frequent treatments, she did not recover. A physician from the capital, whose name was forgotten, realized that her condition required a specific treatment. He asked the cautious and discreet servant of the family to warn her in advance: "Now, with the medicine, you will vomit and have diarrhea. Hold it in a tray or basin. When you vomit, just say that a small frog has gone away. But do not let the lady know that this is a lie." The servant followed the instructions, and the illness was permanently cured.

    He also said that there was a young man who often saw a small mirror in his eyes. The physician Zhao Qing diagnosed him and arranged to meet the young man the next morning to serve him raw fish slices. The young man arrived as agreed and was invited into a small room. He was told to wait calmly until the guests left before proceeding. Soon, a table was set up, and a bowl of mustard vinegar was placed on it, with no other dishes. Zhao Qing had not yet appeared, and by midday, the young man had waited for a long time. He was very hungry and, smelling the vinegar, could not help but take a small sip. He then took another sip and felt a sudden clarity in his chest, but his vision became blurry. He drank the entire bowl. Zhao Qing, realizing what had happened, finally appeared. The young man apologized for drinking the vinegar, saying he was embarrassed. Zhao Qing replied, "Young master, you ate too much raw fish. Without vinegar, it would not taste good. There was also fish skin in your chest, which is why your vision was blurred. The mustard vinegar I prepared was only meant for you to drink because you were hungry." The young man's illness was cured. The use of mustard vinegar as a treatment was a temporary deception, and Zhao Qing suggested, "Please step back and plan for other wonderful meals." Such cases are not within the realm of ordinary physicians. All those who wish to seek sustenance through the art of medicine should strive diligently.

    非意致祸
    　　唐时杜彦林为朝官一日马惊蹶倒踏镫既深抽脚不出为马拖行一步一踏以至于卒古人云乗船走马去死一分是知跨御常宜介意也杜相审权弟延美亦登朝序乗马入门为门楣所轧项颈低曲伸脰前引肩髙于顶乃一生之疾也荆州文献王好马不惜千金没世不遇周先帝命内臣李廷玉赐马与南平王且问所好何马乃
    曰良马千万无一若骏者即可得而选茍要坐下坦【一作且】穏免劳控制唯骟庶几也既免蹄齧不假衔枚两军列阵万骑如一茍未经骟乱气狡愤介胄在身与马争力磬控不暇安能左旋右抽舍辔挥兵乎自是江南蜀马往往学骟甚便乗跨是知蹀躞者夸于目驯柔者便于身此【一作比】君子之难逢假翦剔者抑其次也哉

    Unintentional Disaster

    During the Tang Dynasty, Du Yanlin, a court official, was riding one day when his horse suddenly reared and fell, its hoof deeply embedded in the stirrup. He could not pull his leg free and was dragged along, taking a step at a time, until he died. As the ancients said, "In riding a horse, one must always be cautious, for there is a risk of death at every moment." It is known that one should always be mindful when riding a horse. Du Shentong, the brother of the Prime Minister, also held a position in the imperial court. One day, while riding his horse into the palace gate, he was struck by the lintel, causing his neck to bend downward, his head to tilt forward, and his shoulders to rise above his head, a condition that persisted for the rest of his life.

    The Prince of Jingzhou, a lover of horses, was willing to spend thousands of gold pieces on them, but never found one to his liking. Emperor Zhou ordered the eunuch Li Tingyu to give a horse to Prince Nanping and asked what kind of horse he preferred. The prince replied, "Among ten thousand good horses, there is not one as swift as this. If it can be ridden comfortably and without the trouble of controlling it, then it is suitable for me." Such a horse would not bite or need to be restrained with a bit or mouthpiece, and in battle formation, ten thousand riders would act as one. If the horse had not been castrated, it would be filled with chaotic and fierce energy, and the rider, clad in armor, would struggle to control it, let alone turn left or right, release the reins, and command the troops. Since then, horses in Jiangnan and Shu have often been castrated for easier riding. Thus, those who show off their agility are admired by the eyes, while those who are gentle are convenient for the body. The difficulty of encountering a true gentleman is second only to the challenge of finding someone who can perform the delicate task of castrating horses.

    崔枢食龙子
    　　唐崔枢为小朝官家人于井中汲得一鱼枢本好鲜食意是厨人治鱼误落井中乃令烹而啖之忽梦为防官领过读判云人间小臣輙食龙子所有官爵并削除后一年卒枢甚有声不跻显位误有所食岂命也夫
    　　薛准隂诛
    　　唐薛准官至员外郎防乱后不养继母盘桓江淮间道门寄榻游江南至吉州閤皁观遇脩黄箓斋道士升坛行法事准亦就列忽失声痛叫云中箭速请笔砚口占一诗曰盖国深恩不易讐又离继母出他州谁知天怒无因息积恶终身乞命休顷便卒天复辛酉年事斯人也必有慝而致隂诛古者史籍皆以至孝继母闻于列传盖以常人难行而已能行即亲母可知也岂可以继母而同行路哉薛死仓卒可用垂戒也

    Cui Shu Eats the Dragon's Child

    Cui Shu, a minor official of the Tang Dynasty, had a fish brought up from a well by his household. He was fond of fresh food and thought it was a mistake by the cook who had dropped the fish into the well. He ordered it to be cooked and ate it. Suddenly, he dreamed of being led by a guard official who read a judgment that said: "A low-ranking official in the human world has eaten the dragon's child; all official positions and titles shall be stripped away." One year later, Cui Shu died. Despite having a good reputation, he did not rise to a high position. Was it fate that he made this mistake?

    Execution by Secret Force

    In the Tang Dynasty, Xue Zhun served as a Langzhong (a low-ranking official). After a period of chaos, he neglected to care for his step-mother and wandered around the Jianghuai region. He stayed at Taoist temples and traveled to the southern part of China, reaching the Geshao Temple in Jizhou. There, he encountered a Taoist priest performing a Huangluo ritual. Xue Zhun joined the ceremony and suddenly let out a painful cry, saying, "I am hit by an arrow! Quickly bring me a brush and ink!" He then composed a poem on the spot:

    "The deep kindness of the state is hard to repay,
    Furthermore, leaving the step-mother to go to another state.
    Who knows if the anger of heaven can be appeased?
    Accumulated evil throughout life, begging for the end of one's life."

    He died shortly after. In the year Xinyou of Tianfu (a year in the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches system), this man must have committed some evil deeds that led to his secret execution. In ancient historical records, those who were known for their extreme filial piety toward their step-mothers were recorded in the biographies of notable individuals. This is because it is difficult for ordinary people to practice such virtue, but those who do so can be trusted to treat their biological mothers with the same respect. How can one treat a step-mother as a stranger? Xue Zhun's sudden death can serve as a warning to others.

    崔雍食子肉【李佋苏循附】
    　　唐咸通中厐勋反于徐州时崔雍典和州为勋所陷执到彭门雍善谈笑逊词以从之冀纾其祸勋亦见待甚厚其子少俊饮博击拂自得亲近更无阻猜雍以失节于贼以门戸为忧谓其子曰汝善狎之或得方便能倳刃乎人皆有死但得其所吾复何恨其子承命密怀利刃忽色变身战勋疑讶因搜怀袖得匕首焉乃令烹之翌日召雍赴饮【一作饭】既彻问
    雍曰肉美乎对曰以味珍且饱勋曰此即贤郎肉也亦命杀之后黄巢入广州执节度使李佋随军至荆州令佋草表述其所怀佋曰某骨肉满朝世受国恩腕即可断表终不为寻于江津害之唐宋苏循尚书谄【一作谲】媚茍且梁太祖鄙之他日至并门谒晋王时张承业方以匡复为意而循忽献晋王画勅笔一对承业愈鄙薄之与夫雍佋为人视苏循诚逺矣

    Cui Yong Eats His Son's Meat [With Li Kei and Su Xun Attached]

    During the Xintong era of the Tang Dynasty, Pang Xun rebelled in Xuzhou. At that time, Cui Yong was the governor of Hézhōu and was captured by Pang Xun and brought to Pénmén. Cui Yong was skilled in charming conversation and humble words, using these to comply with Pang Xun, hoping to alleviate his own misfortune. Pang Xun also treated him very well. His son, Shaòjùn, who was carefree and close to Pang Xun, often engaged in drinking, gambling, and playing with a fan. Cui Yong was worried about the family's honor due to his son's association with the rebels. He told his son, "You should be familiar with him and find an opportunity to kill him. Everyone dies, but if one dies in the right place, what do I have to regret?" His son received the order and secretly carried a sharp knife. Suddenly, he changed color and trembled, which made Pang Xun suspicious and surprised. Pang Xun then searched his pockets and found a dagger. He ordered the son to be cooked. The next day, Pang Xun summoned Cui Yong to a drinking party. After the meal, he asked, "Is the meat delicious?" Cui Yong replied, "The taste is precious and filling." Pang Xun said, "This is your noble son's meat." He also ordered Cui Yong to be killed.

    Later, Huang Cháo entered Guangzhou and captured the governor, Li Kēi, bringing him to Jingzhou. Huang Cháo ordered Li Kēi to draft a memorial stating his intentions. Li Kēi said, "My relatives are everywhere in the court, and generations have received national favor. Even if I cut off my wrist, I will not write the memorial." Soon, Li Kēi was killed at Jiangjin.

    During the Tang and Song dynasties, Su Xún, a Shangshu, flattered and acted opportunistically. Liáng Tài Zǔ despised him. Once, Su Xún went to Píngmén to pay respects to the Prince of Jin. At that time, Zhang Chéngyè was just thinking about restoring the rightful ruler. Su Xún suddenly presented a pair of painted imperial brushes to the Prince of Jin. Zhang Chéngyè despised him even more. Compared to Cui Yong and Li Kēi, Su Xún's character was indeed far apart.

    王迪车辗事
    　　王迪舍人早负才业未卜骞翔一日谒宰相杜太尉于宅门十字通衢街路稍狭有二牛车东西交至迪马夹在其间马惊仆而卧为车辙辗靴鼻逾寸而不伤脚指三日后入拜翰林虽幸而免亦神助也
    　　杜孺休种青莲花
    　　唐韩文公愈之甥有种花之异闻于小説杜给事孺休典湖州有染戸家池生青莲花刺史致书问染工曰我家有三世治靛瓮常以莲子浸于瓮底俟经嵗年然后种之若以所种青莲子为种即为红矣盖还本质又何足怪乃以所浸莲子寄奉之道士田匡图亲看此花为愚话之愚见今【一作人】以鸡粪和土培芍药花丛其淡红者悉成深红染之所言益信矣哉蜀王先主将晏驾其年峨嵋山娑罗花悉开白花又荆州之献王未薨前数年沟港城隍悉开白莲花一则染以气类一则表于凶兆斯又何哉

    Final Translation

    Wang Di's Encounter with the Ox-Carts

    Wang Di, a Shèrén (high-ranking official), was known for his early talent and diligence, yet his future success was uncertain. One day, he visited the Prime Minister Du, the Taivéi (a high military rank), at his residence, where the crossroads street was slightly narrow. Two ox-drawn carts were approaching from east and west, and Wang Di's horse was caught in between. The horse was startled, fell down, and lay on its side, with its nose being run over by the cart wheels, more than an inch deep, but the toes remained unharmed. Three days later, he entered the Hanlin Academy to pay respects. Although he was fortunate to escape, it was also divine assistance.

    Du Ruxiu and the Blue Lotus Flowers

    Du Ruxiu, the nephew of Han Wengong Yu of the Tang Dynasty, had a strange story about planting flowers in a novel. Du, the Jigshi Ruxiu, was in charge of Huzhou. There was a dyeing household's pond where blue lotus flowers grew. The governor sent a letter to ask the dyeing worker, saying, "In my family, there are three generations of people who have been treating indigo jars, always soaking lotus seeds at the bottom of the jars, waiting for years before planting them. If the blue lotus seeds are planted, they will turn red. It is still the original nature, so what is there to be surprised about?" He then sent the soaked lotus seeds to him. The Taoist priest Tian Kuangtu personally saw this flower and told me about it. I see that nowadays, people mix chicken manure with soil to cultivate peony flower clusters, and the light red ones all turn deep red. The dyeing worker's words are even more credible.

    Omens of White Flowers

    When the first ruler of Shu was about to pass away, that year, all the bodhi trees on Mount Emei bloomed with white flowers. Several years before the Xian Wang of Jingzhou passed away, all the ditches, canals, and city gates bloomed with white lotus flowers. One is due to the influence of qi, and the other is a sign of an omen. What could this mean?

    严军容猫犬怪
    　　唐左军容使严遵美于阉宦中仁人也自言北司马【一作为】供奉官袴衫给事无秉简入侍之仪又云枢密使署三间屋书柜而已亦无视事防堂状后贴黄指挥公事乃是杨复恭夺宰相权也自是常思退休一旦发狂手足舞蹈家人咸讶傍有一猫一犬猫谓犬曰军容改常也颠发也犬曰莫管他从他俄而舞定自惊自笑且异猫犬之言遇昭宗播迁鳯翔乃求致仕梁川【一作州】蜀军収降兴元因徙于
    劒南依王先主优待甚异于青城山下卜别墅以居之年过八十而终其忠正谦约与西门季元为季孟也于时诛宦官唯西川不奉诏由是脱祸家有北司治乱记八卷备载阉宦忠佞好恶尝闻此传偶未得见即巷伯之流未必俱邪良由南班轻忌太过以致参商盖邦国之不幸也先是路岩相自成都移镇渚宫所乗马忽作人语且曰芦荻花此花开后路无家不久及祸然畜类之语岂有物凭之乎石言于晋殆斯比也

    Explanation

    148

    Yan Junrong, a eunuch of the Tang Dynasty, was known for his benevolence among his peers. He claimed to have served as the Northern Marshal and wore the attire of a ceremonial official, attending to matters without formal protocol. He also mentioned that the Imperial Military Commissioner had a small office with three rooms, used primarily for bookshelves, and had no official duties, only issuing public orders after adding notes to official documents. This was a reference to Yang Fugong, who had seized the power of the chancellor. Since then, Yan Junrong often thought of retiring. One day, he suddenly went mad, dancing with his hands and feet, and his family was surprised. Beside him was a cat and a dog. The cat said to the dog, "The eunuch has changed his usual behavior; he has gone mad." The dog replied, "Don't worry about him; let him be." Soon, he stopped dancing, shocked and laughing at himself, finding the cat and dog's words strange. When Emperor Zhaozong was exiled to Fengxiang, Yan Junrong requested retirement. The Shu army conquered Xingyuan from the region of Liangzhou or Liangzhou and moved to Jian'nan, relying on Wang Xianzhu. He built a villa to live in at Qingcheng Mountain. He lived to be over eighty and died. He was loyal, upright, modest, and restrained, and he was the peer of Xiemen Jiyuan. At that time, the purge of eunuchs was carried out, but only Shu did not obey the decree, thus avoiding disaster. His family had a record of the governance and disorder of the Northern Office, titled "Eight Volumes of the North Office," which detailed the loyalty, deceit, and good or evil of eunuchs. I have heard of this text but have not yet seen it. It is said that eunuchs like Yan Junrong are not all evil; it is due to the excessive suspicion of officials from the south, leading to discord, which is indeed a misfortune for the state. Before this, Lu Yan, the chancellor, was moved from Chengdu to Zhubing Palace. The horse he was riding suddenly spoke in human language, saying, "The reed and bulrush flowers bloom, and after they bloom, there is no home for the road." Soon, he faced disaster. Is it due to some supernatural influence? The speaking stone in Jin is similar to this.

    Duan Family's Wine and Roasting Establishment

    Duan Gong, a respected scholar of the Tang dynasty, came from a family that rarely produced famous officials. His grandfather, Jing, the former Shilang (a high-ranking official), was not adept at managing his livelihood and was in dire straits. Within the capital city, there was a piece of vacant land adjacent to a powerful eunuch. The eunuch desired this land, but it was only worth five or six hundred thousand coins. Duan Gong happily offered this land to the eunuch without mentioning the price, saying, "What is convenient for the general, I dare not disobey." He explained that he had a reason to travel to Jiangsu and Anhui and sought protection from three or four places. The eunuch was pleased and wrote a letter, and in total, Duan Gong received three thousand strings of cash, thus being fortunate to be saved.

    In the eastern market, there was another piece of vacant land that was low-lying and stagnant. Duan Gong bought it at a low price and had the maids bring a tray of fried cakes to attract children. If a child threw a brick or tile, they received a paper ticket for one cake. Children ran around throwing bricks and tiles, gambling for fried cakes. Soon, six or seven out of ten were filled with tickets. Then, they filled the land with good soil and built a shop. They stopped Persian merchants, earning one string of cash daily. Others followed suit, and thus, Duan Gong became wealthy. He invited guests and officials, and at the time, they called him frivolous, dubbing the place the "Wine and Roasting Establishment." He could also help others obtain official ranks, gathering people with food and drink, and seeking profit as one means of doing so. Duan Hui and Duan Yong had no literary talent but gained fame due to the power of drinking and eating. This account was obtained from the Yuan period, recorded by several virtuous officials of the Office of Censorate. The story of Pei Mingli buying a house is the same as the Duan family, and it is suspected that the Duan family imitated Pei Mingli's actions.

    Li Changfu's Praise of Maidservants

    During the Xiantong era of the Tang dynasty, Li Changfu, a candidate for the imperial examinations, was known for his poetic talent but had not yet passed the exams. He often neglected the preparation of his examination scrolls, so he came up with a clever idea. He wrote fifty poems about maidservants and circulated them among the high-ranking officials. One of his poems read: "Chunniang loves to go to a tavern on the upper floor; she doesn't mind coming back late and doesn't leave. She claims that the lady of the house is asleep and asks to stay until she finishes combing her hair." Another poem said: "Regardless of whether it's autumn chrysanthemums or spring flowers, each can drink tea on an empty stomach. Don't let them enter the house too often. One needs a bit of idle time." All the poems hit on the taboo topics of maidservants. Within ten days, the capital was filled with the circulation of his poems. The maidservants and their like were furious and criticized him fiercely, all wanting to slap his face. That year, he passed the examination. Although the story of the peach stick and tiger boots is different, using a clever method is the same.

    The Effectiveness of the Knowledge of Fate Pill for General Zhong

    During the Tang dynasty, General Zhong, a military officer under the Guangnan Circuit Governor, whose name is unknown, wandered and stayed in Lingzhou in his later years. He often stayed in temples. County Magistrate Ouyang Shu, who felt sorry for General Zhong's old age, often invited him to stay. During the hot summer days, he fell ill with abdominal pain and lay in Ouyang Shu's house. He did not eat for over a month. County Magistrate Ouyang was worried that he would die soon and wanted to submit a report to the state office to get a statement from General Zhong about his actions. General Zhong said, "I am sick, but I am not going to die. Since I am already troubled, what harm is there in reporting?" He reported it to the officials. After that, his illness improved. Bao Guangzi, who was an assistant to the prefect at the time, kindly visited and asked about the reason for the report. He said, "I once encountered a battle in Xiangtan and did not advance. With several fellow merchants, we held a vegetarian meal at Yue Lu Temple. The temple monk had newly prepared the Knowledge of Fate Pill. He also said that after taking this medicine, one would..."

    After taking the seaweed decoction or when the appointed time is near, there is a slight pain in the ribs. Once the pill is excreted, one must arrange family matters in preparation for the end. Then each paid a string of coins to swallow a pill. Later, when entering Shu and arriving at Le County, they met a merchant who had also taken the pill and was staying in Le County. They were able to reminisce about the past and discuss the great efficacy of the medicine. Soon after, this gentleman reported a pain in his ribs.     Tang Dynasty, Sun Guangxian, compiled
    Zhang Zhifang Praises Pei Xiu
    In the Tang Dynasty, Zhang Zhifang, a great general of the Gold and White Guards, was a distinguished and talented military officer. He was known for his hospitality to guests, musicians, and singers, and his musical instruments were the best among his peers. When Pei Xiu, the Chancellor, was about to take the imperial examination, he wore mourning clothes and was preparing to take the test. Zhang Zhifang admired his demeanor and sought to meet him through Pei. Pei treated him with special courtesy. Later, in the court, Pei highly praised Pei Xiu's literary talent, which surprised the court officials. The Chancellor was concerned about potential complications and could not find a suitable place to accommodate him. From then on, Zhang Zhifang dared not visit his house. Pei Xiu frequently invited him, but he did not go. Someone said, "Pei Xiu is planning to advance in his career and is concerned about gaining fame, so he is not being humble." One day, he was summoned again and told, "If it is not inconvenient, please come and offer him a recommendation." Pei Xiu was even more apprehensive.

    Xue Zhaowei, the Vice-Minister, Wrapped a Falcon in Paper

    During the Tang Dynasty, Xue Zhaowei, the Vice-Minister, was proud due to his talent and position, often showing arrogance. He considered himself worthy of the highest office and was eager for a high-ranking position. At that time, Zhu Wen, the founder of the Later Liang dynasty, had already controlled four commanderies, and his military power was growing. Zhu Wen had ambitions to seize the throne and was eager to transfer power. Xue Zhaowei was sent on a mission to the state of Liang. Zhu Wen invited him back and told the messenger, "The lord has given an order that cannot be refused. Please return quickly." Upon arriving at the western gate, Zhu Wen had no choice but to greet him personally. Seeing Xue Zhaowei's distinguished appearance and eloquent speech, Zhu Wen changed his attitude and treated him with cordiality. One day, Zhu Wen spoke about hawks and falcons, and Xue Zhaowei praised their excellence. Zhu Wen was delighted and told him, "You have also handled these matters before." After returning to his lodging, Zhu Wen sent a messenger to deliver a hawk. Xue Zhaowei wrote a letter of thanks and instructed his servants, "This hawk must be cherished. It should be wrapped in paper and placed in a pouch." The messenger laughed, and this was reported to Zhu Wen's court.

    The Examination Board Imposed a Penalty on Cui Zhaoju, the Top Scholar

    In the Tang Dynasty, Cui Zhaoju, the top scholar, was part of a group of successful candidates. The officials of the examination board imposed penalties for mistakes. One day, a mistake was made, and the top scholar whipped one of the officials. The official apologized and submitted himself to the ground in front of the other candidates, saying, "Cui Fifteen does not deserve to face the officials before. Please impose a penalty of a certain amount." The people of Boling were speechless and unable to respond.

    程贺为崔亚持服

    　　髙太尉骈请留蛮宰相事
    　　唐南蛮侵轶西川苦无亭障自咸通已后剑南苦之牛丛尚书作镇为蛮寇凭陵无以抗拒髙公自东平移镇成都蛮酋搏蜀城掌武先选骁鋭救急人背神符一道蛮觇知之望风而遁尔后僖宗幸蜀深疑作梗乃许降公主蛮王以连姻大国喜幸逾常因命宰相赵隆眉杨竒鲲段义宗来朝行在且迎公主髙太尉自淮海飞章云南蛮心膂唯此数人请止而鸩之迄僖宗还京南方无虞用髙公之防也杨竒鲲辈皆有词藻途中诗云风里浪花吹又白雨中岚色洗还青江鸥聚处前见林狖啼时枕上听此际自然无限趣王程不敢暂留停甚清美也

    程贺为崔亚持服
    　　唐代，崔亚郎中治理眉州时，程贺因地方事务被差遣担任防子。他的弟弟曾在州里担任过小书吏。崔公见到程贺的风度有些像儒生，于是问他：“你父亲读过书吗？”程贺下阶回答说：“略懂一些文学。”崔公指了一件物品让他赋诗，程贺的诗作颇有意思，崔公于是命令他回去准备选日装写所业，并且对他进行了高度赞扬。程贺因此被称为进士，完全依赖崔公的门路，没有其他途径。他参加了二十五次科举考试才及第，每次进京都会住在博陵的府邸，常常感激崔公的提拔之恩。崔公去世后，程贺为他服丧三年，人们都称赞他的孝行。

    　　髙太尉骈请留蛮宰相事
    　　唐代，南蛮侵犯西川，苦于缺乏防御设施。自咸通年间以后，剑南地区深受其害。牛丛尚书担任镇守时，面对蛮寇的侵袭无能为力。髙公从东平调任成都，蛮酋攻打蜀城，掌武先选精锐士兵前来救援，有人背负神符一道，蛮人得知后望风而逃。后来，僖宗访问蜀地，深怀疑心作梗，于是同意与南蛮联姻，许配公主。蛮王因为与大国联姻而感到幸运，因此命令宰相赵隆眉、杨竒鲲、段义宗前来朝见，并迎接公主。髙太尉从淮海地区迅速上书，指出南蛮的核心人物只有这几人，请求停止联姻并暗中除掉他们。直到僖宗返回京城，南方才得以安定。杨竒鲲等人皆有文学才华，途中作诗云：“风里浪花吹又白，雨中岚色洗还青。江鸥聚处窗前见，林狖啼时枕上听。此际自然无限趣，王程不敢暂留停。”诗作清新优美。

    夏侯相以术而殂

    Xia Houxiang died due to his technique.
    After attaining wealth and status, Chancellor Xia Hou Gongzi acquired Peng Su's technique, which greatly benefited him. He was dispatched to Puzhong and pleased with a courtesan, but she was unable to serve him properly, leading to a significant loss and ultimately his death. There was a man named Xia Hou Changguan, originally a former monk, who had once relied on the chancellor's protection. After the chaos, he took his family to settle in the mountains of Fengzhou, where he later passed away, leaving only a widow and a son. The old woman revealed this technique to the high-ranking official Man Cun, who greatly benefited from it. His son, named Ji, learned to compose poetry and entered the Western Sichuan region, relying on a distinguished minister to serve as an attendant. People called him Xia Hou Lizi, continuing the family's reputation for debauchery. I heard about this from Qiang Shanren, who explained it in great detail. I once knew Ji, and his son-in-law Luo Qiao, who also knew me, had many concubines. I suspect he was influenced by the Xia Hou family's ways. Could Xia Hou Changguan not have been the chancellor's teacher?

    张金吾威势取术
    　　唐金吾大将军张直方一旦开筵命朝士看干水银防制不谬众皆叹羡以谓清河曾遇至人良久张公大笑曰已非所能有自来矣顷任桂府团练使逢一道士蕴此利术就而求之终不可得乃令健卒缚于山中以死胁之道士惊怕但言药即多献术则不传唯死而已由是得药纵其他适今日奉呈唯成丹也非已能也
    　　蔡畋虚诞【何法成附】
    　　唐髙骈镇成都甚好方术有处士蔡畋者以黄白干之取瓦一片研丹一粒半涂入火烧成半截紫磨金乃竒事也蔡生自人皆敬之以为地仙燕公求之不得久而乖露乃是得药于人惑卖弄为元戎笞杀之王先主时有何法成者小人也以卖符药为业其妻微有容色居在北禅院侧左院有毳衲者因与法成相识出入其家令卖药银就其家饮啗

    Explanation

    155

    张金吾威势取术

    唐金吾大将军张直方有一天举办宴会，邀请朝中官员观看干水银的防制过程，众人无不赞叹羡慕，认为张公曾遇到过高人。过了许久，张公大笑道：“这东西已非我所能拥有，它自会来。”不久后，他担任桂府团练使，遇到一位道士，道士掌握了这种有利的术法。张公前去求取，道士始终不肯传授。于是，张公命令健壮的士兵将道士绑在山中，以死相威胁。道士惊恐万分，只说如果给他药物，他就会多献一些术法，但术法不会传授，只有死路一条。因此，张公得到了药物，放任它去其他地方。今天，他只呈上成丹，说这并非他自己的能力。

    蔡畋虚诞【何法成附】

    唐代高骈镇守成都时，非常喜爱方术。有一位隐士蔡畋，以黄白术（炼金术）为业。他取来一片瓦，研磨一粒半的丹药，涂在瓦上，然后点燃，烧成半截紫磨金，这是一件奇事。蔡畋因此受到人们的尊敬，被认为是一位地仙。燕公（高骈）求他传授术法，但始终未能如愿。后来，蔡畋的真实情况被揭露，原来他从别人那里得到了药物，并以此炫耀。最终，他被元戎（高骈）鞭打致死。在王先主（王建）时期，有一个叫何法成的小人，以卖符药为业。他的妻子稍有姿色，住在北禅院旁边。左院有一位毳衲者（僧人），与何法成相识，经常出入他家，让他卖药银，就在他家吃饭。

    156

    而已法成以其内子饵之而求其法此僧秘惜迁延未传乃令其妻冶容而接之法成自外还家掩缚欲报廵吏此僧惊惧因谬授其法并成药数两释缚而窜法成闻【一作得】此术以致发狂大言于人夸解利术未久闻于蜀后主召入苑中与军职然不尽僧法他日药尽遽属更变伶俜而已偶免谬妄之诛也彭韬光者与何生切邻兼得其事为余话之
    　　申屠别驾术祸
    　　髙骈镇维扬有申屠别驾懐至术为吕用之谮毁一旦作窜燕公命吏赍长限牒所在寻捕至襄州禅院中遇之擒得申生寄襄狱絷维申生告狱吏要见督邮韦公吏以告之韦遽面见屏人曰某身上有化金药欲献元戎刘公巨容可乎韦审之遂非时入谒因得道逹防甎瓦半叶以呈之刘公叹讶乃虚以判狱而匿之僖皇在蜀降天使至岘山即田令孜弟也刘公乗醉将药

    Final Translation

    Only the final translation is provided below:

    Final Translation

    Afterward, Fa Cheng used his wife as bait to obtain the monk's method. The monk, secretly cherishing it and procrastinating, did not wish to pass it on. He then instructed his wife to adorn herself and meet him. When Fa Cheng returned home, he tied her up and intended to report the matter to the patrol officer. The monk, in fear, mistakenly taught him the method and gave him a few doses of the medicine, then released her bindings and fled. Upon hearing of this method, Fa Cheng went mad and boasted to others about the money-making technique. Soon, the method became known to the Later Shu Emperor, who summoned him into the garden and granted him a military position, though it was not fully the monk's method. Later, when the medicine ran out, he suddenly changed his ways and became lonely and destitute, narrowly escaping punishment for false claims. Peng Tao Guang, a close neighbor of He Sheng, learned the story and told it to me.

    The Misfortune of Shentu the Magistrate

    Gao Pian, stationed in Weiyang, had a magistrate named Shentu who possessed a secret technique. Lü Yongzhi slandered him, and he was exiled. Yan Gong ordered officials to search for him with a long-term warrant. They captured him at a Zen temple in Xiangzhou, where he was imprisoned. Shentu told the jailer that he wished to see the postal inspector, Wei Gong. The jailer informed Wei, who hurriedly met him in private. Shentu said, "I have a potion that can turn gold. Would you like to offer it to the military governor, Liu Gong Junrong?" Wei agreed and, at an unusual time, went to see Liu. He was able to present half a tile of the potion, which Liu admired and kept, using it to judge cases. Emperor Xizong, while in Shu, sent an envoy to Xianshan Mountain, where Liu was drunk and took the potion.

    金夸衒于中使中使廻闻于田中尉洎刘司空朝觐行在与申生偕往藏此人不令他适田军容衔之于导江庄加害刘申皆不幸也有一子号申司马居朗州尚存防汞药在身荆南节判司空董太监得申生四粒药防四汞奉一百千以慰好竒之心也【王蜀时有一士着緑布衫常在街衢仍栖逆旅廵使萧懐武欲求其术坚确不与遂于马院打杀之盖不能慎持所致也】

    Jin夸衒 was heard by the imperial messenger, who then informed Tian Zhongwei and Liu Sike. They went together to the imperial court with Shen Sheng, but Jin夸衒 was not allowed to go elsewhere.     Zong Xiaozhi's Medicine Demon

    In the Tang Dynasty, there was a man named Zong Xiaozhi in Chang'an who practiced alchemy and was known for his skills in transforming base metals into gold and silver. He spent his time in Pingkang, enjoying the company of women, and was acquainted with Chen Jingxuan, the governor of Sichuan, during Chen's early days. They lost favor due to a matter of jealousy. Later, Chen Jingxuan rose to power and was appointed as the governor of Chengdu. During the turmoil of the kingdom, Emperor Xianzong fled to Sichuan. Zong Xiaozhi also fled to Jinjiang but feared that Yin川 would find out, so he traveled to Zizhong County, where he remained silent and hidden, fearing that others would know about him. He stayed at Yingzhen Temple and began to refine a large furnace of elixir, but he had not completed it. Zong Xiaozhi was skilled in the art of Liunian divination and would perform it every morning to predict the auspiciousness of the day. One day, he suddenly lost his voice and decided to leave. He traveled to Neijiang County, where Yin川 sent officials to find him. The道士 who had been refining the elixir with him took the medicine and passed it on to several families, but none of them benefited from it. No one knew why this was so.

    Translation:

    The Execution of a Monk by Chancellor Li Bi

    During the Tang Dynasty, Chancellor Li Bi was sent to govern the eastern region of Shu. There was a monk, whose name is unknown, who presided over initiation ceremonies and attracted many people from all directions who took the full monastic vows. Donations poured in from all over, and due to his busy schedule, the monk's desire for material things became intense. Eventually, he confessed his misconduct, revealing that he had initiated approximately 145 young girls into the monastic life, and they presented items related to their bodies. The high-ranking officials punished him.

    The author, known as Baoguangzi, once heard from his colleague, General Wang, about a monk in Youzhou who was nearly eighty years old and the elder brother of a military officer. This monk would return to lay life due to his old age and was assisted by a servant named Qing. He engaged in disorderly behavior and eventually decided to renounce his monastic life, taking Qing as his partner. He remarked, "I never thought I would have such joy, and I regret knowing it too late." The military officials found this situation strange and laughed at him.

    The author also mentions a disciple monk of his, whom he does not wish to name, but who is very knowledgeable in scriptures and treatises and has not been revealed to have any misconduct. This monk was once present at an initiation ceremony where nuns sought guidance and called himself a guide. As a result, his reputation was filled with ugly rumors, but he did not feel ashamed.

    Alas, the precepts established by the Buddha are the gateway to the path of enlightenment. If not for the right person, they instead become a gathering place for lust. Indeed, the path is not in vain.

    崔元亮降云【赵驾仙何景冲梁威仪附】
    　　唐崔元亮曾典眉州每公退具简履以朝太上焚脩精至不舍昼夜尝于州衙开黄箓道场为民祈水旱疾疫而已散斋之晨必降祥云鸾州民咸覩【亮典湖州脩斋亦降仙太白为賛】至今眉州每歳设黄箓斋凡执【一作职】事军校及茶酒厮役祗承皆知斋法次第道士罗昭然寿一百一十三歳预崔牧之斋席跨驴出街坠驴而脚在镫内因拖曵而死也　又王蜀时玉局观道士赵驾仙上官道士忘其名住青城山脩斋入坛行法事其厮

    Cui Yuanliang and the Descending Auspicious Clouds [With Appendices on Zhao Jiaxian, He Jingchong, and Liang Wei]

    In the Tang dynasty, Cui Yuanliang once governed Meizhou. After each official session, he prepared and adhered to formal documents to worship the highest deity, performing rituals with utmost devotion, day and night without ceasing. He often opened a yellow script Taoist ceremony in the state office to pray for rain, drought, diseases, and epidemics for the people. During the fasting period in the morning, auspicious clouds and mythical birds would descend, which all the people of the state witnessed. [When Cui Yuanliang governed Huzhou and performed rituals, auspicious clouds and mythical birds also descended, and Li Bai composed an inscription.] To this day, Meizhou holds a yellow script ceremony every year. All military officers in charge, as well as servants who serve tea and wine and attendants, know the proper order of the ceremony. The Taoist priest Luo Zhaoran, who lived to be one hundred and thirteen years old, attended Cui Yuanliang's ceremony. He rode a donkey into the street, fell off the donkey, and with his foot still in the stirrup, was dragged and died. Another Taoist priest, Zhao Jiaxian, from the Shu Kingdom, lived in the Jade Bureau Temple. A Taoist priest named Shangguan, whose name is forgotten, resided in Qingcheng Mountain and performed rituals in the temple. One day, his servant was sleeping and had a nightmare, asking the master where he was. When asked, the servant replied, "I just saw four people wearing red robes descending from the sky, dragging two Taoist priests in front of the altar and whipping their backs twenty times." The questioner stopped him and told him not to speak. Soon after, Zhao Jiaxian and Shangguan Taoist both fell ill and died. Another Taoist priest, He Jingchong, served as the leader of the Taoist order and enjoyed eating garlic. When he performed rituals on the altar, he had a garlic smell. Later, when he performed rituals in Qingcheng and crossed the river, the boat capsized, and he drowned. This was probably a divine punishment for his disrespect to the Tao. Cheng Zhongling, the military general who governed Jingnan, summoned the Taoist priest Liang Wei to perform rituals. Liang Wei knelt and presented a memorial, then fell asleep. Cheng Zhongling dismissed him and destroyed the ritual site. This was also like Zhao Jiaxian and Shangguan Taoist. Generally, Buddhist monks and Taoist priests who attend ceremonies in Jing and Xiang provinces indulge in drinking, and the common people do not consider it wrong. How can they hope for auspicious signs to descend?

    关三郎入关
    　　唐咸通乱离后坊巷讹言关三郎兵入城家家恐悚罹其患者令人寒战栗亦无大苦农杨玭挈家自骆谷路入洋源行及秦岭回望京师乃曰此处应免关三郎相随也语未终一时股栗斯又何哉夫丧乱之间隂厉旁作心既疑矣邪亦随之关妖之说正谓是也愚防年曾省故里传有一夷迷魇人闾巷夜聚以避之凡有隙悉皆涂塞其忽来即扑人惊魇须臾而止
    　　希慕求进

    　　垂血泪

    Explanation

    160

    Guan Sanlang Enters the City

    After the chaos and turmoil of the Tang Xiantong era, there were rumors in the alleys that Guan Sanlang's ghostly army had entered the city, causing every household to be terrified, and those who suffered from it shivered with fear, though it did not cause much suffering. Hongnong's Yang Pin led his family from the Lugu Road into Yangyuan, reaching the Qinling Mountains and looking back at the capital. He said, "Here we should be spared from following Guan Sanlang." Before the sentence was finished, there was a sudden shiver. What else could this mean? During times of chaos and turmoil, evil spirits act from the side. Once the mind is doubtful, evil follows. The superstition about Guan Sanlang is exactly what this means. In my youth, I once visited my hometown and heard a story of a foreign demon that tormented people. People gathered in alleys at night to avoid it, and all gaps and holes were sealed. If the ghost came, it would suddenly attack and scare people, but it would stop after a short time.

    Aspiration for Advancement

    During the Tang Dazhong era, the imperial examination system was particularly active, and scholars from Fengding, Ding Maogui, stood out among the candidates. Those who associated with him often passed the exams first, while the two of them each took twenty attempts before achieving fame. How different were their outcomes? Before that, Li Du, Cui Yong, Sun Hua, and Zheng Ou, four prominent figures, received favor and were promoted. Therefore, it was said, "To seek to communicate with them." Sun Hua, Du, and Ou said, "Scholars without wealth or status, even with extraordinary thoughts, fine conduct, profound learning, and powerful writing, if not supported and promoted, they cannot be widely known. Thus, the admiration of Yan Hui and Lin Xiangru, the pursuit of fame and profit, cannot be avoided."

    Dripping Blood and Tears

    　　心疾不妨文章【李氏子附】
    　　唐世刘崇望弟兄五人内四人皆登进士第仕至将相丞郎其元昆崇彛不及第官至省郎生五男每院各与一人为后崇彛留一男少有才思一旦心疾唯染翰章制诰褒贬朝中卿相咸摭其实骨肉间惧闻于外旋取烬之宛为掌诰之美竟废于时鄙夫蜀乡与前简刺李咏使君有分陇右有一子年十四掌握管草词指挥天曹地府隂隙之事落翰如飞家君忧惧亦苦戒之此子乃曰但为我父勿预我事他日坠井而死心为灵台既婴风恙而才思伦序斯又何哉

    　　北梦琐言卷十一
    <子部,小说家类,杂事之属,北梦琐言>
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十二

    Explanation

    161

    The wife of the Tang dynasty scholar-official Yin Baohui, Lady Feng, was also from a prominent family in the capital. When Yin Baohui first took the imperial examination, all his essays were written by Lady Feng, and they all conformed to the established norms. Everyone knew that Yin Baohui was unrestrained and free-spirited, good at socializing, and never took writing seriously. During the rebellion, the couple suffered great misfortune. At first, Lady Feng was beheaded, and Yin Baohui lost his voice, with blood staining his face. His aunt, who was a nun, witnessed the tragedy and wept, telling the relatives of Yin Baohui. Only then did the relatives of Yin Baohui believe the ancient saying that sorrow is so great that tears cannot express it anymore, and only blood can.

    Having a heart disease does not prevent one from writing well. [Example: A son from the Li family]

    Among the five brothers of Liu Chongwang, four of them passed the imperial examination to become Jinshi and reached high positions such as generals, chancellors, and officials. The eldest brother, Chongyi, did not pass the imperial examination and held a position in the provincial government. He had five sons, each adopted by a different family. Chongyi kept one son, who was young and talented. One day, despite his heart disease, he wrote official documents and praised or criticized the officials in the court, capturing the essence of their actions. His family members were afraid that this information would leak out and quickly burned the documents. His talent for drafting official documents was ultimately wasted. A man from Sichuan, who had a son who was very skilled in writing and could write about supernatural matters quickly, was worried and tried to warn him. The son said, "Just be my father; do not interfere with my affairs." Later, he fell into a well and died. The heart is the seat of the mind, and when it is affected by illness, the order and sequence of thoughts are disrupted, leading to such outcomes.

    唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　卢藩神俊
    　　唐卢尚书藩以文学登进士第以英雄自许厯数镇薨于灵武连帅防赐吊祭内臣厚希例贶其家事力不充未办归装而天使所求无厌家人苦之亲表中有官人于灵前告曰家贫如此将何遵副尚书平生竒杰岂无威灵及此宦者乎俄而馆中天使中恶以至于卒是知精魂强俊者可不畏之哉八座从孙尚在江陵尝闻此説故纪之以儆贪货者
    　　杨不学仙
    　　唐相国杨江州人祖为本州都押衙父直为兰溪县主簿生四子发假严皆登进士第即大拜发以下皆至丞郎发以春为义其房子以柷以乘为名假以夏为义其房子以煚【古鼎反】为名以秋为义其房子以钜鏻镳鉴为名严以冬为义其房子以注渉洞为名尽有文学登髙第号曰脩竹杨家与静恭诸杨比于华盛收相少年于庐山修业一日寻幽至深之地遇一道者谓曰子若学道即有仙分必若作官位至三公终焉有祸能从我学道乎收持疑坚进取之心忽道人之语他日虽登廊庙竟离南荒而殛悲夫薛泽补阙乃杨氏之女孙壻尝语之

    Explanation

    162

    Translation:

    Lu Fan's Heroic Spirit

    During the Tang Dynasty, Lu Shangfu, a high-ranking official, passed the imperial examination through his literary talent and considered himself a hero. He served in several military posts and died in Lingwu. The governor-general sent condolences and a funeral offering, but the eunuch sought a generous gift according to precedent. The family's financial resources were insufficient to prepare the return goods, and the imperial messenger's demands were insatiable, causing great trouble for the family. A relative who held an official position said before the spirit of the deceased, "Our family is so poor, how can we fulfill the deputy's duties? Is there no supernatural power of our esteemed minister to protect us from this eunuch?" Soon after, the imperial messenger fell ill and died. It is known that the spirits of those who were strong and heroic should not be feared. The eighth seat's descendant, who still lives in Jiangling, has heard of this story and records it to warn those who are greedy for wealth.

    Yang Jia's Reluctance to Learn Taoism

    Yang Jia, the prime minister of the Tang Dynasty, was from Jiangzhou. His grandfather was the commandant of the capital city, and his father was the county clerk of Lanchi County. Yang Jia had four sons: Fa, Jia, Yan, and himself. All four sons passed the imperial examination and became Jinshi. Yang Jia was appointed to a high position, and Fa and the others all reached the rank of minister. Fa named his sons according to the seasons: Chuzi, Chengzi, and Chengzi. Jia named his sons according to the seasons: Jiongzhi, Jiongzhi, and Jiongzhi. Yan named his sons according to the seasons: Zhuzi, Dongzi, and Dongzi. All of them were accomplished in literature and passed the imperial examination, and they were known as the Bamboo Grove Yangs. They were compared to the Yangs of Jinggong in terms of their prosperity. A young man from the Yang family studied in the mountains of Lu. One day, he searched for a secluded place deep in the mountains and met a Taoist. The Taoist said to him, "If you study the Tao, you will have the potential to become a sage. But if you choose to serve in office, you will reach the highest ranks, but ultimately you will suffer misfortune. Can you follow me to learn the Tao?" The young man held onto his doubts and continued to strive for advancement, ignoring the Taoist's words. Later, although he reached high office, he was exiled to the southern wilderness and died tragically. Alas, Xue Ze, a relative by marriage, once told him about this.

    张氏子斆壁鱼
    　　唐张裼尚书有五子文蔚彛宪济美仁皆有名第至宰辅丞郎内一子忘其名少年闻说壁鱼入道经函中因蠧食神仙字身有五色人能取壁鱼吞之以致神仙而上升张子惑之乃书神仙字碎翦实于瓶中捉壁鱼以投之冀其蠧蚀亦欲吞之遂成心疾每一发作竟月不食言语麄秽无所避其家扃闭而守之俟其发愈一切如常而倍餐啜一月食料须品味而饫之多年方谢世是知心灵物也一伤神气善犹不可况为恶乎即刘辟吞人张子吞神仙善恶不同其伤一也

    Explanation

    163

    Zhang Xi, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, had five sons: Wenwei, Yi, Xian, Jimei, and Renshen, all of whom achieved high positions. Among them, one son, whose name is forgotten, heard a story about wall fish entering Taoist scriptures and eating the characters of immortals. He believed that by swallowing these wall fish, one could achieve immortality and ascend to heaven. Zhang was deceived by this idea and began to collect wall fish, placing them in a container with the characters of immortals. He hoped that the wall fish would eat the characters, and he would then swallow them to achieve immortality.

    Every time he had an episode, he would go a whole month without eating. His speech became coarse and indecent, and he had no shame or avoidance. His family locked him up and guarded him, waiting for him to recover. When he recovered, everything returned to normal, but he would eat double the amount of food for a month, indulging in a variety of flavors. After many years, he passed away.

    This shows that the mind is a thing, and even a slight injury to the spirit can have serious consequences. If good deeds are not possible, how much more so for evil deeds? Just as Liu Pi swallowed people, Zhang swallowed immortals. Their injuries are the same.

    栁大夫不受润笔【李徳阳附】
    　　唐栁大夫玭清亷耿介不以利回家世得笔法盖公权少师之遗妙也责授泸州牧礼参东川元戎顾彦朗相公适遇降德政碑顾欲濡染以光刋刻亚台曰恶劄固无所恡若以润笔先【一作见】赐即不敢闻命相国钦之书讫竟不干渎也　梁世兖州有下猛和尚聚徒说法檀施云集时号金刚禅也他日物故建塔树碑庐岳道士李德阳善欧书下猛之徒请书碑志许奉一千缗德阳不允乃曰若以一醉相酬得以施展千缗之遗非所望也终不肯书斯亦近代一髙人也

    Lu Dalu Refuses to Accept a Fee [With Li Deyang's Addition]

    Lu Dalu, a high-ranking official during the Tang Dynasty, was known for his integrity and disdain for material gain. His family had inherited the art of calligraphy from his predecessor, Master Gongquan, and he was appointed as the governor of Luzhou. During his time, he participated in the military affairs of the Eastern Shu, specifically with Duke Gu Yanlang. One day, an edict of virtue stone monument was to be erected, and Duke Gu Yanlang wished to embellish and illuminate the carving. The deputy said, "Bad calligraphy is not something I would be reluctant to give. If you were to give me a fee first, then I would not dare to accept the order." The chancellor admired his writing, and he finished without further bothering.

    During the Liang Dynasty, there was a monk named Xia Meng in Yanzhou who gathered disciples and preached. Donations and offerings gathered like clouds, and at that time, he was called the Diamond Chan. After some days, he passed away, and a pagoda and a monument were built. A Taoist priest named Li Deyang from Mount Lu, skilled in Ouyang Xun's calligraphy, was invited by the disciples of Xia Meng to write the inscription on the monument. They offered one thousand strings of coins, but Li Deyang refused. He said, "If you were to reward me with a drink, I could display my skills with the thousand strings of coins, but it is not what I hope for." He finally refused to write it, and this is also a great person of recent times.

    杨寅疑相术【李暠附】
    　　唐十军军容使开府严遵美门客杨寅善许之术于京城西畿逢一李生亦唐之疎属隆准龙顔垂手过膝杨生异之说于中尉由是时【一作暗】有资遗之意其必致非常黄寇犯阙僖宗【一作皇】幸蜀李生为士民挟持入京升含元殿不逾浃旬寻亦遇害岂大人之相只为一升殿乎莫可知之杨生叹嗟不复言知人之鍳也　王蜀先主时有道士李暠亦唐之宗室生于徐州而游于三蜀词辩敏防麤有文章因栖阳平观为妖人扶持上
    有紫气乃聚众举事将举而败妖辈星散而暠独罹其祸焉其适长裕者临卭之大儒也与暠相善不信暠之造妖良由躯干国姓为羣凶所凭所以多事之秋灭迹匿端无为緑林之嚆矢也先是李暠有书召玉局观杨德辉赴斋有老道崔无斁自言患聋有道而托算术往往预知吉凶德辉问曰将欲北行何如崔令画地作字农乃书北千两字崔公以千揷北成乖字去即乖耳杨生不果去而李暠斋日就擒道士多罹其祸杨之幸免由崔之力也

    Yang Yin Doubts the Art of Physiognomy [with Li Hao Attached]

    Yang Yin, a guest of Yan Zunmei, the Military Governor of the Ten Armies, was skilled in the art of physiognomy. In the western suburbs of the capital, he met a man named Li, who was also a distant relative of the Tang imperial family. Li had a high nose and a dragon-like face, with his hands hanging down past his knees. Yang Yin was amazed by this and told the Imperial Commissioner about it, who then had the intention to provide financial support. It was believed that such an appearance would lead to something extraordinary. However, when the Yellow Bandits invaded the palace, Emperor Xizong fled to Shu. Li was forced by the citizens into the capital and ascended to the Hanyuan Hall, but soon after he was killed. Could the great man's appearance only be for ascending a single hall? It is impossible to know. Yang Yin sighed and no longer spoke about the skill of knowing people.

    During the reign of the First Sovereign of Shu, there was a Taoist named Li Hao, who was also a member of the Tang imperial family. Born in Xu Prefecture, he traveled to the Three Shus. He was eloquent and quick-witted, roughly having some literary talent. He settled in Yangping Temple and was supported by evil people. When he saw a purple aura, he gathered a crowd and started a rebellion, but was about to succeed but failed. The evil people dispersed like stars, but Li Hao alone suffered the consequences. The one who was about to become the leader, a great scholar from Linzhou, was friends with Li Hao and did not believe that Li Hao was involved in making evil things. This was because of his noble appearance and imperial lineage, which made him supported by the evil group, especially in times of turmoil. He hid his tracks and disappeared, not becoming the beginning of the Green Forest rebellion.

    Before that, Li Hao wrote a letter inviting Yang Dehui from Yujue Temple to attend a gathering. An old Taoist named Cui Wudi claimed to be deaf and claimed to be skilled in mathematics, often predicting good and bad omens. Yang Dehui asked what it would be like to go north. Cui Wudi had him draw characters on the ground. Hongnong wrote the characters 'north' and 'thousand' on the ground. Cui Gong inserted 'thousand' into 'north' to form the character '乖.' If you go, it will be '乖.' Yang Yin did not go, and Li Hao was captured on the day of the gathering. Many Taoists suffered the consequences. Yang Yin's fortunate escape was due to the power of Cui Wudi.

    杨镳偶大姑神【史光泽附】
    　　唐杨镳収相之子少年为江西推廵优游外幕也属秋祭请祀大姑神西江中有两山孤拔号大者为大孤小者为小孤朱崖李太尉有小孤山赋寄意焉后人语讹作姑姊之姑创祠山上塑像艶丽而风涛甚恶行旅惮之每歳本府命从事躬祭镳预于此行镳悦大姑偶容有言谑浪祭毕囘州而见空中云雾有一女子容质甚丽俯就杨公呼为杨郎逊词云家姊多幸杨郎采顾便希囘桡以成礼也故来奉迎农惊怪乃曰前言戏之耳
    小姑曰家姊本无意輙慕君子而杨郎先自发言茍或中辍恐不利于君农忧惶遂然诺之恳希【一作布】从容一月处理家事小姑亦许之杨生归指挥讫仓卒而卒似有神来迎也薛泽阙与镳姻懿常言此事甚详近者故登州节判史在德郎中子光泽甚聦俊方修举业自别墅归乗醉入泰山庙谓神曰与神作第三儿得否自是归家精神恍惚似有见召逾月而殂也呜呼幽明道隔人路殊以身许之自贻伊戚将来可为鍳戒也

    A Tale of Yang Biao and the Big Sister Goddess [with an Addition on Shi Guangze]

    Yang Biao, the son of Yang Shouxiang, was a young man serving as a circuit inspector in Jiangxi during the Tang Dynasty. He was a leisurely official in the outer court. During the autumn sacrifice, he was ordered to worship the Big Sister Goddess. The West River has two isolated mountains, the larger one called "Big Solitary" and the smaller one called "Small Solitary." Zhu Ya's Li Taishuai wrote a poem about the Small Solitary Mountain, which conveyed a deeper meaning. Later generations misinterpreted the name, calling it "Sister's Sister's Sister." A temple was built on the mountain with a beautiful statue, but the wind and waves were very fierce, making travelers afraid. Every year, the local government ordered officials to personally perform the sacrifice. Yang Biao participated in this ritual and was pleased with the Big Sister Goddess. He jokingly remarked about her beauty. After the sacrifice, he returned to the state capital and saw a beautiful woman in the clouds who called him "Young Master Yang" and expressed her desire to complete a ritual with him. Hong Nong was surprised and said that the previous words were just jokes.

    The younger sister (Xiao Gu) explained that her elder sister had no intention but admired Yang Biao, and if he broke the promise, it might be harmful to him. Hong Nong was worried and agreed, giving her a month to handle family matters. Yang Biao returned home, gave instructions, and suddenly died, as if a ghost or deity had come to welcome him. Xue Ze, a relative of Yang Biao, often spoke about this incident in detail. Recently, the former magistrate of Dengzhou, Shi Zaidi, whose son Guo Guang was very intelligent and was studying, returned from a villa drunk and entered the Temple of Mount Tai, asking the god to make him a third son. After that, he returned home, his spirit was confused, and he seemed to be summoned, dying after a month. Alas, the boundary between the living and the dead is vast, and the path between humans and ghosts is different. To pledge oneself to such a fate is to bring sorrow upon oneself. This serves as a lesson for the future.

    栁氏子幞头脚【许承杰李思益附】

    A Man with Distinctive Headwear [Supplement by Xu Chengjie and Li Siyi]

    I once read the preface of the Liu family, which showed that their family rules were strict and they were the best among the scholarly class. Liu Pin was appointed to an official position in Luzhou County, but he was recalled from his post due to illness and sought medical treatment in Tongquan County, East Sichuan. In the inner chambers, a son of his brother [or nephew, or someone named Pei] came to visit him. The vice-premier turned away and said he did not recognize anyone. The family said, "He is a young official from a certain department." The vice-premier insisted he did not recognize him and could not understand his status. After a long time, the old servant thought, "Is this not the distinctive headwear of the young official?" It was indeed surprising, but if he lowered his headband before entering, he would not be blocked. The young official then lowered his headband, revealing a distinctive feature, and the vice-premier embraced him. His sincerity and thickness were evident in this manner. My relative Liu Kun, a distant relative of the vice-premier, lived temporarily in Yang'an County. His brothers visited him, and the vice-premier first asked if they were studying or writing. If not, he advised them to learn how to become officials. My ancestors became famous through writing and official careers, and I hope you do not neglect even a moment of study. In Luzhou County, there was a high-ranking official named Liu who made public furniture and equipment that were sturdy and heavy. They lasted through multiple administrations, and it is unknown if they still exist today. Xu Cun, a high-ranking official during the Shu dynasty, was a meritorious minister. His son inherited his position.

    杰即故黔使君禧实之子随母嫁许然其骄贵僭越少有伦比作都头军籍只一百二十有七人是音声伎术出即同节使行李凡从行之物一切奢大骑碧暖座垂纷错每脩书题印章微有浸渍即必改换书吏苦之流辈以为话端皆推茂刺顾夐为首许公他日有会乃谓顾曰阁下何太谈谤顾乃分疏因指同席数人为证顾无以对逡廵乃曰三哥不用草草碧暖座为众所知至于鱼袋上铸蓬莱山非我唱扬席上愈笑方知鱼袋更僭也刺茂州入蕃落为蕃酋害之　西川卫前军将李思益者所着衣服莫非华焕纎丽蜀先主左右羡而怪之先主曰李思益一副衣裳大有所费是要为我光扬军府仰与江货场

    Explanation

    168

    杰, the son of the late governor of Qian, Xixi Shi, followed his mother in marrying into the Xu family. He was arrogant and privileged, exceeding his proper bounds, and rarely has there been anyone like him. As a military leader with only 127 people under his command, these were musical and technical skills. When he went out, he treated himself like a high-ranking official, and all the items he carried with him were extravagant and grand. He rode on a green, warm seat with many decorations hanging down. Every time he wrote a letter and stamped it, if there was any slight dampness, he would definitely change it, which the clerks found burdensome. His peers used it as a topic of conversation, and they all recommended Gu Xun as the leader. One day, Xu Gong had a gathering and said to Gu, "Why do you speak so much about slander?" Gu then explained and pointed to several people at the table as evidence. Gu had nothing to say in response after hesitating, and said, "Brother Three, don't be so hasty. The green, warm seat is well-known. As for the fish bag with the Mount Penglai cast on it, it wasn't I who promoted it." The people at the table laughed even more, and they then realized that the fish bag was even more excessive. He was sent to Maozhou and was harmed by the tribal chieftain.

    Li Siyi, a general of the Western Sichuan Guard, wore clothes that were all splendid and luxurious, exquisite and beautiful. The attendants of Shu's first emperor envied and were surprised by him. The first emperor said, "Li Siyi spent a lot of money on one set of clothes. It was to enhance the prestige of my military command. I have entrusted him with the Jiang market."
