    勾当俾其作衣装也先主又于作院见匠人裹小朶帽子前如鹰觜后露脑枕怪而截其觜也又登楼见行人戴褴席帽云破【普没反】头烂额是何好事然自务俭素爱净洁皆此也蜀朝有小朝士裴璨俸薄且闲【一作困】或劝求宰一邑裴曰今之畿县非有仙骨何以得见其爱羡即可知也每云黄寇之后所失已多唯袜头袴穿靴不传旧时也仆同院司空监云木围裹头于事最便何必油拭火熨日日劳烦此一事不请师古又嫌以银棱甆器托里椀楪徒费功夫又曰措大暮年方婚少女一生之事遗丑可知自非铁石为心未有不贻他说戒之慎之因述栁氏幞头引起数事岂资谈笑亦足小惩也

    Explanation

    169

    In arranging for the making of clothes, the First Sovereign also saw in the workshop a craftsman wearing a small cap wrapped around his head, which was shaped like an eagle's beak in front and exposed at the back, resembling a pillow. He found this strange and ordered the beak-like part to be cut off. Later, while on a tower, he saw people wearing simple, rough hats made of straw, and remarked that their heads were broken and their foreheads sunburned, asking what good could come of such things. Yet, he himself valued simplicity and cleanliness, and all his actions reflected this. In the Shu Han court, there was a minor official named Pei Can, who had a low salary and was idle. Someone advised him to seek the position of magistrate of a county, to which Pei replied, "In today's capital region, one must have extraordinary qualities to be envied. It is clear that I do not possess such qualities." He often said that after the Yellow Bandits' rebellion, much had been lost, except for the socks, trousers, and boots that were no longer passed down from the past. My colleague, the Supervisor of the Treasury, said that wrapping the head with wood was the most convenient, and why bother with daily oiling, ironing, and smoothing? This one thing does not require following the ancients. He also disliked using silver-edged ceramic utensils to hold bowls and plates, as it was a waste of effort. He further said, "A scholar in old age marrying a young girl is a disgraceful thing to leave behind. Unless one has a heart of iron and stone, no one can avoid leaving behind warnings and advice." Because of this, I recount the story of the Liu-style headgear, which led to several incidents. These are not meant for idle talk but are sufficient as a small warning.

    铁阙贞澹
    　　唐干宁中阙杨贻德华族科名德孤道直不容于时请告华隂方属京国扰攘乃谋南来藏迹于江陵闾巷僦居不露行止旅舍无烟藜藿不给未尝陨获于时成中令延接朝客士有依刘之言农韬藏不及门宇一旦堂帖追回成令惊讶以为闻听不至阙申情礼兼以入翰苑秉钧轴期之阙曰人之官职又非妄图令公过饰何当奬遇今宰相何必要某至于垂搜

    Explanation

    170

    During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong of the Tang Dynasty, Yang Yide, a man of noble family and high moral integrity, found himself isolated and misunderstood by his contemporaries. He requested permission to leave and went to Huayin, as the capital was in turmoil. He planned to move south and hid in the alleys of Jiangling, renting a house and keeping a low profile. Living in poverty, he had no food and relied on simple, coarse fare, yet he remained undaunted.

    At the time, Cheng Zhongling, a high-ranking official, invited and received guests, and scholars expressed their admiration for him. Someone from Hongnong, so humble that he did not even have a place to meet visitors, was suddenly summoned back by a formal order. Cheng Zhongling was surprised, thinking that the person had not been properly informed or had not come to explain their situation. Cheng also invited the person to enter the imperial academy and hold a high position, promising him that his office was not sought for personal gain. Cheng remarked, "Lord Cheng is overly praising me; what should I do about this favor?" He questioned why the current prime minister needed to go to such lengths to find him.

    罗之命他日不过作南中一刺史尔此际必有奉扰中令赠三百缗只受三十缗办装所剰【一作残】却纳朝廷号为铁阙未久除道州牧却经江陵告成令求十人散从官衣装五十千行资他无所要成令甚重之他日栖南岳与元泰布衲遁希禅师同居车箱源防泉归本长老得祖印于杨公既殁家人亦终似得悬解之道也本公得禅道于三贤乃郑起先辈为愚话之
    　　张林多戏
    　　唐张林本士子擢进士第官至台侍御为诗小巧多采景于园林亭沼间至如菱叶乍翻人采后荇花初没舸行时他皆此受眷于崔相眧纬或谒相庭崔公曰何以久不拜见林曰为饭瓮子发崔讶饭瓮不康之语林曰数日来水米不入非不康耶又寒月遗以衣襦问其所需乃曰一衫向下便是张林相国大笑终始优遇也葆光子曰东方朔以诙谐自容娄君卿以唇舌取适非徒然也皆有意焉今世希酒炙之徒托公侯之势取容茍媚过于优旃自非厚德严正之人未有不为此辈调笑也

    Explanation

    171

    Translation:

    The decree for Luo stated that his future appointment would be no more than a governor of a southern prefecture. At this time, he would certainly receive a gift of 300 strings of cash from the official, but he only accepted 30 strings. After settling his expenses, he returned the remainder to the court, earning the nickname "Iron Gate." Shortly thereafter, he was appointed governor of Daozhou and passed through Jiangling. He asked the official to provide ten attendants with clothing and travel expenses of 50,000 coins, asking for nothing else. The official highly valued him. Later, he lived in the South Mountain with Master Yuan Tai, Master Dun Xi, and Elder Guiben, who received the patriarchal seal from Master Yang. After his death, his family also seemed to attain the way of liberation. Elder Guiben received the Chan teachings from three sages, including the elder Zheng Qi, who spoke to him about it.

    Zhang Lin was known for his playful nature. During the Tang Dynasty, Zhang Lin was originally a scholar who was selected as a Jinshi and rose to the position of Tai Shiyu. His poems were delicate and often depicted scenes from gardens and ponds, such as lotus leaves turning as people pick them, and water caltrop flowers disappearing as boats pass. He was favored by Chancellor Cui Zhaowei. When he visited the chancellor's residence, Cui asked, "Why have you not visited me for so long?" Zhang replied, "I have been without food and water for several days, not well." Cui was surprised by the response and asked, "Have you not been well?" Zhang said, "For several days, I have not eaten or drunk anything, so I am not well." Cui then gave him a robe for the cold month and asked what else he needed. Zhang replied, "Just one shirt is enough." Chancellor Zhang Lin laughed and treated him favorably throughout. The Preserver of Light said that Dongfang Shuo used humor to protect himself, and Lou Junqing used his words to gain comfort; neither did so in vain but had their intentions. In today's world, those who seek to please through alcohol and food rely on the power of nobles and princes, flattering them excessively. Only those with great virtue and strict integrity are not subject to ridicule by such people.

    沈尚书非命【刘建封附】
    　　唐沈询侍郎亚之之子也昆弟二人一人忘其名乗舸泛河为惊湍激船桚梁板漂递沈子亦漂而死询镇潞州宠婢夫人甚妬因配与家人归秦其婢旦夕只在左右归秦惭恨伺隙剚刃于询果罹凶手杀归秦以充祭亦无及也　唐天复中湖南节度使刘建封婬其牵拢官陈之妇陈为同列所戏耻而发怒伺便以蒺【一作冷】藜击杀之马氏有其位于今禁蒺【一作冷】藜盖惩彭城之遭罹也婬为大罚昔贤垂戒作人君父得不以子祸奴祸取鉴哉
    　　王潜司徒烧纸钱【秦威仪附】
    　　唐王潜司徒与武相元衡有分武公仓卒遭罹潜常于四时爇纸钱以奉之王后镇荆南有染户许琛一旦【一作日】暴卒翌日却活乃具牓子诣衙云要见司徒乃通入于阶前问之琛曰初被使人追摄至一衙府未见王且领至判官防见一官人凭几曰此人错来自是鹰坊许琛不干汝事即发遣回谓许琛曰司徒安否我即武相公也大有门生故吏鲜有念旧于

    The Unjust Fate of Minister Shen [With Appendix: Liu Jianfeng]

    Shen Xun, a Tang dynasty official of the rank of Shilang, was the son of Shen Ya Zhi. He had two brothers, one of whom’s name is forgotten. Once, he boarded a boat and set out to drift along the river, but the violent rapids struck the boat, breaking the bridge’s planks, which drifted downstream. Shen’s son was also swept away and died. Later, when Shen was stationed in Lüzhou, he favored a concubine, but his wife was very jealous. As a result, he arranged for the concubine to be married off to a member of his household named Guī Qín. The concubine remained constantly by his side. Guī Qín, feeling ashamed and resentful, waited for an opportunity to stab Shen. Indeed, she became the murderer, killing Shen in order to offer him as a sacrifice, but it was too late.

    In the year Tianfu of the Tang dynasty, Liu Jianfeng, the military governor of Hunan, committed adultery with the wife of an official named Chen, who was one of his subordinates. Chen was mocked by his peers, which shamed and enraged him. Seizing an opportunity, he killed Liu Jianfeng with a蒺藜 [or 冷藜]. The Ma family now holds this position, and the use of蒺藜 [or 冷藜] is now prohibited, as a punishment for the misfortune that befell Pengcheng. Adultery is a great punishment; the wise men of old have warned us. Should not rulers and fathers take heed from the misfortunes of their children and servants?

    Minister Wang Qian and the Burning of Paper Money [With Appendix: Qin Weiyi]

    In the Tang dynasty, Minister Wang Qian had a close relationship with Wu Yuanheng, the chancellor. When Wu met with sudden misfortune, Wang often burned paper money throughout the four seasons as a tribute to him. Later, when Wang became the governor of Jingnan, a dyer named Xu Chen suddenly died one day, but the next day he awoke and was alive again. He then prepared a notice and went to the office, saying he wished to see the Prime Minister. He was then brought before Wang at the steps and questioned. Xu Chen said, "At first I was taken by messengers to a government office, where I did not see you [Wang], but was instead taken to see the chief official. There, I met a man seated at a desk who said, 'This man has come by mistake. He belongs to the falconers. Xu Chen has nothing to do with you. Send him back.' Then the man said to Xu Chen, 'How is the Prime Minister? I am Chancellor Wu. I have many former students and officials, but few still remember the old days.'"

    173

    身后者唯司徒不忘每歳常以纸钱见遗深感恩德然所赐纸钱多穿不得司徒事多防检不至仰为我诣衙具导此意王公闻之悲泣惭讶而鹰坊许琛果亦物故自此选好纸剪钱以奉之此事与杨収相于郑愚尚书处借钱事同　又南岳道士秦保言威仪勤于焚脩者曾白真君云上仙何以须纸钱有所未喻夜梦真人曰钱即吏所籍我又何须由是岳中亦信之
    　　崔从事为庙神赐药【李氏土地神附】
    　　闽从事崔员外忘其名正直检身幕寮所重奉使湖湘复命在道逢寇贼悉遭杀戮唯外郎于仓惶中忽有人引路获免驱驰逺路复患痁疾行迈之次难求药饵途次延平津庙梦为庙神赐药三丸服之惊觉顿愈此亦神辅德也　彭城刘山甫自云外祖李公敬彛郎中宅在东都毓财坊土地最灵家人张行周事之有应未大水前预梦告张求饮食至其日率其遏水岸【一作头】并不冲圮李宅异事也

    Explanation

    173

    Only the final translation of the source text will be provided below:

    After his death, only the Sima (司徒) did not forget and every year he would often leave paper money as a gift, deeply grateful for the kindness. However, the paper money given was often perforated and unusable. The Sima, being busy with many inspections, did not go to the office to convey this meaning. The prince (王公) heard of it and was moved to tears, feeling ashamed and surprised. The falconry official Xu Chen indeed died. From then on, they selected good paper to cut into money to offer to him. This matter is similar to the case where Yang Shou borrowed money from Zheng Yu, the Shangshu.

    Also, the Taoist Qin Bao of Nanyue said that the dignitary who diligently burned incense once told the Immortal Master that the celestial being needed paper money, which was not understood. At night, he dreamed that the Immortal Master said, "Paper money is what the record-keeping officials need; why do I need it?" Therefore, people in the mountains also believed it.

    Cui, an official, was given medicine by the temple deity. Cui, an official from Fujian, whose name is forgotten, was upright and self-disciplined, highly respected by his subordinates. He was sent on a mission to Hunan and returned by way of the road, where he encountered bandits who killed everyone. Only the outer official was suddenly guided by someone in a panic and escaped. He hurried on a long journey and fell ill with malaria. On the way, he stayed at the Yandu Temple and dreamed that the temple deity gave him three pills of medicine. After taking them, he woke up suddenly and was instantly cured. This is also a case of divine assistance for virtue.

    From Pengcheng, Liu Shanfu said that his grandfather, Li Gong Jingyi, the Langzhong, lived in the Yuchai Ward in Dongdu, where the land deity was very powerful. The family servant Zhang Xingzhou had dealings with it and received responses. Before a great flood, he dreamed in advance and was told to prepare food and drink. On that day, he led his family to block the riverbank, and the water did not overflow, protecting Li's house. This is an unusual event.

    张璟为灵庙草奏
    　　庐山书生张璟干宁中以所业之桂州欲谒连帅张相至衡州犬嘷滩损船上岸寝于江庙为庙神所责生以素业对之神为改容延坐从容云有王【一作巫】立仁者罪合族诛庙神为其分理【一作疏】奏于岳神无人作奏璟为草之既奏允神喜以白金十饼为赠刘山甫与廖隲校书亲见璟说其事甚详也
    　　浐水神正直
    　　唐黄寇奔冲有小朝士裴忘其名移挈妻子南趋汉中才发京都其室女路次暴亡兵难挥霍不暇藏瘗其为悲悼即可知也行即浴谷夜闻其女有言不见其形父母怪而诘之女曰我为浐水神之子强暴诱归其家厥父责怒以妄杀生人遽行笞责兼逊谢抚慰差人送来縁夕旦未有托且欲随大人南行俾拔茅为苞致于箱笥之中庶以魂识依止饮食语言不异于常尔后白于严慈云已有生处悲咽告辞去夫神之事世所难言素浐之灵有义方之训所谓聦明正直之流也
    　　堑杜氏山冈事【鲜于仲通唐氏严氏附】

    Explanation

    174

    Zhang Jing drafted a memorial for the temple.

    During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong of Tang, Zhang Jing, a scholar from Mount Lu, traveled to Guilin to meet the military governor Zhang Xiang. On his way to Hengzhou, his boat was damaged by a dog barking at the shore, forcing him to sleep on land near a river temple. There, he was rebuked by the temple deity. Zhang Jing responded with his usual scholarly work, and the deity changed its expression and invited him to sit. The deity then spoke calmly, saying, "There is a man named Li Ren, who is a king or shaman, and his crime warrants the punishment of entire family. The temple deity intervened on his behalf and submitted a petition to the mountain deity. No one had previously composed such a memorial, so Zhang Jing drafted it. After the memorial was submitted, it was approved, and the deity was pleased, giving him ten pieces of white gold as a gift. Liu Shanfu and Liao Zhi, the imperial scholars, personally heard Zhang Jing recount the story in great detail.

    The deity of the Chan River is known for its integrity.

    During the turmoil caused by the Yellow Turban rebels, a minor official named Pei, whose name is forgotten, fled south with his wife and children to Hanzhong. Just after leaving the capital, his daughter suddenly died during their journey. In the chaos of the military conflict, there was no time to properly bury her body. The family was deeply grieved. Later, while passing through a valley, they heard their daughter speak at night, though they did not see her form. Her parents were surprised and asked her what had happened. She said, "I am the son of the deity of the Chan River. A forceful and violent person lured me back to my home. My father was angry and punished me for killing a living being. He then scolded and comforted me, sending me away. Since the evening, I have no place to stay and wish to follow my parents south. Please pull up some grass to wrap me and place me in a box so that my spirit can find a resting place. My diet and speech will be the same as before." Afterward, she informed her mother, saying, "I have already found a new place to be reborn." She then wept and bid farewell, departing. The affairs of ghosts and deities are difficult to speak of in the world, but the deity of the Chan River has given her a lesson in righteousness and virtue, embodying the qualities of wisdom and integrity.

    The story of the trench on Mount Du, involving Xianyu Zhongtong, the Tang family, and the Yan family.

    古有宅墓之书世人多尚其事识者犹或非之杜公正伦与京兆宗派不同常轻逺衔之洎公宦逹后因事堑断杜陵山脉由是诸杜数代不振　鲜于仲通兄弟阆州新井县人崛起俱登将坛望气者以其祖先坟上有异气降勅堑断之裔孙有鲜于岳者防年寝处席底有一小蛇盖新出卵者家人见之以为竒事此侯及壮常有自之色歴官终于普州安岳县令不免风尘其徒戏之曰鲜于蛇也　唐峰亦阆州人有坟茔在茂贤草市峰因贩与一术人偕行经其
    先茔术士曰此坟茔子孙合至公相峰谓曰此即家坟陇也士曰若是君家恐不胜福也【一作耶】子孙合为贼盗皆不令终峰志之尔后遭遇蜀先主开国峰亦典郡其二道袭官【一作等】皆至节将三人典郡竟如术士之言何其騐也　严司空震梓州盐亭县人所居枕釜戴山但有鹿鸣即严氏一人必殒或一日有亲表对坐闻鹿鸣其表曰釜戴山中鹿又鸣严曰此际多应到表兄其表兄遽对曰表兄不是严家子合是三兄与四兄不日严氏子一人果亡是何异也

    Explanation

    175

    In ancient times, there were books on tombs and dwellings, and many people valued these practices. Even knowledgeable individuals sometimes criticized or doubted them. Du Gongzheng, whose surname was different from the Jingzhao clan, often felt slighted and harbored resentment against them. After Du Gongzheng became an official and achieved prominence, he took advantage of an opportunity to cut off the mountain range of Duling. As a result, the Du lineage declined for several generations.

    Xianyu Zhongtong and his brothers were from Xincun County, Langzhou, and they rose to prominence, both becoming generals. Astrologers reported that their ancestors' graves had unusual qi (energy), so the emperor ordered the graves to be cut off. A descendant named Xianyu Yue, when young, found a small snake hatching from an egg under the bed mat. His family thought it was a strange and miraculous event. This lord, when grown, often had a self-important or arrogant look. He held various official positions and ended his career as the magistrate of Anyue County, Puzhou, unable to escape the troubles of the world. His followers joked that he was the "Snake of Xianyu."

    Tang Feng, also from Langzhou, had ancestors' graves in Maoyan Grass Market. While traveling with a fortune-teller, Tang Feng passed by his ancestors' graves. The fortune-teller said that the descendants of this grave would become high-ranking officials. Tang Feng replied, "This is indeed our family's grave." The fortune-teller said, "If so, your family might not be able to bear the good fortune. The descendants would become bandits and not have a good end." Tang Feng remembered this and later encountered the founding of the Shu state. Tang Feng also governed a prefecture, and his two sons inherited official positions, all becoming generals. Three of them governed prefectures, just as the fortune-teller had predicted. How accurate his prediction was!

    Yan Shikong Zhen lived in Yanting County, Zizhou, with his home situated near the Fudi Mountain. Whenever there was a deer's call, one member of the Yan family would die. One day, a relative and a cousin were sitting together and heard a deer's call. The cousin said, "The deer in Fudi Mountain has called again." Yan said, "This time, it should be your elder brother." His elder brother quickly replied, "It's not my elder brother; it should be my third and fourth brothers." Soon, one of the Yan family members died. What a strange coincidence!

    鼠狼智
    　　相国张公文蔚庄在东都北【一作柏】坡庄内有鼠狼穴养四子为蛇所吞防狼雄雌情切于穴外坋土恰容蛇头俟其出穴果入所坋处出头度其囘转不及当腰齧断而劈蛇腹衔出四子尚有气置于穴外衔豆叶嚼而傅之皆活何微物而有情有智若是乎最灵者人胡不思也

    　　北梦琐言卷十二

    　　草贼号令公
    　　王中令铎落都统除滑州节度使寻罢镇以河北安静于杨全玫有旧避地浮阳与其都统幕客十来人从行皆朝中士子及过魏乐彦祯礼之甚至铎之行李甚侈从客侍姬有辇下升平之故态彦祯有子曰从训素无赖爱其车马姬妾以问其父之幕客李山甫以咸通中数举不第尤私愤于中朝贵达因令图之俟铎至甘陵以轻骑数百尽掠其槖装姬仆而还铎与賔客皆遇害及奏朝廷云得贝州报某日有杀刼一人姓王名令公其忽诞也如此彦祯子寻为乱军所杀得非琅琊公诉于上帝乎

    Translation

    The Intelligence of the Wolf

    In the estate of Chancellor Zhang Gong Wenwei, located in the northern part of the Eastern Capital (Luoyang), there was a wolf den. The wolf had four cubs, which were swallowed by a snake. The male and female wolves were deeply concerned and gathered soil outside the den, which was just right to cover the snake's head. They waited for the snake to emerge from the den, and when it did, it found it could not turn back in time. The wolves then bit the snake in the middle and tore open its belly, carrying out the four cubs, which were still alive, and placed them outside the den. They bit beans and leaves and applied them to the cubs, and all of them survived. How could such a small creature have such emotion and intelligence? The most intelligent beings, humans, why do they not think about this?

    Records of the Northern Dreams, Volume Twelve
    Imperially Approved Four Treasuries
    Records of the Northern Dreams, Volume Thirteen
    Tang Dynasty, Compiled by Sun Guangxian

    The Grass Bandit Commander

    Wang Zhongling Duo, who had lost his position as military governor, was appointed as the Jiedushi of Huazhou. Soon after, he was removed from his post. Due to the peaceful situation in Hebei, he had a past relationship with Yang Quanmei and fled to Fuyang. He was accompanied by about ten members of his military governor's staff, all of whom were scholars from the capital. When they passed through Wei, Le Yanzhen treated them very respectfully. Wang's entourage was very opulent, and his guests and attendants displayed the old ways of peace and prosperity in the imperial capital.

    Le Yanzhen had a son named Congxun, who was usually a rascal. He loved Wang's carriages, horses, and attendants and asked his father's staff member Li Shanfu, who had failed the exams several times during the Xiantong era, about his feelings. Li harbored private resentment against the powerful in the capital. Therefore, he ordered to plot against Wang. They awaited Wang's arrival in Ganling and, with a few hundred light cavalry, seized all his belongings, attendants, and servants and returned. Wang and his guests were all killed. When the report was made to the court, it stated that on a certain day in Beizhou, one person named Wang Linggong was killed and robbed. How absurd and fabricated it was! Le Yanzhen's son was soon killed by the rebel army. Was it not the case that Langya Gong complained to the Heavenly Emperor?

    王重荣逐两帅
    　　河中节度使王重荣始为牙将黄巢犯阙元戎李都奉伪畏重荣党附者多因荐为副使一日忽谓都曰凢人受恩只可私报不可以公徇令公助贼防一于国不忠而又日加箕敛众口纷然倐忽变生何以遏也遽命斩其伪使都无以对因以军印授重荣而去及都至行在朝廷又以前京兆尹窦潏间路至河中代都为帅重荣迎之潏前为京兆尹有惨酷之名时谓之堕叠及至翌日集
    军校于庭谓曰天子命重臣作镇将遏贼冲安可轻议斥逐令北门出乎且为恶者必一两人而已尔等可言之潏不知军校皆重荣之亲党也众皆不对重荣乃自屏肃佩剑歴阶而上谓潏曰为恶者非我而谁召潏之仆吏控马及阶请依李都前例速去之潏不敢仰视乃跃马复由北门而出重荣破黄巢有功正授节制封郡王与田令孜结怨他日为部将常行儒杀之时号铁条以其刚也

    Explanation

    177

    Wang Chongrong Drives Out Two Commanders

    Wang Chongrong, the military governor of Hedong, originally served as a military officer. During the rebellion led by Huang Chao, the supreme commander Li Du served the rebel regime. Those who feared Wang Chongrong and supported him were often recommended to become deputy governors. One day, Wang Chongrong suddenly said to Li Du, "Anyone who receives favor should only repay it privately and not abuse it for public gain. You are helping the rebels to guard one province, which is disloyal to the country, and you also impose heavy taxes, causing widespread discontent. Suddenly, a crisis arises, how can it be stopped?" He immediately ordered the execution of the rebel envoy. Li Du had no response and handed over the military seal to Wang Chongrong and left.

    When Li Du arrived at the imperial court, the court appointed the former Jingzhao Governor Dou Yu to take his place in Hedong. Wang Chongrong welcomed him. Dou Yu, before being Jingzhao Governor, had a reputation for being cruel and was called "Duo Die." The next day, Wang Chongrong gathered the military officers in the courtyard and said, "The emperor has appointed a great minister to defend the frontier and stop the rebels, how can you lightly discuss expelling him, should he leave through the north gate? Those who are evil are probably just one or two people, you can speak up." Not knowing that the military officers were all close allies of Wang Chongrong, they remained silent. Wang Chongrong then calmly, with a drawn sword, ascended the steps and said to Dou Yu, "Those who are evil are none other than myself. Summon Dou Yu's servants to control the horses and ask them to follow the precedent set by Li Du and leave quickly." Dou Yu dared not look up and jumped on his horse, leaving through the north gate.

    Wang Chongrong defeated Huang Chao and was rewarded with the title of military governor and the rank of marquis. He later formed an alliance with Tian Lingzi, and one of his subordinates, Chang Xingru, was killed. At that time, Chang was known as "Tie Tiao" because of his strictness.

    郑文公报恩
    　　郑文公畋字台文父亚曾任桂管观察使畋生于桂州小字桂儿时西门思恭为监军有诏征赴阙亚饯于北郊自以衰年因以畋托之曰他日愿以桂儿为念九泉之下不敢忘之言讫然流涕思恭志之及为神策军中尉亚已卒思恭使人召畋馆之于第年未及冠甚爱之如甥侄因选师友教导之畋后官至将相黄巢之入长安西门思恭逃难于终南山畋以家财厚募有勇者访而获之以归岐下温清侍膳有如父焉思恭终于畋所畋葬于鳯翔西冈松柏皆手植之未几畋亦卒葬近西门之坟百官皆造二陇以吊之无不堕泪咸服其义也
    　　韩简听书【李茂贞附】
    　　魏博节度使韩简性麄质每对文士不晓其说心常耻之乃召一孝亷令讲论语及讲至为政篇明日谒诸从事曰仆近知古人淳朴年至三十方能行立外有闻者无不絶倒　秦王李茂贞请三传王利甫讲春秋利甫古僻性狷然演经义文亹亹堪听茂贞连月听之不倦利甫后寄褐于道门改名昼卒于洛中也武臣未必轻儒但未睹通儒多逢鄙薄之辈沮其学善也惜哉

    Explanation

    178

    Zheng Wen Gong Repays a Debt of Gratitude
    Zheng Wen Gong, courtesy name Tai Wen, was the son of Zheng Ya, who once served as the Inspector of the region of Guan. When Xi Men Si Gong was summoned to the capital by imperial edict, Zheng Ya sent Zheng Wen Gong off at the northern outskirts of the city and entrusted him to Xi Men Si Gong, saying, "I hope you will remember my son, Gui Er, in the future." Zheng Ya then wept, and Xi Men Si Gong remembered the promise. When Xi Men Si Gong became the commander of the Divine Strategy Army, Zheng Ya had already passed away. Zheng Wen Gong used his family wealth to hire brave people to find and bring Xi Men Si Gong back to Qishan. He cared for Xi Men Si Gong as if he were his father. Xi Men Si Gong died at Zheng Wen Gong's place, and Zheng Wen Gong planted trees himself at the burial site. Soon after, Zheng Wen Gong also died and was buried near Xi Men Si Gong's grave. Officials visited both graves and shed tears, acknowledging their righteousness.

    Han Jian Listens to Books [Li Maozhen Attached]
    The Governor of Weibo, Han Jian, was rough and crude in nature. Whenever he was in the company of scholars, he did not understand their discourse, which made him feel ashamed. He then summoned a scholar named Xiao Liang to lecture on the Analects of Confucius. When they reached the chapter on "Government," the next day, Han Jian met with his subordinates and said, "I recently learned that ancient people were simple and honest, and it wasn't until they were thirty years old that they could walk and stand properly. Those who heard this were all amazed." The Prince of Qin, Li Maozhen, invited Wang Lifu, a renowned scholar, to lecture on the Spring and Autumn Annals. Wang Lifu was old-fashioned and eccentric, but he explained the meaning of the classics in a way that was both engaging and worth listening to. Li Maozhen listened to him for months without tiring. Afterward, Wang Lifu became a Taoist monk, changed his name to Dayu, and died in Luoyang. It is not that martial officials necessarily look down on scholars, but they often encounter those who are shallow and discourage their studies. This is truly a pity.

    孟方立陈桑梓礼【罗虬附】
    　　昭义军节度使孟方立邢州平乡人也少以勇力于本军为裨将广明中潞帅髙浔攻诸爽于河阳方立出天井关为前锋时浔为大将刘广所逐广忌方立留戍于关后广为潞人所杀三军乃以方立为帅因有首丘之思遂移军于邢州用法平正人皆附之始拜坟墓于乡里诣县令里所陈桑梓之敬有识者赏焉侄迁嗣为潞帅降太原葆光子曰罗虬累举不第务于躁进因罢举依于宦官典台州昼锦也常以展墓勉谒邑宰横笏傲然宰曰某虽尘吏不逹事体然使君岂不看松柏下人乎讥其无桑梓之敬曾武人之不若也虬有俊才尝见雕隂官妓比红儿诗他无闻也

    Explanation

    179

    Shi Fangli's Respect for His Hometown [with Luo Qiu's Appendix]

    Shi Fangli, the Military Governor of the Zhaoyi Circuit, was from Pingxiang, Xing Prefecture. When he was young, he enlisted in the army due to his bravery and strength, serving as a subordinate general. During the Guangming era, the Military Governor of Lushui, Gao Xun, attacked Zhu Shuang at Heyang, and Shi Fangli led the vanguard forces through the Tianjing Pass. At that time, Gao Xun was driven away by the general Liu Guang, who harbored suspicions against Shi Fangli and left him to garrison the pass. Later, Liu Guang was killed by the people of Lushui, and the army then appointed Shi Fangli as their leader. Because of his longing to return to his roots, he moved his troops to Xing Prefecture. He administered the region with fairness and justice, and the people all followed him. He first paid homage to his ancestors' graves in his hometown and visited the county magistrate to express his respect for his hometown. Those with insight praised his actions. His nephew, Shi Qian, succeeded him as the Military Governor of Lushui and submitted to Taiyuan. The Preserver of Light from Taiyuan, Luo Qiu, had repeatedly failed the imperial examinations and sought rapid advancement, so he abandoned his studies and relied on officials in Taizhou. He often encouraged others to visit their ancestral graves, but when he met the county magistrate, he held his tablet arrogantly. The magistrate said, "Although I am a lowly official, I do not understand the importance of this matter. But does Your Excellency not see the people beneath the pine and cypress trees?" He was criticizing Luo Qiu for lacking respect for his hometown, even less than a warrior. Luo Qiu had exceptional talent and was once seen composing poetry about an official courtesan named Hong'er in Diaoyin, but he is otherwise unknown.

    180

    雷电救王镕
    　　景福中幽州帅李匡威率兵救镇州军次博水会军乱推其弟匡俦充留后诸军皆散乃以书报弟付之军政南欲赴阙泊于陆泽镇州赵王王镕以匡威救难失国因请税驾于常山府郭以中离变会匡威有幕客李贞抱自阙囘与匡威相遇同登寺楼观镇州山川之美有爱恋之意乃谋托亲忌王镕既造之逼以兵仗同诣理所乃入自子城东门门内有
    镕亲骑营中之卒忽掩其外关复于阙垣中有一人识是王镕遽挟于马上肩之而去匡威格鬭移时与贞抱俱死镕年十六七疎瘦当与匡威并辔之时雷电忽起雨雹交下而屋瓦皆飞拔大木数株明日镕但觉项偏痛乃因有力者所挟不胜其苦故也访之则曰墨君和鼓刀之士也天意防数信然镕自脱此难更在位三十余年不有神明扶持何以获免

    Explanation

    180

    During the Jingfu era, the military governor of Youzhou, Li Kuangwei, led his troops to Bo Water to rescue the state of Zhenzhou. However, the army became chaotic, and they promoted his younger brother, Kuang Chou, to be the acting military governor. All the troops then dispersed, and Li Kuangwei sent a letter to his brother, entrusting him with the military affairs. Li Kuangwei intended to go south to the imperial court and stopped at Luzhe. The Prince of Zhao, Wáng Róng, seeing that Li Kuangwei had come to rescue him but had lost his country, invited him to stay temporarily in Changshan Prefecture. Amidst the turmoil, Li Kuangwei had a retainer, Li Zhenbao, who had returned from the imperial court. Li Zhenbao met Li Kuangwei and they climbed a temple tower together to admire the beauty of Zhenzhou's mountains and rivers. They developed feelings of affection and decided to seek refuge with Wáng Róng. They forced Wáng Róng to come with them, armed with weapons, and entered through the eastern gate of the inner city. Inside the gate, there were Wáng Róng's personal guards, who suddenly blocked the outer gate. In the courtyard, someone recognized Wáng Róng and quickly lifted him onto a horse, carrying him away. Li Kuangwei fought back for a while, and both he and Li Zhenbao died. Wáng Róng was only sixteen or seventeen years old and was thin. When he was riding alongside Li Kuangwei, a sudden thunderstorm broke out, with hail and rain falling heavily, causing tiles to fly and several large trees to be uprooted. The next day, Wáng Róng felt pain in his neck, which he attributed to being carried by a strong person. He later learned that it was Mò Jūnhé, a butcher, who had helped him. He believed that this was a sign of divine protection, and indeed, he managed to escape this danger and remained in power for over thirty years. Without the assistance of divine beings, how could he have avoided such a fate?

    181

    李全忠芦生三节
    　　唐干符末范阳人李全忠少通春秋好谷子之学曾为棣州司马忽有芦一枝生于所居之室盈尺三节焉心以为异以告别驾张建章建章积书千卷博古之士也乃曰昔者蒲洪以池中蒲生九节为瑞乃姓蒲后子孙昌盛芦者茅也合生陂泽之间而生于室非其常也君后必有分茅之贵三节者传节三人公可志之全忠后事李可举为戎校诸将逐可举而立全忠累加至检校太尉临戎甚有威政全忠死子匡威嗣匡威为三军所逐弟匡俦为太原所攻挈家赴阙至沧州景城为卢彦威所害先是匡威少年好勇不拘小节自布素中以饮博为事渔阳士子多忌之曾一日与诸游侠辈钓于桑干赤栏桥之侧自以酒祷

    Explanation

    181

    In the late years of the Ganfu era of the Tang Dynasty, a reed with three joints sprouted in the residence of Fan Yang's Li Quanzhong, who was then serving as the司马 of Di Prefecture. He considered this unusual and sought an explanation from Zhang Jianzhang, a scholar well-versed in ancient knowledge. Zhang Jianzhang said, "In the past, Pu Hong saw a reed with nine joints grow in a pond, which was considered an auspicious sign, and he founded the Later Zhao dynasty. A reed is a type of grass that grows in wetlands, but it has now grown indoors, which is not its usual place. You will surely achieve a noble status, and the three joints suggest that the leadership will be passed on to three people." Li Quanzhong later served Li Keju and was gradually promoted to the position of Inspector General. In military affairs, he had very strict policies. After Li Quanzhong's death, his son Li Kuangwei succeeded him, but was later expelled by the generals, who then installed Li Kuangchou. Li Kuangchou was later attacked by Lu Yanwei in Jingcheng, and he fled to the capital with his family, reaching Cangzhou. In Jingfu Year 2, he died in Jingcheng.

    Li Quanzhong was from a humble background and often engaged in drinking and gambling. The scholars of Yuyang often envied him. Once, he went fishing with some ruffians at the Red Pillar Bridge on the Sanggan River and prayed with wine.

    182

    曰吾若有幽州节制分则获一大鱼果钓得鱼长三尺人甚异焉有马都【一作郁下同】者少文艺匡威曾问其年都【一作郁】曰弱冠后两周星傲形于色后匡威继父为侯首召焉【一作马】都问曰子今弱冠后几周星歳都但顿颡谢罪匡威曰好子之事吾平生所爱也何惧之有因署以府职其濶逹多如此故人多附之葆光子尝见范阳熟人说李匡俦妻张氏国色也其兄匡威为帅强婬之匡俦按剑而俟夜深妻廻出步辇为其夫杀之匡威羞见其弟及将校或言欲将兵救援镇州既出城三军立匡俦为帅匡威遂称欲归朝觐行次常山又有刼质王镕之事匡俦移牒王镕往复指陈终不及婬秽之事讳国恶也

    Explanation

    182

    If I were to have control over the region of Youzhou, I would catch a great fish. Indeed, I caught a fish that was three feet long, which was quite remarkable. There was a man named Ma Du (also written as Yu), who lacked literary talent. Kangwei once asked him about his age, and Ma Du replied that he had just turned twenty and had been so for two weeks, showing arrogance on his face. Later, Kangwei succeeded his father as a marquis and first summoned Ma Du. Ma Du asked, "How many weeks have passed since your weak crown?" Ma Du then knelt and apologized. Kangwei said, "Your good deeds are all my life's loves. What have you to fear?" He appointed Ma Du to a position in the government, and because of his broad and open-minded nature, many people followed him. Baoguangzi once met a familiar person from Fanyang who told him that Li Kuangchou's wife, Zhang, was a national beauty. Her brother, Kangwei, who was a general, forcibly raped her. Li Kuangchou drew his sword and waited. At night, his wife returned and walked out, and he killed her for his husband. Kangwei was ashamed to see his brother and the generals, and some said he wanted to lead troops to rescue Zhenzhou. Once out of the city, the three armies appointed Li Kuangchou as their commander, and Kangwei claimed he wanted to return to court and passed through Changshan. There was also an incident where Wang Rong was seized as a hostage. Li Kuangchou sent a letter to Wang Rong, repeatedly pointing out the situation, but never mentioned the matter of the rape, hiding the national evil.

    张建章泛海遇仙
    　　张建章为幽州行军司马后歴郡守尤好经史聚书至万卷所居有书楼但以披阅清净为事经渉之地无不理焉曾赍府戎命往渤海遇风涛乃泊其船忽有青衣泛一叶舟而至谓建章曰奉大仙命请大夫建章乃应之至一大防见楼台岿然中有女仙处之侍翼甚盛器食皆建章故乡之常味也食毕告退女仙谓建章曰子不欺暗室所谓君子人也忽患风涛之苦吾令此青衣往来导之及还风涛寂然往来皆无所惧又囘至西岸经太宗征辽碑

    Explanation

    183

    Zhang Jianzhang's Encounter with a Fairy While Crossing the Sea

    Zhang Jianzhang served as a military governor in Youzhou and later as a county governor, particularly fond of the classics and history, collecting up to ten thousand volumes of books. His residence had a library where he spent his time reading and studying in a calm and pure manner, managing all the places he visited.

    Once, he was sent on a mission by the military governor to the Bohai Sea. Upon encountering strong winds and waves, he had to anchor his ship. Suddenly, a servant in blue arrived in a small leaf boat and told Zhang Jianzhang that he was following the command of a great fairy and invited him to come. Zhang Jianzhang agreed, and they reached a grand structure where he saw majestic towers. Inside, a female fairy resided with many attendants. The food and utensils were all familiar flavors from Zhang Jianzhang's hometown.

    After finishing the meal, Zhang Jianzhang took his leave. The female fairy told him, "You do not deceive in the dark; you are a true gentleman." Suddenly, he suffered from the troubles of wind and waves. The fairy sent the servant to guide him, and upon returning, the wind and waves calmed down. They traveled back and forth without fear. They returned to the western shore and passed by a monument commemorating Emperor Taizong's campaign against the Liao.

    半在水中建章则以帛包麦屑置于水中摸而读之不欠一字其笃学也如此蓟门之人皆能说之于时亦闻于朝廷葆光子曾遇蓟门军校姓孙忘其名细话张大夫遇水仙遗鲛绡自赍而进好事者为之立传今亳州太清宫道士有得其本者且曰明宗皇帝有事郊丘建章乡人掌东序之寳其言国玺外唯有二物其一即建章所进鲛绡箧而贮之轴之如帛【一作着】以红线三道劄之亦云夏天清暑展开可以满室凛然迩来变更莫知何在

    　　北梦琐言卷十三
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十四

    Explanation

    184

    A Man Named Jianzhang Who Could Read Through Water

    During the reign of Emperor Mingzong, a man named Jianzhang lived in Jilin. He had the extraordinary ability to read through water by placing a bundle of wheat bran wrapped in silk into the water and touching it to read. His dedication to learning was such that he never missed a single character. Everyone in Jilin could tell about him, and at that time, his story was also known to the court.

    Baoguangzi once met a military officer from Jilin named Sun (his name is forgotten) who recounted a detailed conversation about Zhang Dafu encountering a water fairy who left a piece of silk (鲛绡). Zhang Dafu brought the silk himself and presented it to the court. Those who were interested wrote a biography for him.

    Today, a Taoist priest at the Taqing Palace in Bozhou has obtained the original text. He says that Emperor Mingzong had something to do with the altar in Jianzhang's hometown, and the people there held the eastern treasure. He said that outside the state seal, there were only two other items, one of which was the silk presented by Jianzhang, stored in a box and rolled like silk. It was tied with three red threads. It is also said that in summer, when unfolded, it can fill the room with a cool sensation. Recently, changes have occurred, and no one knows where it is now.

    This translation aims to be faithful to the original text while maintaining clarity and readability in English. It addresses the idiomatic expressions, cultural allusions, syntactic ambiguities, and proper nouns as planned in the pre-drafting research.

    唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　李茂贞胁尹杀宰相
    　　凤翔李茂贞跋扈至甚昭宗谓宰相杜让能曰春秋之义叛而必诛安有甸服之间显违朝防而悖慢如此我若不讨四方其谓我何让能奏曰艰难已来行贞元故事姑息戎臣久矣根牢蔓炽附之者众一旦难骤革之又京师去岐咫尺人心易以危惧设有陵犯损威愈甚愿陛下稍解雷霆而熟计之帝曰政刑弛紊诏令不出都门不欲孱孱守恬而坐因除宰臣徐彦若镇凤翔以茂贞为兴元尹以嗣覃王率禁军送彦或茂贞延不受代即以兵攻之军旅所
    决一委让能让能恳谏不从王师果败或云此举乃让能报私怨也茂贞先以长书与譲能继上表仍拥兵至临皋驿请诛宰相帝遂斩枢密使李周曈以徇乃贬譲能仍诏送至军前茂贞具礼出迎至驿复表请行朝典让能奏曰晁错之辜谬及于臣今若归罪于臣可纾国难帝不得已贬让能雷州司户参军遣中使害于驿内识者以让能临难无茍免亦得其死也后追赠太尉其子晓貌如削玉有制诰之才仕梁至宰相凤厯年洛都有变为乱军误害时皆叹惜之

    Explanation

    185

    The Tang Dynasty, compiled by Sun Guangxian
    　　Li Muzheng Coerced the Prince to Kill the Chancellor
    　　In Fengxiang, Li Muzheng was extremely arrogant and domineering. Emperor Zhaozong said to the chancellor Du Rangneng, "According to the principles of the Spring and Autumn Annals, rebellion must be punished. How can there be such open defiance of the court's laws and disrespect within the inner regions? If I do not punish him, how will the four directions regard me?" Du Rangneng responded, "Since the difficulties began, we have been following the example of the Zhengyuan era, indulging military officials for a long time. Their roots are deep and their influence is widespread, with many people supporting them. It is difficult to suddenly change this situation. Moreover, the capital is only a short distance from Qishui, and people's hearts are easily filled with fear and apprehension. If there is any disrespect or loss of dignity, the damage will be even greater. I hope Your Majesty will temper your anger and carefully consider the matter." The emperor replied, "Political affairs and laws are in disarray, and imperial edicts are not being enforced beyond the capital gates. I do not want to be weak and peaceful while sitting idly by and removing the chancellor Xu Yanruo and appointing Li Muzheng as the governor of Xingyuan Prefecture, with the heir Prince Qitan leading the imperial guards to escort Xu Yanruo. If Li Muzheng refuses to step down, he will attack with his troops. The decision lies entirely with Du Rangneng. Du Rangneng repeatedly advised against it, but the emperor did not listen. The imperial army ultimately suffered a defeat. Some say this action was Du Rangneng's way of avenging a personal grudge. Li Muzheng had previously written a long letter to Du Rangneng and then submitted a memorial, still with his troops at the Lingo Station, requesting the execution of the chancellor. The emperor then ordered the execution of the chief of the Military Council, Li Zhou Tong, as a warning. Du Rangneng was demoted and ordered to be sent to the front lines. Li Muzheng prepared a ceremony and went out to meet him at the station, then submitted another memorial requesting the enforcement of court law. Du Rangneng responded, "The guilt of Chao Cuo has mistakenly fallen upon me. If I am blamed, it can alleviate the country's difficulties." The emperor had no choice but to demote Du Rangneng to the position of a county magistrate in Leizhou, and sent an imperial envoy to kill him at the station. Those who understood the situation felt that Du Rangneng faced danger without seeking to escape, and thus died honorably. Later, he was posthumously bestowed the title of Grand Commandant. His son, Du Xiao, had a face like carved jade and talent in drafting imperial edicts. He served in the state of Liang and became a chancellor. In the years of Fengli, there were rebellious troops in Luoyang who mistakenly harmed him, and at that time, everyone lamented and regretted it.

    三镇拥兵杀二相
    　　唐干宁二年邠州王行瑜防李茂贞韩建入觐决谋废立帝既睹三帅齐至必有异谋乃御楼见之谓曰卿等不召而来欲有何意茂贞等汗流浃背不能对但云南北司紊乱朝政因疏韦昭度讨西川失谋李磎麻下为刘崇所哭陛下不合违众用之及令宦官诏害昭度已下三帅乃还镇内外寃之王行瑜跋扈朝廷欲加尚书令昭度力止之曰太宗以此官防政而登大位后郭子仪以六朝立功虽有其名终身退让今行瑜安可轻授焉因请加尚
    父至是为行瑜所憾遽罹此害后追赠太师李磎字景望拜相麻出为刘崇抱而哭泣改授太子少傅乃上十表及纳谏五篇以求自雪后竟登庸且讦崇之恶时同列崔昭纬与韦昭度及磎素不相协王行瑜专制朝廷以判官崔鋋入阙奏事与昭纬关通因托鋋致意由是行瑜率三镇胁君磎亦遇害其子渷有髙才同日罹害磎著书百卷号李书楼后追赠司徒太原李克用破王行瑜后崔昭纬贬而赐死昭皇切齿下诏捕崔鋋亦寃报之一事也

    Explanation

    186

    In the second year of the Ganning era of the Tang dynasty, Wang Xingyu of Binzhou gathered his army to guard against Li Maogeng and Han Jian, who were summoned to the court to plot the deposition and replacement of the emperor. Upon seeing the three generals arrive together, the emperor suspected an unusual plot and met them on the imperial platform, asking, "Why did you come without being summoned? What is your intention?" Li Maogeng and others were so nervous that they were sweating profusely and could not answer. They merely said that the Northern and Southern Offices had disrupted court politics. The emperor then removed Wei Zhao-du for his failed campaign in Western Sichuan and issued an edict to harm him and others. After the three generals returned to their posts, both inside and outside the court felt wronged. Wang Xingyu was arrogant and domineering in the court and intended to appoint himself as the Grand Commandant. Wei Zhao-du strongly opposed this, saying, "Emperor Taizong used this position to prevent politics and ascend to the throne. Later, Guo Ziyi, who established merit during the Six Dynasties, held this title but never accepted it, always yielding to others. How can it be lightly bestowed upon Wang Xingyu? He should be given the title of Elder Statesman instead." However, at this point, Wang Xingyu resented Li Qi and suddenly suffered this harm. Posthumously, he was bestowed the title of Grand Tutor. Li Qi, courtesy name Jingwang, was appointed as chancellor, and the imperial edict was issued. Liu Chonggui embraced and wept over it, and Li Qi was reassigned to the position of Tutor to the Crown Prince. He submitted ten memorials and five essays on accepting advice to seek exoneration. Eventually, he was promoted and exposed Liu Chonggui's wickedness. At the time, Cui Zhao-wei, who was on good terms with Wei Zhao-du and Li Qi, was demoted and executed by the emperor, who was furious. An edict was issued to arrest Cui Jian, and this was a case of retribution.

    儒将成败
    　　古者文武一体出将入相近代裴行俭郭元振裴度韦臯是也然而时有夷险不可一概而论王铎初镇荆南黄巢入冦望风而遁他日将兵捍潼关黄巢令人传语云相公儒生且非我敌无汚我锋刃自取败亡也后到成都行朝拜诸道都统髙骈上表目之为败军之将正谓是也谏议大夫郑寳【一作宾】曾献书以规其防云未知令公以何人为牙爪何士参帷幄当今大盗移国羣雄奋戈幕下非旧族子弟白面郎君雍容谈笑之秋也尔后罢军权镇滑台竟有贝州之祸郑文公畋首倡中兴传檄讨贼杀戮黄寇镇静关畿一旦部校李昌言胁而逐之尚

    Explanation

    187

    The Success and Failure of Literati Generals
    In ancient times, scholars and warriors were one, capable of becoming generals or ministers. This was the case with figures like Pei Xingjian, Guo Yuanzhen, Pei Du, and Wei Gao. However, times have their ups and downs, and cannot be generalized. Wang Duo, for instance, initially served as the governor of Jingnan but fled when the Huang Chao rebels approached. Later, he led troops to defend Tongguan, but Huang Chao sent a message saying, "Sir, you are a scholar, and not my equal. Do not soil my blades; you will bring about your own downfall." After this defeat, Wang Duo went to Chengdu, where he was appointed as the commander of various armies by Gao Pian, who publicly denounced him as a defeated general. This was indeed the case. Counselor Zheng Bao once wrote to advise Wang Duo, saying, "I do not know what kind of people you have as your generals or advisors. In today's chaotic times, when rebels have taken control and heroes are fighting, it is not the time for idle scholars to engage in leisurely conversation." Later, Wang Duo was stripped of his military power and stationed in Huaitai, where he eventually faced the disaster of Beizhou. Zhang Wen, on the other hand, was the first to advocate for the restoration of order and issued edicts to suppress the rebels, killing Huang Chao and stabilizing the region. However, his efforts were undermined when his subordinates, led by Li Changyan, forced him out.

    188

    不能固位至如越州崔璆湖南崔瑾福建韦岫郓州蔡崇徐方支详许昌薛能河中李都窦潏凤翔徐彦若狼狈恐惧求免不暇唯张濬大言自方管葛以无谋之韩建倅用刚之孙揆出征大卤自贻败亡尔后朱朴踵为大言骤居相位亦曾上表请破凤翔所谓以羊将狼投卵击石幸而不用何过望哉客有谓葆光子曰儒将诚则有之唐自大中已来以兵为戏者久矣廊庙之上耻言韬略以櫜鞬为凶物以钤匮为凶言就有如卢藩薛能者目为麄才一旦宇内尘惊闾左颷起遽以襃衣博令押燕颔虎头适足以取笑耳则韦昭度之惮王建张濬之伐太原是也
    　　外藩从事于东【一作本】省上事

    Explanation

    188

    In their positions, many officials were unable to hold firm, as seen in the cases of Cui Qiu from Yuezhou, Cui Jin from Hunan, Wei Xiu from Fujian, Cai Chong from Yuzhou, Zhi Xiang from Xu Prefecture, Xue Neng from Xuchang, Li Du from Hedong, Dou Yu from Dou Prefecture, and Xu Yanruo from Fengxiang, who were all in a state of panic and desperation, too busy trying to escape to think clearly. Only Zhang Jun made grandiose claims about himself, comparing himself to Zhuge Liang and Guan Yu, but his lack of strategy led to the failure of Han Jian's campaign and the disastrous expedition led by Sun Kui against the Great Hal. Later, Zhu Pu followed in this pattern, making grandiose claims and quickly rising to a high position, even submitting a memorial requesting the defeat of Fengxiang, which was seen as sending weak forces against strong enemies, akin to throwing an egg at a stone. Fortunately, it was not used, but what more could one expect? A guest said to Bao Guangzi, "Indeed, there are scholars who can lead armies, but since the reign of Emperor Xiaozong, military affairs have been treated as a game for too long. In the imperial court, it is shameful to speak of military strategy, and even the tools of war are seen as ominous. Those like Lu Fan and Xue Neng are considered crude talents. Once the dust rises in the land, and the wind stirs in the east, it is ridiculous to send scholars and officials to lead military campaigns, as they are only fit for ridicule. Such was the case with Wei Zhaodu's hesitation against Wang Jian and Zhang Jun's campaign against Taiyuan."

    189

    河东节度副使李习吉【习五代史作袭】常应举不第为李都河中从事都失守习吉自昭义游太原辟为从事习吉好学有笔述虽马上军前手不释卷太原所发牋奏军书皆习吉所为也因从李克用至渭南令其入奏帝重其文章授谏议大夫使上事北省以荣之竟归太原复其戎职庄宗即位追赠礼部尚书梁太祖每覧太原书檄遥景重之曰我何不得此人也陈琳阮瑀亦不是过
    　　韩建始终
    　　韩建两随李茂贞迫胁君上杀戮辅相昭宗出居本幸鄜畤建恳迎奉请至华下供亿之劳具在勤王录而杀害郯王等八人以孤君上抑其罪也近代史臣駮论勤王录数条且曰韩建不遇时可也而云隄防道路拱卫乗舆欲盖而彰则禁固之意可知也又与诸道书云语诏书征赴行在妄也又曽无纠率诸侯述保大定功【一作公】之志也以为唐运陵替皆有【一作由】厯数自黄巢既戮蔡贼生焉宗权灭后而朱玫王行瑜继之才舍茂贞而有韩建所谓一莽虽死十莽复生何天意不祐乎竟为朱温宰相蜀先主闻之笑曰韩建非豹变

    Explanation

    189

    Final Translation

    Deputy Military Governor of Hedong, Li Xi, often failed to pass the imperial examinations and became an assistant to Li Du in Hezhong. When Li Du lost control, Li Xi traveled from Zhao to Taiyuan and was appointed as an assistant. Li Xi was a diligent scholar and skilled writer, never putting down his books even while on horseback or in the midst of military campaigns. All official documents and military reports from Taiyuan were written by Li Xi. He accompanied Li Keyong to Weinan and was ordered to present a report. The emperor valued his literary skills and appointed him as a censor, ordering him to serve in the northern office to honor him. Eventually, Li Xi returned to Taiyuan and resumed his military duties. After Emperor Zhuangzong ascended the throne, he posthumously granted Li Xi the title of Minister of Rites. Emperor Zhuangzong of Later Liang admired the quality of documents from Taiyuan and said, "Why can't I have such a person?" Even Chen Lin and Ruan Yu, famous literary figures, are not superior to this.

    Han Jian consistently followed Li Maozhen in forcing the emperor and killing ministers. Emperor Zhaozong was forced to move to Fuzhi, and Han Jian earnestly invited the emperor to return to Huaxia, showing his loyalty and service. His contributions to the imperial court, recorded in the Qinwang Lu, included the labor of providing supplies and support. However, he also killed Prince Tancheng and seven others, isolating the emperor and suppressing his crimes. Modern historians criticized the Qinwang Lu for several points, noting that Han Jian did not encounter a favorable time but claimed to protect the roads and guard the imperial carriage, trying to cover up but making his actions more obvious. He also claimed to follow imperial edicts in letters to various regions, which were false. Moreover, he never led the feudal lords to preserve and stabilize the state. Believing that the decline of the Tang dynasty was due to fate, with various rebellions and usurpers, and that Han Jian was just another in a series of such figures, the ruler of Shu heard this and laughed, saying that Han Jian did not transform like a leopard.

    190

    之才与朱温作相宜也葆光子曰华州韩建荆渚成汭勤王奉国识有可嘉于时号为北韩南郭【郭即成令冒称也】士大夫可以依頼也古者奉霸主尊本朝德义小诸侯不至葵丘之防是也成韩位居王辅荷宠于唐朱公有无君之心露问鼎之意建等不能效臧洪泣血纠率同盟亦可以结约亲邻共张声势而乃助桀作孽画足成蛇舍我善邻陈诚伪室华隂失守既无力以枝梧鄂渚防师乃无名而陷没非忠非义吾所谓二公始终谬也向使成令睦汉南诸侯结淮甸雄援汴人簒逆亦恐未暇推之天命即吾不知考之人谋固无所取惜哉
    　　孔纬惜盐铁印
    　　孔纬在中书朱全忠并有数镇兵力强盛表请盐鐡印诏下宰相议之纬力争不从请其下邸吏曰朱公収盐鐡印非兴兵不可全忠寻止后韩建讨太原不利为张濬所误贬之他日昭宗欲再攻鳯翔以问纬纬曰鳯翔天子西门若自去窟穴受制一面即大事去矣昭宗曰卿是朕贤臣殊未逹时事纬曰陛下以臣为贤是谤臣也臣若贤肯立于陛下之朝因称疾以太子太师致仕卒于华下

    Explanation

    190

    Zhi's talent is suitable for working with Zhu Wen. The scholar Bao Guang said: Han Jian of Huazhou and Cheng Rui of Jingzhou worked diligently to serve the country and were worthy of praise. At the time, they were known as North Han and South Guo (Guo being Cheng Rui's nickname). Scholars and officials could rely on them. In ancient times, feudal lords who lacked virtue and were small would not attend the Kuizhou conference; this is the standard they followed. Cheng and Han held positions as advisors to the emperor and were favored by the Tang dynasty. Zhu Wen had no loyalty to the emperor and openly showed his intention to usurp power. Han Jian and others could not emulate Zang Hong's loyalty and failed to rally their allies. They could have formed alliances with neighboring states to bolster their strength, but instead, they aided the tyrant and committed evil deeds, turning into a snake that bit itself. They abandoned their virtuous neighbors and created a false sense of security. When Huayin fell, they were powerless to resist the invasion from Ezhu. They were defeated without justification and perished, which was neither loyal nor righteous. This is what I mean by the two men's actions being fundamentally flawed. If Cheng Rui had allied with the feudal lords of the southern regions and secured powerful support, the usurpation by the people of Bian might not have occurred. Even if one cannot determine the will of heaven, one should consider human strategy; there is no point in pursuing such a course. Alas!

    Kong Wei's Concern Over the Salt and Iron Seals

    Kong Wei, while serving as a high-ranking official, Zhu Wen had control over several military regions and was powerful. He requested the salt and iron seals, and the emperor issued an edict for the chancellors to discuss it. Kong Wei strongly opposed it, and when the officials below him urged him to comply, he said, "If Zhu Wen takes the salt and iron seals, he will surely rise in rebellion." Zhu Wen eventually withdrew his request. Later, Han Jian led a campaign against Taiyuan and suffered a defeat, which was attributed to Zhang Jun's miscalculation. He was subsequently demoted. One day, Emperor Zhaozong wanted to launch another attack on Fengxiang and consulted Kong Wei. Kong Wei said, "Fengxiang is the western gate of the imperial palace. If we leave our stronghold and allow ourselves to be controlled by one side, it will be the end of the great cause." The emperor said, "You are my virtuous minister, but you do not understand the current situation." Kong Wei replied, "If the emperor considers me virtuous, it is a slander. If I were truly virtuous, would I remain in your court?" He then claimed illness and retired as a Grand Tutor, dying in Huayang.

    191

    神告罗信【子绍威附】
    　　中和中魏博帅罗信初为本军歩射小校掌牧圉之事曾宿于魏州观音院门外其地有神祠俗号曰白须翁巫有宋迁【一作千】者忽诣信谓曰夜来神忽有语君不久为此地主信怒曰欲危我耶他日复以此言来告信信因令密之不期歳果有军变推信为帅信状貌丰伟多力善射虽声名未振众已服之累加至太尉封临淮王信卒子绍威继之与梁祖通欢结亲情分甚至先是本府有牙军八千人丰其衣粮动要姑息时人云长安天子魏府牙
    军主使频遭斥逐由此益骄绍威不平有意翦灭因与汴人计防诈令役夫肩笼内藏器甲扬言汴帅葬罗氏之女绍威密令人于兵仗库断共甲襻夜防汴人擐甲持戈攻杀牙军牙军觉之排闼入库而弓甲无所施勇也全营杀尽仍破其家人谓牙军久盛宜其死矣绍威虽豁素心而纪纲无有渐为梁祖陵制竭其帑藏以奉之忽患脚疮痛不可忍意其牙军为祟乃谓亲吏曰聚六州四十三县铁打一个错不成也绍威卒其子周翰继之俄而移镇滑台罗氏大去其国矣

    Explanation

    191

    Divine Warning to Luo Hongxin [with Son Shao Wei Attached]

    During the Zhonghe period, Luo Hongxin, the military governor of Weibo, initially served as a low-ranking officer responsible for managing livestock. He once stayed overnight outside the Guanyin Temple in Weizhou, where there was a shrine to a deity known colloquially as "White Beard Old Man." A shaman named Song Qian (or Qian) suddenly visited Luo Hongxin and said, "Last night, the deity spoke and said that you will soon become the ruler of this region." Luo Hongxin angrily replied, "Are you trying to harm me?" The next day, Song Qian repeated the same message. Luo Hongxin then ordered the matter to be kept secret. Unexpectedly, within a year, there was a military uprising, and Luo Hongxin was chosen as the new military governor. Despite his initial lack of fame, Luo Hongxin's imposing appearance, strength, and skill with a bow won the respect of his troops. He was later promoted to Grand Commandant and granted the title of Duke of Linhuai. After Luo Hongxin's death, his son Shao Wei succeeded him and formed close ties with Zhu Wen, the powerful warlord who would later establish the Later Liang dynasty. Before this, the Weibo region had a specialized elite military unit of eight thousand men, who were given generous clothing and rations, and were often indulged by the military governor. People at the time said, "The emperor in Chang'an is less powerful than the Weibo elite soldiers."

    The military governor had been repeatedly deposed and replaced, leading to increasing arrogance among the elite soldiers. Shao Wei grew dissatisfied and decided to eliminate them. He devised a plan with the people of Bian (modern-day Kaifeng) to deceive the elite soldiers. They pretended to be transporting weapons and armor, claiming that the warlord was burying a member of the Luo family. Shao Wei secretly had his men cut the ropes and straps of the weapons and armor in the armory. That night, the people of Bian donned armor and wielded weapons, attacking and killing the elite soldiers. The elite soldiers became aware of the attack and rushed into the armory, but their weapons and armor were useless. The attack was so effective that the entire camp was wiped out, and their families were also destroyed. Shao Wei justified this action by saying that the elite soldiers had long been powerful and deserved their fate. Although Shao Wei had a pure heart, the region fell into chaos and gradually came under the control of Zhu Wen, who drained the treasury to support him. Suddenly, Shao Wei developed a painful foot ailment, which he believed was caused by the spirits of the elite soldiers. He told his close attendants, "Even if all the iron in six states and forty-three counties were used, it would not be enough to make a mistake." Shao Wei died, and his son Zhou Han succeeded him. Soon after, Zhou Han was transferred to Huatai, and the Luo family lost their power.

    192

    燕王刘仁恭异梦
    　　刘仁恭微时曾梦佛旛于手指飞出或占之曰君年四十九必有旌幢之贵后如其说果为幽帅自破太原军于安塞城后士兵精强孩视邻道发管内丁壮号三十万南取邺中图曹之霸先下甘陵无少长悉坑之初治甘陵城下有鸺鹠数头飞下幄帐内逐之复来仁恭恶之竟为魏军汴军夹攻大败之杀其名将单可及仁恭单马而遁于时军败于内黄尔后汴帅攻燕亦败于唐河他日命使聘汴汴帅开宴俳优戏医病人以讥之且问病状内黄以何药可瘥其聘使谓汴帅曰内黄可以唐河水浸之必愈宾主大笑赏使乎之美也

    Explanation

    192

    Duke Liu Rengong of Yan's Strange Dream
    　　When Liu Rengong was still humble, he once dreamed that a Buddhist banner flew out from his fingers. Someone interpreted it, saying, "You will attain noble rank with banners and flags when you are forty-nine." Later, as predicted, he became the commander of You Prefecture. After defeating the Taiyuan army at Anse City, his soldiers were strong and invincible, and he looked down on neighboring regions. He conscripted all able-bodied men within his jurisdiction, numbering thirty thousand, and marched south to capture Ye City, aiming to emulate Cao Cao's ambitions. Upon conquering Ganling, he massacred all, young and old. Initially, while garrisoning Ganling City, several owls flew into his tent, and despite chasing them away, they kept returning. Liu Rengong was displeased, and ultimately, he was attacked by the combined forces of the Wei and Bian armies, suffering a great defeat. They killed his famous general Dan Kajie, and Liu Rengong fled alone on horseback. At that time, his army was defeated at Neihuang. Later, when the Bian commander attacked Yan, they also suffered a defeat at Tang River. One day, he sent envoys to Bian, and the Bian commander held a banquet with jesters and actors playing the role of doctors, mocking Liu Rengong. He asked about the nature of the illness in Neihuang and what medicine could cure it. The envoy replied, "Neihuang can be cured by soaking it in the Tang River water." The host and guests laughed, and they praised the envoy for his cleverness.

    193

    北梦琐言卷十四
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十五
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　披褐至殿门
    　　天复元年凤翔李茂贞请入觐奏事朝廷允之盖军容使韩全诲与之交结昭宗御安福楼茂贞涕泣陈匡救之言时崔允密奏曰此奸人也未足为信陛下宜寛懐待之翌日宴于夀春殿茂贞肩舆衣駞褐入金鸾门易服赴宴咸以为前代跋扈未有此也时韩全诲深相交结崔允惧之自此亦结朱全忠竟致汴州迎驾与凤翔连兵刼迁入洛之始识者以王子召戎崔允比之先是茂贞入阙焚烧京城是宴也俳优安辔新号茂贞为火龙子茂贞惭惕俛首宴罢有言他日须斩此优辔新闻之请假徃凤翔求救茂贞遥见诟之曰此优穷也胡为敢来辔新对曰只要起居不为求救近日京中且卖麸炭可以取济茂贞大笑而厚赐赦之也

    Explanation

    193

    In the fifteenth volume of Beimeng Suoyan, compiled by Sun Guangxian of the Tang dynasty:

    Wearing a Simple Coat to the Palace Gate

    In the first year of the Tianfu era, Li Maozhen of Fengxiang requested to enter the imperial court to report matters, and the court agreed. This was because the military commander Han Quanwei was closely allied with him. Emperor Zhaozong held a ceremony on the Anfulou, where Li Maozhen wept and spoke of his support and rescue. At the time, Cui Yun secretly advised the emperor, saying, "He is a treacherous person and should not be trusted. Your Majesty should treat him with leniency." The next day, during a banquet at the Shouchun Hall, Li Maozhen arrived in a sedan chair, wearing a simple camel hair coat, and entered through the Golden Phoenix Gate. He changed his attire for the banquet, and all present thought that such brazen behavior had never been seen before. At the time, Han Quanwei was deeply allied with Li Maozhen, and Cui Yun was afraid of him. As a result, Li Maozhen also formed an alliance with Zhu Quanzhong, leading to the emperor being invited to visit Bianzhou, and continuous warfare between Fengxiang and Bianzhou, ultimately forcing the emperor to move to Luoyang. Scholars recognized this as a situation similar to the time when Prince Wu summoned troops, comparing Cui Yun to the historical figure. Before Li Maozhen entered the capital, he burned the city. During the banquet, a court jester named An Peixin called Li Maozhen "Fire Dragon Son." Li Maozhen was ashamed and lowered his head. After the banquet, someone said that this jester should be executed. An Peixin heard this and requested to go to Fengxiang to seek help. Li Maozhen saw him from afar and scolded him, saying, "This jester is poor. Why did you dare to come?" An Peixin replied, "I just want to take care of my daily routine; I am not asking for help. Recently, in the capital, I can sell bran and charcoal to make a living." Li Maozhen laughed and generously rewarded and pardoned him.

    194

    朱全忠迎驾于凤翔
    　　军容使韩全诲以驾幸凤翔李茂贞比懐挟帝以令诸侯之意惧朱全忠之盛也西川王公建亦有此虑乃结汴州同起军助其迎驾汴军传【一作傅】城州【一作川】军乃攻兴元其帅王万洪以无救援遂降成都由是山南十四州并为蜀有方变谋却助凤翔于时命掌书记韦庄奉使至军前朱公大怒自此与西川失欢而汴帅军罢

    Explanation

    194

    Zhu Quanzhong welcomed the imperial carriage in Fengxiang. The military official Han Quanhuai, fearing Zhu Quanzhong's growing power, harbored the intention of using the emperor to command the feudal lords. Wang Jian of Western Shu also had this concern and formed an alliance with Bianzhou to raise an army to assist in welcoming the emperor. The Bianzhou army and the army of Western Shu attacked Xingyuan. The governor of Xingyuan, Wang Wanhong, without rescue, surrendered to Chengdu. As a result, the fourteen states of the southern mountains came under Shu control. After changing plans, they instead supported Fengxiang. At this time, the chief secretary Wei Zhuang was sent as an envoy to the front lines. Zhu Quanzhong became very angry and lost favor with Western Shu. The Bianzhou army disbanded.

    195

    韩建卖李巨川
    　　李巨川有笔述歴举不第先以仕伪【一作为】襄王与唐彦谦俱贬于山南褒帅杨守亮优待之山南失守随致仕杨军容复恭与守亮同奔北投太原导行者引出华州复恭为韩建挫辱杨骂为奴以短褐防之毙于枯木守亮槛送至京斩于独栁树京城百姓莫不沾涕此即南山一丈黒本姓訾黄巢时多救防导引朝士令趋行在人有逃黄巢而投附皆济之由是人多感激也巨川为韩建副使
    朱令公军次于华用张濬计先取韩建其幕客张策印率副使李巨川同诣辕门请降朱公谓曰车驾西幸皆公所教也建曰某不识字凡朝廷章奏邻道书檄皆巨川为之因斩之识者谓韩建无行求解怒于朱公遂为所卖时人寃之巨川有子慎仪仕后唐为翰林学士唯张策本与张濬有分携印而降叶濬之谋后仕至梁相朱公既得韩建以兄呼之寻奏移许昌【一作田】梁凤厯初亦遇害也

    Explanation

    195

    Translation

    Han Jian Betrays Li Juchuan

    Li Juchuan was a man of letters who, despite failing the imperial examinations, served under a false regime [one version reads "as a vassal"] for the Prince of Xiang and Tang Yanqian, both of whom were demoted to Shan Nan. The commander of Shan Nan, Yang Shǒuliàng, treated him kindly. After the fall of Shan Nan, Li Juchuan was dismissed from office. Yang Jūnróng Fùgōng and Yang Shǒuliàng fled north to Taiyuan together, with guides leading them out of Huazhou. Yang Jūnróng Fùgōng was humiliated by Han Jian, who called him a slave and confined him in a short robe, ultimately causing his death at the hands of a withered tree. Yang Shǒuliàng was caged and sent to the capital, where he was executed at the Lone Willow Tree. The people of the capital wept profusely, as this was none other than the "One-Zhang Black" of the Southern Mountains, originally surnamed Zī. During the time of Huang Chao, he frequently rescued and guided officials to safety, leading them to the imperial presence. Those who escaped Huang Chao and sought refuge with him were all saved, and thus many people were grateful to him. Li Juchuan served as Han Jian's deputy.

    Zhu Lingong, commanding his troops at Huazhou, used Zhang Jùn's strategy to first capture Han Jian. His aide Zhang Cè, carrying the seal, accompanied Li Juchuan to the camp gate to surrender. Zhu Lingong said to them, "The emperor's flight westward was all your doing." Han Jian replied, "I cannot read; all the imperial edicts, memorials, and military proclamations were written by Li Juchuan." Consequently, he was executed. Those who understood the situation believed that Han Jian had no integrity and sought to appease Zhu Lingong's anger, but he was ultimately betrayed. People at the time felt great sympathy for Li Juchuan. Li Juchuan had a son named Li Shènyí, who served as a翰林学士in the Later Tang Dynasty. Only Zhang Cè, who originally shared a connection with Zhang Jùn, carried the seal and surrendered, following Zhang Jùn's plan. Later, he rose to become a chancellor of the Later Liang. After Zhu Lingong captured Han Jian, he called him his elder brother and soon ordered him to be moved to Xuancheng [one version reads "Tian"]. In the early years of the Later Liang's Feng era, he also met his end.

    196

    天子赐勲臣诗
    　　德宗皇帝好为诗以赐容州戴叔伦文宗宣宗皆以诗赐大臣昭宗驻跸华州以歌辞赐韩建以诗及杨栁枝辞赐朱全忠所赐一也或以敬或以惮受其赐者得不求其义焉
    　　朱令公为昭宗拢马
    　　汴帅朱公再围凤翔与茂贞军战于虢县西槐林驿大败岐军横尸不絶鲍气闻于十里昭宗遂杀宦官韩全诲已下二十二人首宣示茂贞亦斩其义子继筠首以送于是车驾还宫朱令俛首马前请罪涕泣拢帝马行千歩帝为之动容至京师以宰相崔允判六军乃下诏诛宦官第五可范已下七百一十人又凤翔驾前宰相卢光启等一百余人并赐自尽天复三年汴人拥兵杀

    Explanation

    196

    Emperor Dezong loved to compose poems to grant to meritorious ministers, such as Dai Shulun of Rongzhou. Emperors Wenzong and Xuanzong also granted poems to their ministers. Emperor Zhaozong stayed in Huazhou and granted songs to Han Jian, and poems and lyrics about willow branches to Zhu Quanzhong. The grants were essentially the same, and those who received them either out of respect or fear could not help but seek the meaning.

    Zhu Gong, the governor of Bianzhou, besieged Fengxiang again and fought against Maowen's army at Huayin Station west of Guoxian, defeating the army of Qizhou. Bodies lay scattered without end, and the stench reached ten miles. Then, Emperor Zhaozong killed twenty-two eunuchs including Han Quanhui, whose heads were shown to Maowen. Zhu also beheaded his adopted son Ji Jun and sent his head. Thus, the imperial entourage returned to the palace. Zhu Gong bowed before the horse and begged for forgiveness, tears streaming, leading the emperor's horse for a thousand steps. The emperor was moved. Upon reaching the capital, Chancellor Cui Yun was appointed to command the six armies, and an edict was issued to execute 710 eunuchs including the fifth Duke Ke Fan. Also, more than a hundred officials including Prime Minister Lu Guangqi were ordered to commit suicide. In the third year of Tianfu, the people of Bianzhou raised arms and killed.

    197

    宰相崔允京兆尹郑元规刼迁车驾移都东洛既入华州百姓呼万歳帝泣谓百姓曰百姓勿唱万歳朕无能与尔等为主也防路有思帝乡之词乃曰纥干山头冻杀雀何不飞去生处乐况我此行悠悠未知落在何所言讫然流涕行至陜府内宴皇后自捧玉盆以赐全忠内人唱歌全忠将饮酒韩建蹑其足全忠惧辞醉而退至谷水而杀内人可证及随驾五百人自是帝孤立矣
    　　昭宗遇弑
    　　昭宗迁都至洛左右并是汴人虽有尊名乃是虚器如在笼槛郁郁不乐朱全忠以诸侯尽有匡复之志虑帝有奔幸之谋时防驾朱友谅等聚兵殿庭诉以衣食不足帝方劳谕友谅引兵升殿帝颠仆入内军士蹑而追之帝叱曰反耶友谅曰臣非敢无礼奉元帅之令帝奔入御厨以庖人之刀斩数辈竟为乱兵所害内人李渐荣裴正一等弑帝投刃而死又以朱友谅氏叔琮扇动军情请诛朱友谅氏叔琮以成济之罪归之友谅等临刑诉天曰天若有知他日亦当如我后全忠即位为子友珪所杀竟如其言

    Explanation

    197

    In the late Tang Dynasty, Chancellor Cui Yun and Jingzhao Governor Zheng Yuan Gui forcibly relocated the imperial carriage to Donglu (Luoyang). Upon arriving in Huazhou, the common people shouted "Long live the emperor!" The emperor wept and told the people, "Do not shout 'Long live the emperor!' I am unable to be your ruler." Along the way, there were words of longing for the imperial city, and he said, "On the top of Heda Mountain, the birds freeze to death. Why don't they fly away to a place where they can be happy? How much more so in this uncertain journey, I do not know where I will end up." After speaking, he wept bitterly. When they arrived at the imperial banquet in Shaanfu, the Empress personally presented a jade bowl to Zhu Quanzhong, and the imperial concubines sang. Zhu Quanzhong was about to drink when Han Jian stepped on his foot, and Zhu Quanzhong, fearing for his life, pretended to be drunk and withdrew. He later killed the imperial concubines and 500 attendants at Gu River, leaving the emperor isolated.

    Emperor Zhaozong was assassinated. After moving the capital to Luoyang, those around him were all people from Bianzhou (Kaifeng). Although he had a lofty title, it was empty and powerless, like a bird in a cage, feeling depressed and unhappy. Zhu Quanzhong believed that all the feudal lords had the intention to restore order and feared that the emperor might plan to escape. At one point, Zhu Youliang and others gathered troops in the palace courtyard, complaining about insufficient food and clothing. The emperor was trying to comfort and persuade Zhu Youliang, but Zhu Youliang said, "I dare not be disrespectful; I am following the orders of the commander-in-chief." The emperor rushed into the kitchen and killed several people with the cook's knife, but he was ultimately killed by the rebel soldiers. The imperial concubines Li Jianrong and Pei Zhengyi also killed the emperor and died by the sword. Zhu Shucong, Zhu Youliang's brother-in-law, incited the soldiers, and Zhu Quanzhong requested that Zhu Shucong be executed and that the blame for Cheng Ji's crime be placed on Zhu Youliang and others. On the verge of execution, Zhu Shucong cried out to heaven, "If there is a heaven, one day you will also treat me as you do now." Zhu Quanzhong ascended the throne but was later killed by his son Zhu Yougui, just as Zhu Shucong had predicted.

    198

    请杀德王
    　　辉王嗣位社宴德王裕已下诸王子孙并密为全忠所害德王帝之兄曾册皇太子刘季述等废昭宗册为皇帝季述等伏诛令归少阳院全忠以德王眉目疎秀春秋渐盛全忠恶之请崔允密启云太子曾窃寳位大义灭亲昭宗不纳一日驾幸福先寺谓枢密使蒋元晖曰德王吾之爱子何故频令吾废之又欲杀之言讫涙下因齧其中指血流全忠闻之宴罢尽杀之
    　　谋害衣冠
    　　辉王即位天佑中朱全忠以旧朝逹官尚在班列将谋簒夺先俾翦除凡在周行次第贬降旧相裴枢独孤损崔逺陆扆王溥大夫赵崇王替等于滑州白马驿赐自尽时宰相臣栁璨性隂狡贪权恶枢等在己之上与全忠腹心枢密使蒋元晖太常卿张廷范密友交结而害枢等俄而廷范辕裂元晖与栁璨及弟瑶瑊相继伏诛先是故相张濬一家并害而弃尸黄河朱公谋主李振累应进士举不第尤愤朝贵时谓朱全忠曰此清流辈宜投于黄河永为浊流全忠笑而从之尒朱荣河隂之戮衣冠不是过也俄而辉王禅位封济隂王于曹州遇酖而崩唐祚自此灭矣

    Explanation

    198

    Translation:

    Request to Execute the Prince of De

    Upon ascending the throne, Emperor Zhaozong held a grand feast for the Prince of De, Yu, and his descendants. They were all secretly killed by Zhu Quanzhong. The Prince of De was the emperor's older brother who had once been enfeoffed as the crown prince. Liu Jishu and others deposed Emperor Zhaozong and enthroned him as emperor. After Liu Jishu and others were executed, the emperor ordered the Prince of De to return to the Shaoyang Palace. Zhu Quanzhong, seeing that the Prince of De had clear and elegant features and was gradually maturing, grew jealous of him and requested that Cui Yun secretly advise the emperor that the prince had once usurped the throne, and that justice demanded his execution. The emperor refused to comply. One day, while the emperor was at the Fuxian Temple, he said to Jiang Yuanhui, the chief of the Imperial Secretariat, "The Prince of De is my beloved son. Why do you keep having me depose him, and now you want to kill him?" After speaking, tears fell from his eyes, and he bit his middle finger, causing blood to flow. Upon hearing this, Zhu Quanzhong ordered all the princes and their descendants to be killed after the feast.

    Conspiracy to Harm the Literati

    After Emperor Zhaozong ascended the throne, during the Tianyou period, Zhu Quanzhong, seeing that officials from the former court were still in high positions, planned to seize power. He first had them demoted and reduced in rank, gradually eliminating them. Former prime ministers Pei Shu, Dugu Sun, Cui Yuan, Lu Yi, Wang Pu, and other ministers Zhao Chong and Wang Ti were all ordered to commit suicide at the White Horse Inn in Huazhou. At the time, Chancellor Liu Can, who was cunning, greedy for power, and deceitful, hated that the former prime ministers were above him in status. He was close to Zhu Quanzhong's inner circle and secretly colluded with Jiang Yuanhui, the chief of the Imperial Secretariat, and Zhang Tingfan, the Grand Master of Rites, to harm the former prime ministers. Soon after, Zhang Tingfan was torn apart, and Jiang Yuanhui and Liu Can, along with his brothers Yao and Jian, were executed one after another. Prior to this, the entire family of Zhang Jun, the former prime minister, was killed, and their bodies were thrown into the Yellow River. Zhu Quanzhong's chief strategist, Li Zhen, had failed multiple times in the imperial examinations and resented the court officials. He said to Zhu Quanzhong, "These scholars should be thrown into the Yellow River to become part of the muddy waters forever." Zhu Quanzhong smiled and agreed. The massacre at Huayin, where the literati were not to blame, occurred. Soon after, Emperor Zhaozong abdicated and was bestowed the title of Prince of Jiyin, who died from poisoning in Caizhou. The Tang dynasty thus came to an end.

    诬何太后
    　　朱全忠先以蒋元晖为枢密使伺帝动静积庆何太后以昭宗见害之后常恐不保旦夕曽使宫人阿秋面召元晖属戒所乞它日传禅之后保全子母性命言发无不涕零先是全忠速要传禅召元晖到汴州责以太迟元晖以传禅先须封国授九锡之命俟次第行之全忠怒曰我不要九锡看作天子否元晖归奔洛阳与宰相商量为赵殷衡诬谮云与太后交通欲延唐祚乃令殷衡逼杀太后及宫人而诛蒋元晖时人寃之赵殷衡后改姓孔名循亦莫知其实是何姓仕后唐明宗为宣徽使出为许昌沧州两镇时人知其狡谲倾险莫不惮之

    Explanation

    199

    Accusing Empress Dowager He
    　　Zhu Quanzhong first appointed Jiang Yuanhui as the Chief of the Military Council to spy on the emperor's movements. After the assassination of Emperor Zhaozong, Empress Dowager He, fearing for her safety, often summoned Jiang Yuanhui personally to give him instructions and warnings about what she had requested. She spoke of ensuring the safety of mother and child after the future abdication, and her words were always accompanied by tears. Previously, Zhu Quanzhong had urgently demanded the abdication and summoned Jiang Yuanhui to Bianzhou, criticizing him for being too slow. Jiang Yuanhui argued that the abdication should first be granted the nine bestowals and then followed the proper order. Zhu Quanzhong became angry and said, "I don't want the nine bestowals; do you think I am an emperor?" Jiang Yuanhui returned to Luoyang and consulted with the chancellor, who was slandered by Zhao Yinhang, claiming that Jiang Yuanhui was conspiring with Empress Dowager He to prolong the Tang dynasty. As a result, Zhu Quanzhong ordered Zhao Yinhang to force the killing of Empress Dowager He and the palace women, and to execute Jiang Yuanhui. At the time, people felt great injustice towards this. Zhao Yinhang later changed his surname to Kong and took the name Xun, but no one knew his true identity. He served under Emperor Mingzong of Later Tang as an Envoy of the Imperial Household and was later appointed governor of Xuchang and Cangzhou. People knew him to be cunning and treacherous, and no one did not fear him.

    为堂叔母侍疾
    　　唐天祐三年拾遗充史馆修撰崔瑑进状以堂叔母在孟州济源私庄抱疾加甚无兄弟奉养无强近告投兼以年将七十地絶百里阙视药膳不遑晓夕遂乞假躬往侍疾勑防依允时人义之或曰避祸而享义名者亦智也
    　　秦宗权诉不反
    　　黄巢破后蔡州秦宗权继为反逆兵力强锐又复称僭山东诸郡苦之十年之间屠脍生聚汴帅朱全忠尽莭御之宗权为部将申丛擒而折足囚缚朱全忠具表槛送至京京兆尹孙揆率府县吏阅之宗权即槛中举首曰宗权非反也大尹哀之者因以为笑
    　　李摩云掷鉢从事
    　　李罕之河阳人也少为桑门无赖所至不容曾乞食于滑州酸枣县自旦至晡无与之者掷鉢于地毁僧衣投河阳诸葛爽为卒罕之即僧号便以为名素多力或与人相殴殴其左颊右颊流血爽寻署为小校每遣讨贼无不擒之蒲绛之北有摩云山设堡栅于上号摩云寨前后不能攻取时罕之下焉自此号李摩云累歴郡侯河南尹节将官至侍中卒于汴州荆南成汭之流也【自唐至梁下阙】

    Translation:

    Serving One's Aunt with Illness
    In the third year of the Tianyou era of the Tang Dynasty, Cui Zuan, an official appointed to assist in the compilation of historical records, submitted a petition stating that his aunt, residing in a private estate in Jiyuan, Mengzhou, was gravely ill and lacked brothers to care for her. There were no close relatives nearby to provide support, and with her approaching seventy years of age, she was far from home, unable to receive proper medical care and nourishment day and night. Therefore, he requested leave to personally attend to her illness. The emperor granted his request, and the people admired him. Some said that avoiding misfortune while enjoying the name of righteousness was also a form of wisdom.

    Qin Zongquan Accused of Not Rebellious
    After the defeat of Huang Chao, Qin Zongquan, who continued to rebel in Caozhou, had strong and sharp military forces and again claimed imperial authority. The various states of Shandong suffered greatly from his actions. Over ten years, he slaughtered and plundered the local population. The commander of Bianzhou, Zhu Quanzhong, finally managed to subdue him. Qin Zongquan was captured by his subordinate Shen Cong, who broke his leg and bound him. Zhu Quanzhong submitted a report detailing the capture, and Qin Zongquan was sent in a cage to the capital. The governor of the capital region, Sun Kui, inspected him. Qin Zongquan raised his head in the cage and said, "I did not rebel." The governor felt pity for him, and the people found it amusing.

    Li Mohun, Who Threw His Bowl to Become a Soldier
    Li Hanzi was from Heyang. As a young man, he was a disreputable Buddhist monk who was not accepted anywhere. He once begged for food in Suzhou, Suozuo County, but no one gave him anything from morning until evening. In frustration, he threw his bowl to the ground, destroyed his monk's robe, and joined the army of Zhu Geshuang in Heyang. Li Hanzi took the name of the monk he had been and became known as Li Mohun. He was naturally strong and often got into fights, sometimes beating the left cheek of his opponent, sometimes the right, causing them to bleed. Zhu Geshuang soon appointed him as a low-ranking officer. Whenever he was sent to fight rebels, he captured them all. In the north of Pu and Jiang, there was a mountain called Moyun, where a fortress was built and named Moyun Camp. No one could capture it before Li Hanzi, who eventually did so. From then on, he was known as Li Mohun. He served in various positions, including governor of several counties, governor of Henan, and a high-ranking official. He died in Bianzhou, and his fate was similar to that of Cheng Rui of Jingnan. [From the Tang to the Later Liang, the text is incomplete.]

    北梦琐言卷十五
    <子部,小说家类,杂事之属,北梦琐言>
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十六

    　　以酒致祸
    　　梁祖图霸之初夀州刺史江彦温以郡归我乃遣亲吏张从晦劳其勤而从晦无赖酒酣有饮徒何藏耀者与之偕甚昵每事悮禀从晦致命于郡彦温大张乐邀不至乃与藏耀食于主将家彦温果疑恐曰汴王谋我矣不然何使者之如是也乃杀其主将连诛数十人而以状白其事既而又疑惧曰诉其腹心亡我族矣乃自缢而死梁祖大怒按
    其事腰斩从晦留藏耀裂其禁械斩于夀春市葆光子曰后唐明宗皇帝时董璋据东川将有跋扈之心于时遣客省使李仁矩出使梓潼仁矩本节使下小校骤居内职性好狎邪元戎张筵托以寒召之不至乃与营妓曲宴璋闻説甚怒索马诣馆遽欲害之仁矩鞹足端简门迎璋怒稍解他日作叛两川举兵并由仁矩献谋于安重诲之所致也

    Translation:

    Trivial Notes from the North Dream, Volume Fifteen
    <Subclass: Miscellaneous, Trivial Notes from the North Dream>
    Authorized Complete Library in Four Branches of Literature

    Trivial Notes from the North Dream, Volume Sixteen
    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Causing Disaster Through Alcohol

    When Liang Zong was planning his rise to power, Jiang Yantong, the governor of Shouzhou, surrendered his territory to him. Liang Zong then sent his trusted official Zhang Conghui to reward Jiang Yantong for his efforts. However, Zhang Conghui was a good-for-nothing. After drinking, he was accompanied by a drunkard named He Cangyao, with whom he became very close. Every matter was reported incorrectly to Zhang Conghui, who then gave orders to the city. Jiang Yantong held a grand celebration but was not invited. Instead, he had a meal with He Cangyao at the main general's house. Jiang Yantong became suspicious and fearful, thinking that the King of Bian (Liang Zong) was plotting against him. He executed the main general and dozens of others, then reported the matter to Liang Zong. Later, Jiang Yantong became even more suspicious and fearful, thinking that his close confidants were plotting against him. He committed suicide by hanging. Liang Zong became very angry and ordered Zhang Conghui to be executed by decapitation. He released He Cangyao and later had him executed in the market of Shouzhou. Preserving Light said:

    During the reign of Emperor Mingzong of Later Tang, Dong Zhang occupied Dongchuan and had rebellious intentions. At that time, a guest provincial envoy named Li Renju was sent to visit Zitong. Li Renju was originally a low-ranking officer who quickly rose to an important position. He had a fondness for debauchery. The military commander set up a banquet and invited Li Renju under the pretext of cold weather, but Li Renju did not come. Instead, he had a private banquet with a camp prostitute. Dong Zhang heard about this and became very angry, immediately wanting to harm Li Renju. Li Renju appeared at the door with his feet bound and dressed formally. Dong Zhang's anger slightly subsided. Later, Dong Zhang rebelled, and both provinces raised armies, which was due to Li Renju's advice to An Zhonghe.
