    蜀使洪饮
    　　梁太祖初兼四镇先主遣押衙潘岏持聘岏饮酒一石不乱每攀防饮礼容益庄梁祖爱之饮酣梁祖曰押衙能饮一盘器物乎岏曰不敢乃簇在席器皿次第注酌岏并饮之岏愈温克梁祖谓其归馆多应倾泻困卧俾人侦之岏簪笋箨冠子秤所得酒器涤而藏之他日又遣押衙郑顼持聘梁祖问以劒阁道路顼极言危峻梁祖曰贤主人可以过得顼对曰若不上闻恐悮令公军机梁祖大笑此亦近代使令之美者也
    　　朱瑾杀兄
    　　朱瑾之据兖州梁祖攻之未克其从父兄齐州刺史琼先降与琼同诣壁下以晓之瑾乃遣都虞候胡规出献欵曰兄已降愿贷瑾不死请以镇委吏既而啓延夀门陈牌印于笥曰兄来请先奉此梁祖命琼受之葛从周疑诈选勇士孙少迪等仗劒以驭琼曰彼力屈不足疑琼进前受印籥瑾单马曰兄独来密语耳始相及瑾令骁卒董懐进勾曵琼坠马乃发所匿刃杀琼勾曵突出牵入之湏臾城上鼓噪掷琼首于埤也我军失色梁祖哀恸久之斩军谋徐厚署琼弟玭为齐州防御使恩礼殊厚瑾竟弃城投扬州

    Explanation

    202

    The Envoy from Shu Who Drank Heavily
    When Emperor Zhu Wen of Later Liang first controlled four commanderies, he sent an envoy named Pan Wan on a mission. Pan Wan drank a large amount of wine without becoming disordered, and each time he drank, his demeanor became even more solemn. Emperor Zhu Wen admired him. When they were drinking, Emperor Zhu Wen asked, "Can you drink from a whole set of vessels?" Pan Wan replied, "I dare not." Then, the vessels were arranged on the table in order, and Pan Wan drank from them all. He remained even more composed. Emperor Zhu Wen thought that upon returning to his quarters, he would likely be too drunk to sleep, so he had someone spy on him. Upon returning, Pan Wan wore a hat made from bamboo shoots and weighed the wine vessels he had obtained, cleaned them, and stored them. On another occasion, Emperor Zhu Wen sent another envoy named Zheng Xu on a mission. Emperor Zhu Wen asked about the dangerous roads of the Jie Gate. Zheng Xu described them as extremely perilous. Emperor Zhu Wen said, "The wise host can be passed through." Zheng Xu replied, "If it is not reported, it might mislead the general's military plans." Emperor Zhu Wen laughed and said, "This is also an excellent example of a modern envoy."

    The Death of Brother by Brother
    When Zhu Jin held onto Yan Prefecture and Emperor Zhu Wen attacked him without success, his paternal uncle, Governor Qiong of Qi Prefecture, surrendered first. Qiong and Zhu Jin went together to the city wall to explain the situation. Zhu Jin then sent the chief of the guard, Hu Gui, to present a letter saying, "My elder brother has surrendered. Please spare my life and allow me to hand over the prefecture to the officials." Later, they opened the Yan寿 gate and placed the seal in a box, saying, "My elder brother has come and asked to present this first." Emperor Zhu Wen ordered Qiong to take it. Ge Congzhou suspected a trick and selected brave warriors like Sun Shaodi to guard Qiong with swords. Qiong said, "They are exhausted and not worth suspecting." Qiong approached to receive the seal, and Zhu Jin rode alone and said, "My elder brother has come alone to speak privately." As soon as they met, Zhu Jin ordered the brave soldier Dong Huaijin to pull and drag Qiong off his horse. Qiong then revealed a hidden blade and killed Qiong. Zhu Jin pulled and dragged him out and pulled him into the city. Soon, the city walls were filled with drums and shouts, and Qiong's head was thrown at the wall. Emperor Zhu Wen's army was shocked and he mourned deeply for a long time. He ordered the execution of the military strategist Xu Hou and appointed Qiong's younger brother Pin as the governor of Qi Prefecture, giving him special favor and courtesy. Zhu Jin eventually abandoned the city and fled to Yangzhou.

    马景设诈
    　　梁祖宿兵岐下以迎昭宗敌垒尚坚旦思班退亲从指挥使髙季昌抗言曰天下雄杰窥此举者一载矣今奸党已窘更少俟之季昌乃密募人入岐为告事者有骑卒马景应命因朱友伦緫骑军且【一作因】至将大出兵迓景请其时给骏驷杂所出队中十许里跃马西逸叩岐闉以军怨东遁为告且言列寨留卒尚方俟夕将逝宜速掩之当落我机内矣失是往也
    决无生理愿録其妻孥梁祖凄然止其行景固请乃徇之明日军出诸寨屏匿如无人不十里果风骑却走岐人纳之不失厥料岐军启两扉悉众来我师宿已秣马饱士中军一鼓百营俱进大破岐军十不存三四焉李茂贞丧胆昭宗降诏还京始遂奉迎矣功归髙公而马景妻孥倍加轸防且解扬以守正而忠不顾其身也马景以死命行诈非图身也人之难事唯景有之
    　　朱延夀妻王烈女

    Explanation

    203

    Ma Jing Set a Deception
    　　Zhu Wen stationed his troops in Qishan to welcome Emperor Zhaozong. The enemy's defenses were still strong, and in the morning, he thought of retreating. His personal attendant and commander, Gao Jichang, spoke out boldly, saying, "Those who have been watching this move for a year are now in a difficult position. Let us wait a little longer." Gao Jichang then secretly recruited people to enter Qishan as informants. There was a mounted soldier named Ma Jing who responded to the call. Because Zhu Youlun was in charge of the cavalry, and with the impending large-scale military action, Ma Jing asked for a horse to be given at the time, and mixed among the troops that were being sent out. About ten li away, he leaped on horseback and escaped to the west, knocking on the gates of Qishan to communicate the army's resentment and eastward retreat. He also said that the camps were hiding, as if there were no one, and that the enemy was still waiting for the evening to pass, suggesting that it was advisable to quickly attack them, as it would fall into their trap. If they missed this opportunity, there would be no way to survive. He wished to record his wife and children. Zhu Wen, with a sad expression, stopped his journey, but Ma Jing firmly requested, and Zhu Wen agreed. The next day, the army set out, and the camps hid, as if there were no one. Indeed, the cavalry retreated, and the Qishan people accepted them, not losing their expectations. The Qishan army opened the two doors, and all the troops came to us. Our army, having already fed the horses and fed the soldiers, beat the drum once from the central army, and all the camps advanced together, greatly defeating the Qishan army, with only about one-third or four-tenths remaining. Li Maozhen lost his courage, and Emperor Zhaozong issued an edict to return to the capital, finally succeeding in welcoming him. The credit goes to Gao Gong, and Ma Jing's wife and children were given double the concern and protection. Jie Yang upheld righteousness and loyalty, not caring about his own life, while Ma Jing used deception with his life, not for personal gain. The difficulty of the task was only possessed by Jing.
    　　The wife of Zhu Yanshou, a virtuous woman.

    204

    宣州田頵夀州朱延夀将举军以背杨行密请杜荀持笺诣淮都俄而事泄行密悉兵攻宛陵延夀飞骑以赴俱为淮军所杀延夀之将行也其室王氏勉延夀曰愿日致一介以宁所懐一日介不致王氏曰事可知矣乃部分家僮悉授兵器遽阖州中之扉而捕骑已至不得入遂集家僮私阜帑发百燎庐舍州焚之急而稽首上告曰妾誓不以皎然之躯为仇者所辱乃投火而死古之烈女无以过也
    　　木星入斗
    　　唐干符中荆州节度使晋公王铎后为诸道都统时木星入南斗数夕不退晋公观之问诸知星者吉凶安在咸曰金火土犯斗即为灾唯木当应为福耳咸或然之时有术士边冈洞晓天文精通厯数谓晋公曰唯斗帝王之宫宿唯木为福神当以帝王占之然则非福于今必当有騐于后未敢言之他日晋公屏左右密问冈曰木星入斗帝王之兆木在斗中朱字也识者言唐世甞有绯衣之谶或言将来革运或姓裴或姓牛以为裴字为绯衣牛字着人即朱也所以裴晋公度牛相国僧孺每罹此谤李衞公斥周秦行纪乃斯事也安知钟于砀山之朱乎

    Explanation

    204

    Tian Jun of Xuanzhou and Zhu Yanchou of Shouzhou planned to rebel against Yang Xingmi with their armies and asked Du Xunzhi to carry a letter to Huai Prefecture. Soon the plot was exposed, and Yang Xingmi mobilized all his troops to attack Wanling. Zhu Yanchou sent cavalry to join the fight, but both were killed by the Huai army. As Zhu Yanchou was about to leave, his wife Lady Wang encouraged him, saying, "I wish to send a messenger daily to soothe your mind. If one messenger is not sent, the situation is clear." She then organized the household servants and gave them weapons, quickly closing the city gates, but the pursuing cavalry had already arrived and could not enter. They gathered the household servants and opened the private treasury, lit a hundred torches to burn the houses and the city, and urgently knelt and bowed to report, saying, "I swear not to let my clear body be disgraced by the enemy." Then she threw herself into the fire and died. She was an example of a heroic woman from ancient times.

    Jupiter entered the constellation of the Dipper. During the Danyuan period, Wang Duo, the Governor of Jing Prefecture, later became the Commander of All Routes. When Jupiter entered the South Dipper and remained there for several nights, Wang Duo observed it and asked the astrologers about the auspiciousness or inauspiciousness. They all said that if the stars of metal, fire, or earth invaded the Dipper, it would bring disaster, but only wood should bring good fortune. Wang Duo agreed with this. At that time, there was a scholar named Bian Gang who was deeply knowledgeable in astronomy and skilled in calendrical calculations. He told Wang Duo, "The Dipper is the constellation of the emperor's palace, and only wood is the god of good fortune. It should be interpreted in terms of the emperor. Therefore, it is not a blessing for the present, but it will surely be verified in the future. I dare not say more." One day, Wang Duo dismissed his attendants and asked Bian Gang privately, "Jupiter entering the Dipper is a sign of imperial fortune. The character 'wood' (木) is inside the Dipper, forming the character '朱'. Wise people said there was an omen of a red-clothed person in the Tang Dynasty. Some said it would lead to a change in the dynasty, and it could be someone surnamed Pei or Niu. So Pei Jun and Niu Sengru often faced this slander. Li Weigong criticized the records of Zhou and Qin, which is related to this matter. How could it be destined for Zhu from Dangshan?"

    木中异文
    　　梁开平中潞州军前李思安奏壶关县庶穰乡人因伐树倒分为两片内有六字皆如左书曰天十四载石进乃图其状以献仍付史馆尔后唐庄宗皇帝自晋王登位以为应之中间石氏自并门受国称首朝湖南马希范解释此字表闻焉
    　　薛贻矩画赞
    　　梁相国薛贻矩名家子擢进士第在唐至御史大夫先是南班官忌与北司交通天复中翦戮阉官贻矩甞与韩全诲等作写真赞悉纪于内侍省屋壁间坐是谪官他日赍唐帝命禅于梁仕至宰相
    　　舂磨寨
    　　黄巢自长安遁归与其众屯于陈蔡间溵河下寨连络号八山营于时蔡州秦宗权惧巢以城降之时既饥乏野无所掠唯捕人为食肉尽继之以骨或碓捣或硙磨咸用充饥天军四合巢军不利其党骇散频为雷电大雨淹浸其营乃与妻孥昆弟奔于泰山狼虎谷为外甥林言斩首送徐州时溥下禆将李师鋭函首送成都行在也

    Explanation

    205

    Strange Writings in Wood

    During the Kai Ping era of the Later Liang dynasty, Li Si'an, stationed at the military front of the state of Lu, reported that in Shu Rang village of Hu Guan County, a tree had fallen and split into two pieces, revealing six characters written on it. These characters were all written from left to right and read "Tian Shi Si Zai." Shi Jin then drew a diagram of the inscription and presented it, which was subsequently entrusted to the historical archives. Later, after Emperor Zhuangzong of Tang ascended the throne from the Prince of Jin, he considered this inscription to be a response to the middle. In between, the Shi family received the country from Bing Gate and claimed the first court, and Ma Xifan of Hunan explained this character and reported it.

    Eulogy for Xue Yiju

    Xue Yiju, a high-ranking official of the Later Liang dynasty, was a son of a prominent family who passed the imperial examinations and rose to the rank of Grand Censor during the Tang dynasty. Previously, southern court officials feared and avoided communication with the northern service, and during the Tian Fu era, eunuchs were cut and killed. Xue Yiju had once collaborated with Han Quanhuai and others to write a eulogy, which was recorded on the walls of the inner service hall, leading to his demotion. Later, he carried the decree of the Tang emperor to abdicate to the Liang and rose to the position of chancellor.

    Chong Mo Camp

    Huang Chao fled from Chang'an back to his base and stationed his troops between Chen and Cai, setting up a camp on the Yin River, connected and named the Eight Mountain Camp. At that time, Qin Zongquan, the governor of Cai, feared Huang Chao and surrendered the city. The troops were already hungry and lacked resources, with nothing to plunder in the wild. They resorted to capturing people to eat, and when meat was gone, they followed it with bones, either pounded with a pestle or ground with a mill, all used to fill the hunger. The heavenly troops gathered from all sides, and Huang Chao's troops were at a disadvantage, causing his followers to be terrified and scatter. Frequent thunderstorms and heavy rains flooded his camp, and he then fled with his wife, children, and brothers to the Wolf Tiger Valley on Mount Tai. His nephew Lin Yan beheaded him, and his head was sent to Xu Zhou, where Shi Yi, a subordinate general, sent it to Chengdu, the imperial residence.

    梁祖脱难
    　　梁祖亲征郓州军次衞南时筑新垒土工毕因登眺其上见飞鸟止于峻堞之间而噪其声甚厉副使李璠曰是乌鸟也将有不如意之事其前军朱友裕为朱瑄掩扑拔军南去我军不知因北行遇朱瑄军来迎【一作趂】梁祖策马南走入村落间为贼所迫前有沟坑颇极深广仓【一作怱】遽之际忽见沟内蜀黍秆积以为道正在马前遂腾跃而过因获免焉副使李璠都将髙行思为贼所杀张归宇为殿骑授戈力战仅得生还被十四五箭乃知衞南之乌先见之騐也
    　　梁祖梦丁防
    　　丁防为昭义节帅常惧梁祖雄猜疑忌功臣忽谓敬翔曰吾梦丁防在前祗候吾将乗马欲出圉人以马就台忽为丁防跨之以出时梦中怒叱喝数声因惊觉甚恶之是月丁防举潞州军民归河东矣

    Explanation

    206

    Emperor Zhu Wen Escapes a Crisis
    Emperor Zhu Wen personally led a military campaign to Yüan Prefecture, and while his army was stationed at Wèinan, they completed the construction of new fortifications. He then ascended and looked out, seeing birds perching on high walls and making loud noises. Deputy Commander Li Fan remarked, "These birds are an omen, and there will be an unfavorable event." Indeed, the front-line troops led by Zhu Youyu were attacked by Zhu Xuan and retreated southward. Our army did not know this and continued northward, encountering Zhu Xuan's troops who came to meet us. In a state of haste and confusion, Emperor Zhu Wen suddenly saw accumulated corn stalks inside a ditch, which he took as a path. He leaped over the ditch on his horse and thus escaped. However, Deputy Commander Li Fan and General Gao Xingsi were killed by the enemy. General Zhang Guiyu, as a rear guard, fought bravely with a spear and barely survived, being wounded by fifteen or sixteen arrows. Thus, it became known that the birds at Wèinan were an early warning.

    Dream of Ding Fang
    Ding Fang, the commander of the Zhaoyi circuit, often feared that Emperor Zhu Wen would suspect and doubt meritorious subjects. Suddenly, he said to Jing Xiang, "I dreamed that Ding Fang was waiting in front of me. I was about to ride a horse and leave, and the stable boy brought the horse to the platform. Suddenly, Ding Fang leaped onto it and left. In the dream, I shouted angrily several times and woke up in a panic, finding it very ominous. That month, Ding Fang led the people of Lushui to return to Hedong."

    殿栋折坠
    　　梁祖末年多行诛戮一夕寝殿大栋忽坠于御榻之上初闻土落于寝帐上乃惊觉久之又闻有小木坠于帐顶间遂矍然下牀未出殿门其栋乃坠迟明召诸王近臣令观之夜来惊危防不相见由是君臣相泣又曰惊忧之时如有人引头于寝閤门内云里面莫有人否所以怱忙奔起得非宫殿神乎他日又游于大内西九曲池泛鹢舟于池上忽闻倾侧上堕于池中宫嫔并内侍从官并跃入池扶策登岸移时方安尔后发痼疾竟罹其子郢王友珪弑逆之祸舟倾栋折非佳事也
    　　梁祖围枣强事
    　　梁祖末年用军不利河北数镇不顺其命一旦躁挠坚要亲征师次深州界遂令杨师厚分兵攻枣强县半浃旬方拔其垒是邑也池湟坚牢人心犷悍昼夜攻击以至疲竭既陷之日无少长皆屠之时有一百姓来投军中李周彛于部伍间乃谓周彛曰请一劒愿先登以其城未许间忽然抽茶担子挥击周彛头上中檐防仆于地左右乃擒之原是枣强城中遣来令诈降本意欲窥弄梁军招讨使杨师厚斯人不能辨误中周彛是知河朔之民勇劲如此

    Explanation

    207

    The Great Beam Collapsed

    In the later years of Emperor Zhuangzong of Later Liang, he frequently carried out executions. One night, a large beam in the imperial sleeping hall suddenly fell onto the emperor's bed. Initially, he heard soil falling onto the sleeping mat and was startled awake. After a while, he heard a small piece of wood fall onto the top of the canopy, and he hurriedly got out of bed before even leaving the hall, as the beam had fallen. Early the next morning, he summoned various princes and ministers to observe the incident. Fearing they might not see each other again, the emperor and his ministers wept together. He also said that during the time of fear and worry, it seemed as if someone had pulled their head into the door of the sleeping chamber and asked, "Is there no one inside?" This caused him to rush out hastily, wondering if it was not the spirit of the palace. On another day, while roaming in the Western Nine-Bend Pool of the Inner Palace and sailing a swan boat on the pool, he suddenly heard the boat tilt and fall into the pool. The court ladies and attendants jumped into the pool to help him onto the shore. After some time, he finally calmed down. Thereafter, he contracted a chronic illness and eventually suffered the disaster of being assassinated by his son, Prince Ying, who was a rebel. The boat capsizing and the beam breaking were not good omens.

    The Siege of Zaoqiang by Emperor Zhuangzong

    In the later years of Emperor Zhuangzong, his military campaigns were unsuccessful, and several towns in Hebei did not obey his orders. One day, restless and agitated, he insisted on leading a personal campaign and camped near the border of Shen Prefecture. He then ordered General Yang Shihou to divide the troops and attack Zaoqiang County. After half a ten-day period, they finally captured the stronghold. The town was strong, with moats and walls that were difficult to breach, and the people were fierce and wild. They attacked day and night until they were exhausted. On the day it was captured, all, regardless of age, were killed. A commoner came to join the army. Li Zhouyi was among the ranks and said to Zhouyi, "Please give me a sword, and I will lead the charge to capture the city." Before permission was given, he suddenly pulled out a tea ladle and struck Zhouyi on the head, hitting the brim and falling to the ground. The attendants then captured him. Originally sent from Zaoqiang, he had come to feign surrender with the intention of spying on the Liang army. The military commissioner, Yang Shihou, could not distinguish this person and mistakenly struck Zhouyi. Thus it is known that the people of the Hebei region were so brave and fierce.

    仇殷召课
    　　梁司天监仇殷术数精妙每见吉凶不敢明言稍关逆耳秘而不説往往罚俸葢惧梁祖之好杀也梁自昭义失守符道昭就擒柏【一作百下同】乡不利王景仁大败皆为太原节使嗣晋王李存朂之所挫也方懐子孙之忧唯柏乡狼狈亦自咎云违犯天道不取仇殷之言也

    　　梁祖为佣保
    　　梁祖宋州砀山县午沟里人本名温赐名全忠建国后改名晃家世为儒祖信父诚皆以教授为业诚蚤卒有三子俱幼母王氏携养寄于同县人刘崇家昆弟之中唯温狡猾无行崇母抚养之崇弟兄甞加谴杖一日偷崇家釜而窜为崇追回崇母遮防以免朴责善逐走鹿往往及而获之又崇母常见其有龙蛇之异他日与仲兄存入黄巢中作贼伯兄昱与母王氏尚依刘家温既辞去不知存亡及温领镇于汴盛饰舆马使人迎母于崇家王氏皇恐辞避深藏不之信谓人曰朱三落拓无行何处作贼送死焉能自致富贵

    Explanation

    Translation

    Cui Yin and His Prophecies

    Cui Yin, the chief astronomer of the Later Liang, was skilled in divination and astrology. Whenever he foresaw good or bad omens, he dared not speak them plainly if they were likely to be displeasing to the emperor. He would keep such prophecies secret, and as a result, he was often penalized by having his salary reduced. This was due to his fear of Emperor Zhu Wen's (梁祖) penchant for violence.

    The Later Liang suffered several military defeats: the state of Zhao was lost, and General Fu Daozhang was captured. In Boling, General Wang Jingren suffered a significant defeat, all of which were attributed to the military prowess of Li Cunxu, the Prince of Jin, who was the successor to the throne of the Later Tang dynasty. The Later Liang was now concerned about the future, feeling that their misfortunes were due to ignoring Cui Yin's advice.

    Translation

    The Northern Dream Trivia, Volume Sixteen
    The Complete Library in Four Branches of Literature
    The Northern Dream Trivia, Volume Seventeen
    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Emperor Zhu Wen as a Laborer

    Emperor Zhu Wen was born in Wugou Village, Dangshan County, Song Prefecture. His original name was Wen, and he was later given the name Quan Zhong. After establishing the Later Liang, he changed his name to Hu. His family had been scholars for generations. His grandfather, Xun, and his father, Cheng, both made a living through teaching. Cheng died early, leaving behind three young sons. Their mother, Wang, took the children to live with Liu Chong, a fellow villager. Among the brothers, only Wen was cunning and unscrupulous. Liu's mother raised him, and although Liu's brothers sometimes scolded and beat him, Wen once stole a pot from Liu's home and ran away. Liu chased after him, and Liu's mother intervened to prevent punishment. Wen was good at hunting and often caught deer. Liu's mother also observed that Wen had a strange aura, like that of a dragon or snake. Later, Wen and his second brother, Cun, joined Huang Chao's rebellion, while his eldest brother, Yu, and their mother Wang remained with Liu's family. After Wen left, his family did not know his fate. When Wen became the governor of Bian Prefecture, he adorned his carriages and horses and sent people to fetch his mother from Liu's home. Wang was terrified and hid, not believing that Wen could achieve such success. She told others, "Zhu San was a vagrant with no morals. How could he become a bandit and die? How could he ever become wealthy and powerful?"

    209

    汴帅非吾子也使者具陈离乡去里之由归国立功之事王氏方泣而信是日与崇母并迎归汴温盛礼郊迎人士改观崇以旧恩位至列卿为商州刺史王氏以温贵封晋国太夫人仲兄存于贼中为矢石所中而卒温致酒于母欢甚语及家事谓母曰朱五经辛苦业儒不登一命今有子为节度使无忝先人矣母不怿良久谓温曰汝致身及此信谓英特行义未必如先人朱二与汝同入贼军身死蛮徼孤男稚女艰食无告汝未有恤孤之心英特即有诸无取也温垂涕谢罪即令召诸兄子皆至汴友伦皆立军功位至方镇
    　　梁祖张夫人
    　　梁祖魏国夫人张氏砀山富室女父防曽为宋州刺史温时闻张有姿色私心倾慕有丽华之叹及温在同州得张于兵间因以妇礼纳之温以其宿欵深加敬异张贤明有礼温虽虎狼其心亦所景伏每军谋国计必先延访或已出师中途有所不可张氏一介请旋如期而至其信重如此初収兖郓得朱瑾妻温告之云彼既无依

    209

    The General of Kaifeng is not my son. The envoy fully explained the reasons for leaving one's hometown and village, as well as the matters of returning to the country and establishing achievements. Wang was just crying and believed. That day, she and Chong's mother were welcomed back to Kaifeng with warm and grand ceremonies, which changed the perception of the officials. Chong, due to old favors, reached the position of a high-ranking official and became the governor of Shangzhou. Wang, because of Wen's rank, was enfeoffed as the Dowager of Jin State. Chong's second brother survived among the rebels but was hit by arrows and stones and died. Wen brought wine to his mother, who was very joyful, and they talked about family affairs. Wen said to his mother, "Zhu Wujing worked hard studying Confucianism but did not achieve any official rank. Now I have a son who is a military governor and has not disgraced our ancestors." His mother was not pleased for a long time and said to Wen, "You have reached this position; you truly believe that your noble conduct and righteousness may not be as good as your ancestors. Zhu Er and you entered the rebel army together, and he died in a remote border area. Orphaned boys and young girls have difficulty finding food and have no one to turn to. You do not have compassion for orphans. Even if you have noble qualities, it is not desirable." Wen shed tears and apologized, immediately ordered to summon all his brothers' children, and they all came to Kaifeng. You Lun and others all established military achievements and reached the position of regional military governors.

    Liang Zong's wife, the Hui Guo Fu Ren Zhang, was a wealthy woman from Dangshan. Her father, Fang, once served as the governor of Songzhou. During Wen's time, he heard that Zhang had a beautiful appearance and secretly admired her, with admiration for Li Hua. When Wen was in Tongzhou, he found Zhang among the soldiers and accepted her as a wife according to proper rites. Wen deeply respected and treated her differently because of their old acquaintance. Zhang was wise, virtuous, and polite. Although Wen had a heart like a tiger or wolf, he still respected her. He always consulted her first on military strategies and state affairs. Sometimes after troops had been dispatched, if something was not right, Zhang would request to return, and she would arrive on schedule. She was trusted and respected like this. At the beginning, when capturing Yanzheng and Yuying, he captured Zhu Jin's wife. Wen told him, "She has no support."

    寓于辎车张氏遣人召之瑾妻再拜张氏荅拜泣下谓之曰兖郓与司空同姓之国昆仲之间以小故寻戈致吾姒如此设不幸汴州失守妾亦似吾姒之今日也又泣下乃度为尼张恒给其费张既卒继宠者非人及僭号后大纵朋淫骨肉聚麀帷薄荒以致友珪之祸起于妇人始能以柔婉之徳制豺虎之心如张氏者不亦贤乎
    　　朱邪先代
    　　河东李克用其先回纥部人世为蕃中大酋受唐朝官职太宗于北方沙陁碛立沙陁府以招集降戸后克用祖朱邪执宜与其父曽依吐蕃背吐蕃归朝徳宗于盐州置隂山府以执宜为都督后迁于神武川黄花堆之别墅即今应州是也执宜生赤心以讨徐州厐勋功赐国姓并名号李国昌懿宗问其先世所出云本陇西金城人依寓吐蕃帝曰我先与汝同乡里勅令编籍郑王房始为云州大同军节度次授鄜延振武代北三节度其侄克让为羽林将军其子克用最闻名以破黄巢功为太原节度使子存朂平梁蜀奄有中原追尊

    Explanation

    210

    Zhang, staying in a carriage, sent someone to summon him. His wife bowed twice, and Zhang bowed in return, shedding tears and said to him, "Yan and Yun are countries of the same surname as the Duke of Si, and among brothers, a small matter led to the use of weapons, resulting in my sister-in-law's situation. If by misfortune Bianzhou were to fall, I would also be like my sister-in-law today." She shed tears again and was then ordained as a nun. Zhang Heng provided her expenses. After Zhang's death, the one who succeeded in favor was not a suitable person, and later usurped the title, greatly indulging in promiscuity. Family members engaged in promiscuity, and the curtains and screens were in a state of chaos, leading to the disaster of You Gui arising from a woman. Only then could gentle and mild virtue control a fierce heart, like Zhang. Is she not virtuous?

    The ancestors of the Zhu Ya clan:

    Li Keyong of Hedong, whose ancestors were people of the Uyghur tribe, held high positions in the Tang dynasty. Emperor Taizong established the Shatuo Fu in the northern desert to gather surrendered households. Later, Li Keyong's ancestor Zhu Ya Zhiyi, along with his father, relied on the Tibetans, but later defected to the Tang court. Emperor Dezong established the Yinshan Fu in Yanzhou and appointed Zhu Ya Zhiyi as its governor. Later, they moved to the villa in Shenwu River's Huanghuadui, which is now Yinzhou. Zhu Ya Zhiyi gave birth to Zhu Xincheng, who, after defeating the rebels in Xuzhou, was granted the surname Li and the title Li Guochang. Emperor Yizong asked about his ancestors' origin, and he replied that they were originally from Longxi Jincheng, relying on the Tibetans. The emperor said, "My ancestors and yours are from the same village; I have ordered you to be registered in the Prince of Zheng's lineage." He was first appointed as the military governor of Yunzhou and the Datong Army, then granted the three military governorships of Fuyan, Zhenwu, and Dainor. His nephew Li Kelang became a general, and his son Li Keyong, the most famous, was appointed as the military governor of Taiyuan for his victory over Huang Chao. His son Li Cunxu pacified Liang and Shu, eventually dominating the Central Plains. He was posthumously honored as...

    执宜号懿祖国昌号献祖克用号太祖皇帝太祖在姙十三月载诞之夕母后甚危令族人市药于雁门遇神人教以率部人被介持旄击钲鼓跃马大噪环所居三周而止果如所教而生是日红【一作虹】光烛室白气充庭井水暴溢及能言喜道军旅年十二三能连射双鸟至于树叶针锋马鞭皆能中之曽于新城北以酒酹毗沙门塑像请与仆交谈天王被甲持矛隐隐出于壁间或所居帐内时如火聚如有龙形人皆异之甞随献祖征厐勋军阵出没如神号为飞虎子眇一目时号独眼龙功业磊落不可尽述【或云睛邪非眇也】
    　　亲王拜蕃侯
    　　唐干宁中凤翔李茂贞华州韩建邠州王行瑜拥兵胁君诛戮宰辅焚烧宫阙初帝西幸凤翔昭宗出居石门莎城太原克用领蕃汉马步入京三镇大惧是年破邠州斩王行瑜昭宗嘉奬倚赖命延王丕丹王允赍诏赐李公衣服兼令二亲王设拜以兄事之近古未有也仍封晋王以宠之延王才识过人聦悟辩慧在晋阳留宴累月每献酬乐作必为晋王起舞后为韩建所杀

    Explanation

    211

    执宜号懿祖国昌号献祖克用号太祖皇帝太祖在姙十三月载诞之夕母后甚危令族人市药于雁门遇神人教以率部人被介持旄击钲鼓跃马大噪环所居三周而止果如所教而生是日红【一作虹】光烛室白气充庭井水暴溢及能言喜道军旅年十二三能连射双鸟至于树叶针锋马鞭皆能中之曽于新城北以酒酹毗沙门塑像请与仆交谈天王被甲持矛隐隐出于壁间或所居帐内时如火聚如有龙形人皆异之甞随献祖征厐勋军阵出没如神号为飞虎子眇一目时号独眼龙功业磊落不可尽述【或云睛邪非眇也】

    太祖皇帝，执宜号懿祖，国昌号献祖，克用号太祖。太祖在母腹中十三个月，诞辰之夜，母后甚危。族人奉命在雁门购药，遇神人指示，率部人披甲持旗，击鼓鸣钲，跃马大噪，绕所居三周而止。果然如神人所教而生。是日，红光【或作虹】照耀室内，白气充盈庭院，井水突然溢出。及至能言，喜谈军旅之事。年十二三，能连射双鸟，至于树叶、针锋、马鞭皆能命中。曾于新城北以酒祭毗沙门塑像，请求与仆交谈，天王披甲持矛，隐隐出现在壁间或所居帐内，时如火聚，如有龙形，人皆异之。尝随献祖征讨庞勋，军阵出没如神，号为飞虎子。眇一目，时号独眼龙，功业磊落，不可尽述【或云睛邪，非眇也】。

    亲王拜蕃侯

    唐干宁年间，凤翔李茂贞、华州韩建、邠州王行瑜拥兵胁君，诛戮宰辅，焚烧宫阙。初，帝西幸凤翔，昭宗出居石门莎城。太原克用领蕃汉兵马入京，三镇大惧。是年，破邠州，斩王行瑜。昭宗嘉奖倚赖，命延王丕、丹王允赍诏赐李公衣服，兼令二亲王设拜，以兄事之，近古未有也。仍封晋王以宠之。延王才识过人，聪悟辩慧，在晋阳留宴累月，每献酬乐作，必为晋王起舞。后为韩建所杀。

    李习吉溺黄河
    　　太原李克用自渭北班师次河西县王珂于冰上搆浮航公渡浮航马足陷桥李习吉从马轶坠河习吉抱冰舟人拯之获免王珂惧公谓曰公之于吾非机桥者何嫌之有李谏议有闻于时则不吾知也置酒笑乐而罢习吉右相林甫之后应举不第黄巢后游于河东摄榆次令李公辟为掌记牋檄之捷无出其右梁祖每读河东书檄嘉叹其才顾敬翔曰李公计絶一隅何幸有此人如鄙夫之智算得习吉之才笔如虎之得翼也其见重如此
    　　周式抗梁祖
    　　梁祖陷邢州军攻王镕于常山赵之賔佐有周式者性慷慨有口才谓王镕曰事急矣速决所向式愿为行人即出见之梁祖曰王公朋附并汾违盟爽信赋已及于此期于无舍式曰明公为唐室之桓文当以礼义而成霸业王氏今降心纳质愿脩旧好明公乃欲穷兵黩武残灭同盟天下其谓公何梁祖笑引式袂谓之曰与公戏耳镕即送牛酒币货数万犒汴军仍令其子入质于汴因而解围近代之鲁仲连也

    Explanation

    212

    Li Xi Ji Fell into the Yellow River
    　　Li Keyong of Taiyuan, after returning from a campaign in the north of the Wei River, stopped at Xixian County. Wang Ke constructed a floating bridge on the ice for public use, but the horses' hooves caused the bridge to sink. Li Xi Ji fell from his horse into the river. Li Xi Ji clung to the ice, and the boatman rescued him, saving his life. Wang Ke, fearing Li Keyong, said to him, "Your relationship with me is not one of mutual support. What reason do you have to doubt me?" Li Xi Ji, known for his reputation, was not recognized by Li Keyong. They drank wine and laughed, then parted ways. Li Xi Ji was the descendant of the Right Chancellor Li Linfu, who failed the imperial examinations. After the rebellion of Huang Chao, he traveled in Hedong and was temporarily appointed as the magistrate of Yuci. Li Keyong appointed him to write official documents, and his skill was unmatched. Zhu Wen often praised his talent when reading the official documents from Hedong. He told Gu Jingxiang, "Li Gong is isolated in one corner of the map. How fortunate it is to have such a person! With his intelligence and strategy, combined with Li Xi Ji's literary talent, it is like a tiger with wings. He is greatly esteemed."
    　　Zhou Shi Resisted Zhu Wen
    　　Zhu Wen captured Xing Prefecture and attacked Wang Rong in Changshan. Among Wang Rong's advisors was Zhou Shi, who was bold and eloquent. He said to Wang Rong, "The situation is urgent. Make a quick decision on where to go. I am willing to go as an envoy." Zhou Shi went out to meet Zhu Wen. Zhu Wen said, "Prince Wang has allied with Bing and Fen and violated our alliance. His taxes are already due, and we have no choice but to continue the campaign." Zhou Shi replied, "Your Excellency is the Han dynasty's version of Duke Huan and Duke Wen. You should establish your hegemony through propriety and righteousness. Prince Wang now humbles himself and sends his son as a hostage, hoping to renew old friendships. Why do you want to exhaust your troops and destroy your allies? What will people say about you?" Zhu Wen laughed and took Zhou Shi's sleeve, saying, "I was just joking with you." Wang Rong immediately sent oxen, wine, and gifts worth tens of thousands of coins to reward Zhu Wen's army and ordered his son to be sent as a hostage to Bian, thus lifting the siege. Zhou Shi was compared to Lu Zhonglian of modern times.

    213

    宦官隂谋
    　　唐昭宗以宦官怙权骄恣难制常有诛翦之意宰相崔允嫉忌尤甚上勅允凡有密奏当进囊封勿于便殿啓奏以是宦者不之察韩全诲等乃访京城美妇人数十以进求宫中隂事天子不之悟允谋渐泄中官以重赂甘言请藩臣以为城社视崔允眦裂时因伏腊防聚则相向流涕辞防诀别防汴人冦同华知崔允之谋于是韩全诲引禁军陈伏兵逼帝幸凤翔他日崔允与梁祖叶谋以诛阉宦未久祸亦及之庚午絶灭识者归罪于崔允先是其季父安潜甞谓亲知曰灭吾族者必缁儿也缁儿即允小字河东晋王李克用闻允所为谓賔友曰助贼为虐者其崔允乎破国亡家必在此人也

    Explanation

    213

    Eunuch Conspiracy

    Emperor Zhaozong of Tang, due to the eunuchs' arrogance and indulgence in power, often harbored thoughts of exterminating them. The chancellor Cui Yun, who was particularly envious and resentful of them, was ordered by the emperor to submit all confidential reports sealed in a bag, without presenting them in the secondary palace. As a result, the eunuchs did not notice this instruction. Han Quanwei and others then sought to gather information about palace secrets by bringing dozens of beautiful women from the capital to the emperor. The emperor, however, did not realize the true intentions behind these actions. Cui Yun's plans gradually became known, and the eunuchs used heavy bribes and sweet words to persuade the regional lords to support them, viewing Cui Yun with intense anger. During festivals, the eunuchs would gather and cry together, bidding farewell to each other. Kou Tonghua, a person from Kaifeng, became aware of Cui Yun's plans, and Han Quanwei led the imperial guards to force the emperor to seek refuge in Fengxiang. Later, Cui Yun and Zhu Wen, the founder of the Later Liang dynasty, conspired to eliminate the eunuchs. However, the consequences of their actions soon caught up with them. On the day of Gengwu, the eunuchs were completely destroyed. Those who understood the situation blamed Cui Yun for the events. Prior to this, Cui Yun's younger uncle, An Qian, had once told close friends, "The one who will destroy our family is Zi'er," as "Zi'er" was a nickname for Cui Yun. Li Keyong, the Prince of Hedong, upon learning of Cui Yun's actions, said to his guests and friends, "The one who is helping the wicked do evil is Cui Yun. The destruction of the country and the ruin of families must be caused by this person."

    214

    晋王上源驿遇难
    　　晋王李克用妻刘夫人常随军行至于军机多所宏益先是汴州上源驿有变晋王愤恨欲回军攻之夫人曰公为国讨贼而以杯酒私忿必若攻城即曲在于我不如回师自有朝廷可以论列于是班退天复中周徳威为汴军所败三军溃散汴军乗我晋王危惧与周徳威议欲出保云州夫人曰存信本北方牧羊儿也焉顾成败王常笑王行瑜弃城失势被人屠割今复欲效之何也王顷嵗避难达靼防遭陷害赖遇朝廷多事方得复归今一旦出城便有不测之变焉能逺及此晋王止行居数日亡散之士复集军城安定夫人之力也

    Explanation

    214

    The Jin Prince Li Keyong's wife, Lady Liu, often accompanied him on military campaigns, where she had significant influence and benefits in military affairs. Prior to this, at the Shangyuan Inn in Bianzhou, an incident occurred that deeply troubled the Jin Prince. He was furious and wanted to retreat and attack them. Lady Liu said, "Your mission is to fight for the country, and now you want to attack due to a personal grudge. If you were to attack the city, the fault would lie with us. It would be better to withdraw and let the imperial court handle the matter." Thus, the troops withdrew. During the Tiānfù period, General Zhou Dewei was defeated by the enemy forces, and the army was in disarray. The Jin Prince was in a state of panic and discussed with Zhou Dewei the possibility of retreating to Yunzhou for safety. Lady Liu said, "Cunxin was originally a shepherd boy from the north; how could he care about success or failure? The Jin Prince often laughed at Wang Xingyu, who lost his power and status and was humiliated by others. Now, he wants to follow his example. How far can he go? The Jin Prince had fled to the Dàdá tribe to escape danger a few years ago and narrowly escaped being harmed by them. Now, if he were to leave the city, there would be unforeseen dangers. How could he expect to achieve much?" The Jin Prince stopped his plans. After several days, the scattered soldiers returned, and the city was stabilized. This was due to Lady Liu's efforts.

    刘鄩忠于旧主
    　　王师范之镇青州以部将刘鄩窃据兖州先是汴将葛从周镇于是因出征刘鄩将图兖也诈为茶商苞苴铠甲大起店肆剖巨木藏兵伏而入窃发之日得其徒千人据其府舍升堂拜从周之母仍以礼待其妻子子弟职掌妻孥供亿如常俄而从周攻其城梯防云合鄩以板舆请从周母登城谕从周曰刘将军待我不异于儿新妇已下并不失所从周在城下歔欷即时退舍及青州兵败师范纳欵梁祖遣使谕鄩鄩曰臣知王公脩好与梁国通盟但臣本受王公之命保有州城一旦见其势穷擅命不顾非尽心于所事也仆俟王公之命俛首非晩至是师范谕之方以城归梁祖多其义超擢非次官至方镇为梁之名将

    Explanation

    215

    Liu Xun's Loyalty to His Former Master
    Wang Shifan, when he was stationed in Qingzhou, had his subordinate general Liu Xun seize control of Yanzhou. Previously, the Bian general Ge Congzhou was stationed there. Taking advantage of Ge Congzhou's departure on a campaign, Liu Xun planned to take over Yanzhou. He disguised himself as a tea merchant, packaged armor, and built large shops, carving out large trees to hide soldiers. He then stealthily entered and gathered a thousand followers, taking control of the government offices. He ascended the hall to pay respects to Ge Congzhou's mother, still treating his wife, children, and descendants with propriety, and providing supplies as usual. Soon, Ge Congzhou attacked the city with a cloud of ladders and defenses. Liu Xun used a sedan chair to bring Ge Congzhou's mother to the city wall to persuade Ge Congzhou, saying, "General Liu treats me no differently than a son. His wife and concubines have not been deprived of their rightful places." Ge Congzhou, moved by emotion, withdrew his camp immediately. When the Qingzhou forces were defeated, Wang Shifan surrendered, and Liang Ancestor sent an envoy to instruct Liu Xun. Liu Xun said, "I know that Lord Wang has cultivated good relations with the Liang state, but I was originally commanded by Lord Wang to protect this state. Once I saw that his situation was dire, I took command without regard, which was not a sign of my full dedication to my duties. I await Lord Wang's command and am not too late to bow." Only then, upon Wang Shifan's instructions, did Liu Xun return the city to Liang Ancestor. Liang Ancestor praised his loyalty and promoted him beyond his rank, making him a famous general of the Liang state.

    駮昭宗諡号
    　　昭宗先諡圣穆景文孝皇帝庙号昭宗起居郎苏楷等駮议请改为恭灵庄闵皇帝庙号襄宗苏楷礼部尚书苏循之子干宁二年应进士楷人才寝陋兼无才行昭宗恶其滥进率先黜落由是怨望专幸国之灾其父循奸邪附防无誉于时故希防茍进梁祖识其险诐滋不悦时为敬翔李振所鄙梁祖建号诏曰苏楷髙贻休萧闻礼皆人才寝陋不可尘汚班行并停见任放归田里苏循可令致仕河朔人士目苏楷为衣冠土枭
    　　晋世子入觐赐鸂酒器
    　　庄宗年十一从晋王讨王行瑜初令入觐献捷昭宗一见骇异之曰此子有竒表乃抚其背曰我儿将来之国栋勿忘忠孝于吾家乃赐鸂酒巵翡翠盘十三读春秋略知大义骑射絶伦其心豁如采録善言听纳容物殆刘聦之比也又云昭宗曰此子可亚其父时人号曰亚子

    Explanation

    216

    Refuting Emperor Zhaozong's Posthumous Name
    Emperor Zhaozong was initially given the posthumous name of "Shengmu Jingwen Xiaohuangdi" and the temple name of "Zhaozong." The court historian Su Kai and others argued against this, proposing that it should be changed to "Gongling Zhuangmin Huangdi" with the temple name "Xiangzong." Su Kai, the son of Su Xun, who served as the Minister of Rites, was a candidate for the imperial examination in the second year of the Ganning era. His talent had declined, and he lacked ability and virtue. Emperor Zhaozong detested his unqualified advancement and led the way in dismissing him, which caused Su Kai to harbor resentment and seek to exploit the country's misfortunes. His father, Su Xun, was known for his deceitful and flattering behavior, earning no reputation in his time. Thus, Su Kai sought advancement through flattery, but Zhu Wen, the founder of the Later Liang Dynasty, recognized his treacherous nature and was displeased with him. At the time, Su Kai was despised by Zhu Wen's advisors, Jing Xiang and Li Zhen. Zhu Wen issued an edict stating, "Su Kai, Gao Yixiu, and Xiao Wenli are all men of declining talent and should not be allowed to soil the ranks of officials. They are hereby removed from their posts and dismissed to return to their hometowns. Su Xun is hereby ordered to retire." The people of the Huai River region referred to Su Kai as a "scholarly local villain."

    The Prince of Jin Visits the Court and Receives a Decorative Wine Vessel
    At the age of eleven, Li Cunxu, the Prince of Jin, accompanied the Prince of Jin to suppress Wang Xingyu. Upon his initial visit to the court to present his success, Emperor Zhaozong was astonished and remarked, "This boy has extraordinary qualities." He then patted Li Cunxu's back and said, "My son will be the pillar of our nation in the future. Do not forget your loyalty and filial piety to our family." He then bestowed upon Li Cunxu a decorative wine vessel shaped like a bird and thirteen jade plates. Li Cunxu read the Spring and Autumn Annals and had a basic understanding of its principles. He was unparalleled in horsemanship and archery, with an open and broad-minded nature. He selected and recorded good words, listened to and accepted others' opinions, almost like Liu Cong. It was also said that Emperor Zhaozong remarked, "This boy can be second to his father," and people referred to him as "the younger son."

    邺王偷江东诗
    　　邺王罗绍威喜文学好儒士每命幕客作四方书檄小不称防壊裂抵弃自劈牋起草下笔成文又癖于七言诗江东有罗隐为钱镠客绍威申南阮之敬隐以所着文章诗赋酬寄绍威大倾慕之乃目其所为诗集曰偷江东今邺中人士多有讽诵
    　　魏博衙军
    　　魏博富雄列侯专地唐朝三百年唯姑息之罗绍威愤衙军制已密闻梁祖表里应接算杀之杨师厚后入魏城揖出罗周翰因而代之师厚卒梁以贺徳伦领镇分其土宇创立相贝为节镇减其力用三军作乱胁持徳伦背梁归晋其状词云屈原哀郢本非怨望之人乐毅辞燕且异倾邪之行晋王览状拥兵亲临先数张彦胁主虐民罪而斩之便以张彦亲军五百人带甲持仗环马而行晋王寛衣缓带略无猜间众心大服他日资魏博兵力称健竟平河南也衙军自罗绍威杀戮后又迫胁贺徳伦复拥兵持赵在礼天成初赴行在于时又杀三千家乃世袭凶恶也

    Explanation

    217

    Translation:

    The Poems of the Prince of Ye Stolen from Jiangdong
    　　The Prince of Ye, Luo Shao Wei, was fond of literature and respected scholars. He often tasked his attendants with drafting letters and edicts for various regions, and if they were not satisfactory, he would tear them up and discard them, sometimes even tearing the paper himself to start anew. He also had a particular fondness for seven-character poems. In Jiangdong, there was Luo Yin, who served under Qian Liu. Luo Shao Wei expressed his respect for Luo Yin, who reciprocated by sending him his writings and poems. Luo Shao Wei greatly admired Luo Yin and named his collection of poems "Stolen from Jiangdong." Today, many people in Ye often recite these poems.

    The Military Forces of Wei and Bo
    　　Wei and Bo were wealthy and powerful, with their own territories. For three hundred years during the Tang dynasty, they were only tolerated. Luo Shao Wei was furious with the military forces and secretly informed the founder of the Later Liang about their plans, leading to their extermination. After Yang Shihou entered the city of Wei, he dismissed Luo Zhouhan and took his place. After Yang Shihou's death, the Later Liang appointed He Delun to lead the region, dividing its territory and establishing new prefectures in Xiang and Bei. This reduced the military's power, leading to a rebellion that forced He Delun to defect to the Later Jin. In his petition, he wrote, "Qu Yuan mourned Ying but was not a man of resentment; Lü Yi left Yan but was not a man of deceit." The Prince of Jin, upon reading this, personally led his troops and first accused Zhang Yan of threatening the ruler and oppressing the people, ordering his execution. He then took five hundred of Zhang Yan's loyal soldiers, fully armed, and rode around the city. The Prince of Jin wore loose clothing and a relaxed belt, showing no suspicion, which greatly impressed the troops. Later, he relied on the military strength of Wei and Bo to conquer Henan, proving their capability. After Luo Shao Wei's massacre, the military forces again pressured He Delun, who once more held his troops, holding Zhao Zai in rebellion. In the early Tiancheng era, they marched to the capital, where they killed another three thousand families, continuing their tradition of violence and cruelty.

    缚驴戴旗
    　　晋王之入魏博刘鄩先屯洹水寂若无人因令觇之云城上有旗帜来往晋王曰刘鄩一步一计未可轻进更令审探果缚刍为人揷【一作缚】旗于上以驴负之循堞而行故旗帜婴城不息问城中羸老者曰军去已二日矣果趋黄泽欲冦太原以霖潦不克进其计谋如是

    　　杨千郎
    　　庄宗异母弟存乂即郭崇韬女壻伏诛先是郭崇韬既诛之后朝野骇惋议论纷然庄宗令阉人察访外事言存乂于诸将坐上诉郭氏之无罪其言怨望又于妖术人杨千郎家饮酒聚防攘臂而泣杨千郎者魏州贱民自言得墨子术于妇翁能役使隂物帽下召食物果实之又蒱博必胜人有拳握之物以法必取又説炼丹干汞易人形破扃鐍贵要间神竒之官至尚书郎赐紫其妻出入宫禁承恩用事皇弟存乂常朋淫于其家至是与存乂同罹其祸

    218

    Tying Up a Donkey and Wearing a Flag

    When the King of Jin, Li Cunxu, advanced into the territory of Liu Xun, who was stationed at Huanshui, the area was completely silent, as if no one was there. He ordered a more thorough investigation and found that the enemy had tied straw into the shape of a person, placed a flag on it, and had a donkey carry it along the battlements, creating the illusion of movement. Li Cunxu remarked, "Liu Xun has a new strategy for every step." He was cautious and ordered further investigation. Indeed, they had tied straw into the shape of a person, placed a flag on it, and had a donkey carry it along the battlements, causing the flags to flutter continuously. When he asked the old and weak people in the city, they said the army had left two days ago. It turned out that Liu Xun was heading towards Huangze, intending to attack Taiyuan, but heavy rain and flooding prevented him from advancing. His strategy was like this.

    The Northern Dream Trivial Talk, Volume Seventeen
    The Complete Library of the Four Treasuries

    The Northern Dream Trivial Talk, Volume Eighteen
    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Yang Qianlang

    After the execution of Guo Chongtao, his son-in-law and younger brother of Emperor Zhuangzong, Cunyi, was also put to death. After Guo Chongtao's execution, the court and the common people were shocked and saddened, and there was much debate. Emperor Zhuangzong ordered eunuchs to investigate external affairs, and they reported that Cunyi had appealed to the generals, claiming the innocence of the Guo family. His words were filled with resentment and anger. He also gathered with a sorcerer named Yang Qianlang, drank and feasted, and cried out in anger. Yang Qianlang was a lowly man from Weizhou who claimed to have learned the techniques of Mozi from his father-in-law. He could summon food and fruits from under his hat and always won in gambling, using a method to take anything he wanted. He also claimed to be able to transform into different forms, break locks, and was a mysterious official in the court, rising to the rank of Langguan and being granted the purple robe. His wife often entered and exited the palace, receiving favors and wielding influence. The younger brother of the emperor, Cunyi, often engaged in debauchery with her. In the end, Cunyi and Yang Qianlang both suffered the same fate.

    娠子能语
    　　后唐明宗皇帝微时随蕃将李存信廵边宿于雁门逆旅逆旅媪方娠帝至媪慢不得具食腹中儿语谓母曰天子至宜速具食声闻于外媪异之遽起亲奉庖爨敬事尤谨帝以媪前倨后恭诘之曰公贵不可言也问其故具道娠子腹语事帝曰老媪逊言惧吾辱耳后果如其言
    　　明宗不伐
    　　明宗始在军中居常唯治兵仗不事生产雄武谦和临财尤廉家财屡空处之晏如也太祖欲试以诚召于泉府命恣意取之所取不过束帛数缗而已所得赐与必分部下战胜凯还侪自伐帝徐言曰人战以口我战以手众皆心服其能

    Explanation

    219

    A Fetus That Could Speak
    Emperor Mingzong of Later Tang, when he was in humble circumstances, accompanied the foreign general Li Cunxin on a border patrol and stayed at an inn in Yanmen Pass. The innkeeper's woman was pregnant, and when the emperor arrived, she was slow and did not prepare food properly. The child in her womb spoke to his mother, saying, "The emperor has arrived; you should prepare food quickly." The voice was heard outside, and the innkeeper was surprised. She hurriedly got up and personally prepared the food, serving with even greater respect and caution. The emperor asked her, saying, "Your guest is of high status; I cannot speak of it." He then asked about the reason and she fully explained the story of the fetus speaking in the womb. The emperor said, "The old woman spoke humbly out of fear that I would insult her." Later, as he said, it turned out to be true.

    Emperor Mingzong did not boast. When he first joined the army, he always focused on military matters and did not engage in production. He was heroic, martial, and humble, especially frugal with money. His family's wealth often ran out, but he remained calm and composed. Emperor Taizu wanted to test his honesty by inviting him to the treasury and allowing him to take whatever he wanted. He only took a few bolts of silk and a few strings of coins. He distributed any rewards or gifts he received among his subordinates. After winning a battle and returning triumphantly, his fellow soldiers boasted. The emperor calmly said, "Others fight with words; I fight with my hands." Everyone inwardly admired his abilities.

    明宗独见
    　　庄宗晏驾明宗皇帝为将相推举霍彦威孔循上言唐运已衰请改国号明宗谓藩邸近侍曰何为改正朔左右奏曰先帝以锡氏宗属为唐雪寃讐为昭宗皇帝后国号唐今朝之旧人不欲殿下称唐请更名号耳明宗泣下曰吾十三事献祖洎太祖至先帝冒刃血战为唐室雪寃身编宗属武皇功业即吾功业也先帝天下即吾天下也兄亡弟绍于意何嫌运之衰隆吾当身受于是不改正朔人服帝之独见也
    　　庄宗诸弟遇害
    　　赵在礼作乱诸将拥明宗入阙未到间从马直郭从谦攻兴教门帝母弟存渥从上战及宫车晏驾存渥与刘皇后同奔太原至风谷为部下所杀刘皇后欲出家为尼旋亦杀之存霸先除北京留守亦自河中至太原兵众请杀存霸以安人心符彦超不能禁时存霸已翦发衣僧衣谒彦超愿为山僧竟不免也存纪存确匿于南山民家人有以报安重诲重诲曰主上已下诏寻访帝之仁徳必不加害不如密防杀之果并命于民家后明宗闻之切让重诲伤惜久之

    Explanation

    220

    Unique Insight of Emperor Mingzong

    When Emperor Zhuangzong passed away, Emperor Mingzong, who was recommended by the generals and ministers, including Huo Yanwei and Kong Xun, was advised to change the dynasty's name due to the decline of the Tang dynasty. Emperor Mingzong told his close attendants in his private quarters, "Why should we change the calendar?" They replied, "The late emperor, being of the Xī clan, avenged the grievances of the Tang dynasty for Emperor Zhaozong. The current dynasty is still known as Tang. However, those who served the previous dynasty do not want Your Majesty to continue using the name 'Tang.' They ask for a new name." Emperor Mingzong wept and said, "I have served thirteen emperors, from the founding emperor to the late emperor, fighting bloodily to avenge the Tang dynasty. I am a member of the Xī clan, and the achievements of the martial emperor are my achievements. The late emperor's realm is my realm. There is no reason for me to be concerned about the succession. The rise and fall of fortune, I must bear it myself." Thus, he did not change the calendar, and people admired his independent judgment.

    The Brothers of Emperor Zhuangzong Met with Tragedy

    When Zhao Zaiyi rebelled, the generals forced Emperor Mingzong to enter the imperial court. Before he arrived, Guo Congqian, the commander of the cavalry, attacked the Xingjiao Gate. Emperor Mingzong's brother, Li Cunwu, fought alongside him. When the imperial carriage passed away, Li Cunwu and Empress Liu fled to Taiyuan. They were killed at Fenggu Valley by their own men. Empress Liu wanted to become a nun, but she was soon killed as well. Li Cunbai, another brother, was appointed as the governor of Beijing but traveled from Hedong to Taiyuan. The soldiers demanded that he be killed to pacify the people, but Fu Yanchao could not prevent it. At the time, Li Cunbai had already cut off his hair and put on monk's robes, seeking Fu Yanchao, wishing to become a mountain monk, but he could not escape his fate. Li Cunjie and Li Cuo hid in the home of a civilian in the southern mountains. Someone reported this to An Zhonghui, who said, "The emperor has already issued a decree to search for them. Your Majesty's benevolence and virtue will not harm them. It would be better to secretly protect them." However, they were both executed in the civilian's home. Later, when Emperor Mingzong heard of this, he severely reprimanded An Zhonghui and grieved for a long time.

    刘皇后笞父
    　　庄宗刘皇后魏州成安人家世寒微太祖攻魏州取成安得后时年五六嵗归晋阳宫为太后侍者教吹笙及笄姿色絶众声伎亦所长太后赐庄宗为韩国夫人侍者后诞皇子继岌宠待日隆他日成安人刘叟诣邺宫见上称夫人之父有内臣刘建丰认之即昔日黄防丈人后之父也刘氏方与嫡夫人争宠皆以门族夸尚刘氏耻为寒家白庄宗曰妾去乡之时妾父死于乱兵是时环尸而哭妾固无父是何田舍翁诈伪及此乃于宫门笞之其实后即叟之长女也庄宗好俳优宫中暇日自负蓍囊药箧令继岌破帽相随似后父刘叟以医卜为业也后方昼眠及造其卧内自称刘衙推访女后大

    Explanation

    221

    Emperor Zhuangzong's Empress Beat Her Father

    Emperor Zhuangzong's Empress Liu was from Cheng'an, Huzhou, a place of humble origins. When the founding emperor attacked Huzhou and took Cheng'an, he obtained her when she was about five or six years old. She was brought back to the Jin Palace, where she served as a maid to the Empress Dowager and learned to play the flute. By the time she reached adulthood, her beauty surpassed all others, and she also excelled in music and performance. The Empress Dowager granted her to Emperor Zhuangzong, and he bestowed upon her the title of Korea Lady. After she bore Emperor Zhuangzong a son named Jiji, her favor grew daily.

    One day, a man from Cheng'an named Liu, who came to the Yeh Palace, claimed to be the father of the Empress. An eunuch named Liu Jianfeng recognized him as the former Yellow Fang's father-in-law, who was also the Empress's father. Liu was competing for favor with the principal wife, both boasting of their noble lineages. Liu was ashamed to be from a poor family and reported to Emperor Zhuangzong, saying, "When I left my hometown, my father died in the chaos of war. At that time, I surrounded his body and wept. How can this farmer deceive me now?" She then had him beaten at the palace gate. In fact, she was the eldest daughter of the old man.

    Emperor Zhuangzong enjoyed jesters and comedians. During leisure times in the palace, he would carry a bag of divination tools and a medicine box, letting Jiji follow with a tattered hat, resembling her father, Liu, who made a living as a doctor and fortune-teller. One day, the Empress was taking a nap during the day. Someone entered her bedroom and introduced himself as Liu, the district commissioner, looking for his daughter. The Empress was very angry.

    222

    恚笞继岌然为太后不礼复以韩夫人居正无以发明大臣希防请册刘氏为皇后议者以后出于寒贱好兴利聚财初在邺都令人设法禆贩所鬻樵苏果茹亦以皇后为名正位之后凡贡奉先入后宫唯写佛经施尼师他无所赐阙下诸军困乏以至妻子饿殍宰相请出内库俵给后将出妆具银盆两口皇子满喜等三人令鬻以赡军一旦作乱亡国灭族与夫褒姒妲己无异也先是庄宗自为俳优名曰李天下杂于涂粉獶杂之间时为诸优朴扶掴搭竟为嚚妇恩伶之倾玷有国者得不以为前鉴刘后以囊盛金合犀带四欲于太原造寺为尼防路复通皇弟存渥同箦而寝明宗闻其即令自杀

    Explanation

    222

    In anger, he beat Jiji to the point of near-death, and treated the Empress Dowager disrespectfully. Because Lady Han was the legitimate wife, the ministers could not justify making Liu a queen. Those who debated the matter argued that Liu came from a lowly background and favored accumulating wealth. Initially in the capital city of Ye, she made people devise methods to supplement their income by selling various goods, also using the name of the queen. After assuming the position, all tributes first entered the inner palace, and only Buddhist scriptures were given to nuns. The troops under the palace were in dire straits, and even their wives and children were starving. The prime minister requested to distribute from the imperial treasury, and the queen will give out two silver basins as part of her dowry, and the princes Manxi and others three are ordered to sell them to support the army. One day, causing chaos, leading to the destruction of the country and the clan, no different from Bo Si and Da Ji. Previously, Emperor Zhuangzong made himself a clown or jester, naming himself Li Tianxia, mixed among the painted and messy, sometimes acting as a clown, being slapped and hugged, and finally becoming a foolish woman, corrupting the favoring of clowns, and those in power should take this as a warning. Empress Liu, with a bag containing four sets of gold and rhinoceros leather belts, intended to build a temple in Taiyuan to become a nun, preventing the road from reopening, and the royal brother Cunwo slept on the same bed. Emperor Mingzong heard about it and ordered her to commit suicide.

    223

    明宗诛诸凶
    　　明宗即位之初诛租庸使孔谦归徳军节度使元行钦邓州节度温韬太子少保段凝汴州麴务辛庭蔚李继宣等孔谦者魏州孔目吏庄宗图霸以供馈兵食谦有力焉既为租庸使曲事嬖幸夺宰相权专以聚敛为意剥削为端以犯众怒伏诛元行钦为庄宗爱将出入宫禁曽无间隔害明宗之子从璟以是伏诛段凝事梁以奸佞进身至节将末年绾军权束手归朝温韬凶恶发掘西京

    Explanation

    223

    In the early days of Emperor Mingzong's reign, he executed several notorious officials. Among them were Kong Qian, the Commissioner of Rent and Labor; Yuan Xingqin, the Governor of the Guiwei Circuit; Wen Tao, the Governor of the Dengzhou Circuit; Duan Ning, the Grand Tutor to the Crown Prince; and Xin Tingwei, the official in charge of wine affairs in Bianzhou. Kong Qian, originally a clerk in the administrative office of Weizhou, had played a significant role in supporting Prince Zhuangzong's ambitions to become a hegemon by providing military rations. After becoming the Commissioner of Rent and Labor, he flattered the emperor's favorites, usurped the power of the chancellor, and focused solely on accumulating wealth, making exploitation the norm, which ultimately led to his execution. Yuan Xingqin, a favored general of Prince Zhuangzong, had unrestricted access to the palace and was implicated in harming Emperor Mingzong's son, Congjing, leading to his own execution. Duan Ning, who served the Later Liang dynasty through deceit and flattery, rose to the rank of a high-ranking military official but eventually surrendered to the Later Tang dynasty. Wen Tao, known for his cruelty and wickedness, was notorious for excavating the Western Capital, Chang'an.

    224

    陵寝庄宗中兴不寘其罪厚赂伶官阉人与段凝皆赐国姓或拥旄明宗采众议而诛之辛庭蔚开封尹王瓒之牙将也朱友贞时廷蔚依瓒势曲法乱政汴人恶之李继宣汴将孟审澄之子亡命归庄宗刘皇后蓄为子时宫掖之间声流闻此四凶帝在藩邸时恶其为人故废罢之庄宗皇帝为唐雪耻号为中兴而温韬毁发诸帝寝陵宜加大辟而赐国姓付节旄由是知中兴之説谬矣
    　　韩伊二妃【夏夫人附】
    　　庄宗皇帝嫡夫人韩氏后为淑妃伊氏为徳妃契丹入中原石氏乞降宰相冯道尊册契丹主大张宴席其国母后妃列坐同宴王嫱蔡姬之比也夫人夏氏最承恩宠后嫁契丹托云名李賛华所谓东丹王即安巴坚长子先归朝后除滑州节度使性酷毒侍婢微过即以刀刲火灼夏氏少长宫掖不忍其凶求离婚归河阳节度夏鲁竒家今为尼也

    Explanation

    224

    The tomb of Emperor Zhuangzong, despite his role in the revival of the Tang dynasty, was not punished for his sins. Instead, he generously rewarded entertainers, eunuchs, and others, including bestowing the imperial surname. Some held banners and standards, symbolizing authority or command. Emperor Mingzong took public opinion into account and punished accordingly. Xin Tingwei, a subordinate officer under Wang Zan, the governor of Kaifeng, abused power and law during Zhu Youzhen's reign due to his reliance on Wang Zan's influence. The people of Bian (Kaifeng) disliked him. Li Jixuan, the son of Meng Shencheng, a general in Bian, fled to Emperor Zhuangzong. Empress Liu adopted him as her son, and rumors circulated about their relationship. These four notorious figures were disliked by the emperor when he was still a prince, leading to their dismissal. Emperor Zhuangzong restored the Tang dynasty's honor and was hailed as the reviver, but Wen Tao destroyed the tombs of various emperors, and they should be punished severely, including execution and the loss of their titles. This reveals that the notion of the Tang revival is flawed.

    The consorts Han and Yi, with an additional note about Xia, were introduced. Empress Han became a consort after being the emperor's principal wife, and Yi became a consort. When the Khitan entered Central China, the Shi family surrendered, and Chancellor Feng Dao honored the Khitan leader with a grand banquet. The Khitan leader's mother and consorts sat together at the banquet, compared to historical figures known for their beauty. Consort Xia, who was highly favored, later married into the Khitan and took the name Li Zanhua. The so-called Prince of Dongdan was the eldest son of Anba Jian, who first returned to the court and later became the governor of Huazhou. He was cruel, punishing even minor offenses with severe punishments. Consort Xia, who grew up in the palace, could not tolerate his cruelty and sought a divorce, returning to the home of Xia Luqi in Heyang, where she now lives as a nun.

    225

    无官酬勲
    　　乱离以来官爵过滥封王作辅狗尾续貂天成初桂州节度观察使马尔即湖南马殷之弟本无功徳品秩已髙制词云尔名尊四辅位冠三师既非品秩升迁难以井田増益此要语也议者以名器假人至此贾谊所以长叹息也
    　　明宗命相
    　　明宗入朝安重诲用事取谋于孔循旧相豆卢革韦説出官孔循不欲以河朔人入相极荐崔协而任圜力争之云崔协者少识文字时人呼为无字碑有李琪者学际天人奕代轩冕论才校艺可敌时辈百人谗夫巧沮忌害其能必舍李琪而相崔协如弃苏合之丸取蛣蜣之转也重诲笑而止然以孔循故终相之帝曰冯书记先帝判官与物无竞可以相矣由是道与协并命而舍李琪识者惜之
    　　明宗睿相
    　　明宗遣皇子从荣出镇邺都或一日上谓安重诲曰从荣左右有诈宣朕令防不接儒生儒生多懦恐钝志相染朕方知之颇骇其事今此皇子方幼出临大藩故选儒雅赖其禆佐今闻此奸险岂朕之所望也鞫其言者将戮之重诲曰若遽行刑又虑賔从闻后稍难安处且望严戒遂止

    Explanation

    225

    No official post to reward merit.
    Since the time of chaos and disorder, titles and positions have been excessively awarded, likening it to attaching a dog's tail to a precious fur coat. In the early Tiansheng period, the Governor of Guizhou, Ma Er, who is the brother of Ma Yin from Hunan, holds a high rank despite his lack of merit. The imperial decree states that he is one of the four assistants and ranks above the three teachers. This is not a promotion in rank but a difficult situation to manage. This is a key point. Critics argue that the bestowal of titles and honors has become so casual that it leads to the kind of lamentation expressed by Jia Yi.

    Emperor Ming ordered the appointment of a chancellor.
    Emperor Ming entered the capital, and An Zhonghui wielded power, seeking advice from Kong Xun. The former chancellors Doulu Ge and Wei Shuo were removed. Kong Xun did not want a person from the Huai River region to be appointed as chancellor, and he strongly recommended Cui Xie. However, Ren Yuan argued against this, saying that Cui Xie, though somewhat literate, was often called the "wordless stele" by contemporaries. There was also Li Qi, who was highly talented and could rival a hundred of his contemporaries in learning and artistry. Adversaries skillfully obstructed and envied his abilities, and it was decided to appoint Cui Xie instead of Li Qi, as if discarding a precious perfume and choosing a dung beetle's dung. An Zhonghui laughed and stopped, but because of Kong Xun, the appointment was finalized. The emperor said, "Feng Ji, the former judge of the late emperor, is impartial and can be made chancellor." Thus, Dao and Cui Xie were appointed together, while Li Qi was passed over, and those who understood the situation lamented this.

    Emperor Ming's wise chancellor.
    Emperor Ming sent his son Cui Rong to govern Yedu. One day, the emperor told An Zhonghui, "There are false orders circulating around Cui Rong, claiming to be from me. He does not receive the advice of Confucian scholars, who are generally timid and might dull his resolve. I only recently learned of this and am greatly alarmed. Now that this young prince is governing a major province, I have selected learned and refined individuals to assist him. How could I have expected such treachery? I will punish those who spread these false orders. An Zhonghui said, "If we execute them immediately, we may also alarm the guests and followers, making it difficult to maintain stability. Instead, let us strictly warn them." The emperor agreed.

    226

    明宗恶贪吏
    　　明宗皇帝尤恶贪货邓州留后陶玘为内乡县令成归仁所论税外科配贬岚州司马掌书记王惟吉夺歴任告勅配绥州长流百姓亳州刺史李邺以赃赐自尽面戒汝州刺史苌蕳为其贪暴汴州仓吏犯赃内有史彦珣旧将之子又是驸马石敬瑭亲戚王建立奏之希免死上曰王法无私岂可徇亲由是皆就戮
    　　诛不孝
    　　缑氏县令裴彦文事母不谨诛之襄邑人周威父为人所杀不雪父寃有状和解明宗降勅赐死
    　　安重诲枉杀任圜
    　　任圜昆弟五人曰圜圆图回团雍穆有裕风采俱异圜美姿容有口辩负筹略平蜀后除黔南不行天成初入相简拔贤俊杜絶幸门忧国如家切于功名而安重诲忌之常防于私第有妓善歌重诲求之不得嫌隙渐深俄罢三司除太子太保归磁州致仕因朱守殷作乱立遣人称制害之受命之日神气不挠中外寃痛清泰中赠右仆射

    Explanation

    226

    Emperor Mingzong particularly detested corrupt officials. During his reign, Tao Qi, the acting governor of Dengzhou, was accused by Cheng Guiren, the magistrate of Neixiang County, for imposing excessive taxes and levies. As a result, Tao Qi was demoted to the position of司马in Lanzhou. Wang Weiji, the chief secretary, was stripped of his previous titles and appointed to a long-term exile in Suizhou. Li Ye, the governor of Bozhou, was granted the right to commit suicide due to corruption. Chang Yan, the governor of Ruzhou, was directly warned by the emperor for his greed and brutality. In Bianzhou, a corrupt official was reported by Wang Jianli, a relative of Princess Shi Yinxun (who was also a former general and the father-in-law of Prince Shi Jingtao), hoping for a lenient punishment. The emperor said, "The law is impartial; how can it be bent for personal favor? Therefore, they were all executed."

    The emperor punished those guilty of filial impiety. Pei Yanwen, the magistrate of Goushi County, was executed for failing to care for his mother properly. Zhou Wei, a person from Xiangyi, was executed for not seeking justice for his father's murder, despite having evidence and a peaceful resolution.

    An Zhonghui unjustly killed Ren Yuan. Ren Yuan had five brothers: Yuan, Yuan, Tu, Hui, and Yong. They were all distinguished in appearance and personality. Ren Yuan was handsome, eloquent, and skilled in strategic planning. After pacifying Shu, he was appointed to govern Qiannan but did not take up the post. In the early Tiancheng era, he entered the imperial court and began to select and promote talented officials, cutting off the paths of favoritism. He was deeply concerned about the state as if it were his own family, driven by a strong sense of duty and ambition. However, An Zhonghui envied him and often kept him at his private residence. An Zhonghui had a beautiful courtesan who sang well, and he could not obtain her favor. This led to growing resentment between them. Soon after, Ren Yuan was dismissed from his post as head of the Three Departments and appointed as Grand Tutor to the Crown Prince, retiring to Cizhou. When Zhu Shouyin rebelled, Ren Yuan was immediately sent to deal with the situation. On the day he received his orders, he remained calm and composed, causing great sorrow among the people. In the Qingtai era, he was posthumously awarded the title of Right Chancellor.
