    北梦琐言卷十八
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷十九
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　玉界尺
    　　太傅致仕赵光逢仕唐及梁薨于天成中文学徳行风神秀异号曰玉界尺敭歴台省入翰林御史中丞梁时同平章事时以两登廊庙四退丘园百行五常不欺暗室缙绅仰之
    　　周元豹
    　　周元豹燕人少为僧其师有知人之鉴从游十年不惮辛苦遂传其秘还乡归俗卢澄为道士与同志三人谒之元豹退谓人曰适二君子明年花发俱为故人唯彼道士他年甚贵来嵗二人果睹零落卢果登庸后归晋阳张承业犹重之言事多中承业俾明宗易衣列于诸校之下以他人请之曰此非也元豹指明宗于末坐曰骨法非常此为内衙太保乎或问前程唯云末后为镇帅明

    Explanation

    227

    Trivial Talk of the North Dream, Volume Eighteen
    　　Imperially Approved Four Treasuries
    Trivial Talk of the North Dream, Volume Nineteen
    　　Tang Dynasty, compiled by Sun Guangxian

    The Jade Ruler
    The retired Grand Tutor Zhao Guangfeng served in the Tang and Later Liang dynasties and passed away in Tiancheng. Renowned for his literary talent, moral integrity, and distinguished demeanor, he was known as the "Jade Ruler." He held high-ranking positions in the central government, served in the Hanlin Academy, and was the Imperial Censor. During the Later Liang period, he was a co-participant in state affairs, having twice served in the highest government offices and retired four times to private life. Adhering to the tenets of Confucian ethics, he was honest even in private, earning the respect of officials and scholars.

    Zhou Yuanbao
    Zhou Yuanbao, a native of Yan, was a young monk whose master had the ability to discern people's character. He spent ten years in close association with the master, enduring hardships without hesitation, and eventually transmitted the master's secret teachings. Returning to his hometown, he resumed secular life. Lu Cheng became a Taoist priest and, along with three like-minded individuals, sought out Zhou Yuanbao. Later, Zhou Yuanbao told someone, "The two gentlemen will bloom next year and both will be dead. Only that Taoist priest will be very esteemed in the future." The following year, the two men indeed saw their decline, while Lu Cheng rose to prominence. Later, Zhou Yuanbao returned to Jin Yang. Zhang Chengye still held him in high regard, and his predictions were often accurate. Zhang Chengye made Emperor Mingzong change clothes and stand among the lower-ranking officers, saying to others, "This is not right." Zhou Yuanbao pointed to Emperor Mingzong in the last seat and said, "His bone structure is unusual; this is the Grand Tutor of the Inner Court." Someone asked about his future, and he only said he would be a military governor in the end.

    228

    宗夏皇后方事巾栉有时忤防大犯槚楚元豹曰此人有藩侯夫人之相当生贵子其言果验凡言吉凶莫不神中事多不载明宗自镇帅入纂谓侍臣曰周元豹昔曽言朕事诸有征可诏北京津置赴阙赵凤曰许之事元豹所长若诏至辇下即争问吉凶恐近于妖惑乃令就赐金帛官至光禄卿年八十而终【又闻尝与蜀髙祖预説符命嗣主至于云龙将相其言无不符验果异乎哉】
    　　老益贪
    　　礼部尚书崔贻孙年过八十求进不休囊槖之资素有贮积性好干人喜得小惠左降之后二子争财甘防医药咸不供侍书责其子曰生有明君真宰死有天曹地府无为老朽岂放尔邪为缙绅之笑端
    　　解元进诗
    　　道士解元本西蜀节将下军校明宗入纂言自西来对于便殿诗歌圣徳自称太白山正一道士上表乞西都留守兼三州【一作川】制置使要脩西京宫阙上谓侍臣曰此老耄自逺来朝此期别有异见乃为身名甚切堪笑也时号知白先生赐紫斯乃狂妄人也

    Explanation

    228

    During the reign of Emperor Zong, the Queen Consort of the Western Xia (宗夏皇后) was performing the rituals of a newly married woman (方事巾栉) and occasionally offended (有时忤防), leading to severe punishment (大犯槚楚). Zhou Yuanbao (元豹) once said that this person would give birth to a noble son (此人有藩侯夫人之相当生贵子), and his words came true (其言果验). All predictions about good or bad omens (凡言吉凶) were accurate (莫不神中), but many of these events are not recorded (事多不载). After Emperor Ming (明宗) ascended the throne from his position as a military governor (自镇帅入纂), he told his attendants (谓侍臣曰) that Zhou Yuanbao had once predicted his affairs (周元豹昔曽言朕事), and if there were any signs (诸有征), he could be summoned from Beijing to the capital (可诏北京津置赴阙). Zhao Feng (赵凤) said (曰) that Zhou Yuanbao was particularly skilled in predicting the affairs of Xu (许之事元豹所长), but if he were summoned to the imperial court (若诏至辇下), people might ask about good or bad omens (即争问吉凶), which could be seen as bewitching or deceiving (恐近于妖惑). Therefore, the emperor ordered him to be granted gold and silk (乃令就赐金帛) and appointed him as an official (官至光禄卿), and he died at the age of eighty (年八十而终). It is also said that he once predicted auspicious signs for the founding emperor of Shu (蜀髙祖) and his successor (嗣主), even predicting the rise of high-ranking officials (云龙将相), and all his predictions were accurate (其言无不符验), indeed they were extraordinary (果异乎哉).

    Growing Greed

    The Minister of Rites, Cui Yisun (礼部尚书崔贻孙), was over eighty years old and constantly sought promotion (年过八十求进不休). He had always accumulated wealth (囊槖之资素有贮积) and had a nature of meddling in others' affairs, liking to receive small favors (性好干人喜得小惠). After being demoted (左降之后), his two sons fought over his property (二子争财), and none of them provided support for his medical care (甘防医药咸不供侍). He wrote a letter to his son saying (书责其子曰): "I lived under a wise ruler (生有明君真宰), and I will be judged in the afterlife (死有天曹地府). Do not act like a decrepit old man (无为老朽岂放尔邪)." This became a source of laughter among the literati (为缙绅之笑端).

    Zhou Yuanbao Presents a Poem

    Zhou Yuanbao, a Taoist priest (道士解元龟), was originally a lower-ranking military officer under a military commander in the western part of Shu (本西蜀节将下军校). After Emperor Ming ascended the throne, he said he came from the west (明宗入纂言自西来) and spoke in the private palace (对于便殿), praising the emperor's virtues (诗歌圣德) and calling himself a Taoist priest of Mount Taibai (自称太白山正一道士). He submitted a memorial requesting the position of governor of the western capital (上表乞西都留守) and also serving as the governor of three states (兼三州制置使), with the aim of renovating the palaces of the western capital (要脩西京宫阙). The emperor said to his attendants (上谓侍臣曰): "This old man came from afar to court (此老耄自逺来朝), and at this time he had different views (此期别有异见). He was very concerned about his reputation (乃为身名甚切), which was laughable (堪笑也)." At the time, he was called Mr. Zhi Bai (时号知白先生) and was granted a purple robe (赐紫), but he was a reckless and arrogant person (斯乃狂妄人也).

    229

    击碎舍利
    　　天成中有僧于西国取经回得一佛牙舍利十粒行以程上进其牙大如拳褐溃皴裂赵凤言于执政曰曽闻佛牙锤锻不壊请试之随斧而碎时宫中已施数千闻毁碎方遂摈弃之云云此僧号智明幽州人仆尝识之
    　　崔协对敭
    　　明宗问宰相冯道卢质近日吃酒否对曰质曽到臣居亦饮数爵臣劝不令过度事亦如酒过即患生崔协强言于坐曰臣闻食医心镜酒极好不假药饵足以安心神左右见其肤浅不觉哂之
    　　降龙大师
    　　五台山僧诚慧其徒号为降龙大师镇州大水壊其南城诚慧曰彼无信心吾使一小龙警之自言能【一作飞】役使毒龙故也同光初到阙权贵皆拜之唯郭崇韬知其为人终不设拜京师旱迎至洛下祈雨数旬无征应或以焚燎为闻惧而潜去至寺惭恚而终建塔号法雨大师何其谬也

    Explanation

    229

    Final Translation

    Crushing the Relics
    In the Tiancheng era, a monk returned from the Western Regions with a Buddha's tooth relic and ten particles of relics, which he presented to the emperor through the proper channels. The tooth was as large as a fist and was cracked and worn. Zhao Feng spoke to the prime ministers, saying, "I have heard that Buddha's teeth are indestructible even when hammered. Please try it." Under the axe, it broke. At the time, the palace had already destroyed several thousand relics upon hearing of the destruction, and they were discarded, as they said. This monk was known as Zhi Ming, from Youzhou, and I once knew him.

    Cui Xie's Promotion
    Emperor Mingzong asked the chancellor Feng Dao and Lu Zhi whether they had been drinking recently. Lu Zhi replied, "I once came to your residence and drank several cups. I advised him not to drink excessively." Just like drinking too much leads to problems, Cui Xie forced himself to speak at the meeting, saying, "I have heard that the Shiyi Xinjing (Book of Dietetics and Medicine) says that wine is extremely good and sufficient to calm the mind and spirit without the need for medicine." Those around him found his remarks shallow and could not help but smile.

    Master of Subduing Dragons
    A monk named Cheng Hui, who was known as the Master of Subduing Dragons, was from Mount Wutai. When a flood in Zhending destroyed the southern wall of the city, Cheng Hui said, "Since they lack faith, I will send a small dragon to warn them." He claimed to be able to control venomous dragons. At the beginning of the Tongguang era, he arrived at the imperial court, and the powerful and influential all bowed to him. Only Guo Chongtao knew his character and did not bow. When there was a drought in the capital, they invited him to Luoyang to pray for rain, but after several weeks, there was no response. Some people claimed to have heard the sound of fire and fled secretly. He returned to the temple, feeling ashamed and angry, and eventually died. A pagoda was built to honor him as the Master of the Dharma Rain. How mistaken it was.

    230

    鱼目为舍利
    　　泽州僧洪密请舍利塔洪密以禅宗谜语鼓扇愚俗自云身出舍利曽至太原豪民迎请妇人罗拜洪密既辞妇人于其所坐之处拾得百粒正人验之皆枯鱼之目也将辞云山中要千数番麄氊半日获五百番其惑人如此
    　　姚洪忠烈【夏鲁竒附】
    　　阆州守御指挥使姚洪梁时经事董璋璋将叛频诱洪以大义拒之城陷被擒璋责之洪大骂璋曰老贼孤恩背主吾于尔何恩而云相负尔为李七郎奴扫马粪得一脔残炙感恩无尽今天子付以茅土结党反噬尔本奴才即无耻吾忠义之士不忍为也璋怒令十人持刀割其肤然镬于前自取啗食洪至死大骂不已明宗闻之泣下置洪二子于近卫给赐颇优于时夏鲁竒守遂州城破自刎而死并为忠烈也

    Explanation

    230

    Fish Eyes as Relics
    A monk from Zezhou named Hong Mi requested a stupa for relics. Hong Mi used Zen riddles to deceive the ignorant masses, claiming that he had produced relics from his body and had once visited Taiyuan, where wealthy civilians welcomed him and women knelt in worship. After Hong Mi left, the women picked up a hundred grains at the place where he had sat, which were later verified by reputable individuals to be dried fish eyes. Hong Mi claimed that he needed a thousand grains, and within half a day, he collected five hundred grains, thus deceiving people in this manner.

    Gracious Loyalty of Yao Hong [with Xia Luqi]
    Yao Hong, a commander of defense in Langzhou, served under Dong Zhang during the Later Liang period. When Dong Zhang planned to rebel, he frequently tried to persuade Yao Hong with appeals to righteousness, but Yao Hong refused. When the city fell and Yao Hong was captured, Dong Zhang scolded him, and Yao Hong shouted loudly. Dong Zhang said, "Old traitor, you have betrayed your benefactor. What gratitude do I owe you? I was a slave to Li Qilang, sweeping horse dung and receiving a small piece of roasted meat, which I was grateful for. Now the emperor has given me territory, and you form a clique and turn against me. You are a slave and have no shame. I, a loyal and valiant man, cannot do such a thing." Enraged, Dong Zhang ordered ten men to cut Yao Hong's skin and boil a cauldron in front of him, then took pieces of Yao Hong's flesh to eat. Yao Hong continued to shout loudly until his death. Emperor Mingzong heard of this and wept, placing Yao Hong's two sons in the imperial guard and granting them favors and rewards better than usual. Xia Luqi, who defended Suizhou, committed suicide by cutting his throat when the city fell, and both were hailed as loyal and valiant.

    231

    座主门生同入翰林
    　　封舜卿梁时知贡举后门生郑致雍同受命入翰林为学士致雍有俊才舜卿才思拙涩及试五题不胜困因托致雍秉笔当时议者以为座主辱门生同光初致仕
    　　戏萧希甫
    　　萧希甫进士及第有文才口辩多机数梁时不得意弃母妻渡河易姓名为皇甫教书庄宗即位于魏州征希甫知制诰庄宗平汴洛希甫奉诏宣慰青齐方知其母死妻嫁乃持服于魏州时议者戏引李陵书云老母终堂生妻去帷后为谏议大夫性褊忿躁于进取疏宰相豆卢革韦説至于贬死又以毁訾宰臣责授岚州司马
    　　明宗奬冯道
    　　明宗谓侍臣曰冯道纯俭顷在徳胜寨所居一茅庵与从人同器而食卧则刍藳一束其心晏如及以父忧退归乡里自耕耘樵采与农夫杂处不以素贵介懐真士大夫也

    Explanation

    231

    Final Translation

    The Chief Examiner and His Disciple Both Enter the Hanlin Academy

    After Feng Shunqing served as the chief examiner during the Liang dynasty, his disciple Zheng Zhiyong was also appointed to the Hanlin Academy as a scholar. Zheng Zhiyong possessed remarkable talent, while Feng Shunqing's thoughts were slow and clumsy. When he was tasked with composing five essays, he found himself overwhelmed by the difficulty and, unable to cope, entrusted Zheng Zhiyong to write them on his behalf. At the time, critics believed that the chief examiner had disgraced himself by relying on his disciple. In the early years of the Tongguang era, Feng Shunqing retired from office.

    Playful Incident Involving Xiao Xifu

    Xiao Xifu, after passing the imperial examinations and becoming a Jinshi, was known for his literary talent and eloquence. He was also cunning and resourceful. During the Liang dynasty, when he was not favored, he abandoned his mother and wife, crossed the river, changed his name to Huangfu, and became a teacher. When Emperor Zhuangzong established his rule in Wei Prefecture, he summoned Xiao Xifu to serve as the official responsible for drafting imperial edicts. After Zhuangzong conquered Bian and Luo, Xiao Xifu was sent to comfort the regions of Qing and Qi. It was then that he learned his mother had died and his wife had remarried. He observed mourning in Wei Prefecture. At the time, critics playfully quoted a line from Li Ling's letter: "My mother has passed away, and my wife has left the house." Later, Xiao Xifu became a Censorial Adviser, known for his narrow-mindedness, impatience, and eagerness for advancement. He criticized the chancellors Doulu Ge and Wei Shuo, leading to their demotion and eventual death. He was also reprimanded for criticizing the prime minister and was demoted to serve as the magistrate of Lanzhou.

    Emperor Mingzong Commends Feng Dao

    Emperor Mingzong told his court officials, "Feng Dao is simple and thrifty. During his time at the De Sheng Camp, he lived in a thatched hut and ate from the same utensils as his subordinates. When he slept, he lay on a bundle of straw, and his heart remained calm. When he retired to his hometown due to his father's death, he cultivated the land and gathered firewood, mingling with farmers without regard for his former status. He is truly a genuine scholar-official."

    232

    明宗戒秦王
    　　明宗戒秦王重荣曰吾少钟丧乱马上取功名不暇留心经籍在藩邸时见判官论説经义虽不深达其防大约令人开悟今朝廷有正人端士可亲附之庶防有益吾见先皇在藩时爱自作謌诗将家子文非素习未能尽妙讽于人口恐被诸儒窃笑吾老矣不能勉强于此唯书义尚欲耳里频闻时从荣方聚杂进士浮薄之子以歌诗吟咏为事上道此言规讽之或一日秦王进诗上説于俳优敬新磨敬新磨賛美而曰勿讶秦王诗好他阿爷平生爱作诗上大笑
    　　诙谐所累
    　　宰相冯道形神庸陋一旦为丞相士人多窃笑之刘岳与任賛偶语见道行而复顾賛曰新相回顾何也岳曰定是忘持兎园册来道之乡人在朝者闻之告道道因授岳秘书监任賛授散骑常侍北中村墅多以兎园册教童以是讥之然兎园册乃徐庾文体非鄙朴之谈但家藏一本人多贱之也
    　　明宗不乐进马【张防钊附】

    Explanation

    232

    Emperor Mingzhong Admonishes Prince Qin

    Emperor Mingzhong admonished Prince Qin Zhongrong, saying: "When I was young, I was in the midst of chaos and achieved fame on horseback, leaving no time to focus on classical texts. When I was a prince, I saw the judge discuss the meaning of the classics. Although I did not deeply understand it, it generally enlightened me. Now, there are upright and virtuous people in the court who can be befriended; perhaps it will be beneficial. I saw the late emperor, when he was a prince, love to compose songs and poems. A general's son's writing, not cultivated from childhood, cannot be fully refined. If recited by others, it might be secretly laughed at by scholars. I am old and cannot force myself to do it, but I still want to hear the meaning of books frequently. At that time, Prince Zhongrong was gathering various scholars and shallow youths who made poetry and recitation their business. The Emperor spoke these words to admonish him. One day, Prince Qin presented a poem, and the Emperor praised it to the clown Jing Xinmo. Jing Xinmo praised and said, 'Do not be surprised that Prince Qin's poem is good; his grandfather loved to compose poems all his life.' The Emperor laughed greatly."

    "Troubled by humor," the Emperor said.

    Chancellor Feng Dao had an ordinary appearance and spirit. Once he became chancellor, many scholars secretly laughed at him. Liu Yue and Ren Zan happened to be talking when they saw Feng Dao passing by and Ren Zan said, "Why did the new chancellor look back?" Liu Yue replied, "He must have forgotten to bring his Ruyuan book." Feng Dao's fellow townspeople in court heard about it and told him. Feng Dao then appointed Liu Yue as Secretary of the Secretariat and Ren Zan as Attendant of the Imperial Stables. In the northern villages, the Ruyuan book is often used to teach children. Thus, it was used to mock him. However, the Ruyuan book is in the style of Xu and Yu, not crude or vulgar. But because it is a book that many people have at home, it is often looked down upon.

    "Emperor Mingzhong did not enjoy riding horses," [with reference to Zhang Fangzhao].

    233

    泾原帅李金全累歴藩镇所在掊敛非时进马上问其为治如何莫专以进马为事虽黾勉受之圣防不怿张防钊多贪镇沧州日因亢旱民饥发廪赈之方上闻帝甚嘉奬他日秋成倍斗征敛朝论鄙之防钊好与禅毳谜语自云知道心与口背唯利是求只以饭僧更希福利议者以渠于佛上希利愚之甚也后叛入蜀取人产业黩货无厌蜀民怨之或説在蜀问一禅僧云如何是舍利对曰邮置僦居即得舍利清河慙笑而已
    　　康澄章疏
    　　大理少卿康澄长兴中上疏其要云是知国家有不足惧者五深可畏者六勅防褒称之议者曰虽孙伏伽岑文本章疏而澄可与易地而处矣
    　　明宗讽孟鹄
    　　孟鹄自三司勾押官歴许州节度使上曰鹄掌三司防年得至方镇枢密使范延光奏对上曰鹄实干事人以此至方镇争不勉旃上心知其由径忝冒故以此讽也
    　　戮丁延徽
    　　供奉官丁延徽巧事权贵人多拥防监仓犯赃合处极法侍衞使张从賔方便救之上曰食我厚禄偷我仓储期于决死苏秦説吾不得非但卿言竟处死

    Explanation

    233

    The military governor of Jingyuan, Li Jinquan, had repeatedly served in frontier regions, where he oppressedively collected taxes and presented horses at inappropriate times. When asked about his governance, he did not focus solely on presenting horses, but he reluctantly accepted it, which displeased the emperor. Zhang Fangzhao, who was known for his greed, served as the governor of Cangzhou. During a severe drought and famine, he opened the granaries and provided relief. When this was reported to the emperor, the emperor greatly praised him. However, the next year, he imposed heavy taxes and levies, which led to public criticism. Zhang Fangzhao was fond of riddles involving Buddhist monks and their robes, claiming to know the truth, but his heart was at odds with his words, seeking only profit. He was accused of just feeding monks to seek benefits, and people considered him very foolish. Later, he rebelled and fled to Shu, seizing people's property and being corrupt and insatiable, causing resentment among the people of Shu. Someone said he asked a monk in Shu, "What is the essence of the relic?" The monk replied, "To rent a place to stay, you will find the relic." Qinghe was only embarrassed and laughed.

    Kang Cheng, a junior official in the judicial department, submitted a memorial during the Longxing period. The key points of his memorial stated that there are five things the state does not need to fear and six things that are deeply to be feared. The emperor praised him, and some said that although Sun Fuga and Cen Wenben submitted memorials, Kang Cheng could be compared to them in terms of merit.

    Emperor Mingzong criticized Meng Hu, who had risen from a financial officer to the governor of Xu Prefecture. The emperor said, "Meng Hu served in the Three Departments for many years and reached the position of a military governor. When Fan Yanguang responded to the emperor, he said, 'Meng Hu is indeed a capable person who reached this position. Why not strive hard?' The emperor knew that Meng Hu had gained his position through improper means, so he used this as a warning."

    Ding Yanhui, a court official, was skilled in flattering the powerful and often colluded with others to embezzle grain from the granaries. He committed embezzlement and should have been punished severely. The guard commander Zhang Congbin tried to save him, saying, "He enjoys my generous salary while stealing from my granaries, and deserves death." The emperor said, "Su Qin advised me not to do this, not only your words, he was ultimately executed."

    北梦琐言卷十九
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　北梦琐言卷二十
    　　唐　孙光宪　撰
    　　见马抚髀
    　　上问范延光见管马数对曰见管马军三万五千上抚髀叹曰朕从戎四十年太祖在太原时骑军不过七千先皇帝与汴军校战自始至终马数才万今有铁马三万五千不能使九州混一是吾养卒练士将帅之不至也老者马将奈何延光以马数多国力虚耗为言上亦然之
    　　受赂曲法
    　　镇州市人刘方遇家财数十万方遇妻田氏早卒田之妹为尼常出入方遇家方遇使尼长发为继室有田令遵者方遇之妻弟也善货殖方遇以所积财令令遵兴殖也方遇有子年幼二女皆嫁方遇疾卒子幼不能督家业方遇妻及二女以家财素为令遵兴殖乃聚族合谋请以令遵姓刘为方遇继嗣即令鬻劵人安美为亲族请嗣劵书即定乃遣令遵服斩衰居丧而二女初立令遵时先邀每月供财二万及后求取无厌而石李二女夫使二女诣本府论诉云令遵冒姓夺

    Explanation

    234

    Translation

    Random Notes from the North, Volume 19
    　　Qinding Siku Quanshu
    Random Notes from the North, Volume 20
    By Sun Guangxian of the Tang Dynasty

    Seeing Horses and Patting the Thigh
    The emperor asked Fan Yanguang about the number of horses under his command. Fan replied, "There are 35,000 cavalry under my command." The emperor patted his thigh and sighed, "I have served in the military for forty years. When the founding emperor was in Taiyuan, our cavalry did not exceed 7,000. When the late emperor fought against the Bian army, the number of horses was only ten thousand from beginning to end. Now we have 35,000 iron-clad cavalry, yet we cannot unify the nine provinces. This is due to the lack of competent generals and soldiers. What will happen to the old horses?" Fan Yanguang spoke of the excessive number of horses leading to a drain on national resources, and the emperor agreed with him.

    Accepting Bribes and Bending the Law
    In Zhenzhou, there was a man named Liu Fangyu who had a family fortune of several tens of thousands. His wife, Lady Tian, died early, and her sister became a nun and frequently came and went from Liu's home. Liu made the nun grow her hair and marry her as his second wife. Lady Tian's brother, named Tian Lingzun, was skilled in trade and commerce. Liu entrusted his accumulated wealth to Tian Lingzun to manage. Liu had a young son, and his two daughters were married. When Liu died of illness, his young son could not manage the family business. Liu's wife and two daughters used the family wealth to support Tian Lingzun's business. They gathered the family and plotted to have Tian Lingzun adopt the Liu surname and become Liu's heir. They then had the notary An Mei draft the adoption contract, which was finalized. They had Tian Lingzun wear mourning clothes and observe the period of mourning. Initially, the two daughters promised to provide Tian Lingzun with 20,000 units of currency each month. But later, they demanded more and more. The husbands of the two daughters, Shi and Li, sent their wives to the court to file a lawsuit, claiming that Tian Lingzun had usurped the Liu surname and taken control.

    235

    父家财令遵下狱石李二夫族与本府要吏亲党上至府帅判官行军司马随使都押衙各受方遇二女赂钱数千缗而以令遵与姊及书劵安美同情共盗俱弃市人知其寃府帅李从敏令妻来朝惧事发令内地弥缝侍御史赵都嫉恶论奏明宗惊怒下镇州委副使符按问果得事实自亲吏髙知柔及判官行军司马及通货僧人妇人皆弃市惟从敏初欲削官停任中官哀祈竟罚一季俸议者以受赂曲法杀人而八议之所不及失刑也【安重诲诛后王贵妃用事故也】
    　　因事纳谏
    　　冯道对太子食有邪蒿师傅以其名邪令去之况人事乎上退问羣臣邪蒿之义范延光对无名之役不急之务且宜罢之自安重诲伏诛而宦者孟汉琼连宫掖之势居中用事人皆惮之因宰臣奏对延光等深言邪蒿春冰虎尾之戒欲惊悟上意也上圣体乖和冯道对寝膳之间动思调衞因指御前果实曰如食桃不康翌日见李而思戒可也初上因御李暴得风虚之疾冯道不敢斥言因奏事讽悟上意

    Explanation

    235

    The father's family wealth led to Zun being imprisoned, and the clans of Shi and Li, along with important officials and relatives within the local administration, up to the governor, judge, military commander, and other key officials, each received bribes from the two women in the form of thousands of strings of coins. Consequently, Zun and his sister, along with their accomplices, were all executed publicly for their crimes, and people knew they were innocent but could not do anything about it. The governor, Li Congmin, ordered his wife to come to court to prevent the scandal from spreading further. The censor, Zhao Du, reported the corruption to the emperor, who was shocked and angry and sent an official to investigate in the town of Zhenzhou. The investigation confirmed the truth of the matter, and not only the officials but also the monks and women involved in the bribery were all executed publicly. Li Congmin initially wanted to be demoted or dismissed, but after pleading, he was only fined for one quarter of his salary. Critics argued that the officials were guilty of accepting bribes, perverting the law, and killing people, which was beyond the scope of the "eight categories" of leniency and thus constituted a miscarriage of justice. This was a consequence of the fall of An Zhonghe and the influence of Empress Dowager Wang.

    Because of the Situation, Advice Was Given

    Feng Dao told the crown prince that there was a plant called "xie hao" (a type of herb) in his food. The tutor believed the name was unlucky and ordered it to be removed. Feng Dao asked, "How much more so in human affairs?" The emperor asked the ministers about the meaning of "xie hao," and Fan Yangguang replied that unnecessary tasks and non-urgent matters should be discontinued. After An Zhonghe was executed, the eunuch Meng Hanqiong gained power and influence, and everyone was afraid of him. During a meeting with the prime minister, Fan Yangguang and others strongly warned about the dangers of "xie hao," using the metaphors of "spring ice" and "tiger's tail" to shock the emperor into understanding. The emperor's health was poor, and Feng Dao advised him to pay attention to his diet and rest. Feng Dao pointed to the fruits in front of the emperor and said that eating peaches might not be good, and the next day seeing plums should serve as a reminder. Initially, the emperor suddenly fell ill with a wind-damp disease while riding a horse, and Feng Dao did not directly mention it but used the opportunity to subtly advise the emperor.

    秦王轻佻
    　　秦王重荣之为元帅轻佻浅露狎近浮薄列坐将帅而与判官论诗未跻大位而许人祸福由是中外忌惮竟及诛败上闻重荣伏诛悲骇防落御榻气絶复苏者再由是不豫转増以至晏驾自云我今日自作刘窟头也
    　　沈徽曲江吟【温顗附】
    　　吴兴沈徽乃温庭筠诸甥也尝言其舅善鼓琴吹笛亦云有即弹有孔即吹不独柯亭爨桐也制曲江吟十调善杂画每理发则思来輙罢栉而缀文也　有温顗者乃飞卿之孙宪之子仕蜀官至常侍无他能唯以隐僻绘事为克绍也中间出官旋游临邛欲以此献于州牧为谒者拒之然温氏之先貌陋时号钟馗顗之子郢魁形克肖其祖亦以奸而流之

    Explanation

    236

    Translation

    The Qin king was frivolous and shallow.
    When he was made a general, he was superficial and revealing, fond of being close to and associating with superficial people. He would sit with the generals and discuss poetry with his officials, making promises of good or bad fortune before reaching a high position. As a result, both inside and outside the court, people feared him, and his downfall eventually came. When the emperor heard of his execution, he was overwhelmed with grief and shock, falling from his throne, nearly dying, and regaining consciousness twice. This led to his health worsening, and he eventually passed away. He said to himself, "I am now in the same situation as Liu Koutou."

    Shen Hui's "Qujiang Yin" [with a section on Wen Yi]
    Shen Hui of Wu Xing is a relative of Wen Tingyun. He once said that his uncle was skilled in playing the qin and the flute, and that he could play any stringed instrument and blow into any hole, not just the famous instruments like the qin and the flute. He composed ten tunes for "Qujiang Yin" and was skilled in mixed media painting. Whenever he had an idea while combing his hair, he would stop combing and immediately write it down.

    Wen Yi, the grandson of Wen Tingyun and the son of Wen Xian, served in Shu and reached the position of Attendant. He had no other talents besides continuing the tradition of his ancestors in painting. He left his official post and traveled to Linqiong, intending to present his work to the governor, but the gatekeeper rejected it. His ancestor, Wen Tingyun, was unattractive and was often referred to as Zhong Kui. Wen Yi's son, Wen Ying, resembled his grandfather and was also exiled for similar reasons.

    姜志认父
    　　姜志许昌人自小乱离失其父母尔后仕蜀至武信军节度使先是廐中圉人姜春者事之多年频罹鞭朴一旦告老于国夫人请免马廐之役而丐食于道路夫人愍之诘其乡贯姻亲兼云有一子随军入川莫知存亡其小字身上记验一一述之果志之父也洎父子相认悲号殒絶志乃授父杖俾笞其背以偿昔日所误之事举国嗟叹之此事川蜀皆知
    　　王氏子知前生
    　　唐四方馆王鄑尚书自西京乱离挈家入蜀防嘉陵江下至利州百堂寺前其弟年七嵗忽云我曽有经一卷藏在此寺石龛内因令家人相随访获之木梳亦存寺僧曰此我童子也较其所夭之年与王氏之子所生之嵗果騐也其前生父母尚存及长仕蜀官至令録数任即王鄂【近闻殁于雅斜往往灵语説事如平生又言我为隂官云云即记前生不诬也】

    Explanation

    Final Translation

    Jiang Zhi Recognizes His Father

    Jiang Zhi, originally from Xuancheng, lost his parents at a young age due to the turmoil. Later, he served in Shu and rose to the position of Governor of Wuxin Army. Previously, there was a stable-hand named Jiang Chun who had served him for many years and frequently suffered from beatings. One day, Jiang Chun retired to the State Lady and requested to be exempted from the duties of the horse stable, instead begging for food on the roads. The State Lady pitied him and asked about his place of origin, family connections, and also mentioned that he had a son who had followed the army into Sichuan, but his fate was unknown. Jiang Chun recounted his son's pet name and physical marks, which confirmed that he was indeed Jiang Zhi's father. When father and son recognized each other, they cried out in sorrow until they fainted. Jiang Zhi then gave his father a stick to beat his back, seeking to atone for the past mistreatment. The whole country sighed and lamented this story, and it became widely known throughout Sichuan.

    Wang's Son Knew His Past Life

    During the Tang Dynasty, Wang Zi, a high-ranking official in the Four Directions Hall, fled with his family to Sichuan during the turmoil in the Western Capital. They traveled down the Jialing River and arrived at the Bai Tang Temple in Lixian (Lizhou). His younger brother, who was seven years old, suddenly said, "I once had a scroll of scriptures hidden in this temple's stone niche." They sent family members to search and found the scroll, along with a comb. The temple monk said, "This is my former child." By comparing the year of his death with the year Wang Zi's brother was born, it was verified that they were the same person. His former parents were still alive. When Wang Zi grew up, he served in Shu and held several positions as a county magistrate, eventually becoming Wang E. [Recently, it was heard that he died in Ya Xie, often speaking spiritually about past events as if they were his own life, and saying he was an official in the underworld. This confirms that his memory of his past life is not false.]

    舒溥三斥三遇
    　　舒溥者万州人粗解书记事前恩州刺史李希元往广州谒嗣薛王归装甚丰于时蜀兵部毛文晏侍郎宣徽宋光葆开府前陵州王洪使君皆未宦达舒子窃资而奉之尔后三人继登显秩而恃此阶縁多行无礼于恩牧因笞而遣之始依陵州王洪奏授井研令寻为王公所鄙次依宋开府亦以不恭见弃转荐于嘉牧顾珣珣承奉贵近误奏为团练判官赐绯转员外郎未久失意复疎之俾其入贡仍假一表希除畿邑实要斥逺之邸吏知意表竟不行淹留经年乃经唐陈状只望本分入贡之恩泽之相庭其北靣因依莫测本末优与拟议转检校工部郎中所谓三斥三遇也愚甞览吴武陵为李吉甫相所误致及第因而附之

    Explanation

    238

    Shu Pu's Three Rebukes and Three Encounters

    Shu Pu, a native of Wanzhou, had a basic understanding of writing and was once an assistant to Li Xiyuan, the Shizun of Enzhou, who went to Guangzhou to visit the successor of Prince Xue. Upon his return, he brought back a very rich load. At that time, Mao Wenyuan, the Langyuan of the Shu Ministry of War, Song Guangbao, the Kaidou of the Xuanwei, and Wang Hong, the Shizun of Lingzhou, were all not yet successful in their official careers. Shu Pu stole funds to support them. Later, these three rose to prominent positions but depended on this connection and often acted disrespectfully. They were beaten and sent away by the Enzhou Shizun. Initially, they were appointed as the magistrate of Jingyan by the Lingzhou Shizun Wang Hong, but they were soon disdained by him. Next, they were recommended to the Kaidou Song Guangbao, who also rejected them for being disrespectful. They were then recommended to the governor of Jia, Gu Xun, who mistakenly appointed them as a commandant's judge and bestowed upon them a red robe, promoting them to the position of Langyuan. However, they soon lost favor and were again distanced. They were ordered to present tribute, and they fabricated a memorial, hoping to be appointed to a position in the capital. The officials in charge of distant outposts knew the intention but the memorial was ultimately not carried out, and they stayed for many years. They then presented a memorial to the Tang court, hoping for the usual benefits of presenting tribute, but the beginning and end were unclear. They were given favorable consideration and appointed as the Langyuan of the Ministry of Works. This is what is meant by being thrice rebuked and thrice encountered. I have read about Wu Wuling, who was mistakenly promoted by Li Jifu, and thus attached himself to him.

    239

    于何博士【髙讽附】
    　　于何博士相国驸马悰之子仕蜀至五防无他才俊止以贵公子享俸禄而已耻其官卑诣执政陈啓自述门阀其末云昔年入贡在花树韦吏部先徳之前【即韦庄相也】今日通班在新津冯长官小男之后【即少常鋭也】执政愍而慰之　有髙讽者自云太尉诸孙覉旅三川而多忤物每叹歉求官不遂徧告人曰何不还我罗城来葢以掌武所筑蜀人安之其疎濶皆如此也
    　　韦巽尫钝【周仁矩附】
    　　韦巽大尉昭度之子也尫懦钝率由婢妪仕蜀先主以其事旧优容之以至卿监或为同列所讥云三公门前出死狗巽曰死狗门前出三公又能酬酢也　周仁矩者即蜀相庠之子为驸马都尉有才藻而庸劣国亡后与贫丐者为伍俾一人先道爵里于市肆酒坊之间人有哀者日获三二百钱与其徒饮噉而已成都人皆嗟叹之

    Explanation

    239

    Yu He, the Doctor of the Imperial College, was the son of Prince Consort Cong, a high-ranking official. He served in the state of Shu, reaching the rank of Wu Fang, the fifth rank of officials, and had no other talents or accomplishments. He was merely a wealthy nobleman who enjoyed a salary, but he was ashamed of his low-ranking position. He approached the chief executive to present his case, detailing his family's illustrious lineage. In his petition, he mentioned that in his youth, he had participated in the imperial examination alongside Wei Zhuang, the former Minister of the Imperial College, who was renowned for his virtue and reputation. Today, he had advanced in rank to be on par with the son of Feng, a high-ranking official in Xinjin. The chief executive pitied him and consoled him.

    There was also Gao Feng, who claimed to be a descendant of a high-ranking official and was wandering in the three provinces, often offending others. He frequently lamented his inability to obtain an official position and would tell people, "Why don't you bring me back to the city wall?" This was because the city wall was built by the high-ranking military official, and the people of Shu felt secure there. His carelessness and lack of propriety were evident in his actions.

    Wei Xun, the son of Grand Marshal Zhao Du, was weak and dull, following the ways of maids and old women. He served in the state of Shu and was favored by the former ruler due to his long-standing service, allowing him to reach the rank of Qingjian. However, he was often mocked by his peers, who said, "A dog comes out of the gate of the Three Dukes." Wei Xun responded, "Even a dog can come out of the gate of the Three Dukes, and it can still respond to others." Zhou Renju, the son of Minister Xiang of Shu, was a驸马都尉 with some literary talent but was considered mediocre. After the fall of the state, he associated with poor beggars, having one person announce his official title and hometown in marketplaces and taverns. Those who felt pity for him would give him three or four hundred coins a day, which he used to buy food and drink with his companions. The people of Chengdu all sighed at his plight.

    中令忍欲【王彦章附】
    　　唐凤翔李曮令公蜀充馈运使于蜀城东门外下营魏王与郭侍中入居蜀宫玉帛子女他人无复见矣中令寂寞无以遣适颍川陈昭符仕蜀累剖竹符早在歧山微有阶縁而得候谒因求一美人以献之有萧夫人者乃蜀先主之宠爱也曽赐与凤翔归降指挥使王胡【忘其名】赐名丞弇王胡乃歧王赐姓连彦字卒后萧氏寡而无子其容态明悟国人具闻陈致媒氏诱之而献抱衾之夕中令于隙中窥之叹其妍妙乃诘所来左右方以王胡
    为对中令止之曰王胡背恩投蜀诚不可容然其向来吾之子侄矣此事不可遽令约回时有知者皆重中令少年而忍欲复礼诚贵达人难事颍川每为愚话之　周彦章本姓王以军功为金吾衞使后主采选宫妓王有女甚美因命内人欲选入宫王乃按劒曰某是先皇令与周氏作义男本姓王为众所闻也岂有王氏女而事王氏乎因召左右小军将无妇者以女衣襟结之便为夫妻尔后国变王乃领兵于大安楼前胁后主诛君侧韩昭等即其事也

    Explanation

    240

    The Official of Self-Restraint [Appendix: Wang Yanzhang]
    During the Tang dynasty, Li Yan, the Commander of Fengxiang, was dispatched to Shu as the Transport Commissioner. He set up his camp outside the eastern gate of the Shu city. Wei Wang and Guo Shizhong then entered the Shu palace, and the treasures, silks, and concubines were no longer accessible to others. The official, feeling lonely and without companionship, sought solace in the company of people. Chen Zhao Fu from Yingchuan, who had served in Shu and been granted authority early on in Qishan, had a slight connection and was able to gain an audience. He then requested a beautiful woman to present to the official. There was a lady named Xiao, who was favored by the former ruler of Shu. She had once been granted to Wang Hu, a commander who had surrendered to Fengxiang, and was given the name Wai. Wang Hu, who had been given the surname Zhou by the ruler of Qishan and had the courtesy name Yan, died, leaving Xiao widowed and without children. Her appearance was clear and intelligent, and she was well-known among the people. Chen arranged for a matchmaker to bring her to the official. On the night of their union, the official peeped through a crack in the window and was struck by her beauty. He then asked about her origins, and the attendants answered that she was Xiao. The official stopped them, saying, "Wang Hu betrayed his loyalty and defected to Shu; he truly cannot be tolerated. However, he was once a member of my family. This matter cannot be hastily ordered to return." Those who knew about it all regarded the official as young and self-restrained, and resuming propriety is truly valuable, but it is difficult for a great man to do. Yingchuan often told me this story.

    Wang Yanzhang, originally surnamed Wang, was made the Chief of the Gold and Halberd Guard due to his military achievements. The last emperor selected palace dancers, and Wang had a very beautiful daughter. He then summoned a female servant to select her to enter the palace. Wang then drew his sword and said, "I am the late emperor's order to adopt Zhou as my son. My original surname is Wang, which is known by many. How can a Wang daughter serve a Wang?" He then summoned small military officers who were unmarried and tied his daughter's sleeves to theirs, making them husband and wife immediately. Later, when the state changed, Wang led troops to the front of the Dadian Building to threaten the last emperor and kill Han Zhao and others who were close to the emperor, which was the event in question.

    241

    何见
    　　王蜀时阆州人何奎不知何术而言事甚效既非卜相人号何见蜀之近贵咸神之鬻银之肆有患白癞者传于两世矣何见之谓曰尔所苦我知之矣我为嫁娉少环钏钗箆之属尔能致之乎即所苦立愈矣白癞者欣然许之因谓曰尔家必有他人旧功徳或供养之具存焉亡者之魂无依故遣为此但去之必瘳也患者归视功徳堂内本无他物忖思久之老母曰佛前纱乃重围时他人之物曽取而置之得非此乎遽令撤去仍脩斋忏其疾遂痊竟受其镮钏之赠何生未遇不汲汲于官宦末年祈于大官自布衣除兴元少尹金紫兼妻邑号子亦赐绯不之任便归阆州而卒预知死期也虽术数通神而名器逾分识者知后主之政悉此也

    Explanation

    241

    He Who Sees Ghosts

    During the Later Shu period, there was a man named He Kui from Langzhou who did not know any specific technique but was highly effective in predicting events. Although he was not a fortune-teller, he was called "He Who Sees Ghosts." Those close to the imperial court revered him. In a silver shop, there was a person suffering from a skin disease that had been passed down through two generations. He Kui saw this person and said, "I know what you suffer from. I will arrange a marriage for you with a few rings, bracelets, and combs. Can you obtain them?" If you can, your suffering will immediately be cured." The person with the skin disease eagerly agreed. He Kui then said, "There must be some old merit or offerings left by someone in your family. The souls of the dead have no place to rest, so they send this affliction as a result. If you remove them, you will surely recover." The person returned home and searched the hall for religious offerings. There was nothing unusual there. After pondering for a long time, the old mother said, "The silk screen in front of the Buddha statue was placed there during the time of the siege. It might be someone else's item. Could this be it?" They immediately removed it and performed religious rituals for purification. The person's disease was cured, and they eventually received the rings and bracelets as a gift. He Kui, who had not yet found his fortune, was not eager for official positions. In his later years, he prayed to a high official and was appointed as the local administrative official of Xingyuan with the title of "Jinzi" and a purple robe. His son was also granted a red official robe. He did not take up the position and returned to Langzhou, where he died. He knew in advance the time of his death. Although his divination skills were so advanced that they seemed supernatural, his titles and honors exceeded his status. Those who understood recognized that this was typical of Emperor Houzhu's reign.

    242

    孙斋
    　　嘉州夹江县人孙雄人号孙斋其言事亦何奎之流伪蜀主归命时内官宋愈昭将军数员旧与孙相善亦神其术将赴洛都咸问其将来升沈孙俛首曰诸官记之此去无灾无福但行及野狐泉已来税驾处曰孙雄非圣人耶此际新旧使头皆不见矣诸官皆疑之尔后量其行迈合在咸京左右后主罹伪诏之祸庄宗遇邺都之变所谓新旧使头皆不得见之验也愚同席备见説故记之

    Explanation

    242

    Sun Xizhai
    A man from Jiajiang County, Chazhou Prefecture, named Sun Xizhai, was also skilled in predicting the future, much like He Kui. When the false Shu ruler submitted, several court officials, including the generals Song Yuzhao, who were old acquaintances of Sun Xizhai, regarded his skills as divine. As they were about to travel to the capital, they all asked Sun Xizhai about his future prospects. Sun Xizhai bowed his head and said, "Officials, remember this: on this journey, there will be no disaster or good fortune. We will stop at the Wild Fox Spring. The place where we stop will be the place where we will settle." One of the officials said, "Is Sun Xizhai not a sage?" At this moment, neither the new nor the old envoys were seen. All the officials doubted him. Later, it was found that his journey was expected to end near Chang'an. The later ruler suffered a disaster due to a false edict, and Emperor Zhuangzong of Later Tang faced an upheaval in Yedu. This was the proof that neither the new nor the old envoys were seen. The author, who was present, recorded this account.

    243

    冯见
    　　遂宁有冯见【忘其名】似有所睹知人吉凶颍川陈绚为武信军留后而刘令公知俊交替摭其旧事叠有奏论冯生谓颍川曰府主虽号元戎前无旌节所引殆不久乎幸勿忧也未逾嵗而彭城伏诛有官人林泳者本闽人也甞谓僚友曰安有生人而终日见乎无听其妖冯闻之甚不平或一日对众谓之曰阁下为官多不克终葢曽杀一女人为祟以公禄夀未尽莫致其便我能言其姓名公信之乎于是惭惧言诚于冯生许为解其寃也他皆此
    　　休公真率
    　　沙门贯休钟离人也风骚之外精于笔劄举止真率诚髙人也然不晓时事往往诋讦朝贤他亦不知已之是非荆州成中令问其笔法非休公曰此事湏登坛而授非草草而言成令衔之乃遽于黔中因病以诗寄意曰见説气清邪不入不知尔病自何来以诗见意也冯涓大夫有大名于人间沦落于蜀自比杜工部意谓他人无出其右休公初至蜀先谒韦书记庄而长乐公后至遂与相

    Explanation

    243

    Final Translation

    Feng Sees Ghosts

    In Suining, there was a man named Feng who claimed to see ghosts and seemed to have some insight into people's fortunes and misfortunes. Yingchuan Chen Xuan served as the acting commander of Wuxin Army, and Liu Linggong Zhi Jun alternated with him, repeatedly reporting on past incidents. Feng told Chen Xuan, "Although the lord of the mansion is called the supreme commander, without the banner and insignia, his appointment will not last long. Do not worry about it." Within a year, Pengcheng was executed.

    There was an official named Lin Yong, originally from Fujian. Once, he said to his colleagues, "How can a living person see ghosts all day? Do not listen to his nonsense." Feng heard this and was very angry. One day, he spoke to the crowd and said, "You have often failed to complete your duties as an official. Because you once killed a woman, causing her spirit to haunt you, and since your official salary and longevity have not yet ended, it cannot harm you. I can tell you her name. Do you believe me?" He then felt ashamed and fearful, and promised Feng to clear her name. The rest are similar.

    Master Xiu's Straightforwardness

    Shaolin Guanxiu was from Zhongli. Besides being skilled in poetry and prose, he was also proficient in calligraphy. His behavior was straightforward and honest, truly a high person. However, he did not understand current affairs and often criticized officials, not knowing whether he was right or wrong.

    Cheng Zhongling of Jingzhou asked him about his calligraphy techniques, but he did not answer. He said, "Your qi is clear, and evil cannot enter. I don't know what illness you have." He expressed his intention through poetry.

    Feng Juan, the doctor, had a great reputation among people. He fell into obscurity in Shu, comparing himself to Du Gongbu, thinking that no one else could surpass him. Master Xiu first went to Shu and paid respects to Wei Shuji Zhuang, and after Longle Gong arrived, they became acquainted.

    244

    见欣然抚掌曰我与你阿叔有分长乐怒而拂袖他日谒之竟不逢迎乃曰此阿师似我礼拜也自是频投刺字终为阍者所拒休公谓韦公曰我得得为渠入蜀何意见怪【道门杜先生亦以此疎之】国清寺律僧尝许具蒿脯未得间姜侍中宅有斋律僧先在焉休公次至未揖主人大貎乃拍手谓律僧曰乃蒿饼子何在其他皆此通衢徒步行嚼果子未甞跨马时人甚重之异乎广宣栖白之流也
    　　北梦琐言二十卷富春孙光宪纂集唐末后梁后唐石晋时事此书乃武林忻悦学家藏陜刋旧本今归成芥庵夏隐君中间刋误舛讹如日曰纂簒欢叹虽难关阙祸福等字可以意改余不敢强以俟别本订之至正二十四年嵗次甲辰五月七日写起至二十七日庚寅辍卷华亭在家道人孙道明识于泗北村居映雪斋时年六十又八也连日梅雨时雨西南二乡皆成巨浸丰年未卜今日喜晴聊书记耳
    　　丙辰五月侍疾于家因假琴川书屋所藏吴方山抄本核过吴本元缺第二十卷此本不知从何得也二十六日小暑节叶石君识

    　　北梦琐言卷二十

    Explanation

    244

    He joyfully clapped his hands and said, "I and your uncle have a connection." Changle became angry and brushed aside his sleeves. On another day, when he visited, he was not received. He said, "This monk seems to worship me like I do." From then on, he frequently sent letters or messages, but he was ultimately rejected by the gatekeeper. Xiu Gong said to Wei Gong, "I went out of my way to bring him into Shu. What do you find strange about it?" [The Daoist Master Du also distanced himself from him.] A monk at Guoqing Temple had once promised to prepare a dish of wild celery and dried meat, but it was not ready. At the residence of the Attendant-in-Attendance Jiang, there was a gathering. The monk arrived first, but the host, who had a large appearance, clapped his hands and said to the monk, "Where are the wild celery cakes?" The other monks were all like this. He walked on the main roads, eating snacks or fruits, and he never rode a horse. The people of the time held him in high regard, unlike the likes of Guang Xuan and Qi Bai.

    Twenty Volumes of the Random Sayings of the North, compiled by Sun Guangxian of Fuchun, cover events of the late Tang, Later Liang, Later Tang, and Later Jin periods. This book is an old edition printed in Shaanxi and owned by a scholar in Wulin. Now it belongs to Xia Yinjun at Chengjie An. There are errors and mistakes in the middle, such as the word "zuan" being used for "zuan" (usurpation). Although joy and sorrow are related to difficulty and lack, words like "blessing" and "misfortune" can be changed according to meaning. I dare not force it; I wait for another edition to correct it. Started writing on the seventh day of the fifth month of the twenty-fourth year of the Zhizheng era, the year of Jia Chen. Stopped writing on the twenty-seventh day of the fifth month, the day of Geng Yin. Huating monk Sun Daoming recorded this in his hut called Yingsnow Hall at the village of Sibei, at the age of sixty-eight. For several days, the plum rains and seasonal rains turned the southwestern two towns into large bodies of water. This year's harvest is uncertain, but today is sunny, so I just write this down.

    In the fifth month of the Bingchen year, I was taking care of a sick person at home. Because of a copy of Wu Fangshan's manuscript from the Book Room in Qinchuan, I checked it. Wu's version originally lacked the twentieth volume. This version is unknown where it came from. On the twenty-sixth day of the fifth month, the Minor Heat festival, Ye Shijun recorded this.
